<p><b>Sour Alyn</b> is a man-at-arms sworn to House Bolton. He is one of the Bastard's Boys. </p>
<p><b>Lord Redwyne</b> was the Lord of the Arbor and head of House Redwyne during the reign of kings Viserys I, Aegon II and Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>A certain man</b> is a sorcerer who made Varys a eunuch. His true name is not mentioned. In the television adapation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, the sorcerer is portrayed by Harold James McMullan. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Abelar Hightower</b> was a knight from House Hightower during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>tourney at Ashford Meadow</b> or <b>tourney at Ashford</b> was a tourney hosted by House Ashford at Ashford Meadow in 209&nbsp;AC. Due to the accidental death of Prince Baelor Targaryen—the Prince of Dragonstone, son and heir of King Daeron II Targaryen, and Hand of the King—Ashford was one of the most famous and historically significant tourneys. </p>
<p><b>Abelon</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel and the author of <i>When Women Ruled: Ladies of the Aftermath</i>. </p>
<p><b>Aberdolf Strongbeard</b> is a minor character in <i>Game of Thrones</i>. He is a man-at-arms in service to House Baratheon of Dragonstone and later House Stark. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Addam Frey</b> was a knight from House Frey during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. He was a cousin to the daughter of Lord Frey of the Crossing. </p>
<p>The <b>wedding tourney at Whitewalls</b> was a tourney held by Lord Ambrose Butterwell to celebrate his second marriage to Lady Frey in 212&nbsp;AC. It was held at Whitewalls in the riverlands and was the grounds for the Second Blackfyre Rebellion. </p>
<p><b>Addam Hightower</b> was Lord of the Hightower and head of House Hightower during the reign of King Aegon I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Addam Marbrand</b> is a knight of House Marbrand and the son and heir of Lord Damon Marbrand of Ashemark. He is one of the chief knights in the service of Tywin Lannister, Lord of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>House Lannister of Casterly Rock</b> is one of the Great Houses of Seven Kingdoms, and the principal house of the westerlands. Their seat is Casterly Rock, though another branch exists in nearby Lannisport. Their sigil is a golden lion on a field of crimson. Their official motto is "Hear Me Roar!" However, their unofficial motto, equally well known, is "A Lannister always pays his debts." The Warden of the West is a Lannister by tradition. Their gold mines have made the Lannisters the wealthiest of the Great Houses. </p>
<p><b>Addam</b> was a merchant of Duskendale and the subject of the <i>True Account of Addam of Duskendale's Journeys</i>. </p>
<p><b>Addam Osgrey</b> was a squire from House Osgrey during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. He was the third son of Ser Eustace Osgrey of Standfast. </p>
<p>The <b>First Blackfyre Rebellion</b>, originally called the <b>Blackfyre Rebellion</b>, was a war fought between the loyalist forces of King Daeron II Targaryen and the rebel forces of his half-brother, Daemon I Blackfyre. Conflict arose when Daemon, a bastard son of the late King Aegon IV Targaryen, claimed the throne of his older, true born brother, King Daeron II Targaryen, which resulted in open civil war that divided the Seven Kingdoms. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Addam Rivers</b> was a knight and a bastard of the Riverlands who claimed the title of river king or King of the Trident in the generations after the riverlands were conquered by the Storm King Arlan III Durrandon. Addam had a brief, inglorious reign, before being put down by the might of Storm's End. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Addam Velaryon</b>, born <b>Addam of Hull</b>, was a legitimised bastard from Driftmark of dragonseed descent, like his brother Alyn. During the Dance of the Dragons, Addam became a knight and the heir to Driftmark and House Velaryon. He was a dragonrider whose dragon was Seasmoke. </p>
<p>Mutual exhaustion and negotiated peace: </p>
<p>Ser <b>Addam Whitehead</b> is a knight from House Whitehead and the son and heir of old Lord Whitehead. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Addison Hill</b>, known as the <b>Bastard of Cornfield</b>, was a bastard knight from House Swyft and a Lord Commander of the Kingsguard. </p>
<p>The <b>Kingsguard</b>, also known poetically as the <b>White Swords</b> or <b>white cloaks</b>, are the royal bodyguards of the Iron Throne. Regarded as the&nbsp;finest knights in the Seven Kingdoms, they are sworn to protect their king and the royal family with their own lives, to obey his commands, and to keep his secrets. The Kingsguard are sworn for life and are forbidden from owning land, taking a wife, or fathering children, although they can hold non-hereditary commands, such as being warden or Hand of the King. </p>
<p><b>Adrack Humble</b> is an ironborn raider and a member of House Humble. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Adrian Redfort</b> was a knight from House Redfort and a member of Rhaenyra Targaryen's Queensguard. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Adrian Tarbeck</b> was a knight from House Tarbeck who supported King Aegon II Targaryen during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Adrian Thorne</b> was a knight from House Thorne who served as Commander of the City Watch during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Aegon Ambrose</b> was a knight of House Ambrose and a member of the Warrior's Sons at the start of the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Aegon Blackfyre</b> was the eldest son of Daemon Blackfyre and the twin of Aemon Blackfyre. Aegon was Daemon's heir. </p>
<p><b>Aegon Frey</b>, called <b>Jinglebell</b>, is the lackwit son of Ser Stevron Frey and Jeyne Lydden, and the fool of the Twins. </p>
<p><b>Aegon Frey</b>, better known as <b>Aegon Bloodborn</b>, is the eldest son of Ser Aenys Frey and Tyana Wylde. </p>
<p>An <b>outlaw</b> is a person declared outside the protection of the law. </p>
<p>The <b>riverlands</b> is a central region of the Seven Kingdoms of Westeros, consisting of the rich, fertile, and populous areas around the three forks of the Trident and the northern Blackwater Rush. At the time of Aegon's Conquest the riverlands and the Iron Islands were ruled by House Hoare, the Kings of the Isles and the Rivers, although native river kings ruled centuries earlier. </p>
<p><b>Aegon I Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Aegon the Conqueror</b> and <b>Aegon the Dragon</b>, was the first Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and king on the Iron Throne, having conquered six of the Seven Kingdoms during the Conquest. The dragonlord was the founder of the ruling Targaryen dynasty of Westeros. </p>
<p>The <b>Seven Kingdoms</b> is a realm located on the continent of Westeros, ruled by the Lord of the Seven Kingdoms, the king who sits on the Iron Throne in the capital city, King's Landing. Its name derives from the situation three centuries ago when Aegon the Conqueror set to unite the lands of Westeros, which then contained seven independent realms. The new kingdom created from Aegon's Conquest contains nine distinct regions or provinces. </p>
<p><b>Aegon II Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Aegon the Elder</b>, was the sixth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne, succeeding his father, Viserys I Targaryen, as Lord of the Seven Kingdoms. His ascent was disputed by his older half-sister, Princess Rhaenyra Targaryen, who had been their father's designated heir. Aegon and Rhaenyra fought for the throne in the civil war the singers called the Dance of the Dragons, in which both siblings perished. </p>
<p>Mutual exhaustion and negotiated peace: </p>
<p><b>Aegon III Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Aegon the Younger</b>, and later as <b>Aegon the Unlucky</b>, <b>Aegon the Unhappy</b>, <b>the Broken King</b>, and most famously as <b>Aegon the Dragonbane</b>, was the seventh Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He succeeded his uncle, Aegon II Targaryen, at the conclusion of the Dance of the Dragons, which saw the victorious supporters of his late mother Rhaenyra Targaryen install him on the throne. When he was a child, his dragon was Stormcloud. Aegon kept the kingdoms united following the divisions of the civil war with the aid of his brother, Prince Viserys, whom he eventually named Hand of the King. </p>
<p><b>Aegon IV Targaryen</b>, known as <b>Aegon the Unworthy</b>, was the eleventh Targaryen to sit the Iron Throne, and is considered to be one of the worst Targaryen kings. He sired numerous bastards, legitimizing them on his deathbed, an act that led to five Blackfyre Rebellions. </p>
<p><b>Aegon V Targaryen</b> was a Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and the fifteenth Targaryen to sit the Iron Throne as King of the Andals, the Rhoynar, and the First Men. In his youth, he went by the nickname <b>Egg</b> and squired for Ser Duncan the Tall. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Aegon Targaryen</b> was the second child and only son of Prince Rhaegar Targaryen and Princess Elia Martell. </p>
<p><img alt="House Lannister.svg" src="/images/thumb/d/d5/House_Lannister.svg/30px-House_Lannister.svg.png" width="30" height="33" srcset="/images/thumb/d/d5/House_Lannister.svg/45px-House_Lannister.svg.png 1.5x, /images/thumb/d/d5/House_Lannister.svg/60px-House_Lannister.svg.png 2x">Westerlands, led by House Lannister </p>
<p>Prince <b>Aegon Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen and was the second child, and eldest son and heir, of King Aenys I Targaryen and Queen Alyssa Velaryon. After his father's death, he became a dragonrider and rode his late father's dragon, Quicksilver. He became known to history as <b>Aegon the Uncrowned</b> after his uncle usurped the Throne. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Aegon Targaryen</b> was the youngest child of Prince Baelon Targaryen and Princess Alyssa Targaryen. He was named after Aegon the Conqueror. His older brothers were King Viserys I and Prince Daemon Targaryen. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Aegon Targaryen</b> was the firstborn child of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Queen Alysanne Targaryen. He was named Aegon in honor of both Aegon the Conqueror and their deceased brother Aegon. He was born too early, however, and died three days after being born. </p>
<p><b>Aegon Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen during the Century of Blood, the son of Lord Gaemon and Lady Daenys Targaryen of Dragonstone. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Aegor Rivers</b>, frequently called <b>Bittersteel</b>, was one of the Great Bastards and a son of King Aegon IV Targaryen by his fifth mistress, Lady Barba Bracken. Aegor was the founder of a famed group of exiled sellswords, the Golden Company. In his personal arms, he combined the red stallion of House Bracken with black dragon wings from House Blackfyre, on a golden field. </p>
<p><b>Aelinor Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Aelinor Penrose</b> was a noblewoman of House Penrose and the queen consort of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Aelor Targaryen</b> was the son of Prince Rhaegel Targaryen and Lady Alys Arryn. He had a twin sister, Aelora, to whom he was married, and a younger sister, Daenora. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Aelora Targaryen</b> was the daughter of Prince Rhaegel Targaryen and Lady Alys Arryn. She had a twin brother, Aelor, to whom she was married, and a younger sister, Daenora. </p>
<p><b>Aelyx Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen during the Century of Blood, the first son of Lord Aerys Targaryen of Dragonstone. He had two younger brothers, Baelon and Daemion Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Aemma Arryn</b> was the queen consort and first wife of King Viserys I Targaryen, and a granddaughter of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and his sister-wife, Queen Alysanne Targaryen. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Daella Targaryen</b> was the eighth born child of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Queen Alysanne Targaryen. She was married to Lord Rodrik Arryn, with whom she had one child, Aemma Arryn. </p>
<p><b>Viserys I Targaryen</b> was the fifth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne, ruling from 103&nbsp;AC to 129&nbsp;AC. He succeeded his grandfather, the Old King Jaehaerys I. Viserys continued the prosperous peace and legacy of his grandsire, but the seeds for the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons that would much later engulf the realm were inadvertently sown in his reign. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Rhaenyra Targaryen</b>, cheered as <b>the Realm's Delight</b> when she was young and later called <b>the Half-Year Queen</b>, was the first-born child of King Viserys I Targaryen. Rhaenyra was King Viserys I's only living child by his first wife, Queen Aemma of House Arryn. At the age of eight, she was made her father's heir and grew up expecting to become the first ruling Queen of Westeros. Rhaenyra was a dragonrider whose mount was Syrax. </p>
<p><b>Aemon Blackfyre</b> was the second son of Daemon Blackfyre. He was Aegon Blackfyre's twin brother, the younger of the two. </p>
<p><b>Aemon Costayne</b> is a member of House Costayne and is a traveling singer. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Aemon Estermont</b> is a knight of House Estermont. He is the son of Eldon Estermont and the father of Alyn Estermont. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Aemon Rivers</b> is a knight and the only son of Ser Walder Rivers, the oldest of Lord Walder Frey's bastard sons. </p>
<p><b>Aemon Steelsong</b> is the name to be given to the free folk son of Mance Rayder and his wife Dalla when he is two years of age. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Aemon Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen. He was the third born child of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Queen Alysanne Targaryen. Aemon was married to Lady Jocelyn Baratheon. Together, they had a daughter, Princess Rhaenys. Aemon was a dragonrider whose mount was Caraxes. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Aemon Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>the Dragonknight</b>, was the second son of King Viserys II Targaryen and his wife, Lady Larra Rogare. Aemon joined the Kingsguard during the reign of his uncle, King Aegon III Targaryen, at the age of seventeen, and eventually rose to become Lord Commander. After Aegon III, Aemon served four other kings. He died saving the life of his brother, King Aegon IV Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>Kingsguard</b>, also known poetically as the <b>White Swords</b> or <b>white cloaks</b>, are the royal bodyguards of the Iron Throne. Regarded as the&nbsp;finest knights in the Seven Kingdoms, they are sworn to protect their king and the royal family with their own lives, to obey his commands, and to keep his secrets. The Kingsguard are sworn for life and are forbidden from owning land, taking a wife, or fathering children, although they can hold non-hereditary commands, such as being warden or Hand of the King. </p>
<p><b>Aemon</b>, born <b>Aemon Targaryen</b>, is the third son of King Maekar I Targaryen and his wife Dyanna Dayne. He has served as a maester to the Night's Watch at Castle Black for so long that the rest of the Seven Kingdoms has forgotten about his Targaryen blood. In the television series <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Peter Vaughan. </p>
<p>The <b>Night's Watch</b> is a military order dedicated to holding the Wall, the immense fortification on the northern border of the Seven Kingdoms, defending the realms of men from what lies beyond the Wall. The order's foundation dates back to the Age of Heroes, at the time when the Others were pushed back. The men of Night's Watch wear only black, and they are known as <b>black brothers</b>. Recruits who join the Watch are said to <b>take the black</b>. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Aemond Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Aemond One-Eye</b> and <b>Aemond the Kinslayer</b>, was a member of House Targaryen. He was the second son of King Viserys I Targaryen by his second wife, Queen Alicent Hightower, and the younger brother of King Aegon II Targaryen. Like his siblings, Aemond was a dragonrider, and rode the dragon Vhagar. </p>
<p><b>Aenys Blackfyre</b> was the fifth son of Daemon I Blackfyre and Rohanne of Tyrosh. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Aenys Frey</b> is a knight from House Frey and is the third son of Walder Frey, Lord of the Crossing, and his first spouse, Lady Perra Royce. Aenys is married to Tyana Wylde, and has two sons with her, Aegon and Ser Rhaegar. </p>
<p><b>Aenys I Targaryen</b> was Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and the second Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He was the son of King Aegon I Targaryen and his younger sister-wife, Queen Rhaenys Targaryen. He had a younger half-brother, Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Aerea Targaryen</b> was the eldest daughter of Prince Aegon and Princess Rhaena Targaryen. She had a younger twin sister, Rhaella. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Aerion Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Aerion the Monstrous</b>, or <b>Aerion Brightflame</b> as he liked to call himself, was the second son of King Maekar I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Aerion Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen during the Century of Blood, the only son of Lord Daemion Targaryen of Dragonstone. He was married to Lady Valaena Velaryon of Driftmark, together they had three children: Visenya, Aegon, and Rhaenys Targaryen. Aerion also fathered Orys Baratheon on an unknown woman. </p>
<p><b>Aeron Greyjoy</b> is the youngest surviving son of the late Lord Quellon Greyjoy and Lady Sunderly, and is a younger brother of Balon Greyjoy, Lord of the Iron Islands. As a result of a near-death experience during Greyjoy's Rebellion, Aeron became a priest of the Drowned God, and is now called the <b>Damphair</b> because of his wet hair. His acolytes are known as the drowned men. </p>
<p>The <b>Drowned God</b>, also known as <b>He Who Dwells Beneath the Waves</b>, is a sea deity worshipped by the ironborn of the Iron Islands in Westeros. The religion of the Drowned God is old, dating back to before the coming of the Andals, and the attempts of the Andal invaders to supplant it with the Seven all failed. The Drowned God religion supports the ironmen's naval, pirate culture. </p>
<p><b>Aerys Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen during the Century of Blood, the second son of Lord Aegon and Lady Elaena Targaryen of Dragonstone. He had one older brother, Maegon, and three sons, Aelyx, Baelon, and Daemion Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Aerys I Targaryen</b> was Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and the thirteenth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He succeeded his father, King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Aerys II Targaryen</b>, also called <b>the Mad King</b> and <b>King Scab</b>, was the seventeenth and last member of the Targaryen dynasty to sit the Iron Throne, ruling from 262&nbsp;AC to 283&nbsp;AC. His children that lived to adulthood, by his sister-wife, Rhaella, were Rhaegar, Viserys, and Daenerys Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Aerys II Targaryen's last mistress</b> was the daughter of one of King Aerys II Targaryen's household knights. </p>
<p><b>Aethan</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch of Castle Black. </p>
<p><b>Aethan Velaryon</b> was the powerful Lord of the Tides, Master of Driftmark, and head of House Velaryon during the reigns of Aegon I Targaryen and Aenys I Targaryen. He was married to Lady Alarra Massey and had several sons, including Daemon, and at least one daughter, Alyssa. </p>
<p><b>Aethelmure</b> was a Grand Maester of the Citadel. His life was noteworthy enough for a biography to appear in Winterfell's library. </p>
<p>The <b>Citadel</b> is a complex of buildings in Oldtown that serves as the central home to the order of the maesters. The name is also employed to refer to order of maesters as an institution, or the higher placed members. At the Citadel, the residing archmaesters teach and train new students, and convene in the Conclave. The Citadel is funded by taxes from Oldtown and payments from lords for the service of maesters. Maesters rigorously copy books at the Citadel. Leyton Hightower, the Lord of Oldtown, includes Protector of the Citadel among his titles. </p>
<p><b>Aggar</b> is an ironborn warrior. </p>
<p><b>Aggo</b> is a Dothraki horserider in the <i>khalasar</i> of Khal Drogo. </p>
<p><b>Aggo</b> is a Dothraki warrior in Moro's <i>khalasar</i>, appearing in <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Aglantine</b> is a septa of the Faith of the Seven in King's Landing. She has white hair and a sharp face. She is one of the Most Devout. </p>
<p><b>Agnes Blackwood</b> was a Lady of Raventree Hall and head of House Blackwood. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Agramore Cobb</b> was a knight from House Cobb and a member of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Agrivane</b> is an archmaester at the Citadel in Oldtown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Aladore Florent</b> was a knight from House Florent and the heir to Brightwater Keep during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alan Beesbury</b> was a knight from House Beesbury during the Dance of the Dragons. He was the heir of his grandfather, Lord Lyman Beesbury of Honeyholt. </p>
<p><b>Alan of Rosby</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch, stationed at Castle Black. He comes from Rosby in the crownlands. He is a good archer. </p>
<p><b>Alan o' the Oak</b>, also known as <b>the Blind Bowman</b>, is a legendary figure from the Age of Heroes that founded House Yew. </p>
<p><b>Alan Tarly</b> was the Lord of Horn Hill and the head of House Tarly during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Alanna</b> is a commoner from King's Landing, appearing in <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Alanna Penrose</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Alannys Harlaw</b> is the wife of Lord Balon Greyjoy and sister to Lord Rodrik Harlaw. She had four children with Balon; Rodrik, Maron, Asha and Theon. She is nicknamed "Lanny" by her brother, Lord Rodrik. </p>
<p><b>Alaric of Eysen</b> is a far-traveled singer from Eysen. </p>
<p><b>Alaric Stark</b> was the Lord of Winterfell and the head of House Stark during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Alarra Massey</b> was a noblewoman of House Massey during the reign of King Aegon I Targaryen. She was married to Lord Aethan Velaryon, Lord of the Tides and the Master of Driftmark. </p>
<p><b>Alarra Stark</b> was the daughter of Lord Alaric Stark and his wife from House Mormont. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alastor Reyne</b> was a knight from House Reyne during the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and the master-at-arms at Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Alayaya</b>, sometimes called <b>Yaya</b>, is a prostitute working at the whorehouse owned by her mother, Chataya, in King's Landing. She is a Summer Islander, but was born in King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Alayne</b> was the mother of Petyr Baelish. </p>
<p><b>Alayne Royce</b> was a noblewoman of House Royce in the reigns of kings Aenys I, Maegor I, and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Albar Royce</b> is a knight and the son and heir of Lord Nestor Royce, Keeper of the Gates of the Moon. </p>
<p><b>Albett</b> is a young recruit of the Night's Watch. He is called <b>Pimple</b> by Ser Alliser Thorne. </p>
<p><b>Albin Manwoody</b> was the last king of House Manwoody in Dorne. </p>
<p><b>Albin Massey</b> was the Lord of Stonedance and head of House Massey in the late reign of King Maegor I Targaryen and the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>alchemist</b> is a man encountered by Pate, a novice of the Citadel, in Oldtown. It is unknown if he is connected with the Alchemists Guild of King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Alebelly</b> is a fat guard of Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Alec Hunter</b> was the Lord of Longbow Hall and the head of House Hunter during the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Alekyne Florent</b> is the only son of Lord Alester Florent and Lady Melara Crane, and the heir to Brightwater Keep. He has two younger sisters, Melessa and Rhea. </p>
<p><b>Alequo Adarys</b>, known as <b>Silvertongue</b> and <b>the Tyrant of Tyrosh</b>, was a wealthy and ambitious Tyroshi merchant and a key member of the Band of Nine. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Alerie Hightower</b> is the daughter of Lord Leyton Hightower of Oldtown, and the spouse of Lord Mace Tyrell of Highgarden. She is the mother of his four children, Willas, Garlan, Loras, and Margaery. </p>
<p><b>Alesander Frey</b> is a singer and the son of Symond Frey, the seventh son of Lord Walder Frey, and Betharios of Braavos. </p>
<p><b>Alesander Staedmon</b>, called <b>Pennylover</b>, is the Lord of Broad Arch and the head of House Staedmon. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Alesandor Torrent</b> is the current Lord of Littlesister and head of House Torrent. </p>
<p><b>Alester II Arryn</b> was a King of Mountain and Vale from House Arryn. </p>
<p><b>Alester Florent</b> is the Lord of Brightwater Keep and the head of House Florent, sworn to House Tyrell of Highgarden. He is married to Lady Melara Crane and they have three children, Alekyne, Melessa, and Rhea. His niece, Selyse, is married to Stannis Baratheon, Lord of Dragonstone. </p>
<p><b>Alester Norcross</b> is the eldest son of Ser Hosman Norcross and Delena Florent. He has a younger brother, Renly, and a bastard half-brother, Edric Storm. He is probably named after his mother's uncle, Lord Alester Florent. </p>
<p><b>Alester Oakheart</b> was a member of House Oakheart. There is a tapestry at Old Oak depicting him in the Prince's Pass, blowing a warhorn with his last breath. </p>
<p><b>Alester Wynch</b> was a nobleman of House Wynch. </p>
<p><b>Alf of Runnymudd</b> is a builder of the Night's Watch from Runnymudd. </p>
<p><b>Alfador</b> was a maester who served House Hightower at the Hightower in Oldtown during the reign of Viserys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Alford</b> was a Grand Maester of the Citadel during the late reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alfred Broome</b> was a knight from House Broome, sworn to House Targaryen during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Alfyn</b>, also known as <b>Alfyn Crowkiller</b>, is an infamous wildling leader. He has at least four sons. </p>
<p><b>Alfyn</b> was a septon of the Faith of the Seven during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen, later becoming the High Septon. </p>
<p><b>Alia of Braavos</b> is a singer from the Free City of Braavos. </p>
<p><br> The <b>Purple Wedding</b> is the fan-given nickname for the wedding between King Joffrey I Baratheon and Margaery Tyrell on the first day of the new century, 300&nbsp;AC. The wedding is a lavish affair, but ends in disarray when Joffrey chokes to death. Unlike the Red Wedding, this wedding is not called so in the books. </p>
<p><b>Aliandra Martell</b> was the ruling Princess of Dorne and head of House Nymeros Martell during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Alicent Hightower</b> was a member of House Hightower who became the second wife to King Viserys I Targaryen. She was the daughter of Ser Otto Hightower, who had been Hand of the King to Jaehaerys I, Viserys I, and later his grandson Aegon II. She was the mother of King Aegon II, Queen Helaena, Prince Aemond and Prince Daeron. </p>
<p><b>All-for-Joffrey</b> is an old man held captive by Ser Gregor Clegane and his men in a village at the Gods Eye. His real name is not mentioned. Other prisoners start calling him All-for-Joffrey because he keeps insisting that he and his son do all for King Joffrey. </p>
<p><b>Alios Qhaedar</b> is a candidate to become a triarch of Volantis. </p>
<p><b>Alla Tyrell</b> is the eldest daughter of Ser Leo Tyrell and Lady Alys Beesbury. She is a granddaughter of Ser Victor Tyrell, the latter being a cousin of Lord Mace Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Allana Tyrell</b> is a cousin of Margaery Tyrell, mentioned in <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Allaquo</b> is a mummer of the Ship. </p>
<p><b>Allar</b> was a maester of the Citadel. </p>
<p><b>Allar Deem</b> is a member of the City Watch of King's Landing and one of Janos Slynt's most ardent supporters. </p>
<p><b>Allard Royce</b> was the Lord of Runestone and the head of House Royce during the reign of King Aenys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Allard Seaworth</b> is the second son of Ser Davos Seaworth and his wife Marya. He is the captain of the <i>Lady Marya</i>, named for his mother. </p>
<p><b>Alleras</b>, known as the <b>Sphinx</b>, is an acolyte studying at the Citadel in Oldtown. His mother is a trader and he claims not to be a noble's son as claimed by a few others. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alliser Thorne</b> is a knight from House Thorne who now serves as the master-at-arms of the Night's Watch at Castle Black. While capable, he is bitter and humorless, and is particularly hated by many recruits of the Night's Watch who have been trained by him. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Owen Teale. </p>
<p><b>Castle Black</b> is the main stronghold of the Night's Watch and the seat of their Lord Commander. The castle is situated along the Wall between Queensgate to the west and Oakenshield to the east, near the center of the Wall, at the northern end of the kingsroad. The village of Mole's Town is located half a league to the south along the kingsroad. </p>
<p><b>Allyria Dayne</b> is a member of House Dayne, and according to semi-canon sources the younger sibling of Ser Arthur Dayne and Lady Ashara Dayne. She is the aunt of the young Edric Dayne, Lord of Starfall, whose father was her older brother. </p>
<p><b>Alton Butterwell</b> was a Lord of Lord Harroway's Town and head of House Butterwell. He was the master of coin during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Alton Greyjoy</b>, known as the <b>Holy Fool</b>, was a Lord of the Iron Islands and head of House Greyjoy. </p>
<p><b>Alton Celtigar</b> was the Lord of Claw Isle and the head of House Celtigar during the reign of King Aegon I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alton Lannister</b> is the cousin of Ser Jaime Lannister, Tyrion Lannister and Queen Cersei Lannister. The character was created specifically for the TV Series and is played by Karl Davies. He replaces Cleos Frey from the books, as being a captive of House Stark and delivering terms to House Lannister. His name appears to have been changed so that TV viewers would not be confused that he is on the Lannisters' side, despite House Frey officially declaring for Robb Stark. </p>
<p><b>Alvyn Sharp</b> is a member of House Sharp and an ironborn captain. </p>
<p><b>Alyce</b> is a serving girl at the Peach in Stoney Sept. </p>
<p><b>Alyce Graceford</b> is the Lady of Holyhall and the head of House Graceford. </p>
<p><b>Alyn</b> is a member of the household guard of Lord Eddard Stark at Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Red Alyn of the Rosewood</b> is a steward of the Night's Watch. He comes from the Rosewood. </p>
<p><b>Sour Alyn</b> is a man-at-arms sworn to House Bolton. He is one of the Bastard's Boys. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Ambrose</b> is a squire from House Ambrose. The son of Lord Arthur Ambrose and Lady Alysanne Hightower, Alyn is betrothed to Elinor Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Ashford</b> was a knight of House Ashford during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Blackwood</b> is the fifth son of Lord Tytos Blackwood of Raventree Hall. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alyn Bullock</b> was a knight in service to House Targaryen. His father, Ser Merrell Bullock, was the commander of the castle garrison at Dragonstone during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. Alyn and his brother Ser Howard served alongside their father. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Cockshaw</b> was the Lord and head of House Cockshaw during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alyn Connington</b>, also known as <b>the Pale Griffin</b>, was a knight from House Connington, who eventually became Lord Commander of the Kingsguard at an unknown time. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alyn Estermont</b> is a knight of House Estermont. He is the son of Aemon Estermont and the grandson of Eldon Estermont. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Frey</b> is the son of Ser Arwood Frey and Ryella Royce. He is the twin brother of Androw Frey. His older sister is Ryella Frey, and his younger sister is Hostella Frey. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alyn Garner</b> was a knight of House Garner during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Haigh</b> is the youngest son of Ser Leslyn Haigh and Perriane Frey. He has two older brothers; Ser Harys and Ser Donnel Haigh. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alyn Hunt</b> is a knight of House Hunt. He is the cousin of Ser Hyle Hunt. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Marbrand</b> was the Lord of Ashemark and head of House Marbrand during the reign of kings Maekar I and Aegon V Targaryen. He was the father of Lady Jeyne Marbrand, the wife of Lord Tytos Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Orkwood</b>, called <b>Orkwood of Orkmont</b>, is the head of House Orkwood and is the Lord of Orkmont. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alyn Stackspear</b> is a knight from House Stackspear and the second son of Lord Selmond Stackspear. </p>
<p>The <b>westerlands</b> is a region in the west of the continent of Westeros. Before Aegon's Conquest, it was known as the Kingdom of the Rock. People from the westerlands are known as westermen. The customary surname of bastards of noble origin born in the westerlands is Hill. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Stokeworth</b> was Lord of Stokeworth and head of House Stokeworth. He served as Hand of the King during the late reign of Aegon I Targaryen and the early reign of Aenys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Tarbeck</b> was the Lord of Tarbeck Hall and the head of House Tarbeck during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Alyn Terrick</b> was a knight of House Terrick during the Faith Militant uprising. </p>
<p><b>Alyn Velaryon</b>, born <b>Alyn of Hull</b> and later called <b>Alyn Oakenfist</b>, was Lord of the Tides, Master of Driftmark and head of House Velaryon. Alyn was a legitimised bastard of dragonseed descent, coming from Hull on the island of Driftmark. His brother was Ser Addam Velaryon, a dragonrider. </p>
<p><b>Alynne Connington</b> is the younger sister of Ser Ronnet Connington, the Knight of Griffin's Roost. She resides in Griffin's Roost. </p>
<p><b>Alys Arryn</b> was a noblewoman of House Arryn, the only daughter of Lord Jasper Arryn. Alys had two brothers Lord Jon and Ser Ronnel Arryn. She was married to Ser Elys Waynwood. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Alys Arryn</b> was the wife of Prince Rhaegel Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Alys Beesbury</b> is a member of House Beesbury. She is married to Ser Leo Tyrell. They have five children: Alla, Leona, Lyonel, Lucas and Lorent Tyrell. According to semi-canon sources, she is the sister of Jeyne and Beony Beesbury. Her relation to Lord Warryn Beesbury, the head of the House, is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Alys Frey</b> was a descendant of a minor branch of House Frey. She was married to her cousin Ser Jared Frey, the fourth son of Lord Walder Frey, with whom she had two children; Tytos and Kyra. She is deceased. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Alys Harroway</b> was a lady of House Harroway and was the daughter of Lord Lucas Harroway of Harrenhal. She eventually married Prince Maegor Targaryen, becoming his second (of many) wives. </p>
<p><b>Alys Karstark</b> is a noblewoman of House Karstark and is the only daughter of Rickard Karstark, Lord of Karhold. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Megan Parkinson. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Alys Karstark</b> was a member of House Karstark, she married Lord Brandon Stark, youngest son Lord Cregan Stark, together they had three children: Rodwell, Beron and Arsa Stark. </p>
<p><b>Alys Oakheart</b> was a member of House Oakheart during the reign of King Aegon I Targaryen </p>
<p><b>Alys Reyne</b> was a member of House Reyne mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Alys Rivers</b> was a bastard servant of House Strong and a bedmate of Prince Aemond Targaryen. She allegedly saw visions in fires, similar to an ability exhibited by some red priests of R'hllor. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Alys Stackspear</b> was a member of House Stackspear, and the first wife of Jason Lannister. She was the mother of Damon Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Alys Stark</b> was a member of House Stark. She was the second daughter of Lord Cregan Stark and Lady Alysanne Blackwood. </p>
<p><b>Alys Stone</b> is the eldest bastard daughter of Ser Harrold Hardyng. Her mother is Cissy, a lowborn woman in the service of House Waynwood. Alys is two years old. </p>
<p><b>Alys Turnberry</b>, called <b>Sweetberry</b>, was a lady companion to Princess Saera Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Alysane Mormont</b>, known as <b>Aly</b> and the <b>She-Bear</b>, is a member of House Mormont. She is the second daughter of Maege Mormont, Lady of Bear Island. </p>
<p><b>Alysanne</b> was the eldest child of Prince Aegon Targaryen and his mistress, Megette. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Alysanne Blackwood</b>, also known as <b>Black Aly</b>, was a member of House Blackwood. She was the aunt of Lord Benjicot Blackwood of Raventree Hall, and the second wife of Lord Cregan Stark of Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Alysanne Bracken</b> is a member of House Bracken, the fifth daughter of Lord Jonos Bracken of Stone Hedge, and the third by his third wife. </p>
<p><b>Alysanne Bulwer</b> is Lady of Blackcrown and head of House Bulwer. She may have a brother. </p>
<p><b>Alysanne Farman</b> was a noblewoman of House Farman and the first wife of Gerold Lannister. They had no issue. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Alysanne Hightower</b> is a daughter of Lord Leyton Hightower. She is married to Lord Arthur Ambrose. Together, they have a son, Alyn Ambrose. </p>
<p><b>Alysanne Lefford</b> is the Lady of the Golden Tooth and head of House Lefford. </p>
<p><b>Alysanne Osgrey</b> was the only daughter of Ser Eustace Osgrey. She died of the Great Spring Sickness. </p>
<p><b>Alysanne Stark</b> was a member of House Stark, the fifth child and second daughter of Beron Stark, Lord of Winterfell, and his wife Lady Lorra Royce. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Alysanne Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Good Queen Alysanne</b>, was the queen consort of her brother, King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. Alysanne was a dragonrider, whose mount was Silverwing. </p>
<p><b>Alysanne Tarth</b> was a daughter of Lord Selwyn Tarth of Evenfall. She died while still in the cradle. </p>
<p><b>Alyse Ladybright</b> is a member of House Ladybright and the lord treasurer at Sunspear. </p>
<p><b>Alyssa Arryn</b> is a half-legendary figure of House Arryn. She gives her name to Alyssa's Tears in the Vale. </p>
<p><b>Alyssa Blackwood</b> was a noblewoman from House Blackwood who married Lord Walder Frey of the Twins and became his fourth wife. </p>
<p><b>Alyssa Royce</b> was a possible marriage candidate for King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Alyssa Targaryen</b> was the fifth born child of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Queen Alysanne Targaryen. Alyssa was a dragonrider whose dragon was Meleys, the Red Queen. </p>
<p><b>Alyssa Velaryon</b> was a member of House Velaryon during the first century after Aegon's Conquest. She was married to King Aenys I Targaryen, and gave birth to his six children. Some years after Aenys's death Alyssa served as Queen Regent to her youngest son, King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. She remarried to Lord Rogar Baratheon, and gave birth to two more children during the marriage. </p>
<p><b>Alyx Frey</b> is the only daughter of Symond Frey, the seventh son of Lord Walder Frey, and Betharios of Braavos. </p>
<p>Goodwife <b>Amabel</b> is a servant in Lady Shella Whent's household at Harrenhal. </p>
<p><b>Amanda Arryn</b> was a member of House Arryn during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Amarei Crakehall</b> was a noblewoman of House Crakehall. She was the third wife of Lord Walder Frey and had seven children with him. </p>
<p><b>Amarylis Manderly</b> was an ancestor of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Amarys</b> was a septa who was a religious tutor of Baela Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Amaury Peake</b> was a knight from House Peake and a member of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. He was a nephew of Lord Unwin Peake of Starpike. </p>
<p><b>Ambrode</b> is a shipwright in the Iron Islands. </p>
<p><b>Ambrose Butterwell</b> was Lord of Whitewalls and head of House Butterwell during the reigns of kings Aegon IV, Daeron II, and Aerys I Targaryen. He served as master of coin for Aegon IV and later as Hand of the King for Daeron II. </p>
<p><b>Amerei Frey</b>, called <b>Ami</b>, is a member of House Frey and the eldest daughter of Merrett Frey and Mariya Darry. Her promiscuity has earned her the nickname <b>Gatehouse Ami</b>. </p>
<p>The <b>Amethyst Empress</b> was the legendary eighth ruler of the mythic Great Empire of the Dawn and one of its last monarchs. She succeeded her father, the Opal Emperor but was cast down and slain by her envious younger brother, who crowned himself the Bloodstone Emperor. According to the annals of the Further East, it was the Blood Betrayal, as his usurpation was named, that ushered in the Long Night. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Amory Lorch</b> is a knight of House Lorch and bannerman of House Lannister. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Fintan McKeown. </p>
<p><b>House Lannister of Casterly Rock</b> is one of the Great Houses of Seven Kingdoms, and the principal house of the westerlands. Their seat is Casterly Rock, though another branch exists in nearby Lannisport. Their sigil is a golden lion on a field of crimson. Their official motto is "Hear Me Roar!" However, their unofficial motto, equally well known, is "A Lannister always pays his debts." The Warden of the West is a Lannister by tradition. Their gold mines have made the Lannisters the wealthiest of the Great Houses. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Amos Bracken</b> was a knight from House Bracken. His father was Lord Humfrey Bracken of Stone Hedge and his bastard half-brother was Ser Raylon Rivers. </p>
<p><b>Anara</b> is a prostitute living in Braavos, working in the same brothel as Lhara and Brea. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is played by Ollie Kram. </p>
<p><b>Andahar</b> was a presumed river king in the vicinity of Lord Harroway's Town in the riverlands. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Andar Royce</b> is a knight from House Royce and is the eldest son and heir of Yohn Royce, Lord of Runestone. </p>
<p><b>Andar Royce</b> was the father of Yohn Royce, mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Anders Yronwood</b> is the Lord of Yronwood and head of House Yronwood. He also holds the titles the Bloodroyal and Warden of the Stone Way. He has a son, Cletus and two daughters, Ynys, and Gwyneth. Prince Quentyn Martell had previously been his ward. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Andrew Estermont</b> is a knight from House Estermont. </p>
<p><b>Andrew Tollett </b> is a knight from House Tollett. His relation to the head of the House, Lord Uthor Tollett, is unknown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Andrey Charlton</b> is a knight of House Charlton. His squire is young Lucas Roote. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Andrey Dalt</b>, sometimes called <b>Drey</b>, is the brother and heir of Ser Deziel Dalt, the Knight of Lemonwood. </p>
<p><b>Andrik the Unsmiling</b> is an ironborn warrior serving Lord Dunstan Drumm and Balon Greyjoy. </p>
<p><b>Andros Brax</b> is the Lord of Hornvale and head of House Brax. He has three knighted sons: Tytos, Robert, and Flement. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Androw Ashford</b> was a knight from House Ashford, the eldest son and heir of Lord Ashford during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>tourney at Ashford Meadow</b> or <b>tourney at Ashford</b> was a tourney hosted by House Ashford at Ashford Meadow in 209&nbsp;AC. Due to the accidental death of Prince Baelor Targaryen—the Prince of Dragonstone, son and heir of King Daeron II Targaryen, and Hand of the King—Ashford was one of the most famous and historically significant tourneys. </p>
<p><b>Androw Farman</b> was a member of House Farman. He was the second son of Lord Marq Farman of Fair Isle. </p>
<p><b>Androw Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, a son of Ser Arwood Frey and Ryella Royce. He has a twin brother, Alyn, and two sisters, Ryella and Hostella Frey. </p>
<p><b>Anguy</b>, called the <b>Anguy the Archer</b> or simply <b>Archer</b>, is a commoner from the Dornish Marches who is skilled with the bow. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Philip McGinley. </p>
<p>The <b>brotherhood without banners</b>, also known as the <b>knights of the hollow hill</b> and the <b>forgotten fellowship</b>, is an outlaw group who initially fights Lannister rule in the name of King Robert I Baratheon. Led by the Lightning Lord, Beric Dondarrion, the group is founded in the riverlands by soldiers and nobles who were sent by the then-Hand of the King, Eddard Stark, to bring Gregor Clegane to justice. After they are ambushed while crossing a ford and nearly defeated, the group continues the fight as a guerrilla group. Their numbers increase as they are joined by defeated soldiers from other battles, deserters, and refugees from the War of the Five Kings. Every man of the brotherhood receives a knighthood from Beric. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Annara Farring</b> was a noblewoman of House Farring and the seventh wife of Lord Walder Frey. They had six children. She is deceased. </p>
<p><b>Walder Frey</b> is the Lord of the Crossing and head of House Frey. Though almost ninety years old and infirm, he still maintains an active hand in the running of his house at the Twins. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by David Bradley. </p>
<p><b>Anselm</b> was a maester of the Citadel who served House Targaryen at Dragonstone during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Anson</b> is a maester from the Citadel of Oldtown. He has written <i>Truth</i>, in which he expresses the belief that the idea that dragons can change sex at need is erroneous. According to Anson, this is a misunderstanding of the metaphor which was used by Septon Barth, when discussing the higher mysteries. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Antario Jast</b> is head of House Jast in the westerlands. He is married to Lady Lanna Lannister. They have sons together. </p>
<p><b>Anya Waynwood</b> is Lady of Ironoaks and head of House Waynwood. She is widowed and has three sons: Morton, Donnel and Wallace, and an unspecified number of daughters, granddaughters, and grandsons. Her wards include the young Harrold Hardyng, her cousin and the heir-presumptive of the Vale of Arryn, and Cynthea Frey, whose mother was Carolei Waynwood. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Anya is portrayed by Paola Dionisotti. </p>
<p><b>Anya Weatherwax</b> was a member of House Weatherwax during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Archibald Yronwood</b>, called <b>Arch</b> and <b>the big man</b>, is a knight from House Yronwood and a nephew to Anders Yronwood, Lord of Yronwood. </p>
<p><b>Archie</b> was a soldier in service to House Lannister. He has only been mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>This <b>Archon of Tyrosh</b>, was the ruler of Tyrosh in the time preceding the War of the Ninepenny Kings. </p>
<p>The <b>Archon's daughter</b> was the daughter of the Archon of Tyrosh during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. She was the wife of Ser Orryn Baratheon. Her given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Ardrian Celtigar</b>, known as <b>the Red Crab</b>, is the Lord of Claw Isle and head of House Celtigar. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Aregelle Stark</b> was a noblewoman from House Stark during the latter half of the second century after Aegon's Conquest. She was the younger daughter of Edric Stark and Serena Stark. </p>
<p><b>Areo Hotah</b> is the captain of the household guard at Sunspear for the Prince of Dorne, Doran Martell. He is originally from the Free City of Norvos, where he was trained by the bearded priests. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by DeObia Oparei. </p>
<p><b>House Nymeros Martell of Sunspear</b>, usually simply called <b>House Martell</b>, is one of the Great Houses of the Seven Kingdoms and the ruling house of Dorne. "Nymeros" indicates "of the line of Nymeria," referring to the union of the Martells with the Rhoynish warrior queen Nymeria around 700 BC. The Prince of Dorne rules from Sunspear in southeastern Dorne. </p>
<p><b>Argella Baratheon</b> was a member of House Baratheon, mentioned in <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Argella Durrandon</b> was the daughter and only child of Argilac the Arrogant, the last Storm King. After her father was killed in Aegon's Conquest, she married Orys Baratheon, the first Lord of Storm's End, founding the new House Baratheon. </p>
<p><b>Argilac Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Argilac the Arrogant</b>, was the last Storm King from House Durrandon who reigned in the stormlands before the Conquest by Aegon I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Argos Sevenstar</b> was an Andal warlord. </p>
<p><b>Argoth Stone-Skin</b>, called the <b>Grey Giant</b>, is a character in the legend of Maris the Maid. Among fifty lords, he won Maris's hand in the first tourney held in Westeros. Maris wed King Uthor of the High Tower before Argoth could claim her, however, and Argoth spent the rest his life roaring for Maris outside the walls of Oldtown. It is unconfirmed if Argoth was a man or a giant. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Argrave the Defiant</b> was a knight from Nunny in service to Lord Ambrose Butterwell during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Arianne Nymeros Martell</b>, better known simply as <b>Arianne Martell</b>, is a member of House Martell and is the eldest daughter of Doran Martell, the ruling Prince of Dorne, and his consort, Lady Mellario of the Free City of Norvos. According to Dornish customs, she is the heiress of Sunspear, and the future ruling Princess of Dorne. Arianne is a POV character in <i>A Feast for Crows</i> and <i>The Winds of Winter</i>. </p>
<p><b>Sunspear</b>, also known as the Old Palace, is the seat of House Nymeros Martell and the capital of Dorne. The castle is located on the Broken Arm, north of the Greenblood on the far southeastern coast of Westeros and is surrounded on three sides by the sea, and by the shadow city on the fourth side. The palace of the Water Gardens lies three leagues away on the coastal road. </p>
<p><b>Arianne Tarth</b> was a daughter of Lord Selwyn Tarth of Evenfall. She died while still in the cradle. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Arlan of Pennytree</b> was a hedge knight and the master of Dunk, the later Ser Duncan the Tall. </p>
<p><b>Arlan I Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Arlan the Avenger</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon who ruled during the Age of the Hundred Kingdoms. </p>
<p><b>Arlan III Durrandon</b> was the Storm King from House Durrandon who conquered the riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Arlan V Durrandon</b> was a Storm King of the stormlands from House Durrandon during the Century of Blood. </p>
<p><b>Armeca</b> is a prostitute working in the brothel owned by Petyr "Littlefinger" Baelish in King's Landing. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is played by Sahara Knite. </p>
<p><b>Armen</b>, better known as <b>Armen the Acolyte</b>, is an acolyte at the Citadel. </p>
<p><b>Armen Peake</b> was the Lord of Starpike, Dunstonbury, and Whitegrove, and the head of House Peake during Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Armistead Vance</b> was a member of House Vance and the mightiest of the Andal warlords that invaded the riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Armond Caswell</b> was the Lord of Bitterbridge and the head of House Caswell during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. He had at least one son, Lord Joffrey Caswell. </p>
<p><b>Armond Connington</b> was the Lord of Griffin's Roost and the head of House Connington during the reign of King Aerys II Targaryen. He was the father of Jon Connington. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Arnel</b> was the author of <i>Mountain and Vale</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Arneld</b> is a knight in service at King's Landing. He may be a member of the Gold Cloaks. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Arnell</b> is a knight and a brother of the Night's Watch. His mother was a green-apple Fossoway, but it is unknown if he is a legitimate son or a bastard. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Arnold Arryn</b>, called <b>the Mad Heir</b>, was a knight from House Arryn and a claimant to the Eyrie. </p>
<p><b>Arnolf Karstark</b> is a member of House Karstark and the uncle of Lord Rickard Karstark. He is the castellan of Karhold, but the followers of Stannis Baratheon refer to him as <b>Lord Arnolf</b> as a courtesy. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Aron Santagar</b> is a knight from House Santagar and the master-at-arms at the Red Keep. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Arra Norrey</b> was a member of House Norrey and the first wife of Lord Cregan Stark of Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Arrec Durrandon</b> was a Storm King of the stormlands from House Durrandon who lost the wealthy riverlands to the Iron Islands. He was also the grandsire of the last Storm King, Argilac Durrandon. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Arrana Stark</b> was a noblewoman from House Stark during the latter half of the second century after Aegon's Conquest. She was the older daughter of Edric Stark and Serena Stark. </p>
<p><b>Arron</b> is a Night's Watch recruit. He is the twin brother of Emrick, and is from Fair Isle. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Arron Qorgyle</b> is the second son of Lord Quentyn Qorgyle. </p>
<p><b>Arryk</b> is a guardsman for Olenna Tyrell, the dowager Lady of Highgarden. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Arryk Cargyll</b> was a knight from House Cargyll. He and his twin brother, Ser Erryk Cargyll, were members of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Viserys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Mutual exhaustion and negotiated peace: </p>
<p><b>Lord Arryn</b> was the Lord of the Eyrie and the head of House Arryn during the late reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Arsa Stark</b> was a member of House Stark during the latter half of the second century after Aegon's Conquest. She was the only daughter of Lord Brandon Stark and his wife, Lady Alys Karstark. Arsa had two full older brothers, Rodwell and Beron and an older bastard brother as well, Lonnel Snow. </p>
<p><b>Arson Iceaxe</b> was a wildling raider. </p>
<p><b>Arstan Selmy</b> is the Lord of Harvest Hall and the head of House Selmy. </p>
<p><b>Arthor Celtigar</b> was a member of House Celtigar during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Arthor Karstark</b> is a member of House Karstark and the second son of Arnolf Karstark. </p>
<p><b>Arthor Oakheart</b> was a knight of House Oakheart during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Arthur Ambrose</b> is head of House Ambrose. He is married to Alysanne Hightower and has a son named Alyn. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Arthur Dayne</b>, known as the <b>Sword of the Morning</b>, was a famed and legendary knight from House Dayne and a member of Aerys II Targaryen's Kingsguard. Many considered him to have been the most chivalrous warrior of the Seven Kingdoms. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Luke Roberts during a flashback in Season 6. </p>
<p><b>Arthur Goodbrother</b> was a member of House Goodbrother. </p>
<p><b>Artos Flint</b> is the second son of Lord Torghen Flint, known as The Flint, or Old Flint clan chief of the first Flints, a mountain clan in the North. He is the half-brother of Black Donnel Flint. </p>
<p><b>Artos Stark</b>, also known as <b>Artos the Implacable</b>, was a member of House Stark during the reign of King Maekar I Targaryen. He was the third son of Lord Beron Stark and Lady Lorra Royce. </p>
<p><b>Artos the Strong</b> is one of the many legendary heroes of the Riverlands, whose tales date back to the Age of Heroes. </p>
<p><b>Artys I Arryn</b> was the first King of Mountain and Vale and the founder of House Arryn in Westeros. Prior to his coronation, Ser Artys, called the <b>Falcon Knight</b>, was an Andal knight who defeated the First Men of the Vale in the Battle of the Seven Stars. He is sometimes combined in tales with the Winged Knight, a legendary hero of the Vale from thousands of years before the Andal invasion. </p>
<p><b>Arwaya Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, appearing in <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Arwen Swann</b> was a member of House Swann and House Umber, appearing in <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Arwen Upcliff</b> was a lady of House Upcliff who married Alester II Arryn, King of Mountain and Vale. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Arwood Frey</b> is a knight of House Frey, the only son of Ser Hosteen Frey and Bellena Hawick. He is married to Ryella Royce and they have four children; Ryella, Androw, Alyn and Hostella Frey. </p>
<p><b>Arwyn Frey</b> is the (supposed) sixth daughter of Lord Walder Frey. She is the first born and eldest daughter of Lord Walder and his seventh spouse, Lady Annara Farring. However according to Merrett Frey, Black Walder Frey was rumored to be sleeping with Lady Annara casting doubts on the parentage of her children. </p>
<p><b>Arwyn Oakheart</b> is the head of House Oakheart and the Lady of Old Oak. Her husband is deceased and gave her several sons, including the youngest, Ser Arys, a member of the Kingsguard of King Robert I Baratheon since 290&nbsp;AC. </p>
<p><b>Arya Flint</b> was a noblewoman of House Flint of the mountains. She was married to Rodrik Stark, the fifth son of Lord Beron Stark, with whom she had two daughters; Branda and Lyarra Stark. </p>
<p><b>Arya Stark</b> is the third child and second daughter of Lord Eddard Stark and Lady Catelyn Tully. A member of House Stark, she has five siblings: brothers Robb, Bran, Rickon, half-brother Jon Snow, and older sister Sansa. Arya is one of the major POV character in <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Arya is portrayed by Maisie Williams. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Arys Oakheart</b> is a knight from House Oakheart and a member of the Kingsguard of Robert I Baratheon. Arys is the youngest son of Lady Arwyn Oakheart of Old Oak. He becomes a POV character in <i>A Feast for Crows.</i> </p>
<p>The <b>Kingsguard</b>, also known poetically as the <b>White Swords</b> or <b>white cloaks</b>, are the royal bodyguards of the Iron Throne. Regarded as the&nbsp;finest knights in the Seven Kingdoms, they are sworn to protect their king and the royal family with their own lives, to obey his commands, and to keep his secrets. The Kingsguard are sworn for life and are forbidden from owning land, taking a wife, or fathering children, although they can hold non-hereditary commands, such as being warden or Hand of the King. </p>
<p><b>Ash</b> is one of the children of the forest in service to the last greenseer. He/she does not speak the Common Tongue. His/her true name is too long for the human tongue according to Leaf, so Meera Reed and Bran Stark make up the name Ash. </p>
<p><b>Asha Greyjoy</b> is a member of House Greyjoy and is the daughter of Lord Balon Greyjoy by his wife, Alannys Harlaw. She becomes a POV character in <i>A Feast For Crows</i>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is named <b>Yara Greyjoy</b> to avoid confusion with the wildling Osha, and she is played by Gemma Whelan. </p>
<p><b>Ashara Dayne</b> was a noblewoman of House Dayne and a sister of Ser Arthur Dayne, the Sword of the Morning. She committed suicide shortly after the end of Robert's Rebellion. </p>
<p><b>Lord Ashford</b> was the Lord of Ashford and the head of House Ashford during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. Lord Ashford had two sons, Ser Androw and Ser Robert, and a daughter. </p>
<p><b>Assadora</b>, also known as <b>Assadora of Ibben</b>, is a prostitute at the Happy Port in Braavos. </p>
<p><b>Braavos</b> is the wealthiest and likely the most powerful of the Free Cities. It is located in a lagoon on the northwestern end of Essos, where the narrow sea and the Shivering Sea meet. Braavos is also known as <b>Braavos of the Hundred Isles</b> and the <b>Secret City</b>, a name also attributed to the city Nefer, the last remaining city of N'ghai. Braavos is sometimes referred to as the "bastard daughter of Valyria". </p>
<p>Ser <b>Aubrey Ambrose</b> was a knight from House Ambrose during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Aubrey Crakehall</b> was a knight from House Crakehall who briefly ruled as King of the Iron Islands. </p>
<p><b>Aurane Waters</b>, called the <b>Bastard of Driftmark</b>, is a bastard member of House Velaryon. He is the half-brother of Monford Velaryon, Lord of the Tides and Master of Driftmark. </p>
<p><b>Aurion</b> was one of the few dragonlords who survived the Doom of Valyria. According to histories of Qohor, he raised forces from Qohorik colonists and declared himself first Emperor of Valyria. Atop his dragon, he flew south to lay claim to what remained of Valyria and reestablish the Freehold along with his thirty thousand men. Neither Emperor Aurion nor his host were ever seen again </p>
<p><b>Axel Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Axel Tully</b> was a head of House Tully and the first Lord of Riverrun. His father was Ser Edmure Tully, a turncoat who supported the Andal warlord Armistead Vance after the death of Tristifer IV Mudd, King of the Rivers and the Hills. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Axell Florent</b> is a knight of House Florent who serves as the castellan of Dragonstone for his nephew-in-law, Lord Stannis Baratheon. He is the younger brother of Lord Alester Florent of Brightwater Keep. </p>
<p><b>Aya</b> is a young girl working at a brothel in Braavos. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is played by Aifric O'Donnell. </p>
<p><b>Ayrmidon</b> is the author of <i>Engines of War</i>, a Valyrian scroll hard to find in its entirety in Westeros. A complete version can be found in the Winterfell library. </p>
<p><b>Azor Ahai</b> was a legendary hero who wielded a burning sword called Lightbringer, according to tales from Asshai and followers of R'hllor. In some other cultures this warrior is called <b>Hyrkoon the Hero</b>, <b>Yin Tar</b>, <b>Neferion</b>, and <b>Eldric Shadowchaser</b>. </p>
<p><b>R'hllor</b>, also known as the <b>Lord of Light</b>, the <b>Heart of Fire</b>, the <b>God of Flame and Shadow</b>, is a prominent god in Essos, but has only a few followers in Westeros, where he is more commonly known as the <b>red god</b>. His symbol is a fiery heart. Red priests lead prayers to R'hllor at red temples. </p>
<p><b>Azzak</b> is a boy from the House of Ghazeen, one of the noble ruling families of Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Bael the Bard</b> was a King-Beyond-the-Wall. According to legend, he was one of the greatest free folk raiders of his time, a man who outwitted the northmen and impregnated the daughter of Lord Brandon Stark. He was also a singer who wrote songs about his own life, which are still sung to this day. </p>
<p>The <b>grandfather</b> of Petyr Baelish was a hedge knight of the Vale of Arryn. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p>The <b>father</b> of Petyr Baelish was "the smallest of small lords" in the Vale of Arryn. His first name is unknown. </p>
<p>The <b>great-grandfather</b> of Petyr Baelish was a Braavosi sellsword that came to the Vale of Arryn in the service of Lord Corbray. His line was continued by his son, who became a hedge knight and took the head of the Titan of Braavos as his sigil. According to semi-canon sources, the son also acquired a small bit of land and a keep on the smallest of the Fingers. His first name is unknown. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Baela Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Baela Velaryon</b>, was a daughter of Prince Daemon Targaryen and Lady Laena Velaryon. She had a younger twin sister, Rhaena Targaryen, and two younger half-brothers, Aegon and Viserys. She was a dragonrider who rode Moondancer. </p>
<p><b>Baelon Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen during the Century of Blood, the second son of Lord Aerys Targaryen of Dragonstone. He had one older brother, Aelyx and one younger brother Daemion Targaryen. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Baelon Targaryen</b> was the secondborn son of King Viserys I Targaryen and his wife, Queen Aemma Arryn. </p>
<p><b>Viserys I Targaryen</b> was the fifth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne, ruling from 103&nbsp;AC to 129&nbsp;AC. He succeeded his grandfather, the Old King Jaehaerys I. Viserys continued the prosperous peace and legacy of his grandsire, but the seeds for the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons that would much later engulf the realm were inadvertently sown in his reign. </p>
<p><b>Aemma Arryn</b> was the queen consort and first wife of King Viserys I Targaryen, and a granddaughter of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and his sister-wife, Queen Alysanne Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Baelor Blacktyde</b> is the Lord of Blacktyde and the head of House Blacktyde. Baelor captains the <i>Nightflyer</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Baelor Hightower</b>, also known as <b>Baelor Brightsmile</b>, is a knight from House Hightower. He is the eldest son and heir of Lord Leyton Hightower of Oldtown. Baelor is wed to Rhonda Rowan. </p>
<p><b>Baelor I Targaryen</b>, known as <b>Baelor the Beloved</b> and <b>Baelor the Blessed</b>, was the ninth Targaryen king to reign on the Iron Throne as Lord of the Seven Kingdoms. Known for his piety, Baelor was a septon as well as a king. He was the second son of King Aegon III Targaryen and Queen Daenaera Velaryon, and ruled after the death of his older brother, King Daeron I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Baelor Targaryen</b>, known as <b>Baelor Breakspear</b>, was a member of House Targaryen and a Prince of Dragonstone. He was the eldest son and heir of King Daeron II Targaryen and Myriah Martell. Named after his grandfather's cousin, King Baelor I, Prince Baelor served as his father's Hand of the King from 196&nbsp;AC until his death in 209&nbsp;AC. </p>
<p><b>Black Balaq</b> is a sellsword in service to the Golden Company, in command of the company's archers. </p>
<p><b>Balder</b> was a maester of the Citadel in service to the Night's Watch at Eastwatch-by-the-Sea near 400 BC. He wrote the book <i>The Edge of the World</i> when Osric Stark served as Lord Commander. </p>
<p><b>Baldric I Durrandon</b>, known as <b>Baldric the Cunning</b>, was a Storm King of the stormlands from House Durrandon. </p>
<p><b>Baldrick</b> was a septon of the Faith of the Seven during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Balerion Otherys</b> was the youngest of the three bastard children of King Aegon IV Targaryen and his fourth mistress, Bellegere Otherys. </p>
<p><b>Ballabar</b> is the maester assigned to House Redwyne in the Arbor. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Balman Byrch</b> is a knight from House Byrch and the husband of Lady Falyse Stokeworth, the heir to Stokeworth. </p>
<p><b>Balon Blackskin</b> is a legendary ironborn raider who supposedly lived during the Age of Heroes. </p>
<p><b>Balon Botley</b> is the eldest son of Lord Germund Botley. </p>
<p><b>Balon Greyjoy</b> is the Lord of the Iron Islands and the head of House Greyjoy of Pyke. The captain of the <i>Great Kraken</i>, he is a follower of the Old Way of the ironborn and desires to bring them back to prominence. In 289&nbsp;AC he proclaimed their independence from the Iron Throne, but Greyjoy's Rebellion was defeated by King Robert I Baratheon's forces. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Balon is played by Patrick Malahide. </p>
<p><b>Balon V Greyjoy</b>, known as <b>Coldwind</b>, was a High King of the Iron Islands from House Greyjoy. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Balon Swann</b> is a knight from House Swann and the second son of Lord Gulian Swann of Stonehelm. </p>
<p><b>Balon Tawney</b> is the Lord and head of House Tawney on Orkmont in the Iron Islands. </p>
<p><b>Bambarro Bazanne</b> was a Lysene magister who had custody of Prince Viserys Targaryen during the time he was presumed dead by those in Westeros. </p>
<p><b>Bandy</b> is the twin sister of Shyra and daughter of Joseth, the master of the horse at Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Bannen</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch at Castle Black. He is from the lands of House Manderly near White Harbor. He is a good tracker. </p>
<p><b>Barba Bolton</b> was a member of House Bolton during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Barba Bracken</b> was a member of House Bracken during the reigns of kings Baelor I, Viserys II, and Aegon IV Targaryen. She was the fifth of Aegon the Unworthy's mistresses. </p>
<p><b>Barbara Bracken</b> is a member of House Bracken, the first daughter of Lord Jonos Bracken of Stone Hedge by his first wife. </p>
<p><b>Barbrey Dustin</b>, née <b>Ryswell</b>, is the Lady of Barrowton as the widow of Willam Dustin, Lord of Barrowton. She was born into House Ryswell as the younger daughter of Rodrik Ryswell, Lord of the Rills. </p>
<p><b>Barneby</b> is a maester of the Citadel of Oldtown who researched the First Men. His translations of runes support the claim of House Blackwood that they had once ruled most of the wolfswood before being driven from the north by the Kings of Winter. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Barquen Peake</b>, known as <b>Barquen the Besieger</b>, was a knight and an illustrious and legendary ancestor of House Peake. </p>
<p><b>Barra</b> is a bastard daughter of King Robert I Baratheon. She is being raised in Chataya's brothel in King's Landing. Her mother is unnamed in <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>, but is called Mhaegen in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Barre</b> is a septon on Dragonstone. </p>
<p><b>Barris Hightower</b> was a head of House Hightower and Lord of the Hightower. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Barristan Selmy</b>, also called <b>Barristan the Bold</b>, is a knight from House Selmy and the Lord Commander of the Kingsguard of Robert I Baratheon. A celebrated hero, he has served in the Kingsguard since a time when these knights were still considered to be the greatest of the Seven Kingdoms. Barristan becomes a POV character in <i>A Dance with Dragons</i>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Ian McElhinney. </p>
<p>King <b>Barron Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Barron the Beautiful</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon and the successor of Durran XI Durrandon. He is remembered for having yielded up territories his grandfather had conquered and more. </p>
<p><b>Barsena Blackhair</b> is a pit fighter famed in Meereen. Her origin is unknown, but she supports the pit fighting culture of the city. </p>
<p><b>Barth</b> was a septon who served as Hand of the King for King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Barth</b> is the brewer at Winterfell. His wife took Theon Greyjoy's virginity. </p>
<p><b>Barthogan Stark</b>, also called <b>Barth Blacksword</b>, was Lord of Winterfell and the head of House Stark during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. He was the fourth born son of Lord Cregan Stark, the third by his last wife Lady Lynara Stark. </p>
<p><b>Bartimos Celtigar</b> was the Lord of Claw Isle and the head of House Celtigar during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b> Bartimus</b> is an old knight, the chief gaoler and castellan of the Wolf's Den. </p>
<p><b>Bass</b> is a member of the Night's Watch at Castle Black, where he acts as kennelmaster. </p>
<p>The <b>Bastard of Blackhaven</b> was a bastard of House Dondarrion during the reign of the Storm King Argilac Durrandon. His given name has not been published, although "Storm" is the surname for bastards of noble origin in the stormlands. </p>
<p>The <b>Bastard of Harrenhal</b> was a bastard of House Lothston during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>The bastard's bastard</b> is how Victarion Greyjoy refers to a thrall and oarsman in the Iron Fleet. He's the bastard son of a bastard. </p>
<p>Empress <b>Bathi Ma Lo</b> was the wife of God-Emperor Lo Doq, called Lo Lackwit, ruler of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti. Some suggest she was the true ruler behind her simpleton husband, who despite his affliction ruled wisely for more than thirty years. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Bayard Norcross</b> is a knight of House Norcross. </p>
<p><b>Bean</b> was a crossbowman during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Beans</b> is a sellsword and member of the Windblown. His true name is <b>Baqq</b> which means <i>Beans</i>. </p>
<p>A <b>bearded woman</b> is a slave owned by Yezzan zo Qaggaz. She is a part of Yezzan's grotesquerie, one of his <i>special treasures</i>. </p>
<p><b>The Beastmaster</b> is a name the Windblown, a sellsword company hired by Yunkai, mockingly gave to a Yunkish nobleman commanding some of the Yunkai slave solders. </p>
<p><b>Beatrice Butterwell</b> was a member of House Butterwell in the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Bearded Ben</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Beardless Dick</b> is a man of the riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Becca</b> is a former lover of King Robert I Baratheon. </p>
<p><b>Becca</b>, better known as <b>Becca the Baker</b>, is an inhabitant of the Riverlands. </p>
<p>Goodman <b>Beck</b> was an inhabitant of Donnelwood. He was slain by the forces of House Lannister during the War of the Five Kings. </p>
<p><b>Bedwyck</b>, nicknamed <b>Giant</b> due to his short height, is an experienced ranger of the Night's Watch. He is well-respected by younger members. </p>
<p><b>Belandra</b> is a servant of House Martell at Sunspear. </p>
<p><b>Belaquo Bonebreaker</b> is a pit fighter famed in Meereen. His origin is unknown, but he supports the pit fighting culture of the city. Belaquo wields a flail. </p>
<p><b>Beldecar</b> is the author of the <i>History of the Rhoynish Wars</i>. A copy can be found in the Red Keep's library. Beldecar's book is considered to be without equal in describing the Rhoynish Wars. </p>
<p><b>Beldon</b> was a maester of the Citadel who served at Casterly Rock for Lord Gerold Lannister and later Lord Tytos Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Lord Belgrave</b> was head of House Belgrave during the reign of Baelor I Targaryen. His given name has not been published. </p>
<p><b>Belicho</b> was one of the ruling triarchs of the Free City of Volantis. </p>
<p><b>Belicho Paenymion</b> is a prominent noble of Volantis. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is played by Eddie Jackson. </p>
<p><b>Belicho Staegone</b> is a candidate to become a triarch of Volantis. He appears to have been named after a legendary triarch, Belicho. </p>
<p>Wisdom <b>Belis</b> was a member of the Alchemists' Guild of King's Landing during the reign of King Aerys II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Bella</b> is a young prostitute at the Peach in Stoney Sept. She is a bastard daughter of King Robert I Baratheon. </p>

<p><b>Harrenhal</b>, the largest castle in the Seven Kingdoms, is the seat of House Whent in the riverlands, on the north shore of the Gods Eye. Since the burning of Harrenhal by dragonfire in Aegon's Conquest, however, the castle has become a dark and ruinous place. </p>

<p>The <b>Dreadfort</b> is a fortress in the north and the seat of House Bolton in northeastern Westeros. Located on the banks of the upper Weeping Water, it is southeast of the Lonely Hills and north of the Sheepshead Hills. <p><b>Strongsong</b> is the seat of House Belmore in the Vale of Arryn. <p><b>Casterly Rock</b>, nicknamed <b>the Rock</b>, is a castle and the seat of House Lannister. The capital of the westerlands, it is on the ocean road and overlooks the harbor of Lannisport and the Sunset Sea. Nearby strongholds include Kayce and Feastfires to the west, Sarsfield to the north, and Cornfield and Clegane's Keep to the south. </p>

<p>The <b>Night's Watch</b> is a military order dedicated to holding the Wall, the immense fortification on the northern border of the Seven Kingdoms, defending the realms of men from what lies beyond the Wall. The order's foundation dates back to the Age of Heroes, at the time when the Others were pushed back. The men of Night's Watch wear only black, and they are known as <b>black brothers</b>. Recruits who join the Watch are said to <b>take the black</b>. </p>
<p><b>Castle Black</b> is the main stronghold of the Night's Watch and the seat of their Lord Commander. The castle is situated along the Wall between Queensgate to the west and Oakenshield to the east, near the center of the Wall, at the northern end of the kingsroad. The village of Mole's Town is located half a league to the south along the kingsroad. </p>

Scholars believe an ancient king's actions have been exaggerated into legend, or the reigns of multiple kings have been remembered as one through the passage of time. </p>

<p><b>Brandon Stark</b>, also called <b>Brandon the Daughterless</b>, was supposedly the Lord of Winterfell and head of House Stark when the legendary Bael the Bard was just a common wildling raider. </p>
<p><b>Brandon Stark</b>, called <b>Brandon the Boastful</b>, was the Lord of Winterfell and the head of House Stark during the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Brandon Stark</b> was a member of House Stark. The second son of Bennard Stark and Lady Margaret Karstark. </p>
<p><b>Brandon Stark</b> was the Lord of Winterfell and head of House Stark during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. He was the youngest son of Lord Cregan Stark and Lady Lynara Stark. </p>
<p><b>Brandon Stark</b> was a member of House Stark, the only son of Lord Willam Stark and his first wife, Lady Lyanne Glover. </p>
<p><b>Brandon Stark</b> was a member of House Stark. He was the eldest of Artos Stark and Lysara Karstark's twin sons. His younger brother was Benjen. Brandon had children. </p>
<p><b>Brandon Stark</b> was the oldest son of Lord Rickard Stark and Lady Lyarra Stark and the heir to Winterfell prior to Robert's Rebellion. His younger siblings were Eddard, Lyanna, and Benjen. </p>
<p><b>Brandon Stark</b>, typically called <b>Bran</b>, is the second son of Lord Eddard Stark and Lady Catelyn Tully. He is one of the major POV characters in the books. He has four older siblings—Robb, Jon, Sansa, Arya—and one younger—Rickon. Like his siblings, he is constantly accompanied by his direwolf, Summer, with whom he shares a strong warg connection. He is seven years old at the beginning of <i>A Game of Thrones</i>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Isaac Hempstead-Wright. </p>
<p><b>Brandon Tallhart</b> is a member of House Tallhart. He is the eldest son of Leobald Tallhart and Berena Hornwood. </p>
<p><b>Brandon Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Branston Cuy</b> is the Lord of Sunflower Hall and head of House Cuy in the Reach. </p>
<p>A <b>brass-seller</b> is a merchant who sells brass in the port of Qarth. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Braxton Beesbury</b>, known as <b>Stinger</b>, was a knight from House Beesbury and the heir to Honeyholt during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Brea</b> is the oldest daughter of Brusco, a fishmonger. She has one younger sister, Talea, and a couple of brothers. </p>
<p><b>Brella</b> is a servant in King's Landing. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Brendel Byrne</b> is a sellsword and knight in service to the Golden Company. As a serjeant, he is a high-ranking officer. </p>
<p><b>Brenett</b> is a maester who serves House Frey at the Twins. </p>
