<p><b>Briar</b> was a female wildling skinchanger who could inhabit the body of a shadowcat. </p>
<p><b>Brienne Tarth</b>, commonly called <b>Brienne of Tarth</b> after her island home, is the only living child and heir of Lord Selwyn Tarth of Evenfall. Brienne is sometimes called <b>the Maid of Tarth</b> and mocked as <b>Brienne the Beauty</b>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Gwendoline Christie. </p>
<p><b>Briony</b> is a common woman. She is the mother of Joy Hill, the bastard daughter of Gerion Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Brogg</b> is a free Folk leader. </p>
<p>The <b>free folk</b> are a race of people who live beyond the Wall in northern Westeros. They are more commonly referred to as <b>"wildlings"</b> everywhere south of the Wall. </p>
<p><b>Bronn</b> is a low-born sellsword of great skill and cunning. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Jerome Flynn. </p>
<p><b>Brozho</b> is a Dothraki <i>khal</i> appearing in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Brude</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel. </p>
<p><b>Brune Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Bruni</b> was the husband of Osha mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Brus Buckler</b> is a knight from House Buckler. He is the cousin of Ralph Buckler, Lord of Bronzegate. </p>
<p><b>Brusco</b> is a fishmonger from Braavos. He has two daughters, Brea and Talea, and at least two sons. </p>
<p><b>Big Brusco</b> is a mummer from Braavos. He is part of the group of mummers led by Izembaro at The Gate. </p>
<p><b>The brute</b> is how Victarion Greyjoy refers to a thrall and oarsman in the Iron Fleet. He has been rowing for twenty years. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Bryan Fossoway</b> is a knight from House Fossoway of Cider Hall. </p>
<p><b>House Fossoway of Cider Hall</b> is a noble house from the Reach, one of the principal bannermen sworn to House Tyrell. Cider Hall is located at the fork of the Mander and the Cockleswent. Their banner is a red apple over a golden field. Their words are "<i>A Taste of Glory</i>". </p>
<p><b>Bryan of Oldtown</b> was a merchant-adventurer who once journeyed through the Shivering Sea. Hailing from Oldtown in the Reach, he was captain of the cog <i>Spearshaker</i>. He reported that the Dothraki language name for the lost race that inhabited the Kingdom of the Ifequevron means "those who walk in the woods". He also reported that the Ibbenese he met claimed these woods walkers bless households that leave offerings of leaf, stone, and water. </p>
<p><b>Bryce Caron</b> is the Lord of Nightsong and the head of House Caron. </p>
<p>The <b>Rainbow Guard</b>, also called the <b>rainbow knights</b>, is an organization created by Renly Baratheon to serve as his equivalent of the Kingsguard. Its members wear rainbow-striped silk cloaks, although they use their own sigils on their shields and garb. The rainbow connects the organization to the Faith of the Seven, for which the rainbow is a religious symbol. Each member of the Rainbow Guard wears armor of a single different color, with the group of seven together representing the seven-colored rainbow. Unlike the Kingsguard, the Rainbow Guard appears to have no restriction on its members holding hereditary lands, with one lord being a member of the Rainbow Guard. </p>
<p><b>Bryen</b> is the captain of the guards for House Baelish at their tower. </p>
<p><b>Bryen Caron</b> was Lord of Nightsong and head of House Caron. </p>
<p><b>Bryen Farring</b> is a member of House Farring, and a squire of Stannis Baratheon. He is the son of Ser Gilbert Farring. </p>
<p><b>Bryndemere Tarth</b> was the Evenstar and the Lord of Tarth, and the head of House Tarth during King Aegon III Targaryen's regency. </p>
<p><b>Brynden Blackwood</b> is the eldest son and heir of Lord Tytos Blackwood of Raventree Hall. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Brynden Rivers</b>, called "<b>Lord Bloodraven</b>", was the bastard son of King Aegon IV Targaryen by his sixth mistress, Lady Melissa Blackwood. He had two older sisters, Mya and Gwenys, and numerous half-siblings. As his mother was highborn, Brynden was counted among the Great Bastards. Like his bastard siblings, Brynden was legitimized by King Aegon IV in 184&nbsp;AC. Brynden's personal arms were a white dragon with red eyes breathing red flame on a black field. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Brynden Tully</b>, also known as <b>Brynden Blackfish</b>, <b>Brynden the Blackfish</b>, or simply the <b>Blackfish</b>, is a knight from House Tully. He is the younger brother of Hoster Tully, Lord Paramount of the Trident, and the uncle of Lady Catelyn Stark, Lady Lysa Arryn, and Ser Edmure Tully. The Blackfish has served as the Knight of the Gate for House Arryn since Robert's Rebellion. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Clive Russell. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Bryndon Hightower</b> was a knight from House Hightower during the Dance of the Dragons. He was the cousin of Lord Ormund Hightower. </p>
<p><b>Bryte Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Bu Gai</b>, seventeenth of the azure emperors, is the God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti. His seat is located at the city of Yin, in a palace said to be larger than all of King's Landing. His rule is challenged by imperial general Pol Qo at Trader Town and by a sorcerer lord at the city of Carcosa. </p>

<p><b>Calon</b> is the son of Cayn, one of the House Stark guards at Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Winterfell</b> is the ancestral castle and seat of power of House Stark and is considered to be the capital of the north. It is in the center of the northernmost province of the Seven Kingdoms, on the kingsroad that runs from Storm's End to the Wall. It is situated at the eastern edge of the wolfswood, north of the western branch of the White Knife and Castle Cerwyn. Winterfell is south of the northern mountains and southwest of Long Lake, one hundred leagues (three hundred miles) southeast of Deepwood Motte. </p>
<p><b>Calor</b> is the father of Crawn. He is a member of the Moon Brothers. </p>
<p><b>Camarron of the Count</b> is a pit fighter famed in Meereen. His origin is unknown, but he supports the pit fighting culture of the city. </p>

<p><b>Canker Jeyne</b> is a dockside whore in Braavos. </p>
<p><b>Braavos</b> is the wealthiest and likely the most powerful of the Free Cities. It is located in a lagoon on the northwestern end of Essos, where the narrow sea and the Shivering Sea meet. Braavos is also known as <b>Braavos of the Hundred Isles</b> and the <b>Secret City</b>, a name also attributed to the city Nefer, the last remaining city of N'ghai. Braavos is sometimes referred to as the "bastard daughter of Valyria". </p>

<p>Archmaester <b>Cassander</b> is an Archmaester of the Citadel and the author of <i>Song of the Sea: How the Lands Were Severed</i>, where he argues that the Arm of Dorne was not shattered by the children of the forest's greenseers with the Hammer of the Waters, but rather covered by the Song of the Sea, a slow rising of the waters caused by a series of long, hot summers and short, warm winters that melted the ice in the frozen lands north of the Shivering Sea.. </p>
<p><b>Cassandra Baratheon</b> was a noblewoman from House Baratheon during the reign of kings Viserys I, Aegon II and Aegon III Targaryen. She was the eldest of the four daughters of Lord Borros Baratheon of Storm's End. She and her sisters were known as the Four Storms. </p>
<p><b>Cassella Vaith</b> was a member of House Vaith and a Lady of Vaith. She was the third mistress of Aegon IV Targaryen, although prior to his ascent the Iron Throne. </p>
<p><b>Cassella Staunton</b> was a noblewoman from House Staunton during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. She was the daughter of Lord Staunton of Rook's Rest. </p>
<p><b>Casso Mogat</b> is the captain of the <i>Merry Midwife</i>. His mother was a Sisterton whore, and his father an Ibbenese whaler. </p>
<p><b>Caster</b> is a figure from the Age of Heroes and the father of Corlos, the first lord of House Casterly, who took their name from Corlos' father. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Castos</b> is an archmaester at the Citadel in Oldtown. </p>
<p><b>Lady Caswell</b> was the wife of Lord Caswell, the ruling Lord of Bitterbridge and the head of House Caswell during the reigns of kings Viserys I and Aegon II Targaryen. Her given name and birth house are unknown. </p>
<p><b>Lord Caswell</b> was a Lord of Bitterbridge and head of House Caswell. His given name is unknown. Lord Caswell's son is Lorent Caswell. </p>
<p><b>Bitterbridge</b>, formerly known as <b>Stonebridge</b>, is the seat of House Caswell in the Reach. </p>
<p><b>Lord Caswell</b> was the Lord of Bitterbridge and the head of House Caswell during the reigns of kings Viserys I and Aegon II Targaryen. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Catelyn Bracken</b> is a member of House Bracken, the third daughter of Lord Jonos Bracken of Stone Hedge, and the first by his third wife. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Catelyn Stark</b>, née <b>Tully</b>, is the wife of Eddard Stark, Lord of Winterfell and Warden of the North. Together they have five children: Robb, Sansa, Arya, Bran, and Rickon. Catelyn is known as <b>Cat</b> to close family and friends. </p>
<p><b>House Tully of Riverrun</b> is one of the Great Houses of the Seven Kingdoms. Lord Hoster Tully, the Lord Paramount of the Trident, rules over the riverlands from the Tully seat of Riverrun. Their sigil is a silver trout leaping on a striped field of blue and mud red, and their house words are "Family, Duty, Honor." </p>
<p>An unnamed <b>catspaw</b> or <b>footpad</b> is an assassin who tries to kill Bran Stark. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Lalor Roddy. </p>

<p><b>Cayn</b> is a guard sworn to House Stark. He has a son, Calon. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Cedric Payne</b> was a knight from House Payne. </p>

<p><b>Cedrik Storm</b>, also known as <b>the Bastard of Bronzegate</b>, was a bastard of House Buckler. </p>

<p><b>Cerenna Lannister</b> is a member of House Lannister and the daughter of Ser Stafford Lannister and Myranda Lefford. She is the sister of Daven and Myrielle Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Cerion Lannister</b> was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. He extended the rule of the Kingdom of the Rock as far east as the Golden Tooth and its surrounding hills, defeating three lesser kings when they made an alliance against him. </p>
<p><b>Cerissa Brax</b> was a member of House Brax. She was married to Damon Lannister, Lord of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Cerrick</b> was the maester at Coldmoat at the start of the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. He was in the service of Lady Rohanne Webber. </p>
<p><b>Cersei Frey</b>, also know as <b>Little Bee</b>, is the second daughter of Ser Raymund Frey and Beony Beesbury. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Cersei Lannister</b> is the only daughter and eldest child of Lord Tywin Lannister of Casterly Rock and his wife, Lady Joanna Lannister. She is the twin of her younger brother, Ser Jaime Lannister. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> Cersei is played by Lena Headey, and is portrayed when she is a child by Nell Williams in a Season 5 flashback. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Ceryse Hightower</b> was a lady of House Hightower and was the daughter of Lord Manfred Hightower of Oldtown. Her maternal uncle was one of the High Septons during the reign of King Aegon I Targaryen. She eventually married Prince Maegor Targaryen, becoming his first (of many) wives. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Cetheres</b> is an archmaester at the Citadel in Oldtown. </p>
<p><b>Chai Duq</b> was a God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti and the fourth member of his dynasty. He took to wife a noblewoman of Valyria and kept a dragon at his court. </p>
<p><b>Chain</b> is a sellsword in service to the Golden Company. As a serjeant, he is a high-ranking officer, and he claims to be a knight. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Lord Chambers</b> was the head of House Chambers during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>The Charioteer</b> is a name the Windblown, a sellsword company hired by Yunkai, mockingly gave to a Yunkish nobleman commanding some of the Yunkai slave solders. </p>
<p><b>Chatana Qo</b>, the Arrow of Jhahar, was a warrior woman of the Summer Isles and the daughter and successor of Xanda Qo, Princess of Sweet Lotus Vale. She fought in a series of wars, which came to be known as the Slavers' Wars. The unity of the Summer Isles, that her mother achieved, did not survive Chatana's reign however, for she wed unwisely and did not rule as well as she fought. </p>
<p><b>Chataya</b> is the owner of an upscale whorehouse in King's Landing. She has a daughter named Alayaya who works in her establishment. </p>
<p><b>Chayle</b> is a septon from the Faith of the Seven. He is the guardian of Winterfell's sept, where he hangs carved masks of the Seven, and the librarian of the castle's library tower. </p>
<p><b>Cheese</b> was the alias of a ratcatcher who, during the Dance of the Dragons, helped Blood murder six-year-old Prince Jaehaerys, King Aegon II Targaryen's firstborn son and the heir to the Iron Throne. Cheese's true name is lost to history. </p>
<p><b>Chella</b> is the daughter of Cheyk and clan chief of the Black Ears, one of the Vale mountain clans. She has sons who have claimed fifty ears between them. She herself has claimed forty-six. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Natalie Lee. </p>
<p><b>Chett</b> is a steward of the Night's Watch. Before he was sent to the Wall, he was a leechman's son in the riverlands. He is the POV character in the prologue of <i>A Storm of Swords</i>. </p>
<p><b>Cheyk</b> is a member of the Black Ears, one of the Vale mountain clans. Chella is the daughter of Cheyk, but Cheyk's gender and living status are unknown. </p>
<p><b>Chezdhar zo Rhaezn</b> is a Yunkish Nobleman. </p>
<p><b>Chiggen</b> is a sellsword who rides with Bronn. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Childer</b> was a maester of the Citadel. He wrote the book <i>Winter's Kings, or the Legends and Lineages of the Starks of Winterfell</i>. </p>
<p><b>Chiswyck</b> is a man-at-arms in service to Ser Gregor Clegane. </p>
<p><b>Choq Choq</b> was a God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti and the fifteenth and last member of his dynasty. </p>
<p><br> <b>Ch'Vyalthan</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel, and the author of <i>An History of the Great Sieges of Westeros</i> and <i>An History of the House of Lannister</i>. He is deceased by the time of King Robert Baratheon's death. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Chyttering</b> is the head of House Chyttering. He is the father of Lucos Chyttering. </p>
<p><b>Cissy</b> is a lowborn woman in the service of House Waynwood. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Clarence Crabb</b> is a legendary hero from House Crabb of Crackclaw Point. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Clarence Crabb</b>, better known as <b>Clarence the Short</b>, was a knight from House Crabb who became a member of the Kingsguard at an unknown time. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Clarent Crakehall</b> was a knight from House Crakehall during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Clarenzo</b> is a member of Izembaro's theater troupe. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is played by Rob Callender. </p>
<p><b>Clarice Osgrey</b> was a member of House Osgrey during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. She was mistress of the households of Aegon's two queens, Jaehaera Targaryen and Daenaera Velaryon. </p>
<p><b>Clarisse Dayne</b> was the Lady of Starfall and head of House Dayne during the reign of Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Clayton Suggs</b> is a knight from House Suggs and a supporter of Stannis Baratheon. His coat of arms is a winged pig. </p>
<p>The second <b>Clegane</b> was the father of Gregor and Sandor Clegane. His first name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Clegane</b> was the founder of House Clegane and the first Knight of Clegane's Keep. He was originally the kennelmaster of Casterly Rock. His first name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Clegg</b> was a Grand Maester of the Citadel who served on the small council under an unknown Targaryen King. </p>
<p><b>Clement</b> is a brother of the order on the Quiet Isle. He is forty-eight years old. </p>
<p>The <b>Quiet Isle</b> is an upthrust island that sits at the mouth of the Trident where it flows into the Bay of Crabs, southeast of Saltpans and northwest of Maidenpool. Its septry is a refuge for those sworn to the Faith of the Seven. Septon Meribald has often visited the isle. </p>
<p><b>Clement Celtigar</b> was a member of House Celtigar during the Dance of the Dragons. He was the son and heir of Lord Bartimos Celtigar. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Clement Crabb</b> was a knight from House Crabb and a member of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Clement Piper</b> is the Lord of Pinkmaiden and head of House Piper. He has at least two sons, Ser Marq and Lewys Piper, but no daughter. </p>
<p><b>Pinkmaiden Castle</b>, also known simply as <b>Pinkmaiden</b>, is the seat of House Piper in the southwestern riverlands. The castle is located on the Red Fork south of Riverrun, southeast of Acorn Hall, northwest of Stoney Sept, and northeast of Hornvale. </p>
<p><b>Cleoden I Durrandon</b> was a Storm King of the stormlands from House Durrandon. During the coming of the Andals to the stormlands, he made an unlikely alliance with three Dornish kings and won a major victory over Drox the Corpse-Maker on the river Slayne near Stonehelm. </p>
<p><b>Cleon</b> is a butcher and cook enslaved to Grazdan mo Ullhor. </p>
<p><b>Cleon the Second</b> was the brief King of Astapor, succeeding the first Cleon. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Cleos Frey</b> is a knight of House Frey and the eldest son of Emmon Frey and Genna Lannister. He is married to Jeyne Darry and has two young sons, Tywin and Willem. His personal coat-of-arms is the twin towers of House Frey and the golden lion of House Lannister, quartered. </p>
<p><b>Cleos Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Cletus Yronwood</b> is a knight of House Yronwood, the son and heir of Lord Anders Yronwood of Yronwood. </p>
<p><b>Cley Cerwyn</b> is a member of House Cerwyn. He is the son of Lord Medger Cerwyn and the heir to Castle Cerwyn. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Cleyton Caswell</b> was a knight of House Caswell during the reign of Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><br> Ser <b>Clifford Conklyn</b> was the head of House Conklyn during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Leafy Lake</b> is a lake in the Reach. It lies within the lands of House Webber. The mouth of the Chequy Water flows into it. </p>
<p><b>Clifford Swann</b> is a member of House Swann. In the appendix of <i>A Dance with Dragons</i> he is listed as the Lord of Stonehelm, despite the fact that the earlier established Lord of Stonehelm, Lord Gulian Swann, had two sons, Donnel and Balon, the former of which is still eligible to inherit. </p>
<p><b>Clubfoot Karl</b> is a ranger or steward of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p>The <b>Night's Watch</b> is a military order dedicated to holding the Wall, the immense fortification on the northern border of the Seven Kingdoms, defending the realms of men from what lies beyond the Wall. The order's foundation dates back to the Age of Heroes, at the time when the Others were pushed back. The men of Night's Watch wear only black, and they are known as <b>black brothers</b>. Recruits who join the Watch are said to <b>take the black</b>. </p>
<p><b>Clydas</b> is a steward of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Coals</b> is one of the children of the forest in service to the last greenseer. He/she does not speak the Common Tongue. His/her true name is too long for the human tongue according to Leaf, so Meera Reed and Bran Stark make up the name Coals. </p>
<p><b>Cohollo</b> is a bloodrider to Khal Drogo. </p>
<p>A <b>bloodrider</b> is a sworn protector of a <i>khal</i> among the Dothraki <i>khalasars</i>. </p>
<p><b>Coldhands</b> is a mysterious figure from beyond the Wall. "Coldhands" is a name given to him by Samwell Tarly; his actual name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Colemon</b> is a maester in service to House Arryn at the Eyrie. </p>
<p>The <b>Eyrie</b> is an ancient castle and seat of House Arryn, one of the oldest lines of Andal nobility, within the Vale of Arryn. It is situated in the Mountains of the Moon on a shoulder of the peak known as the Giant's Lance, several thousand feet above the valley below. Although small compared to the seats of other Great Houses in Westeros, the Eyrie is considered impregnable to attack. During wintertime, the Arryns seek refuge against the cold in the Gates of the Moon at the base of the mountain. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Colen of Greenpools</b> is a knight from Greenpools. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Colin Florent</b> is a knight from House Florent and the younger brother to Alester Florent, Lord of Brightwater Keep. </p>
<p><b>Collio Quaynis</b> is a Tyroshi singer. His accent is thick, making it sometimes hard to understand him when he sings in the Common Tongue. </p>
<p><b>Colloquo Votar</b> was a Volantene adventurer and the author of the <i>Jade Compendium</i>, a collection of stories and legends from the east. At some point in his life Votar traveled east and visited all the lands of the Jade Sea. He was from Volantis. </p>
<p><b>Colmar Frey</b> is the twentieth son of Lord Walder Frey, the second son born of his marriage to Annara Farring. However, the rumor at the Twins is that Annara Farring was sleeping with Black Walder Frey, making Colmar's parentage dubious. Colmar is promised to the Faith. </p>
<p><b>Conn</b>, known as <b>Conn son of Coratt</b> because of his father, is a member of the Stone Crows, one of the Vale mountain clans found in the Mountains of the Moon. </p>
<p><b>Conwy</b> is a recruiter or wandering crow of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Coratt</b> is one of the Stone Crows from the Mountains of the Moon in the Vale of Arryn. He is the father of Conn. </p>
<p><b>Lady Corbray</b> is a merchant's daughter and the second wife of Lyonel Corbray, the Lord of Heart's Home and the head of House Corbray. </p>
<p><b>Lord Corbray</b> was the Lord of Heart's Home and the head of House Corbray during Robert's Rebellion. </p>
<p><b>Corenna Swann</b> was a member of House Swann, her relation to Gulian Swann, the Lord of Stonehelm, is unknown. She was the first wife of Ser Stevron Frey and had one son by him, Ser Ryman Frey. She died of a wasting illness. </p>
<p><b>Corin Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Corliss Penny</b> is a knight of House Penny and a supporter of Stannis Baratheon. </p>
<p><b>Corlos</b> is a figure from the Dawn Age and the founder of House Casterly. His father's name was Caster. </p>
<p><b>House Casterly of Casterly Rock</b> was a noble house who lived at Casterly Rock in the Dawn Age. They were the richest house of First Men in Westeros and the most powerful family in the westerlands. </p>
<p><b>Corlys Velaryon</b>, known as <b>the Sea Snake</b>, was a fabled Lord of the Tides, Master of Driftmark, and head of House Velaryon. He was the husband of Princess Rhaenys Targaryen. During the Dance of the Dragons, he became Hand to Queen Rhaenyra Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Corlys Velaryon </b> was a knight from House Velaryon and a son of Daemon Velaryon, the Lord of the Tides and Master of Driftmark. He was a younger brother to Aethan Velaryon. Ser Corlys was the first Lord Commander of the Kingsguard. </p>
<p>A <b>corsair king</b>, a leader of pirates, is reported as being active in the Summer Sea. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Cortnay Penrose</b> is a knight of House Penrose. The son of Lord Penrose, he is named by Renly Baratheon as castellan of Storm's End. </p>
<p><b>Storm's End</b> is the seat of House Baratheon, the Lords Paramount of the Stormlands. The castle is located at Durran's Point on the northern coast of Shipbreaker Bay, south of Bronzegate and northeast of Griffin's Roost. The kingsroad runs north from Storm's End through the stormlands to King's Landing, the capital of the Seven Kingdoms. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Corwin Rogers</b> was a knight from House Rogers during the reign of Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Corwyn Corbray</b> was a knight from House Corbray during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons and the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. During the regency, Corwyn became one of Aegon III's regents, whilst his older brother, Lord Leowyn, was the Protector of the Realm. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Corwyn Corbray</b> was a knight from House Corbray during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons and the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. During the regency, Corwyn became one of Aegon III's regents, whilst his older brother, Lord Leowyn, was the Protector of the Realm. </p>
<p><b>Corwyn Velaryon</b> was one of the children of Lord Daemon Velaryon, the Lord of the Tides and the head of House Velaryon during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen and King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Coryanne Martell</b> was a noblewoman from House Martell during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. She was a younger daughter of Prince Qoren Martell and sister to Princess Aliandra Martell. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Coryanne Wylde</b> was a member of House Wylde during the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Cosgrove</b> was the steward of House Butterwell during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Cossomo the Conjurer</b> is a patron of the Happy Port. He is a conjurer who performs sleight of hand tricks and calls it magic. </p>
<p><b>Lord Costayne</b> was the Lord of the Three Towers and the head of House Costayne during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lord Costayne</b> was the Lord of the Three Towers and the head of House Costayne during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. He was married to one of Lord Ambrose Butterwell's daughters. </p>
<p><b>Cotter Pyke</b> is a member of the Night's Watch and the commander of Eastwatch-by-the-Sea. </p>
<p><b>Eastwatch-by-the-Sea</b> is the easternmost castle of the Night's Watch along the Wall, located on a grey, windswept shore by the Bay of Seals. Near Eastwatch live some fisherfolk and to the west lies Greenguard. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Courtenay Greenhill</b> is a household knight in King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Crackbones</b> is a legendary hero from Crackclaw Point. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Craghas Drahar</b>, called <b>Craghas Crabfeeder</b>, was a prince admiral from Myr who served the Triarchy. </p>
<p><b>Craghorn Hoare</b>, known as <b>Craghorn of the Red Smile</b>, was a King of the Iron Islands from House Hoare. The Hoare kings of his era were opposed by the priests of the Drowned God because of their support for the Faith of the Seven, discouraging of reaving, and promotion of trade. </p>
<p><b>Cragorn</b> is a member of Euron Greyjoy's crew aboard the <i>Silence</i>. </p>
<p><b>Crake the Boarkiller</b> is a legendary figure from the Age of Heroes that founded House Crakehall. </p>
<p><b>Craster</b> is a wildling and is the master of Craster's Keep, located beyond the Wall. Despite his unsavory reputation, he is regarded as a friend to the Night's Watch. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Robert Pugh. </p>
<p><b>Crawn</b>, known as <b>Crawn son of Calor</b> because of his father, is a member of the Moon Brothers, one of the Vale mountain clans. </p>
<p><b>Craya</b> is a prostitute in King's Landing. She was specifically created for the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Cregan Karstark</b> is a member of House Karstark, the eldest son of Arnolf Karstark, and the cousin of Lord Rickard Karstark of Karhold. </p>
<p><b>Cregan Stark</b>, known as <b>the Wolf of the North</b> and later in life <b>the Old Man of the North</b>, was the Lord of Winterfell and head of House Stark during the reigns of kings Viserys I, Aegon II, Aegon III and Daeron I Targaryen. He briefly served as Hand of the King for Aegon III after the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Cregard Stark</b> was a member of House Stark. He was the older brother of his twin Torrhen, and the eldest son of Edric Stark and Serena Stark. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Creighton Longbough</b> is a hedge knight. His coat of arms is a green field with a brown chief. His traveling partner is Ser Illifer the Penniless. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Creighton Redfort</b> is a knight of House Redfort and is the son of Lord Horton Redfort. </p>
<p><b>Cressen</b> is a maester of the Citadel in service to Stannis Baratheon, Lord of Dragonstone. He is the POV character in the prologue of <i>A Clash of Kings</i>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Oliver Ford Davies. </p>
<p><b>Lord Cressey</b> was the head of House Cressey during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Crey</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel during the late reign of Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Creylen</b> is a maester of the Citadel assigned to Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Crispian Celtigar</b> was the Lord of Claw Isle and head of House Celtigar during the reign of King Aegon I Targaryen. He served as the first master of coin. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Criston Cole</b> was a knight from House Cole who rose to become Lord Commander of the Kingsguard for Viserys I Targaryen. His relationship with Viserys's daughter, Princess Rhaenyra Targaryen, was first friendly and then adversarial. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Criston Wylde</b> was a knight of House Wylde during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Cromm</b> is one of the crew on Asha Greyjoy's ship, <i>Black Wind</i>. </p>
<p><b>Lord Commander Crowl</b> was a member of House Crowl who served as Lord Commander of the Night's Watch over a thousand years ago. His given name has not been revealed. </p>
<p><b>Cuger</b> or <b>Cugen</b> is a recruit of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Culiper</b> was a maester of the Citadel who served House Targaryen at Dragonstone during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Cutjack</b> is one of the recruits for the Night’s Watch found by Yoren and is part of the band marching north to the Wall. </p>
<p><b>Cynda Lannister</b> is a member of a lesser branch of House Lannister in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. She is the mother of Alton Lannister, who replaces Cleos Frey in the television continuity. </p>
<p><b>Cynthea Frey</b> is the only daughter of Ser Geremy Frey and Carolei Waynwood. She is a ward of Lady Anya Waynwood. </p>
<p><b>Cyrelle Tarbeck</b> was a member of House Tarbeck and the younger daughter of Lord Walderan and Ellyn Tarbeck. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Cyrenna Swann</b> was a member of House Swann and the second wife of Lord Walder Frey, with whom she had two sons, Ser Jared and Septon Luceon. Her relation to Gulian Swann, Lord of Stonehelm, is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Daario Naharis</b> is a Tyroshi captain of the sellsword company, the Stormcrows. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Ed Skrein and Michiel Huisman. </p>
<p>The <b>Stormcrows</b> are a mercenary company found in the Free Cities. Their banner displays four crows between crossed lightning bolts. They number five hundred horses. </p>
<p><b>Dacey Mormont</b> is the heir of House Mormont. She is the daughter of Maege Mormont, Lady of Bear Island, and the niece of Jeor Mormont, Lord Commander of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Bear Island</b> is a remote island in the north that is home to House Mormont. It lies within the Bay of Ice, north of Deepwood Motte and south of the Frozen Shore. The Mormonts live at Mormont Keep. </p>
<p><b>Dacks</b> was a squire for House Redfort. </p>
<p><b>Daegon Shepherd</b>, known as the <b>Black Shepherd</b>, is the captain of the ship <i>Dagger</i> in the Iron Fleet. He is under the command of Victarion Greyjoy. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Daella Targaryen</b> was the eighth born child of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Queen Alysanne Targaryen. She was married to Lord Rodrik Arryn, with whom she had one child, Aemma Arryn. </p>
<p><b>Kingship</b> is the position and power of a king. There have been many kings in the Known World. In Westeros, kings inherit the title through male-preference primogeniture, save for the Kingdom of the Iron Islands which has revived the elective kingsmoot system. Each of the Seven Kingdoms had a king once, though Dorne started using the title "Prince of Dorne" after Lord Mors Martell married Queen Nymeria, and the new rulers chose to abandon the Andal customs in favor of those of the Rhoynar. </p>
<p><b>Jaehaerys I Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>the Conciliator</b>, <b>the Wise</b>, or later in life as <b>the Old King</b>, was the fourth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He ascended the throne in 48&nbsp;AC following the death of his uncle, Maegor I Targaryen. Jaehaerys was the longest reigning Targaryen monarch, sitting on the throne for fifty-five years. He was a dragonrider, riding Vermithor, the largest dragon after Balerion and Vhagar. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Alysanne Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Good Queen Alysanne</b>, was the queen consort of her brother, King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. Alysanne was a dragonrider, whose mount was Silverwing. </p>
<p><b>Aemma Arryn</b> was the queen consort and first wife of King Viserys I Targaryen, and a granddaughter of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and his sister-wife, Queen Alysanne Targaryen. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Daella Targaryen</b> was the eldest daughter and fourth child of King Maekar I Targaryen and his wife Dyanna Dayne. </p>
<p><b>Maekar I Targaryen</b> was Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and the fourteenth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He was the fourth son of King Daeron II Targaryen, and was given the Targaryen seat of Summerhall, and was thus known as the Prince of Summerhall. Maekar was a capable army commander who served in two of the Blackfyre Rebellions. After a number of unexpected deaths in the royal family, he came to the throne in 221&nbsp;AC. </p>
<p><b>Daemion Velaryon</b> was a member of House Velaryon during the reign of kings Viserys I, Aegon II and Aegon III Targaryen. He was a son of Ser Vaemond Velaryon and his lady wife, and had a brother, Daeron Velaryon. </p>
<p><b>Daemion Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen during the Century of Blood, the third son of Lord Aerys Targaryen of Dragonstone, and the father of Aerion Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Daemon I Blackfyre</b>, born <b>Daemon Waters</b>, was the bastard son of Princess Daena Targaryen and King Aegon IV Targaryen. Daemon founded House Blackfyre, named after the Targaryen Valyrian steel sword. He fought against his trueborn half-brother, King Daeron II Targaryen, for the Iron Throne in the First Blackfyre Rebellion. </p>
<p><b>House Targaryen of Dragonstone</b> is a noble family of Valyrian descent who once ruled the Seven Kingdoms of Westeros. The Targaryen sigil is a three-headed dragon breathing flames, red on black. The house words are <i>"Fire and Blood"</i>. It eventually became the first royal house of the Seven Kingdoms, as <b>House Targaryen of King's Landing</b>. </p>
<p>The <b>First Blackfyre Rebellion</b>, originally called the <b>Blackfyre Rebellion</b>, was a war fought between the loyalist forces of King Daeron II Targaryen and the rebel forces of his half-brother, Daemon I Blackfyre. Conflict arose when Daemon, a bastard son of the late King Aegon IV Targaryen, claimed the throne of his older, true born brother, King Daeron II Targaryen, which resulted in open civil war that divided the Seven Kingdoms. </p>
<p><b>Daemon II Blackfyre</b>, also known as <b>Daemon the Younger</b>, was the third son of Daemon I Blackfyre. He used the alias <b>John the Fiddler</b>, a hedge knight, while traveling incognito through the Seven Kingdoms. He led the brief Second Blackfyre Rebellion. </p>
<p><b>Daemon III Blackfyre</b> was the eldest son of Haegon I Blackfyre. </p>
<p><b>Daemon Blackfyre</b> was a member of House Blackfyre. He was a cousin of Maelys I Blackfyre and a captain-general of the Golden Company. Daemon's descent from his namesake, the first Daemon Blackfyre, is currently unknown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Daemon Sand</b>, known as the <b>Bastard of Godsgrace</b>, is the bastard son of Ser Ryon Allyrion, the heir of House Allyrion. The knight is one of Dorne's finest swords. </p>
<p>A <b>knight</b> is a member of a warrior tradition that is heavily interwoven in the feudal culture of the Seven Kingdoms and the Faith of the Seven. Knights occupy a social standing between that of lords and smallfolk. In contrast to nobility, this rank is not hereditary. Knights are referred to with the title "<b>Ser</b>". </p>
<p>Prince <b>Daemon Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen, being a younger son of Prince Baelon Targaryen and a brother of King Viserys I Targaryen. Daemon was the second husband of Rhaenyra Targaryen, Princess of Dragonstone, following Ser Laenor Velaryon. </p>
<p><b>Viserys I Targaryen</b> was the fifth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne, ruling from 103&nbsp;AC to 129&nbsp;AC. He succeeded his grandfather, the Old King Jaehaerys I. Viserys continued the prosperous peace and legacy of his grandsire, but the seeds for the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons that would much later engulf the realm were inadvertently sown in his reign. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Rhaenyra Targaryen</b>, cheered as <b>the Realm's Delight</b> when she was young and later called <b>the Half-Year Queen</b>, was the first-born child of King Viserys I Targaryen. Rhaenyra was King Viserys I's only living child by his first wife, Queen Aemma of House Arryn. At the age of eight, she was made her father's heir and grew up expecting to become the first ruling Queen of Westeros. Rhaenyra was a dragonrider whose mount was Syrax. </p>
<p><b>Daemon Velaryon</b> was the Lord of the Tides, Master of Driftmark, and head of House Velaryon during Aegon's Conquest. Amongst the oldest supporters and closest friends of House Targaryen, Daemon served as the first master of ships to Aegon the Conqueror. </p>
<p><b>Daemon Velaryon</b> was the Lord of the Tides, Master of Driftmark, and the head of House Velaryon during the reign of the kings Maegor I Targaryen and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. He served as master of ships and lord admiral for both kings, as well as Hand of the King for his nephew, King Jaehaerys I. </p>
<p><b>Daena</b> is a mummer at the Gate in Braavos. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Daena Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Daena the Defiant</b>, was the eldest daughter of King Aegon III Targaryen and Queen Daenaera Velaryon. She was the sister-wife of King Baelor I Targaryen, and was the mother of Daemon Blackfyre, her bastard son by the future King Aegon IV Targaryen. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Daenaera Velaryon</b> was the queen consort and second wife of King Aegon III Targaryen, and a member of House Velaryon. Daenaera was the daughter of Daeron Velaryon, a cousin of Lord Alyn Velaryon, and his wife, Hazel Harte. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Daenerys Targaryen</b> was the secondborn child of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Queen Alysanne Targaryen. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Daenerys Targaryen</b> was the daughter of Aegon IV Targaryen and Naerys Targaryen, and the younger sister of King Daeron II Targaryen. Daenerys Targaryen, daughter of Aerys II Targaryen and Rhaella Targaryen, was named after her. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Daenerys Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Daenerys Stormborn</b>, is one of the last confirmed members of House Targaryen, along with her older brother Viserys, who refers to her as <b>Dany</b>. She is the youngest child of King Aerys II Targaryen and his sister-wife, Queen Rhaella. She is one of the major POV characters in <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Daenerys is played by Emilia Clarke. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Daenora Targaryen</b> was a daughter of Prince Rhaegel Targaryen and Lady Alys Arryn. She had an older brother and sister, the twins Aelor and Aelora. Daenora was married to her cousin, Prince Aerion. </p>
<p><b>Daeron I Targaryen</b>, known as <b>the Young Dragon</b> and <b>the Boy King</b>, was the eldest son of King Aegon III Targaryen and Queen Daenaera Velaryon, and the eighth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He ascended to the throne at the age of fourteen and is famous for invading Dorne, which he wrote about in his <i>The Conquest of Dorne</i>. </p>
<p><b>Daeron II Targaryen</b>, known as <b>Daeron the Good</b>, was the twelfth Targaryen to sit the Iron Throne. Daeron brought Dorne peacefully into the realm, uniting all the lands of Westeros south of the wall. His bastard half-brother, Daemon Blackfyre, challenged his rule and the result was a terrible civil war, the First Blackfyre Rebellion. Daeron died during the Great Spring Sickness in 209&nbsp;AC. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Daeron Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Daeron the Daring</b>, was the third and youngest son of King Viserys I Targaryen and his second wife, Queen Alicent Hightower. He was a younger brother to King Aegon II Targaryen. Like his siblings, Daeron was a dragonrider, and he rode the she-dragon Tessarion. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Daeron Targaryen</b>, sometimes referred to as <b>Daeron the Drunken</b>, was the eldest son of King Maekar I Targaryen and his wife Dyanna Dayne. Daeron was one of the rare Targaryens who had prophetic dragon dreams. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Daeron Targaryen</b> was the youngest son and fourthborn child of King Aegon V Targaryen and Queen Betha Blackwood. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Daeron Targaryen</b> was the secondborn son of King Aerys II Targaryen and Queen Rhaella Targaryen. He lived for only half a year. </p>
<p><b>Daeron Vaith</b> is Lord of the Red Dunes and head of House Vaith. </p>
<p><b>Daeron Velaryon</b> was a member of House Velaryon during the reign of kings Viserys I, Aegon II and Aegon III Targaryen. He was a son of Ser Vaemond Velaryon and his lady wife, and had a brother, Daemion Velaryon. His grandson, King Daeron I Targaryen, was presumably named after him. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Daeryssa </b> is a character in a song. According to the song, she was once saved by Serwyn of the Mirror Shield from giants. </p>
<p><b>Serwyn of the Mirror Shield</b> is a legendary figure from the Age of Heroes, although singers now claim he was a knight of the Kingsguard. He is a favorite of the smallfolk. Serwyn served the ancient Kings of the Reach from House Gardener. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Dafyn Vance</b> is the husband of Maegelle Frey. They have three children, Marianne, Walder and Patrek Vance. It is unknown if he comes from the Atranta or the Wayfarer's Rest branch of House Vance. </p>
<p><b>Dagmer</b>, known as <b>Cleftjaw</b> and <b>Dagmer Cleftjaw</b>, is the ironborn captain of the longship <i>Foamdrinker</i> and the master-at-arms for House Greyjoy of Pyke. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Ralph Ineson. </p>
<p>The <b>ironborn</b> are the natives of the Iron Islands in the Sunset Sea off the western coast of Westeros. They are also known as <b>ironmen</b>, especially by those they raid. The men from the green lands of Westeros also call them <i>squids</i> as the isles are ruled by House Greyjoy, whose sigil is a kraken. </p>
<p><b>Dagon Codd</b> is an ironborn warrior and a member of House Codd. </p>
<p><b>Dagon Ironmaker</b> is a member of House Ironmaker and a grandson of Erik Ironmaker. </p>
<p><b>Erik Ironmaker</b>, known as <b>Erik the Just</b> and <b>Erik Anvil-Breaker</b>, is an ironborn raider and the head of House Ironmaker. </p>
<p><b>Dagon Greyjoy</b>, called the <b>Last Reaver</b>, was Lord of the Iron Islands and Lord Reaper of Pyke during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. According to his great-grandson, Victarion, he last sat in the Seastone Chair "almost a hundred years" before the events of <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>. </p>
<p><b>Dagon Greyjoy</b>, also known as <b>Dagon the Drunkard</b>, is a distant cousin of Asha Greyjoy, more distantly related to her than her cousin Quenton Greyjoy. He is named after the famous Dagon Greyjoy, Lord of the Iron Islands. </p>
<p><b>Dagos Manwoody</b> is the Lord of Kingsgrave and head of House Manwoody. </p>
<p><b>Daisy</b> is a prostitute working in the brothel owned by Petyr "Littlefinger" Baelish in King's Landing. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is played by Maisie Dee. She replaces the unnamed maid from the books, who is in bed with Grand Maester Pycelle, when he is arrested by Tyrion. </p>
<p><b>Dake</b> was a peasant who served House Osgrey. </p>
<p><b>Dake</b> is a guard in service to House Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Dalbridge</b>, called <b>Squire Dalbridge</b>, is a veteran ranger of the Night's Watch stationed at the Shadow Tower. </p>
<p><b>Droopeye Dale</b> is an ironborn sailor and a member of the crew on Asha Greyjoy's ship, <i>Black Wind</i>. </p>
<p><b>Dale Drumm</b>, known as <b>Dale the Dread</b>, was a member of House Drumm. </p>
<p><b>Dale Seaworth</b> is the eldest son of Ser Davos Seaworth and his wife Marya. He is the captain of the <i>Wraith</i>. </p>
<p><b>Dalla</b> is a wildling and the wife of Mance Rayder. She has a sister, Val. </p>
<p><b>Dalla</b> is a serving woman at Dragonstone. She is in service to House Baratheon of Dragonstone. </p>
<p><b>Dalton Greyjoy</b>, known as <b>the Red Kraken</b>, was Lord of the Iron Islands, Lord Reaper of Pyke, and head of House Greyjoy during the final days of Viserys I Targaryen and then the Dance of the Dragons. He is regarded as a great hero of the ironborn of the Iron Islands. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Damion Lannister</b> is a knight of House Lannister, a cousin of the main branch. He is married to Shiera Crakehall. They have two children, Ser Lucion and Lanna Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Damon</b>, known as <b>Damon Dance-for-Me</b>, is a man-at-arms sworn to House Bolton. He is one of the Bastard's Boys. </p>
<p><b>Ramsay Snow</b> is the bastard son of Roose Bolton, Lord of the Dreadfort and head of House Bolton, and is known as <b>the Bastard of Bolton</b> and <b>the Bastard of the Dreadfort</b>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Iwan Rheon. </p>
<p>The <b>Bastard's Boys</b> are men-at-arms of House Bolton, in service to Ramsay Bolton. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Damon Darry</b> was a knight from House Darry. He may have been a Lord of Darry. </p>
<p><b>Damon Hightower</b>, known as <b>Damon the Devout</b>, was a head of House Hightower and Lord of the Hightower. </p>
<p><b>Damon Lannister</b>, better known as <b>the Grey Lion</b>, was the Lord of Casterly Rock and the head of House Lannister during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. He wed Cerissa Brax and was the father of Tybolt and Gerold. </p>
<p><b>Damon Lannister</b> is a nobleman of House Lannister and the only son of Ser Jason Lannister by his first wife, Alys Stackspear. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jason Lannister</b> was a knight from House Lannister. He was the fourth and youngest son of Lord Gerold Lannister and his second wife, Lady Rohanne Webber. </p>
<p><b>Damon Marbrand</b> is Lord of Ashemark and head of House Marbrand in the westerlands. He is the father of Ser Addam Marbrand. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Damon Morrigen</b>, called <b>Damon the Devout</b>, was a pious knight from House Morrigen who was a devout member of the Warrior's Sons. He became Grand Captain of the Warrior's Sons, and led the chapter in King's Landing based at the Sept of Remembrance early in the Faith Militant uprising. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Damon Paege</b> is a knight of House Paege. His squire is Hoster Frey, a kinsman and son of Sylwa Paege. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Damon Shett</b> is the Knight of Gull Tower and head of House Shett of Gull Tower. </p>
<p><b>Damon Teague</b> was the last monarch of House Teague. He was the younger brother and champion of King Humfrey I Teague, who instigated a massive uprising of Riverlords by attempting to suppress worship of the old gods. In the campaign's final battle, Humfrey I perished, passing the crown to his heir Humfrey, only for the latter to be killed. The bloody crown then passed to Damon's second nephew, Hollis, who died shortly after, thus making Tyler Teague, the youngest of Humfrey I's sons, the new king. However, Tyler was also killed. And so, the crown passed to Damon, who also perished in battle. Thus by the end of the day, House Teague was extinct. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Damon Vypren</b> is a knight from House Vypren, the son and heir of Lord Lucias Vypren. </p>
<p><b>Hempen Dan</b> is a free folk raider. He is a ropemaker. </p>
<p><b>Dancy</b> is a whore at Chataya's brothel in King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Danelle Lothston</b>, known as <b>Mad Danelle</b>, was the Lady of Harrenhal and the head of House Lothston during the reigns of kings Aerys I and Maekar I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Dannel</b> is a steward of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Danny Flint</b> was a girl from House Flint who dressed up as a boy to become a member of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Danos Slynt</b> is the third son of Janos Slynt. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Danwell Frey</b> is a knight of House Frey, the eighth son of Lord Walder Frey, the third son born of Walder's marriage to Amarei Crakehall. He is married to Wynafrei Whent, with many stillbirths and miscarriages. </p>
<p><b>Daragh Umber</b> was an ancestor of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Dareon</b> is a recruit of the Night's Watch, known primarily for his excellent singing voice. Ser Alliser Thorne refers to him as <b>Lover</b>. </p>
<p><b>Dareon Hunter</b> is a member of House Hunter mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Darke</b> is a servant at the Seven Swords inn in Duskendale. </p>
<p><b>Lord Darklyn</b> was the Lord of Duskendale and the head of House Darklyn during the reign of kings Maegor I and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Darla Deddings</b> was a member of House Deddings during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Darlessa Marbrand</b> is the widow of Ser Tygett Lannister. She had one son with him, Tyrek. </p>
<p><b>Darnold Darry</b> was a Lord of Darry and head of House Darry during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Darnold Arryn</b> was the Lord of the Eyrie, Defender of the Vale, Warden of the East, and the head of House Arryn at the beginning of the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lord Darry</b> was the Lord of Darry and the head of House Darry during the reign of King Aegon II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lord Darry</b> was a Lord of Darry and head of House Darry. He was the father of Ser Raymun, Mariya, and Jeyne Darry. It is unclear if he is still alive at the start of <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>, and his given name has not been mentioned yet. </p>
<p><b>Daryn Hornwood</b> is a member of House Hornwood and the heir to the Hornwood. He is the son of Lord Halys Hornwood and Lady Donella Manderly. He has a bastard half-brother, Larence Snow. </p>
<p>The <b>daughter of the captain of the <i>Myraham</i></b> is Theon Greyjoy's bedmate during his journey back to the Iron Islands. Her father is the captain of the <i>Myraham</i> out of Oldtown. Her name is never mentioned. </p>
<p>The <b>Daughter of the Dusk</b> is a courtesan in Braavos. She is beautiful. She has her own barge and servants to pole her to trysts. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Daven Lannister</b> is a knight from House Lannister. He is the son of Ser Stafford Lannister, a cousin and brother-in-law of Lord Tywin Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Davos the Dragonslayer</b> is a legendary figure of the Reach who lived during the Age of Heroes. Tales describe him as a knight even though knights came to Westeros thousands of years later with the Andal invasion. </p>
<p><b>Davos Baratheon</b> was the son of Lord Orys Baratheon and Lady Argella Durrandon, and a brother to Ser Raymont Baratheon. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Davos Darklyn</b> was one of the seven members of House Darklyn to be knights of the Kingsguard. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Davos Dayne</b> was a knight from House Dayne and the Sword of the Morning. </p>
<p><b>Davos Deddings</b> was a member of House Deddings during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Davos Seaworth</b>, commonly called the <b>Onion Knight</b>, and sometimes <b>Davos Shorthand</b>, is the head of House Seaworth. He was once a smuggler, but after Robert's Rebellion he became a landed knight and Stannis Baratheon's most honest and loyal supporter. Davos created his own house sigil, a black ship with an onion on the sails upon a grey field. Davos becomes a POV character starting with <i>A Clash of Kings</i>. He is played by Liam Cunningham in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Deana Hardyng</b> is a member of House Hardyng and the wife of Walton Frey. They have three children; Steffon, Walda and Bryan Frey. </p>
<p><b>Lady Deddings</b> is the wife of Lord Deddings. </p>
<p><b>Lord Deddings</b> is the head of House Deddings in the riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Del</b> is a young free folk raider. </p>
<p><b>Delena Florent</b> is the mother of Edric Storm and niece to Lord Alester Florent. She is married to Ser Hosman Norcross and has two children by him, Alester and Renly. </p>
<p><b>Edric Storm</b> is the bastard son of King Robert I Baratheon and Delena Florent. </p>
<p><b>Della Frey</b>, known as <b>Deaf Della</b> among her kin, is a member of House Frey. She is the eldest child of Ser Benfrey Frey and his wife and cousin, Jyanna Frey. </p>
<p><b>Dellono</b> is a dyer from Braavos. He is one of the regulars at the Gate. </p>
<p><b>Delonne Allyrion</b> is the Lady of Godsgrace and the head of House Allyrion. She is the mother of Ser Ryon Allyrion. </p>
<p><b>Delp</b> is a guard at Riverrun. </p>
<p><b>Riverrun</b> is the ancestral castle of House Tully, the Lords Paramount of the Trident. It is situated in the western riverlands, at the confluence of the Tumblestone and Red Fork rivers. Riverrun is north of Pinkmaiden and northwest of Acorn Hall. The castle sits along the river road, an easy ride which links Lannisport and the crossroads. </p>
<p>The <b>Demon of Darry</b> was a famous knight who eventually became Lord Commander of the Kingsguard at an unknown time. His given name has not been published, but he presumably came from Darry. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Denestan</b> is the author of the book <i>Questions</i>. In his book, Denestan argues that it has been two thousand years since the last kingsmoot, and Alyssa Arryn's lifetime. He also speculates that the runic armor of House Royce is far less ancient than it appears to be. </p>
<p><b>Dennet</b> (or <b>Dennett</b>) is a member of the brotherhood without banners. He is a longbowman. </p>
<p>The <b>brotherhood without banners</b>, also known as the <b>knights of the hollow hill</b> and the <b>forgotten fellowship</b>, is an outlaw group who initially fights Lannister rule in the name of King Robert I Baratheon. Led by the Lightning Lord, Beric Dondarrion, the group is founded in the riverlands by soldiers and nobles who were sent by the then-Hand of the King, Eddard Stark, to bring Gregor Clegane to justice. After they are ambushed while crossing a ford and nearly defeated, the group continues the fight as a guerrilla group. Their numbers increase as they are joined by defeated soldiers from other battles, deserters, and refugees from the War of the Five Kings. Every man of the brotherhood receives a knighthood from Beric. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Dennis Plumm</b> is a knight from House Plumm and is the eldest son and heir of Lord Philip Plumm. He has two younger brothers, Peter and Harwyn. </p>
<p><b>Dennis</b>, known as <b>Dennis the Lame</b>, was a leader of the Poor Fellows during the Faith Militant uprising against King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Dennis Whitfield</b> was a knight of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Denyo Terys</b> is the youngest son of Ternesio Terys. He works aboard the <i>Titan's Daughter</i>. </p>
<p><b>Silver Denys</b> was a man living on Dragonstone at the outset of the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Denys Arryn</b>, known as <b>the Darling of the Vale</b>, was a knight of House Arryn. A distant cousin to the ruling line, he married Lord Jon Arryn's niece. </p>
<p>The <b>Vale of Arryn</b> or <b>the Vale</b> is one of the constituent regions of the Seven Kingdoms of Westeros. It was formerly a sovereign nation ruled by the Kings of Mountain and Vale before Aegon's Conquest. The Mountains of the Moon surround the smaller Vale proper, although the valley's name is often applied to all of House Arryn's realm. </p>
<p><b>Denys Darklyn</b> was the Lord of Duskendale and the head of House Darklyn during the reign of King Aerys II Targaryen. He and his family were executed after the Defiance of Duskendale. </p>
<p><b>Denys Drumm</b> is a member of House Drumm, a son of Lord Dunstan Drumm of Old Wyk. </p>
<p><b>Denys Harte</b> was a knight from House Harte during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Denys Mallister</b> is a knight of House Mallister and a member of the Night's Watch. He has commanded the Shadow Tower for thirty-three years. Denys is an uncle of Jason Mallister, Lord of Seagard. </p>
<p>The <b>Shadow Tower</b> is one of three castles along the Wall that are still inhabited by the Night's Watch. It is located next to mountains at the western end of the Wall. It lies west of Sentinel Stand and east of Westwatch-by-the-Bridge, both abandoned castles. </p>
<p>Ser <b> Denys Oakheart</b> was a knight of House Oakheart during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. He was the eldest son and heir of Lord Oakheart. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Denys Woodwright</b> was a knight from House Woodwright and a sworn sword to Corlys Velaryon, Lord of the Tides and Hand of the Queen to Rhaenyra Targaryen, during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Denyse Hightower</b> is a daughter of Lord Leyton Hightower. She is married to Ser Desmond Redwyne and they have one child, Denys. </p>
<p><b>Denzo D'han</b> is a sellsword captain of the Windblown. A warrior bard, he is the left hand of the Tattered Prince. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Derrick Fossoway</b>, dubbed <b>the Bad Apple</b>, was a member of House Fossoway. It is unknown if he was a red or green Fossoway. </p>
<p><b>Derwa Frey</b> is a daughter of Lord Walder Frey in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Desmera Redwyne</b> is a member of House Redwyne and is the daughter and youngest child of Lord Paxter Redwyne and Mina Tyrell. </p>

Riverrun is north of Pinkmaiden and northwest of Acorn Hall. The castle sits along the river road, an easy ride which links Lannisport and the crossroads. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Desmond Redwyne</b> is a knight of House Redwyne. He is married to Denyse Hightower and they have one child, Denys. His relation to Paxter Redwyne, Lord of the Arbor and the head of the house, is currently unknown. </p>

<p><b>Dickon Frey</b> is a member of House Frey. He is the son of Ser Jammos Frey and Sallei Paege, and the twin brother of Mathis Frey. </p>

<p><b>Dickon Tarly</b> is the second son and fifth child of Lord Randyll Tarly and Lady Melessa Florent. Since his less martial older brother Samwell has joined the Night's Watch, he is the heir to Horn Hill. Dickon is a young squire. </p>
<p><b>Horn Hill</b> is the seat of House Tarly in the Reach. Located on an eponymous hill, the castle lies south of Highgarden and a hundred leagues northeast of Oldtown among the thickly-wooded foothills of the Red Mountains. The Tarlys are marcher lords of the Dornish Marches. </p>
<p><b>Dirah</b> is a prostitute in King's Landing. She was specifically created for the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Dirk</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Dobber</b> is one of the criminals Yoren picked for the Night’s Watch when he cleaned out the dungeons of King’s Landing and is part of the group marching north to the Wall. </p>
<p><b>Dogkiller</b> is a captain of the Unsullied sworn to Daenerys Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Dolf</b>, known as <b>Dolf son of Holger</b> because of his father, is the father of Shagga son of Dolf and a member of the Stone Crows. He taught Shagga everything he knew about warfare. It is unknown if Dolf is still alive. </p>
<p><b>Domeric Bolton</b> was a member of House Bolton, the sole trueborn son of Lord Roose Bolton and Lady Bethany Bolton, and heir to the Dreadfort. </p>
<p><b>Donal Noye</b> is an armorer, smith, and steward of the Night's Watch. He used to be a smith for House Baratheon of Storm's End. </p>

<p><b>Donal Royce</b> is a member of House Royce mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Lord Dondarrion</b> was the Lord of Blackhaven and the head of House Dondarrion during the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. It is unknown if this is the same individual as Lord Harmon Dondarrion. </p>
<p><b>Lord Dondarrion</b> was the Lord of Blackhaven and the head of House Dondarrion during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Donel Greyjoy</b> was a member of House Greyjoy, the third son of Lord Quellon Greyjoy and his first wife, Lady Stonetree. </p>
<p><b>Donella Hornwood</b> is the Lady of Hornwood, wife of Lord Halys Hornwood, and mother of Daryn Hornwood. Originally from House Manderly, she is a cousin of Wyman Manderly, Lord of White Harbor. </p>
<p><b>Doniphos Paenymion</b> is one of the current ruling triarchs of the Free City of Volantis. </p>
<p><b>Donnel Arryn</b> was the Lord of the Eyrie and the head of House Arryn during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen, whom he staunchly supported during the First Blackfyre Rebellion. </p>
<p><b>Donnel Drumm</b> is a member of House Drumm, a son of Lord Dunstan Drumm of Old Wyk. </p>
<p><b>Donnel Flint</b>, also known as <b>Black Donnel Flint</b>, is the son and heir of Lord Torghen Flint, the clan chief of the first Flints. Donnel has a half-brother, Artos. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Donnel Haigh</b> is a knight from House Haigh. The second son of Ser Leslyn Haigh and Perriane Frey, Donnel has two brothers, Ser Harys and Alyn. </p>
<p><b>House Frey of the Crossing</b> is a noble house of the riverlands. Their main seat is the Twins, a pair of castles on each bank of the northern Green Fork of the Trident that serves as a vital bridge across the river. The lord of the house is called the Lord of the Crossing. Their sigil is two blue towers united by a bridge on silver-grey, representing the Twins. Their house words are not mentioned in the books. </p>
<p><b>Donnel Hightower</b>, called <b>Donnel the Delayer</b>, was Lord of the Hightower and head of House Hightower during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Donnel Hill</b>, known as <b>Sweet Donnel</b>, is a steward of the Night's Watch and is the squire of Ser Mallador Locke. He claims to be a bastard of the Lannisters. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Donnel Locke</b> is a knight from House Locke. According to the semi-canon <i>A Song of Ice and Fire Campaign Guide</i>, he is a son of Lord Ondrew Locke and sees to House Locke's lands in his elderly father's stead. </p>
<p><b>Oldcastle</b> is the seat of House Locke in the north. It lies on the northern shore of the Bite, southeast of White Harbor and north of the Three Sisters. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Donnel of Duskendale</b> was a knight of the Kingsguard during the reigns of the kings Daeron II and Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Donnel Swann</b> is a knight of House Swann and the eldest son and heir of Gulian Swann, Lord of Stonehelm. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Donnel Waynwood</b> is a knight from House Waynwood and the second son of Lady Anya Waynwood, Lady of Ironoaks. </p>
<p>The <b>Bloody Gate</b> is a series of battlements in the Vale of Arryn. It is located along the high road which leads into the Vale proper from the Mountains of the Moon. It protects against mountain clansmen and invading armies. </p>
<p><b>Donnis</b> is a member of the guard at Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Donnor Stark</b> was the Lord of Winterfell and the head of House Stark. He was the eldest son of Lord Beron Stark and his wife, Lady Lorra Royce. He had four younger brothers (Willam, Artos, Errold and Rodrik) and two younger sisters (Berena and Alysanne). </p>
<p><b>Donnor Saltcliffe</b> is the Lord of Saltcliffe and the head of House Saltcliffe. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Dontos Hollard</b>, called <b>Dontos the Red</b>, is a knight and the last surviving member of House Hollard. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is portrayed by Tony Way. </p>
<p><b>Donyse</b> is a septa of the Faith of the Seven in service at King's Landing. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Doran Nymeros Martell</b>, also known simply as <b>Doran Martell</b>, is the head of House Martell, the Prince of Dorne, and the Lord of Sunspear. Married to Lady Mellario, of the Free City of Norvos, he has three children: Arianne, Quentyn, and Trystane. He's also the elder brother of Elia and Oberyn Martell. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Alexander Siddig. </p>
<p><b>Sunspear</b>, also known as the Old Palace, is the seat of House Nymeros Martell and the capital of Dorne. The castle is located on the Broken Arm, north of the Greenblood on the far southeastern coast of Westeros and is surrounded on three sides by the sea, and by the shadow city on the fourth side. The palace of the Water Gardens lies three leagues away on the coastal road. </p>
<p><b>Dorne</b> is the large peninsula which makes up the southernmost part of Westeros, and is one of the constituent regions of the Seven Kingdoms. The lords of the ruling House Nymeros Martell style themselves "Prince" and "Princess" in the Rhoynish fashion. </p>
<p><b>Dorcas</b> is a servant of House Lannister in King's Landing. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Dorden the Dour</b> is a knight in the service of King Stannis Baratheon. He is one of the queen's men. </p>
<p><b>Dorea Sand</b> is the thirdborn bastard daughter of Prince Oberyn Martell and his paramour Ellaria Sand. She is one of the famous Sand Snakes. </p>

<p><b>Dorgas Hunter</b> is a member of House Hunter mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Dorian Hightower</b> was a head of House Hightower and Lord of the Hightower. </p>
<p><b>Dormund</b> is a son of Tormund. </p>

<p><b>Dornish Dilly</b> is a member of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Doro Golathis</b> was a Norvoshi historian. He stated there are remnants of Rhoynish outposts in Andalos. </p>
<p><b>Dorren Stark</b> was a King in the North and head of House Stark before the War of Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Doshi</b> was a Dothraki woman and the mother of Khal Mengo, who united all Dothraki under his command during the Century of Blood. She was a purported witch queen. </p>
<p><b>Blind Doss</b> is a free folk leader. </p>
<p><b>Drako Rogare</b> was a member of House Rogare, a Lysene noble banking family. He was the son of Lysandro Rogare, the First Magister of Lys. </p>
<p>A <b>draper's wife</b> was the paramour of Ser Preston Greenfield. She met him while her husband was away. </p>
<p><b>Draqaz</b> is a child of one of the noble ruling families of Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Drazenko Rogare</b> was a member of House Rogare, a wealthy noble family of Lys dedicated to banking. </p>
<p><b>Drennan</b> is an ironborn raider. </p>
<p>The <b>Drinkwater twins</b> are members of House Drinkwater and the twin sisters of Ser Gerris Drinkwater. Their given names have not been revealed. </p>
<p><b>Drogo</b> is a powerful <i>khal</i> or warlord of the fearsome Dothraki nomads. Daenerys Targaryen is promised to him at the beginning of <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> Drogo is played by Jason Momoa. </p>
<p>The <b>Dothraki</b> people are a culture of nomadic warriors in Essos who range across the vast grasslands of the Dothraki sea in hordes known as <i>khalasars</i>. People of the Seven Kingdoms and the Free Cities also refer to the Dothraki as <b>horselords</b>. </p>
<p><i><b>Khal</b></i> is a title that the Dothraki use to designate the leader of a <i>khalasar</i>, the nomadic groupings upon which their society is based. </p>
<p><b>Drox the Corpse-Maker</b> was an Andal warlord who fought during the coming of the Andals to the stormlands. He was defeated by a Storm King, Cleoden I Durrandon, and three Dornish kings in a battle on the river Slayne. </p>
<p>The <b>Drunken Daughter </b> is a dockside whore in Braavos of uncertain temper. She is sweet when sober but not when with wine in her. </p>
<p><b>Druselka</b> was a Rhoynish priestess that took part in the Rhoynar migration. When Nymeria had her people abandon the Abulu, one of the Summer Isles, Druselka and her followers abandoned Nymeria and returned to Essos, as Druselka claimed to have heard Mother Rhoyne calling her children home. Druselka and the others returned to the abandoned and ruined Rhoynish cities, only to find the Valyrians waiting to hunt them down or enslave them. </p>
<p><b>Dryn</b> is a son of Tormund Giantsbane. He is about the same age as Bran Stark. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Dudley</b> was a knight. He was slain in the riverlands during the War of the Five Kings by House Lannister forces. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Dunaver</b> is a knight in service to House Lannister. His squire is Jodge. </p>
<p><b>Harrenhal</b>, the largest castle in the Seven Kingdoms, is the seat of House Whent in the riverlands, on the north shore of the Gods Eye. Since the burning of Harrenhal by dragonfire in Aegon's Conquest, however, the castle has become a dark and ruinous place. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Duncan the Tall</b> was a Lord Commander of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Aegon V Targaryen. His personal arms were a green shooting star above an elm tree proper on sunset, but he also briefly used the sigil of an unknown knight, "a hanged man swinging grim and gray beneath a gallows tree." </p>
<p><b>Duncan Liddle</b>, known as <b>Big Liddle</b>, is a ranger of the Night's Watch. He is the eldest son of Lord Torren Liddle, known as the Liddle, the clan chief of House Liddle, one of the northern mountain clans. </p>
<p><b>Duncan Strong</b> is a sellsword in service to the Golden Company. As a serjeant, he is a high-ranking officer. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Duncan Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Duncan the Small</b> and the <b>Prince of Dragonflies</b>, was a member of House Targaryen. He was the first son of King Aegon V Targaryen and his Queen Betha Blackwood, but gave up the throne for love. </p>
<p><b>Aegon V Targaryen</b> was a Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and the fifteenth Targaryen to sit the Iron Throne as King of the Andals, the Rhoynar, and the First Men. In his youth, he went by the nickname <b>Egg</b> and squired for Ser Duncan the Tall. </p>
<p><b>Dunsen</b> is one of the Mountain's men, the men-at-arms in service to Ser Gregor Clegane. </p>
<p><b>Dunstan Drumm</b>, also known as <b>The Drumm</b> and the <b>Bone Hand</b>, is head of House Drumm, Lord of Old Wyk, and captain of <i>Thunderer</i>. </p>
<p><b>Dunstan Pryor</b> was the Lord of Pebble and head of House Pryor during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Duram Bar Emmon</b> is the Lord of Sharp Point and head of House Bar Emmon. </p>
<p><b>Sharp Point</b> is the seat of House Bar Emmon in the crownlands. The castle is located along the Gullet at the northern end of Massey's Hook, north of Stonedance. It has a large watchtower upon which a great fire burns atop. </p>
<p><b>Duran</b> is an Unsullied sworn to Daenerys Targaryen. He's among the Unsullied who went back to their birth names after being freed from bondage. </p>
<p><b>Durran</b>, called <b>Durran Godsgrief</b>, was the mythic first Storm King and the founder of House Durrandon. Legend has that he was married to Elenei and was the builder of Storm's End. </p>
<p>The title of <b>Storm King</b> was held by the ancient Durrandon kings, who ruled the <b>Kingdom of the Storm</b>, most of which is now the stormlands and at one point included the Riverlands, Crownlands and the eastern part of the Reach. </p>
<p>King <b>Durran II Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Durran the Devout</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon and the son and successor of King Durran Godsgrief. He returned most of the Rainwood to the children of the forest. </p>
<p>King <b>Durran Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Durran Bronze-Axe</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon. </p>
<p>King <b>Durran Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Durran the Dour</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon. He is remembered for slaying Lun the Last, King of the Giants, at the Battle of Crookwater. Scholars debate whether he was <b>Durran V</b> or <b>Durran VI</b>. </p>
<p>King <b>Durran Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Durran the Ravenfriend</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon. </p>
<p>King <b>Durran Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Durran the Young</b> and <b>the Butcher Boy</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon. </p>
<p>King <b>Durran Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Durran the Fair</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon. He brought the independent island Kingdom of Tarth into the Kingdom of the Storm by taking the daughter of King Edwyn Evenstar as his wife. He was also the grandfather of Erich the Sailmaker </p>
<p>King <b>Durran Durrandon</b>, to most scholars <b>Durran X</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon. He extended the Kingdom of the Storm northward to the Blackwater Rush. He was the father of Monfryd I Durrandon. </p>
<p>King <b>Durran XI Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Durran the Dim</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon and the sucessor of Monfryd I Durrandon. He is remembered for having yielded up territories his father had conquered and more. He was succeeded by his son Barron Durrandon. </p>
<p><b>Durran XXI Durrandon</b> was a Storm King of House Durrandon during the Andal Invasion. </p>
<p><b>Durran XXIV Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Durran Half-Blood</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon. He was born during the late Andal invasion of the stormlands, from the union of his father Maldon IV Durrandon with an Andal maiden he took as his wife, thus earning Durran his nickname. He followed the example of his father and also took a wife of pure Andal blood. During his reign, and the following ones, Andal warlords became lords and petty kings and married the daughters of Stormlords and gave them their daughters in return, swearing fealty and their swords for lands. </p>
<p>King <b>Durran Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Durran the Third</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon. He attempted two invasions of Dorne, but was thrown back by Nymeria. </p>
<p>King <b>Durwald I Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Durwald the Fat</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon. During his long rule House Massey broke away from the Kingdom of the Storm, Tarth revolted thrice, and at Cape Wrath a woods witch known only as the Green Queen held the rainwood for the best part of a generation. Thus, it was said that Durwald's rule extended no farther than the distance a man could urinate off the walls of Storm's End. </p>
<p>The <b>dusky woman</b> is a comely mute. She was a gift from Euron Greyjoy to his brother Victarion Greyjoy prior to Victarion embarking with the Iron Fleet for Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Dyah</b> is a wildling. She is one of the nineteen wives of Craster. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Dyanna Dayne</b> was a member of House Dayne during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. She married Daeron's fourth son, Prince Maekar, and together they had six children: Daeron, Aerion, Aemon, Aegon, Daella and Rhae Targaryen. She died before 209&nbsp;AC, well before Maekar's ascendance to the Iron Throne in 221&nbsp;AC, thus she never became queen consort. </p>
<p><b>Dykk Harlaw</b> is an ironborn raider from House Harlaw. His relation to Lord Rodrik Harlaw, the head of the house, is currently unknown. </p>
<p><b>Dywen</b> is a veteran ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Dywen Shell</b> was a petty king of the First Men from House Shell who claimed the title King of the Fingers before the Andal invasion. </p>
<p><b>Earl Harlaw</b> is a member of House Harlaw and one of the crew on Asha Greyjoys ship <i>Black Wind</i>. His relation to Lord Rodrik Harlaw, the head of the house, is currently unknown. </p>
<p><b>Easy</b> is a steward of the Night's Watch. He is half-mad, believing himself to be Florian the Fool reborn. </p>
<p><b>Ebben</b> (or <b>Eggen</b>) is a veteran ranger of the Night's Watch stationed at the Shadow Tower. </p>
<p><b>Ebrose</b> is the archmaester at the Citadel who tests novices seeking their link in the arts of healing. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Jim Broadbent. </p>
<p>The <b>Citadel</b> is a complex of buildings in Oldtown that serves as the central home to the order of the maesters. The name is also employed to refer to order of maesters as an institution, or the higher placed members. At the Citadel, the residing archmaesters teach and train new students, and convene in the Conclave. The Citadel is funded by taxes from Oldtown and payments from lords for the service of maesters. Maesters rigorously copy books at the Citadel. Leyton Hightower, the Lord of Oldtown, includes Protector of the Citadel among his titles. </p>
<p><b>Eddara Tallhart</b> is the daughter of Ser Helman Tallhart. </p>
<p><b>Eddard Karstark</b>, affectionately called <b>Edd</b> by his sister Alys, is the second son of Lord Rickard Karstark of Karhold. He is named after Eddard Stark. </p>
<p><b>Eddard Stark</b>, also called <b>"Ned"</b>, is the head of House Stark, Lord of Winterfell, and Warden of the North. He is a close friend to King Robert I Baratheon, with whom he was raised. Eddard is one of the major POV characters in <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>. </p>
<p><b>Winterfell</b> is the ancestral castle and seat of power of House Stark and is considered to be the capital of the north. It is in the center of the northernmost province of the Seven Kingdoms, on the kingsroad that runs from Storm's End to the Wall. It is situated at the eastern edge of the wolfswood, north of the western branch of the White Knife and Castle Cerwyn. Winterfell is south of the northern mountains and southwest of Long Lake, one hundred leagues (three hundred miles) southeast of Deepwood Motte. </p>
<p>King <b>Edderion Stark</b>, better known as <b>Edderion the Bridegroom</b>, was King in the North. He is buried in the crypts beneath Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Eddie</b> is a man-at-arms in service to House Lannister. He was specifically created for a cameo by Ed Sheeran in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Eddison Peake</b>, known as <b>Eddison the Elder</b>, was a Lord of Starpike. He was an illustrious and legendary ancestor of House Peake. </p>
<p><b>Eddison Peake</b>, known as <b>Eddison the Younger</b>, was a Lord of Starpike. He was an illustrious and legendary ancestor of House Peake. </p>
