<p>Ser <b>Edmure Tully</b> is a knight from House Tully of Riverrun, the liege lords of the riverlands. He is the heir of Hoster Tully, the Lord Paramount of the Trident, and Lady Minisa Whent, and the younger brother of Catelyn Stark and Lysa Arryn. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> Edmure is portrayed by Tobias Menzies. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Edmure Tully</b> was the head of House Tully and the father of Axel Tully, who would become the first Lord of Riverrun. </p>
<p><b>Edmyn Tully</b> was the Lord of Riverrun and the head of House Tully during Aegon's Conquest. The first of the riverlords to join Aegon the Conqueror against King Harren Hoare, Aegon rewarded Edmyn by raising him to Lord Paramount of the Trident when Harren and his line perished. </p>
<p><b>Riverrun</b> is the ancestral castle of House Tully, the Lords Paramount of the Trident. It is situated in the western riverlands, at the confluence of the Tumblestone and Red Fork rivers. Riverrun is north of Pinkmaiden and northwest of Acorn Hall. The castle sits along the river road, an easy ride which links Lannisport and the crossroads. </p>
<p><b>Edric Baratheon</b> was the thirdborn son of Lord Stannis Baratheon and Lady Selyse Florent in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. He was stillborn. </p>
<p><b>Edric Dayne</b>, also known as <b>Ned</b>, is the Lord of Starfall and head of House Dayne. His father, whose name is unknown, was the elder brother of Ser Arthur, Lady Ashara, and Lady Allyria Dayne. </p>
<p><b>Starfall</b> is the ancestral castle of House Dayne in Dorne. </p>
<p><b>Edric Stark</b> was a Lord of Winterfell and head of House Stark during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Edric Stark</b> was the third son of Lord Cregan Stark, second by his last wife Lynara Stark. He was married to Serena Stark, the daughter of his half-brother Rickon Stark, they had four children; twin sons Cregard and Torrhen, and two daughters Aregelle and Arrana Stark. </p>
<p><b>Edric Storm</b> is the bastard son of King Robert I Baratheon and Delena Florent. </p>
<p><b>Edrick Stark</b>, known as <b>Edrick Snowbeard</b>, was a King in the North from House Stark. </p>
<p><b>Edwell Celtigar</b> was Lord of Claw Isle and head of House Celtigar during the reigns of kings Maegor I and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Edwina Royce</b> is a member of House Royce mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Edwyd Fossoway</b> is a knight from House Fossoway of Cider Hall. </p>
<p><b>House Fossoway of Cider Hall</b> is a noble house from the Reach, one of the principal bannermen sworn to House Tyrell. Cider Hall is located at the fork of the Mander and the Cockleswent. Their banner is a red apple over a golden field. Their words are "<i>A Taste of Glory</i>". </p>
<p><b>Edwyle Stark</b> was the Lord of Winterfell and the head of House Stark during the late reign of King Maekar I Targaryen and the reign of King Aegon V Targaryen. He was the only son of Lord Willam Stark and his second wife, Lady Melantha Blackwood. </p>
<p><b>Edwyn Frey</b> is a member of House Frey. He is the eldest son of Ser Ryman Frey, a grandson of Ser Stevron Frey, and a great-grandson of Walder Frey, Lord of the Crossing. </p>
<p><b>Edwyn Osgrey</b> was a knight of House Osgrey during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. He was the eldest son of Ser Eustace Osgrey. </p>
<p>The <b>Redgrass Field</b> is the site of the Battle of the Redgrass Field. It was an unnamed field before the battle. It was renamed the Redgrass Field after the battle for the color grass had been stained by the blood. </p>
<p>King <b>Edwyn Stark</b>, better known as <b>Edwyn the Spring King</b>, was a King in the North. He is buried in the crypt of Winterfell and has a statue. </p>
<p><b>Edwyn Tarth</b>, known as <b>Edwyn Evenstar</b>, was a King of Tarth from House Tarth. </p>
<p><b>Edyth</b> was a novice, and later septa, who was a beloved religious tutor of Queen Alysanne Targaryen. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Egbert</b> is a maester of the Citadel. He wrote the book <i>Justice and Injustice in the North: Judgments of Three Stark Lords</i>. </p>
<p><b>Eggon</b> is an armsman in service to Ser Gregor Clegane. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gregor Clegane</b> is the Knight of Clegane's Keep and the head of House Clegane, a landed knight and bannerman to House Lannister of Casterly Rock. Gregor is a freakishly large man and for this he is often called <b>the Mountain That Rides</b> or simply <b>the Mountain</b>. His soldiers are known as the Mountain's men. </p>
<p><b>Eglantine</b> is a septa of the Faith of the Seven. She is the personal septa of Princess Myrcella Baratheon. </p>
<p><b>Egon Emeros</b>, also known as <b>Egon Emeros the Exquisite</b>, is a member of the Pureborn of Qarth. </p>
<p><b>Eladon Goldenhair</b> is an Unsullied sworn to Daenerys Targaryen. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Elaena Targaryen</b> was the third daughter and youngest child of King Aegon III Targaryen and his wife, Queen Daenaera Velaryon. </p>
<p><b>Elaena Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen during the Century of Blood, the eldest daughter of Lord Gaemon and Lady Daenys Targaryen of Dragonstone. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Elbert Arryn</b> was a knight of House Arryn and nephew of Lord Jon Arryn. At the time of his death he was the heir to the Vale of Arryn. </p>
<p>The <b>Elder Brother</b> is the leader of a septry on the Quiet Isle. He is reputed to have powers as a healer. This elder brother's given name is unknown. </p>
<p>The <b>Elder Brother</b> or <b>elder brother</b> is the senior contemplative brother at septries of the Faith of the Seven. At septries where brothers take vows of silence, only the Elder Brother and his proctors may speak. </p>
<p>The <b>Quiet Isle</b> is an upthrust island that sits at the mouth of the Trident where it flows into the Bay of Crabs, southeast of Saltpans and northwest of Maidenpool. Its septry is a refuge for those sworn to the Faith of the Seven. Septon Meribald has often visited the isle. </p>
<p>An <b>old man</b> is a ship insurer operating in Braavos. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Eldiss</b> was an ironborn sailor. He had a brother, Skyte. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Eldon Estermont</b> is a knight of House Estermont. He is around seventy years old. He is Lord of Greenstone in <i>A Feast for Crows</i>. </p>
<p><b>Greenstone</b> is the seat of House Estermont on the island of Estermont in the stormlands. </p>
<p><b>Eldred Codd</b> is an ironborn raider and a member of House Codd. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Eldric Arryn</b> was a knight from House Arryn during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. He attempted to claim the Eyrie for his father, Ser Arnold Arryn. </p>
<p><b>Eldrick Sarsfield</b> is a knight of House Sarsfield who appears in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Eleanor Mooton</b> is the eldest daughter of Lord William Mooton of Maidenpool, and his heir. She has at least two brothers and an unknown number of sisters. </p>
<p><b>Eleanor Swann</b> was a Lady of Stonehelm mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Elena Egen</b> is the mother of Yohn Royce, mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Elenda Baratheon</b>, née <b>Elenda Caron</b>, was the Lady of Storm's End through her marriage to Lord Borros Baratheon during the Dance of the Dragons. During the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen, she ruled Storm's End as regent. </p>
<p><b>Elenei</b> is said to have been the daughter of the sea god and the goddess of the wind. According to legend, she married Durran Godsgrief, the first Storm King. </p>
<p><b>Lord Elesham</b> was a Lord of the Paps and the head of House Elesham. </p>
<p><b>Eleyna Westerling</b> is a member of House Westerling. She is the youngest daughter of Lord Gawen Westerling and Sybell Spicer. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Elia Nymeros Martell</b>, also known simply as <b>Elia Martell</b> or <b>Elia of Dorne</b> was a Dornish princess from House Martell. She was married to the crown prince, Rhaegar Targaryen, and by him birthed Rhaenys and Aegon. Elia was raped and murdered by Ser Gregor Clegane in the Sack of King's Landing during Robert's Rebellion. </p>
<p><b>Elia Sand</b>, known as <b>El</b> by her family and <b>Lady Lance</b> by others, is the oldest bastard daughter of Prince Oberyn Martell by his paramour, Ellaria Sand. She is one of the Sand Snakes. </p>
<p><b>Elinda Massey</b> was a noblewoman of House Massey and a lady-in-waiting to Queen Rhaenyra Targaryen during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Elinor Costayne</b> was a member of House Costayne and one of the many brides of King Maegor I Targaryen. Along with Lady Jeyne Westerling and Princess Rhaena Targaryen, she was one of the so-called "Black Brides". </p>
<p><b>Elinor Massey</b> was a member of House Massey during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Elinor Tyrell</b> is a member of a junior branch of House Tyrell, and a lady-in-waiting of Lady Margaery Tyrell. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Elissa Farman</b> was a noblewoman of House Farman and the daughter of Lord Marq Farman during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Maester <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Elkin is a maester from the Citadel at Oldtown. He has translated <i>The Red Book</i>, many centuries after it was originally written. </p>
<p><b>Ella Broome</b> was a lady of House Broome. She was the younger sister of Lady Lucinda Tully. </p>
<p><b>Ella Lannister</b> is a member of House Lannister of Lannisport. It is currently unknown if she is still alive in the main series. </p>
<p><b>Ellard Stark</b> was the Lord of Winterfell and the head of House Stark during the late reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Ellard Crane</b> was a member of House Crane during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Ellaria Sand</b> is the beloved paramour of Prince Oberyn Martell, and the mother of the four youngest "Sand Snakes," Oberyn's bastard daughters. Ellaria herself is the bastard daughter of Harmen Uller, Lord of Hellholt. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Indira Varma. </p>
<p><br> <b>Ellendor</b> was a maester of the Citadel. He was made Grand Maester when he was close to 90 years old and was sent to serve the court of King Aegon V Targaryen in King's Landing. He succeeded Grand Maester Kaeth. He died within a year of being made Grand Maester and was succeeded by Grand Maester Merion. </p>
<p><b>Ellery Vance</b> is a knight from House Vance of Atranta and the third son of Lord Norbert Vance. He has four brothers; Ser Ronald, Ser Hugo, Ser Kirth and Maester Jon. </p>
<p><b>Ellyn Baratheon</b> was a noblewoman from House Baratheon during the reign of kings Viserys I, Aegon II and Aegon III Targaryen. She was one of the four daughters of Lord Borros Baratheon of Storm's End. She and her sisters were known as the Four Storms. </p>
<p><b>Ellyn Caron</b> was the Lady of the Marches, Lady of Nightsong, and the head of House Caron during the early reign of Aenys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Ellyn Ever Sweet</b> is a legendary daughter of Garth Greenhand and mother of House Beesbury. According to legend, she loved honey so much she sought the King of the Bees in his vast mountain hive and made pact with him, to care for his children and his children's children for all time, becoming the first beekeeper. </p>
<p><b>Ellyn Reyne</b>, also known as <b>Ellyn Tarbeck</b>, was a noblewoman of House Reyne who married into first House Lannister and later House Tarbeck. She was the daughter of Lord Robert Reyne and the sister of Lord Roger Reyne, the Red Lion of Castemere, and Ser Reynard Reyne. </p>
<p><b>Elmar Frey</b> is a member of House Frey and is the youngest son of Lord Walder Frey. Elmar is the twenty-second-born son of Walder and the fourth son born of Walder's marriage to Annara Farring. </p>
<p><b>Elmo Tully</b> was the Lord of Riverrun and head of House Tully during the Dance of the Dragons, briefly succeeding his grandfather, Lord Grover Tully, before passing away forty-nine days later. </p>
<p><b>Elric Stark</b> was a member of House Stark. He was the third son of Bennard Stark and Lady Margaret Karstark. </p>
<p><b>Elron</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Elston Tully</b> was Lord of Riverrun during the reign of Humfrey I Teague. When King Humfrey attempted to suppress the worship of the old gods, Lord Elston rose in rebellion along with Lord Roderick Blackwood. He did not survive to see the end of the rebellion and the extinction of House Teague. </p>
<p><b>Elwood</b> is a guard at Riverrun. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Elwood Blackbar</b> was a knight of House Blackbar during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Elwood Harte</b> is a knight from House Harte. </p>
<p><b>Elwood Meadows</b> is the Lord of Grassfield Keep and the head of House Meadows. He is a cousin of the Fossoways. </p>
<p><b>Elyana Vypren</b> is a member of House Vypren, a daughter of Lord Lucias Vypren. She is married to Ser Jon Wylde and has one child, Rickard Wylde. </p>
<p><b>Elyas Willum</b> is the son of Lord Willum. He has one brother, Josua. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Elyas Scales</b> was a knight from House Scales in service to House Targaryen. He was the master-at-arms at Dragonstone during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Elyn Norridge</b> is a member of House Norridge and the wife of Ser Luthor Tyrell. They have three children, Ser Theodore, Olene, and Medwick Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Elys Arryn</b> was a member of House Arryn during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Elys Waynwood</b> was a knight from House Waynwood. He was the uncle of the current head of the House, Lady Anya Waynwood. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Elys Westerling</b> was a knight from House Westerling during the reign of Aerys II Targaryen. His relation to Gawen Westerling, the Lord of the Crag, is unknown. </p>

<p><b>Elysar</b> was a maester of the Citadel who served as Grand Maester during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Elza</b> (or <b>Ella</b>) was a very fine weaver slave from Meereen owned by Grazdan zo Galare. </p>
<p><b>Emberlei Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, the third daughter of Lothar Frey and Leonella Lefford. </p>
<p><b>Emerick Peake</b>, known as <b>Emerick the Avenger</b>, was a Lord of Starpike. He was an illustrious and legendary ancestor of House Peake. </p>
<p><b>Emilia Blackbrow</b> is a member of House Blackbrow mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. She may or may not be still alive, as she was born sometime in the middle of the third century. </p>
<p><b>Emilia Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Emma</b> is one of the oldest servers at the Quill and Tankard, a drinking tavern in Oldtown. She has a daughter, Rosey. </p>
<p><b>Emmett</b>, called <b>Iron Emmett</b>, is a young ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Emmon Cuy</b>, also known as <b>Emmon the Yellow</b>, is a knight of House Cuy. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Emmon Frey</b> is a knight from House Frey and is the second son of Lord Walder Frey and Lady Perra Royce. He is married to Lady Genna Lannister, with whom he has four sons: Cleos, Lyonel, Tion, and Walder. </p>
<p><b>Emmond</b> is a boy of the Iron Islands whom Aeron Greyjoy drowns and brings back to life. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Emory Hill</b>, called the <b>Bastard of Lannisport</b>, was a knight from the westerlands, likely a bastard of the Lannisters of Lannisport. </p>
<p><b>Emphyria Vance</b> is a noblewoman of House Vance of Wayfarer's Rest. She is the third and youngest daughter of the heir of Wayfarer's Rest, Ser Karyl Vance. </p>
<p><b>Emrick</b> is a Night's Watch recruit. He is the twin brother of Arron, and is from Fair Isle. </p>
<p><b>Endehar</b> is an ironborn raider. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Endrew Tarth</b> is a knight from House Tarth and member of the Night's Watch. His relation to Lord Selwyn Tarth of Evenfall is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Enger</b> is a guard at Riverrun. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Eon</b> is a maester of the Citadel of Oldtown. He wrote <i>Account of the War of the Ninepenny Kings</i>, filled with details on the fighting that occured. The book is considered one of the finest works of its kind. </p>
<p><b>Eon Hunter</b> is the Lord of Longbow Hall and the head of House Hunter. He has three quarrelsome sons: Gilwood, Eustace and Harlan Hunter. </p>
<p><b>Longbow Hall</b> is the seat of House Hunter in the Vale of Arryn. It is located south of the Fingers, east of Heart's Home, and north of Old Anchor. It appears to be located in the foothills between a mountain range and the east of the valley. Willamen is the maester at Longbow Hall. </p>
<p><b>Erena Glover</b> is the daughter of Robett and Sybelle Glover. </p>
<p><b>Erich Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Erich Kin-Killer</b>, was a member of House Durrandon who slew his own brother, King Durran. Scholars debate whether this King Durran, who had become besotted with Erich's daughter, was the same as King Durran the Young. </p>
<p>King <b>Erich III Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Erich the Sailmaker</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon. He was the first to claim Estermont and the lesser isles farther south for the Kingdom of the Storm. Scholars speculate he was most likely <b>Erich III</b>. He was the grandson of King Durran the Fair. </p>
<p>King <b>Erich VII Durrandon</b>, also known as <b>Erich the Unready</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon during the beginnings of the Andal invasion. He took little note of the invaders, declaring he had no interest in "the quarrels of strangers in a land far away", as he was embroiled in his own war to reconquer Massey's Hook from pirate king Justin Milk-Eye and whilst fending off incursions of King Olyvar Yronwood. He died while the Andals conquered the Vale. His grandson was Qarlton II Durrandon. </p>
<p><b>Erich Hoare</b>, known as <b>Erich the Eagle</b>, was an ironborn raider from House Hoare. He was a grandson of Harrag Hoare, a King of the Iron Islands. Erich led an attack against the western shores of the north, which had been liberated from occupation by King Theon Stark. </p>
<p><b>Erich I Greyiron</b>, known as <b>Erich the Ugly</b>, was a High King of the Iron Islands from House Greyiron. He was the son of Urras Greyiron, the first High King. </p>
<p><b>Erich V Harlaw</b> was a High King of the Iron Islands from House Harlaw. </p>
<p><b>Erich Blackbrow</b> was a member of House Blackbrow mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Erik Ironmaker</b>, known as <b>Erik the Just</b> and <b>Erik Anvil-Breaker</b>, is an ironborn raider and the head of House Ironmaker. </p>
<p><b>Erik Ironmaker</b>, known as <b>Erik the Just</b> and <b>Erik Anvil-Breaker</b>, is an ironborn raider and the head of House Ironmaker. </p>
<p><b>Ermesande Hayford</b> is the Lady of Hayford and the head of House Hayford, a noble house of the crownlands. She is still a baby and is the last of her line. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ernest Dabell</b> was a knight during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. He had two brothers: Ser Lester and Ser Pascal Dabell. </p>
<p><b>Eroeh</b> is a Lhazareen girl who lives in Lhazar. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Erreck</b> is the bastard son of a hedge knight. He is considered to have considerable ability as a maester. </p>
<p><b>Erreg the Kinslayer</b> was a legendary Andal king. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Erren Florent</b> is knight of House Florent, the son of Ser Ryam Florent and brother to Selyse and Imry. Erren is brother-in-law to Stannis Baratheon. </p>
<p><b>Errok</b> is a wildling raider. He is a thin man. He is quiet. </p>
<p><b>Errold Stark</b> was a member of House Stark. He was the fourth son of Lord Beron Stark and wife, Lady Lorra Royce. He had three older brothers (Donnor, Willam and Artos), two older sisters (Berena and Alysanne), and one younger brother (Rodrik). </p>
<p><b>Erryk</b> is a guardsman for Olenna Tyrell, the dowager Lady of Highgarden. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Erryk Cargyll</b> was a knight from House Cargyll. He and his twin brother, Ser Arryk Cargyll, were members of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Viserys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Mutual exhaustion and negotiated peace: </p>
<p>Ser <b>Erwin Lannister</b> was a knight from House Lannister during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Esgred</b> is the mother of Sigrin, a shipwright at Lordsport. He named the first ship that he built after her. </p>
<p><b>Essie</b> was a whore in the House of Kisses and the mother of Gaemon Palehair. During the Moon of the Three Kings, Essie declared Gaemon was a bastard of King Aegon II Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>Estermont female cousin</b> of King Robert I Baratheon is a noblewoman of House Estermont. </p>
<p><b>Ethan Glover</b> was a member of House Glover during the reign of King Aerys II Targaryen. He was the squire for Brandon Stark, the heir of Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Ethelide Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>A <b>eunuch strangler</b> is one of the foul-looking, impotent mercenaries that Varys gets for Tyrion Lannister to guard Shae's manse in King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Euron Greyjoy</b>, known as <b>Crow's Eye</b> and <b>Euron Crow's Eye</b>, is a member of House Greyjoy and is the eldest of Lord Balon Greyjoy's younger brothers. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Pilou Asbæk. </p>
<p><b>Eustace</b> is a disgraced and defrocked septon of the Faith of the Seven who used to be attached to the Sept-Beyond-the-Sea in Braavos. </p>
<p><b>Eustace</b> was a septon attached to the royal sept of the Red Keep during the reign of King Viserys I Targaryen. The writings of Eustace, among them <i>The Reign of King Viserys, First of His Name, and the Dance of the Dragons That Came After</i>, were used as a source for <i>The Princess and the Queen</i> as well as <i>The Rogue Prince</i> by Archmaester Gyldayn. Eventually, he rose to the ranks of the Most Devout. </p>
<p><b>Eustace Brune</b> is Lord of the Dyre Den and head of House Brune of the Dyre Den. He is the cousin of Ser Bennard Brune, the Knight of Brownhollow. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Eustace Hightower</b> was a knight from House Hightower during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. He was a grandson of Lord Donnel Hightower and an accomplished mariner. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Eustace Hunter</b> is a knight from House Hunter. He is the second son of Lord Eon Hunter. </p>
<p><b>Eon Hunter</b> is the Lord of Longbow Hall and the head of House Hunter. He has three quarrelsome sons: Gilwood, Eustace and Harlan Hunter. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Eustace Osgrey</b> was the head of House Osgrey during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. The landed knight held Standfast in the Reach and became Lord of Coldmoat after wedding Lady Rohanne Webber. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Evlyn</b> is a maester of the Citadel. He opposes Archmaester Harmune's belief that the Andals carved axes as a symbol of the Faith of the Seven in addition to seven-pointed stars, only for the latter to gain greater devotion whereas the former fell by the wayside. Evlyn argues that what Harmune calls axes were in fact hammers, the sign of the Smith, explaining the irregularity of the depictions of these hammers as the results of the Andals being warriors, not artisans. </p>
<p><b>Eyron</b> is an archmaester of the Citadel. He wrote that the crannogmen of old believed their Marsh Kings were the first among equals and that they were influenced by the old gods. </p>
<p>King <b>Eyron Stark</b> was King in the North. He is buried in the crypts beneath Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Ezzara</b> is a Ghiscari priestess of Meereen. She is a Blue Grace. </p>
<p><b>Ezzelyno</b> is a red priest of R'hllor in Braavos, who is oft drunk, yet cheerful. </p>
<p><b>R'hllor</b>, also known as the <b>Lord of Light</b>, the <b>Heart of Fire</b>, the <b>God of Flame and Shadow</b>, is a prominent god in Essos, but has only a few followers in Westeros, where he is more commonly known as the <b>red god</b>. His symbol is a fiery heart. Red priests lead prayers to R'hllor at red temples. </p>
<p><b>Faezhar zo Faez</b> is a Yunkai'i nobleman. The men of the Windblown mock him as <b>the Rabbit</b>. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Falena Stokeworth</b> was a noblewoman of House Stokeworth during the reigns of kings Viserys I, Aegon II, Aegon III, Daeron I, Baelor I, Viserys II and Aegon IV Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Falia Flowers</b> is the bastard daughter of Lord Humfrey Hewett. Falia is made to be a servant in Lord Hewett's castle by her trueborn sisters and her step-mother. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Falyse Stokeworth</b> is the heir of Lady Tanda Stokeworth of Stokeworth. She has been married to Ser Balman Byrch for ten years, but they remain childless. </p>
<p><b>Stokeworth</b>, also known as <b>Castle Stokeworth</b>, is the seat of House Stokeworth in the crownlands. It lies north of King's Landing, and south of Duskendale. The maester at Stokeworth is Frenken. </p>
<p><b>Farlen</b> is the kennelmaster at Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Lord Farman</b> was the Lord of Fair Isle and the head of House Farman during the Dance of the Dragons. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p>The <b>fat fellow</b> is a secret servant of the Many-Faced God in the House of Black and White in Braavos and a Faceless Man. </p>
<p><b>Fearless Ithoke</b> is a pit fighter famed in Meereen. His origin is unknown, but he supports the pit fighting culture of the city. </p>
<p><b>Lady Fell</b> was the Lady of Felwood and the head of House Fell during the reigns of kings Viserys I and Aegon II Targaryen. Her given name is unknown. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Fell</b> was the Lord of Felwood and the head of House Fell during the reign of King Aerys II Targaryen, and the early stages of Robert's Rebellion. His given name is not yet known. </p>
<p><b>Silveraxe</b> was the nickname of a famous member of House Fell during Robert's Rebellion. His given name is not yet known. </p>
<p><b>Fergon Hoare</b>, known as <b>Fergon the Fierce</b>, was a King of the Iron Islands from House Hoare. The Hoare kings of his era were opposed by the priests of the Drowned God because of their support for the Faith of the Seven, discouraging of reaving, and promotion of trade. </p>
<p><b>Fern</b> is a peasant who lives in Lambswold in the riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Ferny</b> is a wildling. She was the wife of Craster until he died. She is an old woman. </p>
<p><b>Ferrego Antaryon</b> is a member of House Antaryon who serves as the current Sealord of Braavos. Qarro Volentin is the current First Sword of Braavos, his protector. The Sealord's pleasure barge is decorated with laughing faces. </p>
<p><b>Ferret</b> was a child from King's Landing during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. He was both a beggar and a thief. </p>
<p><b>Ferris Fowler</b> was a King of Stone and Sky from House Fowler in Dorne. </p>
<p><b>Fingers</b> is an ironman and one of the crew on Asha Greyjoy's ship, <i>Black Wind</i>. </p>
<p><b>Finn Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>The <b>First King</b> was a sovereign who once reigned supreme over all First Men and led them to Westeros, according to legends from the north. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Flement Brax</b> is a knight from House Brax and the third son of Lord Andros Brax. He is married to Morya Frey and they have three sons together: Robert, Walder and Jon. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Florence Fossoway</b> was a noblewoman of House Fossoway during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. She was married to Lord Martyn Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Lord Florent</b> was the Lord of Brightwater Keep and the head of House Florent during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Florian</b>, called <b>Florian the Fool</b>, is a legendary hero of the riverlands from the Age of Heroes. He is known for falling in love with a maiden named Jonquil. </p>
<p><b>Florian Greysteel</b> was a knight and the personal champion of Manfryd Mooton, Lord of Maidenpool, during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Florian V Mooton</b>, known as <b>Florian the Brave</b>, was a petty king of Maidenpool from House Mooton. </p>
<p><b>Floris Baratheon</b> was a noblewoman from House Baratheon during the reign of kings Viserys I, Aegon II and Aegon III Targaryen. She was one of the four daughters of Lord Borros Baratheon of Storm's End. She and her sisters were known as the Four Storms. </p>
<p><b>Florys the Fox</b> is a legendary daughter of Garth Greenhand and the cleverest of his children. According to myth, she kept three husbands, each ignorant of the existence of the other two. Her sons became the founders of House Florent, House Ball and House Peake. In some tales of the Reach, Lann the Clever was a bastard born to Florys or her sister, Rowan Gold-Tree. </p>
<p><b>Flynn Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Fogo</b> is the <i>khalakka</i>, or son and heir of Khal Ogo. </p>
<p><b>Lord Follard</b> was the head of House Follard during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Fomas</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel. He wrote the book <i>Lies of the Ancients</i>. He argues that the mythic Others were nothing more than a tribe of First Men established on the far north and forced by the Long Night to engage in conquests to the south, becoming monstrous in tales told thereafter by House Stark and the Night's Watch to give themselves a heroic background as saviors of mankind. </p>
<p><b>Lord Footly</b> was the head of House Footly and Lord of Tumbleton during the Dance of the Dragons. His given name has not been revealed. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Forley Prester</b> is a knight of House Prester. He is a cousin to Garrison Prester, Lord of Feastfires. According to a semi-canon source, he is the heir presumptive to Feastfires. </p>
<p><b>Fornio</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Forrest Frey</b>, called <b>Fool Frey</b>, was the head of House Frey and the Lord of the Crossing during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Forzho</b> is a Dothraki <i>khal</i> appearing in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Foss the Archer</b> is a legendary son of Garth Greenhand and founder of House Fossoway of Cider Hall. He was renowned for shooting apples off the head of any maid who took his fancy. </p>
<p>The <b>Fossoway twins</b> were members of House Fossoway of Cider Hall during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. Their given names have not been revealed. </p>
<p><b>Fralegg the Strong</b> is an ironborn raider and captain. </p>
<p><b>Franklyn Farman</b> was the first-born son and heir of Lord Marq Farman of Fair Isle. He became the head of House Farman and Lord of Fair Isle during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Franklyn Flowers</b>, also known as the <b>Bastard of Cider Hall</b>, is a knight in service to the Golden Company. </p>
<p><b>Franklyn Fowler</b>, called <b>the Old Hawk</b>, is the Lord of Skyreach and the head of House Fowler. He also holds the title Warden of the Prince's Pass. He is the father of the Fowler twins. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Franklyn Frey</b> was a knight from House Frey and the brother to Lord Frey of the Crossing during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. He was considered a good tourney fighter. </p>
<p><b>Fredo Rogare</b> was a member of House Rogare, a Lysene noble banking family. He was the son of Lysandro Rogare, the First Magister of Lys. </p>
<p><b>Frenken</b> is the maester assigned to House Stokeworth of Stokeworth. </p>
<p><b>Frenya</b> is a wildling spearwife. </p>
<p>A <b>spearwife</b> is a free folk woman who is also a warrior. </p>
<p><b>Lady Frey</b> was a member of House Frey, the daughter of Lord Frey of the Crossing, elder sister to Walder Frey, niece to Ser Franklyn Frey, and cousin to Ser Addam Frey. When she was fifteen, she married Lord Ambrose Butterwell at Whitewalls in 212&nbsp;AC, becoming his second wife. </p>
<p><b>Lord Frey</b> was the Lord of the Crossing and the head of House Frey during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Freya Frey</b> is a granddaughter of Lord Walder Frey in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Frynne</b> is the daughter of a smith in Dorne. </p>
<p><b>Fulk the Flea</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Gael Targaryen</b> was the thirteenth and last child of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Queen Alysanne Targaryen. Born during winter, Gael was also called <b>the Winter Child</b>. </p>
<p><b>Gaemon Palehair</b> was a pretender king during the Dance of the Dragons. His mother Essie, a whore in the House of Kisses, claimed he was a bastard son of Aegon II Targaryen. After the war, Gaemon became the cupbearer, food taster, and whipping boy of his friend, King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Gaemon Targaryen</b>, known as <b>Gaemon the Glorious</b>, was the second Lord of Dragonstone of House Targaryen. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Gaemon Targaryen</b> was the eleventh child of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Queen Alysanne Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Gage</b> is the head cook at Winterfell. He has a daughter, Turnip. </p>
<p><b>Galazza Galare</b> is the Green Grace, the high priestess of the Ghiscari Temple of the Graces in Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Galbart Glover</b> is the head of House Glover and Master of Deepwood Motte. He is unwed. Larence Snow, the bastard of Hornwood, is a ward of Galbart. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Galbart is portrayed by Mark Coney. </p>
<p><b>Deepwood Motte</b>, sometimes called simply <b>Deepwood</b>, is the seat of House Glover in the north. It is a wooden motte-and-bailey castle. It lies in the northern wolfswood, east of Sea Dragon Point. North of Deepwood Motte lie tidal flats leading to the Bay of Ice. Deepwood is five leagues south of the sea and one hundred leagues (three hundred miles) northwest of Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Galendro</b> was an historian who wrote the book <i>The Fires of the Freehold</i> recording the History of Valyria. No complete copy of the book is known to Westeros - even the Citadel's copy lacks 27 scrolls. </p>
<p><b>Galeo</b> is a sausage-maker from Braavos. He is one of the regulars at the Gate. It is said that the only meat he puts in his sausages is rat. He wears a greasy leather apron. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Galladon of Morne</b>, called the <b>Perfect Knight</b>, was a legendary knight from Morne on the isle of Tarth. Many nobles and smallfolk from the island claim to be descended from him. </p>
<p><b>Galladon Tarth</b> was the only son of Lord Selwyn Tarth of Evenfall. He was presumably named after Ser Galladon of Morne, a legendary figure of the island of Tarth. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Gallard</b> is an archmaester at the Citadel in Oldtown. He is the author of <i>Children of Summer</i>, the chief source on the history of the Summer Isles in the Seven Kingdoms, which he wrote after translating the highly complicated, formal verses narrating Summer Islander history carved on the Talking Trees of Tall Trees Town. </p>
<p><b>Galon Whitestaff</b> was a priest of the Drowned God who lived during the Age of Heroes. </p>
<p><b>Galt</b> is a member of the Stone Crows, one of the Vale mountain clans. </p>
<p>The <b>Stone Crows</b> are one of the mountain clans that inhabit the Mountains of the Moon, in the Vale of Arryn. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Galtry the Green</b> was a hedge knight during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. He bore nine jade mullets upon a field of leek-green as his coat-of-arms. </p>
<p><b>Galyeon of Cuy</b> is a singer from Cuy in the Reach. He is renowned for the length of his songs. </p>
<p><b>Gared</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is portrayed by Dermot Keaney. </p>
<p><b>Gareth</b> was a maester who wrote the book <i>Red Sands</i>. In it, he chronicles several Dornish letters, which suggest that it was Lord Qorgyle of Sandstone who had arranged the murder of Lord Lyonel Tyrell during the conquest of Dorne. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gareth Clifton</b> is a knight and the head House Clifton. He is sworn to the Farmans of Fair Isle. He is married to Jeyne Farman, the sister of Lord Sebaston Farman. They have twelve children. </p>
<p><b>Gareth II Gardener</b>, called <b>the Grim</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gareth Long</b> was a knight and master-at-arms in the service of House Peake during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. It is unconfirmed if he was from House Long, a family from the north. </p>
<p><b>Gareth the Grey</b> was a knight in support of Daemon Blackfyre during the First Blackfyre Rebellion. He was considered one of the finest knights of his time. </p>
<p><b>Gareth Tyrell</b> was a head of House Tyrell and the first High Steward of Highgarden for House Gardener. He was the second son of Ser Alester Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Gareth Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Gargon Qoherys</b>, also known as <b>Gargon the Guest</b>, was the Lord of Harrenhal and head of House Qoherys during the reigns of kings Aegon I and Aenys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garibald</b> is a sellsword of the Second Sons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garibald Grey</b> was a knight from House Grey during the Targaryen civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garibald of the Seven Stars</b>, known as <b>the septon knight</b>, was a septon knight of the Warrior's Sons at the start of the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garibald Shells</b> is a young knight from Sunspear. </p>
<p>Wisdom <b>Garigus</b> was a member of the Alchemists' Guild of King's Landing during the reign of King Aerys II Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>Alchemists' Guild</b>, also called the <b>Guild of Alchemists</b>, is an old order of <b>pyromancers</b>. The guild, was once powerful, though in the recent centuries, the maesters have largely replaced the alchemist everywhere. The pyromancers claim to posses vast secret stores of knowledge. </p>
<p><b>Garin</b> is an orphan of the Greenblood. He is named after Prince Garin the Great, a famous leader of the Rhoynar. </p>
<p>The <b>Greenblood</b> is a river in southern Dorne. It takes its name from its murky green waters which are slow-moving and shallow. </p>
<p><b>Garin the Great</b> was a noble of the Rhoynar and the Prince of Chroyane. </p>
<p><b>Gariss</b> is a man sworn to House Stark. He is considered one of the better huntsmen of Winterfell. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Garizon</b> is an archmaester at the Citadel in Oldtown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garlan Tyrell</b>, known as <b>Garlan the Gallant</b>, is a knight of House Tyrell and the second son of Lord Mace Tyrell and Lady Alerie Hightower. His personal coat of arms is two golden roses on green, to denote his status as second son. </p>
<p><b>Garland II Gardener</b>, called <b>Garland the Bridegroom</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. </p>
<p><b>Garland VI Gardener</b> was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. During his minority, a member of House Tyrell ruled the Reach in his name as Regent. </p>
<p><b>Garmon Hightower</b> was a nobleman of House Hightower and a younger son of Lord Manfred Hightower. </p>
<p><b>Garmund Hightower</b> was a member of House Hightower during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garon Baratheon</b> was a knight from House Baratheon during the reigns of kings Aegon I, Aenys I, Maegor I and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. He was a younger brother of Lord Rogar Baratheon of Storm's End. </p>
<p><b>Garrett Flowers</b> is a bastard of House Tyrell, and the first cousin to Mace Tyrell, the current Lord of Highgarden. He is the youngest son of Garth Tyrell, and he has an older brother, Garse Flowers. </p>
<p><b>Garrett Greenspear</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Garrett Paege</b> is a squire from House Paege. He is the son of Ser Halmon Paege. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garrick Hall</b> was a landed knight from Middleton along the Blackwater Rush during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Garris</b>, called <b>Garris the Grey</b>, was a legendary Rhoynish prince of Ny Sar that drove the hairy men away from the land where Norvos stands today. After expelling the hairy men, the Rhoynar did not linger, preferring the more temperate climes of the lower river to the dark skies and cold winds of the hills. </p>
<p><b>Garrison Fowler</b>, known as the <b>Blind King</b>, was a head of House Fowler and was the last King of Stone and Sky in Dorne. </p>
<p><b>Garrison Prester</b> is the Lord of Feastfires and the head of House Prester. His cousin is Ser Forley Prester. </p>
<p><b>Garse</b> is a guardsman at Castle Black. </p>
<p><b>Garse Flowers</b> is a bastard of House Tyrell, and the first cousin to Mace Tyrell, the current Lord of Highgarden. He is the eldest son of Garth Tyrell, and he has a younger brother, Garrett Flowers. </p>
<p><b>Garse VII Gardener</b> was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener during the Century of Blood. His relation to King Mern IX Gardener is unknown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garse Goodbrook</b> is a knight of House Goodbrook. He is the husband of Kyra Frey with whom he has two children, Walder and Jeyne Goodbrook. His relation to Lord Lymond Goodbrook, the head of the House is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Garth of Greenaway</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. He comes from Greenaway. </p>
<p><b>Garth the Gardener</b> was the legendary first King of the Reach and the founder of House Gardener. </p>
<p><b>Garth III Gardener</b>, called <b>Garth the Great</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. He extended the borders of the Reach northward, winning Old Oak, Red Lake, and Goldengrove with pacts of friendship and mutual defense. In the annuals of history the name of Garth III is writ large. </p>
<p><b>Garth V Gardener</b> was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. He was dubbed <b>Hammer of the Dornish</b> for his legendary conflicts with Dornishmen. </p>
<p><b>Garth VI Gardener</b>, called <b>the Morningstar</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. He died in battle against the ironborn. </p>
<p><b>Garth VII Gardener</b>, called <b>the Goldenhand</b> or <b>Garth Goldenhand</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. He is considered the greatest Gardener King in the history of the Reach, for his deeds both in war and in peace. He became king at twelve and had reigned for eighty-one years when he died. </p>
<p><b>Garth IX Gardener</b> was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. Along with his son and grandson, he is remembered as one of the Three Sage Kings who dealt with the Andal invasion of the Reach with a policy of accord and assimilation rather then armed resistance. </p>
<p><b>Garth X Gardener</b>, called <b>Garth Greybeard</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. During his long reign House Gardener reached the nadir of its power. </p>
<p><b>Garth XI Gardener</b>, also known as <b>Garth the Painter</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. He was the son and successor of Mern VI Gardener. </p>
<p><b>Garth XII Gardener</b> was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garth Greenfield</b> is the Knight of Greenfield and head of House Greenfield. </p>
<p><b>Garth Greenhand</b>, also called <b>Garth Greenhair</b> and <b>Garth the Green</b>, was a mythical High King of the First Men and said to have been the common ancestor of numerous houses from the Reach. His firstborn son, Garth the Gardener, founded House Gardener, the Kings of the Reach. </p>
<p><b>Garth Greyfeather</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garth the Harelip</b> was a captain of the City Watch of King's Landing during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. The knight commanded the Dragon Gate. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garth Hightower</b>, called <b>Greysteel</b>, is a knight of House Hightower and the second son of Lord Leyton Hightower. </p>
<p><b>Garth of Oldtown</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. He comes from Oldtown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Garth Oldflowers</b> was a knight and member of House Oldflowers during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Garth Tyrell</b>, known as <b>Garth the Gross</b>, is a member of House Tyrell and an uncle of Lord Mace Tyrell of Highgarden. He serves his nephew as the Lord Seneschal. Garth has two bastard sons, Garse and Garrett Flowers. </p>
<p><b>Garth</b> is a gaoler, headsman, and torturer in the Wolf's Den at White Harbor. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gascoyne of the Greenblood</b> is a knight and the sworn shield of Prince Trystane Martell. He comes from the banks of the Greenblood. </p>
<p><b>Gaven Greywolf</b> was a First Men skinchanger who was killed along his kin by a King of Winter of House Stark during "the savage War of the Wolves". </p>
<p><b>Gavin the Trader</b> is a free folk leader. </p>
<p>The <b>free folk</b> are a race of people who live beyond the Wall in northern Westeros. They are more commonly referred to as <b>"wildlings"</b> everywhere south of the Wall. </p>
<p><b>Gawen</b> was a maester of the Citadel who served as Grand Maester during the reigns of Kings Aegon I, Aenys I, and, albeit briefly, Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gawen Corbray</b> was a knight of House Corbray during the reign of King Aegon I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Gawen Gardener</b> was a member of House Gardener of Highgarden and the second son of Mern IX Gardener, King of the Reach. </p>
<p><b>Gawen Glover</b> is a member of House Glover, the eldest son of Robett and Sybelle Glover. The appendices of <i>A Clash of Kings</i> and <i>A Storm of Swords</i> state that Gawen is the heir to Deepwood Motte, while the appendices of <i>A Feast for Crows</i> and <i>A Dance with Dragons</i> state that his father Robett is the heir of Galbart Glover. </p>
<p><b>Gawen Swann</b> was the Lord of Stonehelm and the head of House Swann during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Gawen Westerling</b> is the Lord of the Crag and the head of House Westerling. </p>
<p>The <b>Crag</b> is the seat of House Westerling in the westerlands. It is more of a ruin than a castle as the Westerlings no longer have the funds to maintain it. It sits along the coast of the Sunset Sea, south of Banefort, northwest of Ashemark, and northeast of Fair Isle. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gawen Wylde</b> was a knight from House Wylde and the master-at-arms at Storm's End during Robert's Rebellion. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gedmund Peake</b>, called <b>Gedmund Great-Axe</b>, was a knight from House Peake who became commander of the royal fleet, and later lord admiral and master of ships during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. He was the younger brother of Lord Peake and uncle of Unwin Peake of Starpike. </p>
<p><b>Gella</b> is the granddaughter of Lord Godric Borrell, through one of his daughters. </p>
<p><b>Gelmarr</b>, also known as <b>Gelmarr the Grim</b>, is an ironborn raider. </p>
<p><b>Gendel</b> was a former King-Beyond-the-Wall, a title he shared with his brother, Gorne. He led an invasion into the North. He lived three thousand years before the War of the Five Kings. </p>
<p><b>King-Beyond-the-Wall</b> (or <b>King-beyond-the-Wall</b>) is the title given to a person who has united the many tribes of free folk (or wildlings) who dwell beyond the Wall. Despite its name, the title is not a hereditary or absolute position. It is not a position of any authority except that of the person who can establish it through persuasion and force. For long periods of time there have been no recognized kings. </p>
<p><b>Gendry</b> is a blacksmith apprentice for Master Tobho Mott in King's Landing. He does not know he is a bastard son of King Robert I Baratheon. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Gendry is portrayed by Joe Dempsie. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Genna Lannister</b> is a member of House Lannister wed to Ser Emmon Frey, with whom she has four children: Ser Cleos, Lyonel, Tion, and Walder Frey. </p>
<p><b>Geoff</b>, called <b>the Squirrel</b>, is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Geoff</b> is a man-at-arms in service to House Lannister. He was specifically created for a scene in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>George Graceford</b> was the Lord of Holyhall and head of House Graceford during the Dance of the Dragons. He was later named Lord Confessor during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gerald Gower</b> is a knight of House Gower in service to King Stannis Baratheon. </p>
<p><b>Gerardys</b> was a maester who served Princess Rhaenyra Targaryen on Dragonstone. He later became the Grand Maester of Queen Rhaenyra, and sat on her black council. </p>
<p>The <b>maesters</b> are an order of scholars, healers, messengers, and scientists. They educate new students at the Citadel, which is located in Oldtown, a city in the Reach. House Hightower was integral in the Citadel's foundation, and continues to patronize the order. As advisers to the Westerosi nobility, the maesters have largely supplanted the Alchemists' Guild. They are sometimes called "the knights of the mind." </p>
<p>Ser <b>Geremy Frey</b> was a knight of House Frey. The tenth-born son of Lord Walder Frey, and fifth son by his third wife Lady Amarei Crakehall. He was married to Carolei Waynwood and had two children, Sandor and Cynthea Frey. </p>
<p><b>Gerion Lannister</b> was a member of House Lannister, and was the youngest brother of Tywin Lannister, Lord of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Germund Botley</b> is a member of House Botley and the younger brother of Lord Sawane Botley. </p>
<p><b>Gerold</b> is a Westerosi given name. It can refer to several people: </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gerold Dayne</b>, known as <b>Darkstar</b>, is the Knight of High Hermitage. His house is a cadet branch of the Daynes of Starfall. </p>
<p><b>Gerold Grafton</b> is the Lord of Gulltown and head of House Grafton. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gerold Grafton</b> was an Andal knight from Andalos who established the rule of House Grafton over Gulltown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gerold Hightower</b>, known as <b>the White Bull</b>, was a knight from House Hightower and the Lord Commander of the Kingsguard during the reigns of kings Jaehaerys II Targaryen and Aerys II Targaryen. He was the uncle of Lord Leyton Hightower of Oldtown. An amalgamation of Gerold and Ser Oswell Whent is portrayed by Eddie Eyre during a flashback in Season 6 in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Gerold Lannister</b>, also known as <b>Gerold the Golden</b>, was the Lord of Casterly Rock, the Shield of Lannisport, the Warden of the West, and the head of House Lannister during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen, King Maekar I Targaryen, and part of the reign of King Aegon V Targaryen. He was the second son of Lord Damon Lannister and Lady Cerissa Brax, and the younger brother of Lord Tybolt Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Gerold Lannister</b> was a King of the Rock of House Lannister. </p>

<p><b>Gerold III Lannister</b> was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. He died without male issues, thus a council cronwed his only daughter's husband, Ser Joffrey Lydden, who took the Lannister name and became the first Andal to rule Casterly Rock. </p>

<p>The <b>God-on-Earth</b> was the legendary first ruler of the mythic Great Empire of the Dawn. According to the tales told by the priestly scribes of Yin, he was the only begotten son of the Maiden-Made-of-Light and the Lion of Night, and traveled about his domains in a palanquin carved from a single pearl and carried by a hundred queens, his wives. He ruled for ten thousand years, until at last he ascended to the stars to join his forebears. He was succeeded by his eldest son, the Pearl Emperor. </p>

<p>The <b>tourney at Ashford Meadow</b> or <b>tourney at Ashford</b> was a tourney hosted by House Ashford at Ashford Meadow in 209&nbsp;AC. Due to the accidental death of Prince Baelor Targaryen—the Prince of Dragonstone, son and heir of King Daeron II Targaryen, and Hand of the King—Ashford was one of the most famous and historically significant tourneys. </p>

<p><b>Grazdan the Great</b> is the legendary founder of Old Ghis. He is still so revered that men of the slaver families of Slaver's Bay are still often given his name. According to legend, Grazdan founded the lockstep legions, with which Old Ghis colonized its surroundings and subjugated its neighbors, forming the first empire. Grazdan is also credited with raising the ancient brick walls of Old Ghis. </p>
<p>The <b>Old Empire of Ghis</b> was one of the oldest known nations and cultures in the world. It reigned supreme over much of Essos. Its founding and golden age predate that of its successor, the Valyrian Freehold, by thousands of years. </p>

<p><b>Pello of Tyrosh</b>, better known as <b>Greenbeard</b>, is a Tyroshi member of the brotherhood without banners and one of its leaders. </p>
<p>The <b>brotherhood without banners</b>, also known as the <b>knights of the hollow hill</b> and the <b>forgotten fellowship</b>, is an outlaw group who initially fights Lannister rule in the name of King Robert I Baratheon. Led by the Lightning Lord, Beric Dondarrion, the group is founded in the riverlands by soldiers and nobles who were sent by the then-Hand of the King, Eddard Stark, to bring Gregor Clegane to justice. After they are ambushed while crossing a ford and nearly defeated, the group continues the fight as a guerrilla group. Their numbers increase as they are joined by defeated soldiers from other battles, deserters, and refugees from the War of the Five Kings. Every man of the brotherhood receives a knighthood from Beric. </p>
<p><b>Tyrosh</b> is a harbor city and one of the Free Cities. It is on an island to the north of the Stepstones, just off the coast of the Disputed Lands of Essos. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gregor Clegane</b> is the Knight of Clegane's Keep and the head of House Clegane, a landed knight and bannerman to House Lannister of Casterly Rock. Gregor is a freakishly large man and for this he is often called <b>the Mountain That Rides</b> or simply <b>the Mountain</b>. His soldiers are known as the Mountain's men. </p>

<p>The <b>Grey King</b> is a legendary monarch of the Iron Islands who is said to have ruled for 1,007 years. <p>The <b>Unsullied</b> are eunuch slave soldiers, trained from a young age in Astapor to unquestioning obedience and martial prowess. Sold by the century or the thousand, they are used as guards all over the Free Cities. They make excellent guards, do not loot, and will never rape. </p>

In the annals of history the name of Gwayne III Gardener is writ large. </p>

<p><b>Gyles I Gardener</b>, called <b>the Woe</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. He once sacked Oldtown and reportedly sold three quarters of its population into slavery, but failed to breach the defenses of the Hightower on Battle Isle. </p>
<p><b>Gyles II Gardener</b> was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. He was taken captive in a naval battle near the Misty Islands and tortured to death by Joron I Blacktyde, an ironborn High King of the Iron Islands. Gyles corpse was then cut into small pieces to bait his captor's fishhooks with "a chunk of king". </p>
<p><b>Gyles III Gardener</b> was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. During his rule Highgarden reached the apex of its power. </p>
<p><b>Gyles Grafton</b> is a squire of House Grafton and is the youngest son of Lord Gerold Grafton. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gyles Morrigen</b> was a knight from House Morrigen. He served in the Kingsguard as Lord Commander during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Gyles Rosby</b> is the Lord of Rosby and the head of House Rosby. Lord Gyles has no immediate heir, though he has a ward at Rosby. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Gyles Yronwood</b> was an exiled knight from House Yronwood who was loyal to the blacks during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Gylo Rhegan</b> is the captain and commander of the Long Lances. </p>

<p><b>Gynir</b>, also known as <b>Gynir Rednose</b> and simply <b>Rednose</b>, is an ironborn raider. </p>

<p><b>Haggon</b> was a free folk skinchanger. He was known as a friend of the Night's Watch, trading with them and bringing news of life beyond the Wall. He was a mentor of Varamyr Sixskins. He was tall, grim, had hard hands and a rough voice. </p>

<p><b>Hallyne</b>, also known as <b>Hallyne the Pyromancer</b>, is the head of the Alchemists' Guild. He is a third generation alchemist. He was trained by Wisdom Pollitor. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Roy Dotrice. </p>
<p>The <b>Alchemists' Guild</b>, also called the <b>Guild of Alchemists</b>, is an old order of <b>pyromancers</b>. The guild, was once powerful, though in the recent centuries, the maesters have largely replaced the alchemist everywhere. The pyromancers claim to posses vast secret stores of knowledge. </p>
<p><b>King's Landing</b> is the capital of the Seven Kingdoms, located in the crownlands on the east coast of Westeros. It is situated along the kingsroad at the mouth of the Blackwater Rush and overlooks Blackwater Bay. King's Landing is the site of the Iron Throne and the Red Keep, which is the seat of the king, Robert I from House Baratheon of King's Landing. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Halmon Paege</b> is a knight and current head of House Paege. </p>

<p><b>Hornwood</b> is a castle in the north and the seat of House Hornwood. The castle is located in the Hornwood forest near the northwestern edge of the Sheepshead Hills, which are within the dominion of House Manderly, and the Hornwood lands also neighbor those of House Bolton to the north. Medrick serves as maester at the castle to Lord Halys Hornwood. </p>
<p><b>Hammer</b> is a drunken blacksmith and armorer in the service of the sellsword company the Second Sons. His apprentice is called Nail. </p>
<p>The <b>Hammer of the Hills</b> was an Andal king who controlled part of the eastern Vale during the Andal invasion. His given name is unknown. He died near Ironoaks fighting the army of Robar II Royce, a First Men high king. </p>

It is north of the Last River, northeast of Long Lake, and west of the Bay of Seals. With the exception of the castles of the Night's Watch, Last Hearth is the northernmost major castle of the Seven Kingdoms. </p>

He completed the grand castle, Harrenhal, which would serve to be his doom. </p>

<p>The <b>fat High Septon</b> is the High Septon of the Faith of the Seven at the beginning of <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>. His real name is unknown as High Septons abandon their names once elected to office. </p>
<p>The <b>High Septon</b> was High Septon of the Faith of the Seven during the late reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>High Septon</b> was High Septon of the Faith of the Seven during the reign of kings Maekar I and Aegon V Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>High Septon</b> was High Septon of the Faith of the Seven during the regency and reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>This <b>High Septon</b>, whose birth name was <b>Pate</b>, was appointed High Septon after King Baelor I Targaryen informed the Most Devout that the Seven had revealed the new High Septon's identity to him. </p>
<p>The <b>High Septon</b> of the Faith of the Seven is chosen to his office by Tyrion Lannister after the death of his fat predecessor. His real name is unknown as High Septons abandon their names once elected to office. </p>
<p>The <b>High Sparrow</b> is a leading member of the Sparrows, a sect of the Faith of the Seven. His real name is unknown. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Jonathan Pryce. </p>
<p><b>Lord Hightower</b> was the Lord of the Hightower and head of House Hightower during the late reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and the reign of King Viserys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Hildy</b> is the lover of a sworn sword in the service of Lord Tytos Blackwood of Raventree Hall. </p>
<p><b>Hilmar Drumm</b>, known as <b>Hilmar the Cunning</b>, was a member of House Drumm. </p>
<p><b>Hizdahr zo Loraq</b>, Fourteenth of That Noble Name, is a Ghiscari noble of the city of Meereen. He is extremely wealthy and can trace his descent from several notable Ghiscari citizens such as Mazdhan the Magnificent, Hazrak the Handsome and Zharaq the Liberator. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Joel Fry. </p>
<p><b>Lord Commander Hoare</b> was a member of House Hoare who served as the Lord Commander of the Night's Watch during Aegon's Conquest. His given name has not been revealed. He was a son of King Halleck Hoare and a brother to King Harren Hoare. </p>
<p><b>Hoarfrost Umber</b> was a Lord of the Last Hearth, the grandfather of Greatjon Umber and father of Hother Umber and Mors Umber. </p>
<p><b>Last Hearth</b>, sometimes called <b>the Last Hearth</b>, is the seat of House Umber in the north. It lies close to the Gift in a forest east of the kingsroad. It is north of the Last River, northeast of Long Lake, and west of the Bay of Seals. With the exception of the castles of the Night's Watch, Last Hearth is the northernmost major castle of the Seven Kingdoms. </p>
<p><b>Three-Finger Hobb</b> is the main cook at Castle Black for the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Hobb the Hewer</b> was a woodsman who gained fame during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Hobber Redwyne</b>, mocked as <b>Ser Slobber</b>, is a knight from House Redwyne. He is the son of Paxter Redwyne, Lord of the Arbor, and Lady Mina Tyrell, and he is the younger twin to Ser Horas. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Hobert Hightower</b> was a knight from House Hightower during the Dance of the Dragons. He may have been a landed knight. </p>
<p><b>Hod</b> is a traveler at an inn in the Crownlands. </p>
<p><b>Hodor</b> is a stableboy serving at Winterfell. His real name is <b>Walder</b>, but he is commonly called "Hodor" because it is the only word he says. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Kristian Nairn as well as by Sam Coleman in a Season 6 flashback. ‎ </p>
<p><b>Hoke</b>, known as <b>Hoke the Horseleg</b>, is a guard in service with House Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Holger</b> is the father of Dolf, who is the father of Shagga. Holger is a member of the Stone Crows. It is unknown if Holger is still alive. </p>
<p><b>Hollis Teague</b> was one of the last monarchs of House Teague. </p>
<p><b>Holly</b> is a wildling spearwife. </p>
<p>A <b>spearwife</b> is a free folk woman who is also a warrior. </p>
<p><b>Hollys Tallhart</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>The <b>hooded man</b> is the fan-given name for a man encountered by Theon Greyjoy at Winterfell. </p>
<p>The <b>Hooded Man</b> is a legendary figure from the Age of Heroes from whom House Banefort claims descent. His visage is present in the hooded sigil of the family. </p>
<p><b>Hop-Bean</b> was Penny and Oppo's father. He was a dwarf. </p>
<p><b>Hop-Robin</b> is a Night's Watch recruit. </p>
<p><b>Horas Harroway</b> was a member of House Harroway during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Horas Redwyne</b>, mocked as <b>Ser Horror</b>, is a knight of House Redwyne and heir to the Arbor. He is the son of Paxter Redwyne, Lord of the Arbor, and Lady Mina Tyrell, and he is the older twin to Ser Hobber. </p>
<p><b>Horgan Hoare</b>, known as <b>Horgan Priestkiller</b>, was a King of the Iron Islands from House Hoare. The Hoare kings of his era were opposed by the priests of the Drowned God because of their support for the Faith of the Seven, discouraging of reaving, and promotion of trade. </p>
<p>The <b>Horned Lord</b> was a King-Beyond-the-Wall long before Bael the Bard. His given name is not known. </p>
<p><b>Horonno</b> was one of the ruling triarchs of the Free City of Volantis during the Century of Blood. </p>
<p><b>Horro</b> was a <i>khal</i> who lived during the Century of Blood. He was the last great <i>khal</i> to command the allegiance of all Dothraki. </p>
<p><b>Horton Redfort</b> is Lord of Redfort and head of House Redfort. He has been married three times and has four sons: Ser Jasper, Ser Creighton, Ser Jon, and Mychel. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Horys Hill</b> was a hedge knight who led Poor Fellows during the Faith Militant uprising against King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Hosman Norcross</b> is a knight of House Norcross. He is married to Delena Florent. They have two children; Alester and Renly. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Hosteen Frey</b> is a knight of House Frey, the sixth son of Lord Walder Frey, the first one born of his third wife, Amarei Crakehall. He is married to Bellena Hawick. </p>
<p><b>Hostella Frey</b> is the second daughter of Ser Arwood Frey and Ryella Royce. She is a newborn babe. </p>
<p><b>Hoster Blackwood</b>, called <b>Hos</b> by family and friends, is the third son of Lord Tytos Blackwood of Raventree Hall. </p>
<p><b>Hoster Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, the eldest child of Ser Whalen Frey and Sylwa Paege. He is a squire to Ser Damon Paege. </p>
<p><b>Hoster Tully</b> is the Lord Paramount of the Trident, the Lord of Riverrun, and the head of House Tully. He was married to Lady Minisa Whent, with whom he had three children who survived infancy: Catelyn, Lysa, and Edmure. His younger brother is Ser Brynden Tully, the Knight of the Gate. </p>
<p><b>Hot Pie</b> is an orphan baker's boy of King's Landing. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Ben Hawkey. The boy's given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Hother Umber</b>, nicknamed <b>Whoresbane</b>, is a member of House Umber and is the uncle of Lord Greatjon Umber. Hother is the joint castellan of Last Hearth with his older brother, Mors. </p>
<p><b>Hotho Harlaw</b>, known as <b>Hotho Humpback</b>, is a member of House Harlaw and the master of the Tower of Glimmering. His personal sigil is the Harlaw scythe girdled within an embattled border. He has a daughter. </p>
<p><b>Hothor Umber</b> was an ancestor of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>A Qartheen dwarf is a <b>servitor</b> in the House of the Undying. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Howard Bullock</b> was a knight in service to House Targaryen. His father, Ser Merrell Bullock, was the commander of the castle garrison at Dragonstone during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. Howard and his brother, Ser Alyn, served alongside their father. Alyn was married. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Howard Pyle</b> was a knight from House Pyle during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Howd Wanderer</b> is a free folk leader. </p>
<p><b>Howland Reed</b> is the Lord of Greywater Watch and head of House Reed, holding dominion over the crannogmen of the Neck. Howland's children with his wife Jyana are Meera and Jojen, and he is a close friend of Lord Eddard Stark of Winterfell. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Howland is played by Leo Woodruff during flashbacks in Season 6. </p>
<p><b>Hrothgar</b> was a legendary ironborn raider from Pyke who supposedly lived during the Age of Heroes. He possessed a horn capable of summoning krakens. </p>
<p><b>Hubard Rambton</b> is a knight from House Rambton sworn to Stannis Baratheon. He has three sons. </p>
<p><b>Hubert</b> is a maester of the Citadel. He is the author of <i>Kin of the Stag</i>, in which he suggests that Galladon of Morne was not a warrior of the Age of Heroes turned into a knight by singers, but an actual historical figure of more recent times, noting that Morne was a royal seat of petty kings on the eastern coast of Tarth until the Storm Kings made them submit, though its ruins were made by Andals and not the First Men. </p>
<p><b>Hubert Arryn</b> was the Lord of the Eyrie and the head of House Arryn during the reign of King Aenys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Hugh</b>, also called <b>Hugh of the Vale</b>, is a squire to Lord Jon Arryn who became a knight upon his lord's death. </p>
<p><b>Hugh Arryn</b>, called <b>Hugh the Fat</b>, was a King of Mountain and Vale of House Arryn. He extended Arryn rule to include the isle of Pebble. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Hugh Beesbury</b> is a knight from House Beesbury. His relation to Lord Warryn Beesbury, the head of the House, is unknown. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Hugh Hammer</b>, called <b>Hugh the Hammer</b>, <b>Hard Hugh</b>, and <b>Lord Hammer</b>, was a dragonseed who became a dragonrider during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Hugh Hungerford</b> is a sellsword of Westerosi origin, and member of the Windblown. </p>
<p><b>Hugo Arryn</b>, called <b>Hugo the Hopeful</b>, was the grandson of King Hugh Arryn and a King of Mountain and Vale of House Arryn. He extended Arryn rule to include the isle of the Paps. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Hugo Vance</b> is a knight from House Vance of Atranta and the second son of Lord Norbert Vance. He is a friend and companion to Ser Edmure Tully. </p>
<p><b>Hugo Vance</b> was the Lord of Wayfarer's Rest and the head of House Vance of Wayfarer's Rest during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Hugo Wull</b>, called <b>Big Bucket</b> and <b>the Wull</b>, is the clan chief of House Wull in the north. He commands the most men of the northern mountain clans. </p>
<p><b>Hugor of the Hill</b> was the first King of the Andals in Andalos. </p>
<p><b>Hukko</b> is the name given by Pentoshi singers to a legendary Andal hero. According to legend he slew the swan maidens, who lured travelers to their deaths in the Velvet Hills; though not for their crimes but as sacrifices to the Seven. Some maesters note "Hukko" may be a rendering of the name of Hugor, the first King of the Andals. </p>
<p><b>Hullen</b> is a member of the Stark household. He is the master of horse at Winterfell. He is the father of Harwin. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Humfrey Clifton</b> is a knight of House Clifton. He is sworn to King Stannis I Baratheon. His relation to the head of the house, Ser Gareth Clifton, is unknown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Humfrey Hardyng</b> was a tourney knight of renown during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. His brother by marriage was Ser Humfrey Beesbury. </p>
<p><b>Humfrey Hewett</b> is the head of House Hewett and is the Lord of Oakenshield, one of the Shield Islands in the Reach. He has seven daughters and good-daughters, as well as a bastard daughter, Falia Flowers. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Humfrey Hightower</b> is a knight of House Hightower. He is the fourth and youngest son of Lord Leyton Hightower. </p>
<p><b>Humfrey Lefford</b> was the Lord of the Golden Tooth and the head of House Lefford during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Humfrey Stone</b> is a sellsword in service to the Golden Company. As a serjeant, he is a high-ranking officer. His surname of Stone suggests he may be a bastard from the Vale of Arryn. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Humfrey Swyft</b> is a knight of House Swyft. </p>
<p><b>Humfrey I Teague</b> was one of the last monarchs of House Teague to rule the Riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Humfrey II Teague</b> was one of the last monarchs of House Teague. He was the eldest son of Humfrey I Teague, who caused a massive uprising of Riverlords by attempting to suppress worship of the old gods. In the campaign's final battle, Humfrey I perished. Prince Humfrey picked up his father's crown and sword and became Humfrey II, only to die short time later, thus passing the crown to his younger brother Hollis. By the end of the battle, Hollis, his younger brother Tyler, and their uncle Damon had all inherited the crown and died. And so, House Teague became extinct. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Humfrey the Mummer</b> was a hedge knight during the reign of King Aegon I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Humfrey Wagstaff</b> was a knight from House Wagstaff and the castellan of Grandview for House Grandison. When already a man of sixty-five, he was betrothed to a sixteen-year-old Brienne of Tarth. </p>
<p><b>Humfrey Waters</b> is a member of the City Watch of King's Landing and the captain of the Dragon Gate. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Humphrey Bulwer</b> was a knight of House Bulwer during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>A <b>hunchbacked septon</b> was a septon at Stoney Sept living during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Hunnimore</b> was a maester who served at Dragonstone during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Husband</b> is the husband of Sharna, the innkeep of the Inn of the Kneeling Man. </p>
<p>The <b>ruby ford</b> or <b>Ruby Ford</b> is a crossing of the Trident in the eastern riverlands. It is so named for the rubies that were knocked from Prince Rhaegar Targaryen's breastplate during the Battle of the Trident. The inn at the crossroads lies near the ford. There is no crossing of the Green Fork north of it until the Twins. </p>
<p><b>Huzhor Amai</b>, called <b>"the Amazing"</b>, is a legendary hero and ancestor of the Tall Men, the nation that founded the Kingdom of Sarnor. According to legend, he was born of the last of the Fisher Queens and took to wife the daughters of the greatest lords and kings of the Gipps, the Cymmeri, and the Zoqora. His Zoqora wife drove his chariot, and his Cymmeri wife made his armor. He also wore about his shoulders a great cloak made from the pelt of a king of the Hairy Men. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Hyle Hunt</b> is a knight of House Hunt and a captain in service to House Tarly. </p>
<p><b>Iain Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Iain Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Iggo</b> is a Dothraki member of the Brave Companions. </p>
<p>The <b>Brave Companions</b> are a sellsword company of considerably ill repute from Essos. The company comprises criminals and outcasts from many nations. </p>
<p><b>Igon Vyrwel</b> is a member of House Vyrwel who serves as captain of the household guard for House Tyrell at Highgarden. </p>
<p><b>Highgarden</b> is a castle which serves as the seat of House Tyrell, the regional capital of the Reach, and the heart of chivalry in the Seven Kingdoms. It lies on the Mander where the ocean road meets the roseroad, making it an important crossroads. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Illifer the Penniless</b> is a hedge knight. His coat-of-arms is gold and ermine gyronny. His traveling partner is Ser Creighton Longbough. </p>
<p><b>Illister</b> is a maester from the Citadel of Oldtown who wrote <i>Horse Tribes, Being a Study of the Nomads of the Eastern Plains of Essos</i>. </p>
<p><b>Illyrio Mopatis</b> is a wealthy magister from the Free City of Pentos who deals in spices, gemstones, dragonbone, cheese, and slaves, among other things. He has a variety of plans. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Roger Allam. </p>
<p><b>Pentos</b> is one of the Free Cities of western Essos. It is a port located on the eastern coast of the Bay of Pentos. </p>
<p>The <b>first wife</b> of Magister Illyrio Mopatis of Pentos was a cousin of the Prince of Pentos. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ilyn Payne</b> is a knight from House Payne. He serves as the King's Justice, the royal headsman, for King Robert I Baratheon. Ilyn is a cousin to Podrick Payne. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Wilko Johnson. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Imry Florent</b> is a knight of House Florent. He is the son of Ser Ryam Florent and brother to Selyse and Erren. Imry is brother-in-law to Stannis Baratheon. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Gordon Mahon. </p>
<p><b>Ironbelly</b> is a master smith in King's Landing. </p>

<p><b>Isembard Arryn</b>, called <b>the Gilded Falcon</b>, was the head of House Arryn of Gulltown and a claimant to the Eyrie during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Fearless Ithoke</b> is a pit fighter famed in Meereen. His origin is unknown, but he supports the pit fighting culture of the city. </p>
<p><b>Izembaro</b>, also called the <b>King of the Mummers</b> and <b>Izembaro the Great</b>, is a mummer from Braavos. He is the founder and leader of the group of mummers at The Gate. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Jacaerys Velaryon</b>, also known as <b>Jace</b>, was the firstborn son of Princess Rhaenyra Targaryen and her first husband, Ser Laenor Velaryon. When Rhaenyra was crowned queen during the Dance of the Dragons, she named Jacaerys as Prince of Dragonstone and heir to the Iron Throne. Jacaerys was a dragonrider whose dragon was Vermax. </p>
<p><b>Jace</b> is a recruit of the Night's Watch. </p>
