<p><b>Jacks</b> is a member of the household guard of Lord Eddard Stark at Winterfell. </p>
<p>The <b>Jade Emperor</b> was the legendary third ruler of the mythic Great Empire of the Dawn. He succeeded the Pearl Emperor and was in turn succeeded by the Tourmaline Emperor. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Jaehaera Targaryen</b> was the daughter of King Aegon II Targaryen and his sister-wife and Queen Helaena Targaryen. She was the first wife and queen of her cousin King Aegon III Targaryen. Jaehaera had a twin brother, Jaehaerys, and a younger brother, Maelor. The dragon Morghul was bound to Jaehaera. </p>
<p><b>Jaehaerys I Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>the Conciliator</b>, <b>the Wise</b>, or later in life as <b>the Old King</b>, was the fourth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He ascended the throne in 48&nbsp;AC following the death of his uncle, Maegor I Targaryen. Jaehaerys was the longest reigning Targaryen monarch, sitting on the throne for fifty-five years. He was a dragonrider, riding Vermithor, the largest dragon after Balerion and Vhagar. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Jaehaerys Targaryen</b> was the son of King Aegon II Targaryen and his sister-wife and Queen Helaena Targaryen. He was Aegon's firstborn son and heir, next in line to the Iron Throne. He had a twin sister, Jaehaera, and a younger brother Maelor. The dragon Shrykos was bound to Jaehaerys. </p>
<p><b>Jaehaerys II Targaryen</b> was a Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and the sixteenth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He was the second born son of King Aegon V Targaryen and Queen Betha Blackwood. Jaehaerys was the father of King Aerys II Targaryen and Queen Rhaella Targaryen, and the grandfather of Rhaegar, Viserys and Daenerys. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Jaehaerys Targaryen</b> was the fourthborn son of King Aerys II Targaryen and Queen Rhaella Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Jaenara Belaerys</b> was a dragonrider who flew her dragon, Terrax, farther south in Sothoryos than anyone had gone before. She returned to the Valyrian Freehold after three years, having found only endless jungle, deserts, and mountains. Jaenara declared that Sothoryos was as large as Essos and "a land without end". </p>
<p><b>Jafer Flowers</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. He is a bastard from the Reach, judging by his surname. </p>
<p><b>Jaggot</b> is a member of the Stone Crows, one of the Vale mountain clans found in the Mountains of the Moon. </p>
<p><b>Jaime Corbray</b> was an Andal knight and a member of House Corbray during the latter stage of the Andal invasion of the Vale. </p>
<p><b>Jaime Frey</b> is the third son of Ser Raymund Frey and Beony Beesbury, the twin of Tywin. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jaime Lannister</b>, also known as the <b>Kingslayer</b>, is a knight from House Lannister. He is the second child and first-born son of Lord Tywin Lannister of Casterly Rock and his wife, Lady Joanna, also of House Lannister. He is the twin brother of Queen Cersei Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Jalabhar Xho</b>, Prince of the Red Flower Vale, is an exiled prince from the Summer Isles residing in the Red Keep. </p>
<p>The <b>Summer Isles</b>, sometimes called the <b>Summer Islands</b>, are a large archipelago located south of Westeros and Essos and west of Sothoryos and Naath. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jammos Frey</b> is a knight of House Frey and the thirteenth son of Lord Walder Frey, the second by his fourth wife, Lady Alyssa Blackwood. Jammos is married to Sallei Paege and has three children: Big Walder, Dickon, and Mathis Frey. </p>
<p><b>Janei Lannister</b> is the only daughter of Ser Kevan Lannister and his wife, Dorna Swyft. She is their youngest child. </p>
<p><b>Janna Fossoway</b>, née <b>Tyrell</b>, is the wife of Ser Jon Fossoway. She is the youngest daughter of Lord Luthor Tyrell and Lady Olenna Tyrell. Janna has two siblings, Mace Tyrell, the current Lord of Highgarden, and an older sister, Mina. </p>
<p><b>Janos Slynt</b> is the head of House Slynt and commander of the City Watch of King's Landing. His father was a butcher. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Dominic Carter. </p>
<p><b>Janyce Hunter</b> is a member of House Hunter and the wife of Edwyn Frey. They have one daughter, Walda. </p>
<p><b>Jaqen H'ghar</b> is a sellsword from Lorath. He is taken as a criminal by Yoren to join the Night's Watch. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Tom Wlaschiha. </p>
<p><b>Jar Han</b> was a God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti and the eight member of his dynasty. Under his rule, the Golden Empire reached the apex of its power that had began under the rule of his father, Jar Har and then his elder brother, Jar Joq. Jar Han exacted tribute from Qarth, Old Ghis, and Asshai. </p>
<p><b>Jar Har</b> was a God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti and the sixth member of his dynasty. Under his rule, the Golden Empire began the apex of its power with the conquest of Leng. He had at least two sons: Jar Joq, his successor, and Jar Han. </p>
<p><b>Jar Joq</b> was a God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti and the seventh member of his dynasty. Under his rule, the Golden Empire continued the apex of its power with the conquest of Great Moraq. He succeeded his father, Jar Har, and was in turn succeeded by his younger brother, Jar Han. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jared Frey</b> is a knight of House Frey. He is the fourth son of Lord Walder Frey, the first son born from his second wife, Cyrenna Swann. He is married to his cousin Alys Frey and has two children, Ser Tytos and Kyra Frey. </p>

<p>Maester <b>Jellicoe</b> was a maester of the Citadel that supposedly lived among the children of the forest. He suggested that the settlement at the top of the Whispering Sound that would eventually become Oldtown began as a trading post where ships from Valyria, Old Ghis, and the Summer Isles put in to replenish their provisions, make repairs, and trade with the "elder races". According to this theory, Oldtown would date to the Dawn Age and predate even the arrival of the First Men to Westeros. </p>

<p><b>Robert I Baratheon</b> is the King of the Andals, the Rhoynar, and the First Men, Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and Protector of the Realm of Westeros, and the head of House Baratheon of King's Landing. Robert was crowned king after King Aerys II Targaryen, his first cousin once removed, was killed during Robert's Rebellion. Following the war, Robert married Cersei Lannister to ensure political stability. With her, Robert has three children: Joffrey, Myrcella, and Tommen. <p><b>John the Oak</b> is a legendary son of Garth Greenhand and a giantess. He was a huge man, eight feet tall in some tales, or even ten or twelve in others. John is credited with bringing chivalry to Westeros. His descendants became House Oakheart. </p>

<p><b>John II Gardener</b>, called <b>the Tall</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. He sailed his barge up the Mander to its very headwaters, planting the Gardener banner wherever he went and receiving homage from lords and petty kings whose lands lined the river's banks. In the annals of history the name of John II Gardener is writ large. </p>
<p><b>Jojen Reed</b> is a member of House Reed. He is Lord Howland Reed's only son and Meera Reed's younger brother. Jojen has greensight, the power of prophetic green dreams. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Jojen is portrayed by Thomas Brodie-Sangster. </p>
<p><b>Greywater Watch</b>, also known as <b>Greywater</b>, is the seat of House Reed in the north. It is roughly located in an eastern headwater of the Green Fork in the swamps of the Neck, southwest of Moat Cailin. It is a castle built upon a crannog, one of the man-made floating islands of the swamps, and it does not stay in the same place, making it impossible for ravens or enemies to find. According to Meera Reed, there is no maester there, nor any knights or masters-at-arms. </p>

<p><b>Jon Penny</b> is a boy orphaned by the War of the Five Kings. He might have been a member of House Penny. </p>
<p>The <b>inn at the crossroads</b> or <b>crossroads inn</b> is an inn that lies at the crossroads between the kingsroad running north-south, the river road west through the riverlands to the westerlands, and the high road east to the Vale of Arryn. It is sometimes called the <b>Old Inn</b> and was formerly named the <b>Two Crowns</b>, the <b>Bellringer Inn</b>, the <b>Clanking Dragon</b>, and the <b>River Inn</b>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jon Penrose</b> was a knight from House Penrose during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Jon Piper</b> was the Lord of Pinkmaiden Castle and the head of House Piper during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. He fought for Prince Aegon Targaryen during the Battle Beneath the Gods Eye. He had two younger brothers and a sister, Lady Melony. </p>
<p><b>Jon Pox</b> is the friend of the brother of Septon Meribald. He died in the War of the Ninepenny Kings. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jon Redfort</b> is a knight of House Redfort and the third son of Lord Horton Redfort of Redfort. </p>
<p><b>Jon Rosby</b> was the Lord of Rosby and the head of House Rosby during the early reign of King Aegon I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jon Roxton</b>, also known as <b>Bold Jon Roxton</b>, (also spelled <b>John</b>) was a knight and the head of House Roxton during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Jon Snow</b> is the bastard son of Eddard Stark, Lord of Winterfell. He has five half-siblings: Robb, Sansa, Arya, Bran, and Rickon Stark. Unaware of the identity of his mother, Jon was raised at Winterfell. At the age of fourteen, he joins the Night's Watch, where he earns the nickname <b>Lord Snow</b>. Jon is one of the major POV characters in <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Jon is portrayed by Kit Harington. </p>
<p><b>Jon Stark</b> was a King in the North and head of House Stark before the War of Conquest. There is a statue of Jon within the crypt of Winterfell. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jon Tollett</b> was a knight from House Tollett and a member of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Jon Umber</b>, known as <b>Greatjon Umber</b> and <b>the Greatjon</b>, is Lord of the Last Hearth and head of House Umber, a vassal family to the Starks of Winterfell. His eldest son, also named Jon, is called the Smalljon. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> the Greatjon is played by Clive Mantle. </p>
<p><b>Last Hearth</b>, sometimes called <b>the Last Hearth</b>, is the seat of House Umber in the north. It lies close to the Gift in a forest east of the kingsroad. It is north of the Last River, northeast of Long Lake, and west of the Bay of Seals. With the exception of the castles of the Night's Watch, Last Hearth is the northernmost major castle of the Seven Kingdoms. </p>
<p><b>Jon Umber</b>, known as <b>the Smalljon</b> and <b>Smalljon Umber</b> in comparison to his father, is the eldest son of Lord Greatjon Umber and is the heir to the Last Hearth. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Dean S. Jagger. </p>
<p><b>Jon Umber</b> was the Lord of the Last Hearth and the head of House Umber during the latter half of the second century after Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Jon Vance</b> is a maester of the Citadel formerly of House Vance of Atranta. He is born the fifth and youngest son of Lord Norbert Vance, his four older brothers are: Ser Ronald, Ser Ellery, Ser Hugo and Ser Kirth. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jon Waters</b> was the bastard son of Lord Alyn Velaryon and Princess Elaena Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jon Wylde</b> is a knight of House Wylde. He is married to Elyana Vypren and has one child, Rickard Wylde. </p>
<p><b>Jonah Mooton</b> was the heir to, and later Lord of Maidenpool and head of House Mooton during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Jonelle Cerwyn</b> is a member of House Cerwyn and is the daughter of Lord Medger Cerwyn. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Jonnel Stark</b>, also known as <b>One-Eye</b>, was a Lord of Winterfell and the head of House Stark in the latter half of the second century after Aegon's Conquest. He was the second son of Lord Cregan Stark, and the first by his third and final wife, Lynara Stark. </p>
<p><b>Jonos Arryn</b> was a member of House Arryn and the younger brother of Ronnel Arryn, the last King of Mountain and Vale and first Lord of the Vale after Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Jonos Bracken</b> is the Lord of the Stone Hedge and head of House Bracken. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is portrayed by Gerry O'Brien. </p>
<p><b>Jonos Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, the second son of Rhaegar Frey and Jeyne Beesbury. He is one of the numerous great-grandchildren of Lord Walder Frey. </p>
<p>King <b>Jonos Stark</b> was a King In The North. He is buried in the crypts beneath Winterfell. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jonothor Darry</b>, also known as <b>Jon Darry</b>, was a knight from House Darry and a member of King Aerys II Targaryen's Kingsguard. According to semi-canon sources, he was the brother of Ser Willem Darry, master-at-arms at the Red Keep. </p>
<p><b>Jonquil</b> is a legendary character from the Age of Heroes. Associated with Jonquil's Pool at Maidenpool in the riverlands, she is known known for falling in love with a knight named Florian the Fool. </p>
<p><b>Jonquil Darke</b> was a member of House Darke and born a bastard daughter of Lord Darklyn of Duskendale. </p>
<p><b>Jorah Mallister</b> was the Lord of Seagard and the head of House Mallister during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Jorah Mormont</b> is an exiled knight, the former head of House Mormont and Lord of Bear Island. He fled Westeros to escape execution for trading in slaves and took up work as a mercenary in the Free Cities, eventually entering the service of the last Targaryens. He becomes one of the most trusted companions of Daenerys Targaryen. Jorah is portrayed in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> by Iain Glen. </p>
<p><b>Bear Island</b> is a remote island in the north that is home to House Mormont. It lies within the Bay of Ice, north of Deepwood Motte and south of the Frozen Shore. The Mormonts live at Mormont Keep. </p>
<p>King <b>Jorah Stark</b> was King in the North. He is buried in the crypts beneath Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Joramun</b> was a legendary King-Beyond-the-Wall. According to myth, in ancient days he blew the Horn of Winter and "woke the giants from the earth". </p>
<p><b>Jordan Towers</b> was the Lord of Harrenhal and the head of House Towers during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Jore Blackbrow</b> was a member of House Blackbrow mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Jorelle Mormont</b>, also called <b>Jory</b>, is one of the many daughters of Lady Maege Mormont. </p>
<p><b>Jorgen</b> was a peasant sworn to House Webber of Coldmoat. </p>
<p><b>Jorgen Velaryon</b> was one of the children of Lord Daemon Velaryon, the Lord of the Tides and the head of House Velaryon during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen and King Jaehaerys. </p>
<p><b>Jorl the Whale</b> is a legendary ironborn raider from the Age of Heroes. </p>
<p><b>Joron I Blacktyde</b> was a High King of the Iron Islands from House Blacktyde. He was dubbed <b>Maidensbane</b>. </p>
<p><b>Jorquen</b> was a septon of the Faith who served on the Wall. He wrote the <i>Annals of the Black Centaur</i> about Lord Commander Orbert Caswell. </p>
<p><b>Jory Cassel</b> is a member of House Cassel and the captain of the household guard at Winterfell for House Stark. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Jamie Sives. </p>
<p><b>Joseran</b> was the maester assigned to House Blacktyde. </p>
<p><b>Joseth</b> is the master of horse at Winterfell upon the departure of Hullen. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Joseth Mallister</b> was a knight from House Mallister during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Joseth Smallwood</b> was the Lord of Acorn Hall and the head of House Smallwood during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Joseth Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Josmyn Peckledon</b>, called <b>Peck</b> by Ser Jaime Lannister, is a squire from House Peckledon. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Joss Hood</b> is a young knight from Sunspear. </p>
<p><b>Joss Stilwood</b> is a squire of Ser Gregor Clegane, along with a pimply Sarsfield squire. </p>
<p><b>Joss the Gloom</b> is a mummer of the Ship. </p>
<p>King <b>Josua Massey</b>, also known as <b>the Softspear</b>, was the last King of House Massey. He was slain by the Storm King Qarlton II Durrandon. His daughter was taken as wife by Togarion Bar Emmon, while his son was installed as a puppet king, after Togarion drove the stormlanders away from Stonedance. </p>
<p><b>Josua Willum</b> is the son of Lord Willum. He has at least one brother, Elyas Willum. </p>

<p>Lady <b>Joyeuse Erenford</b> is a member of House Erenford and the eighth wife of Lord Walder Frey. </p>
<p><b>Walder Frey</b> is the Lord of the Crossing and head of House Frey. Though almost ninety years old and infirm, he still maintains an active hand in the running of his house at the Twins. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by David Bradley. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Julian Wormwood</b> was a knight fighting for King Aegon II Targaryen during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Junia Royce</b> was a member of House Royce mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Junia Royce</b> is a member of House Royce mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Jurne</b> is the maester in service to Lord Renly Baratheon at Storm's End. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Justin Massey</b> is a knight from House Massey, and a queen's man. </p>
<p>King <b>Justin Massey</b>, called <b>Justin Milk-Eye</b>, was a monarch of House Massey and an infamous pirate-king. </p>
<p><b>Jyana</b> is a crannogwoman and the wife of Lord Howland Reed. Together they have two children: Meera and Jojen Reed. </p>
<p><b>Jyanna Frey</b> is the wife and cousin of Ser Benfrey Frey. They have two children; Della and Osmund Frey. </p>
<p><b>Jyck</b> is a guard sworn to House Lannister who serves as escort to Tyrion Lannister when he travels to the Wall. </p>
<p><b>Jynessa Blackmont</b> is a noblewoman of House Blackmont. She is the eldest child and heir of Larra Blackmont, the Lady of Blackmont. </p>
<p><b>Jyzene</b> is a serving wench at the Peach in Stoney Sept. </p>
<p><b>Kaeth</b> was a Grand Maester of the Citadel. </p>
<p>The <i><b>Lives of Four Kings</b></i> is a book written by Grand Maester Kaeth about the lives of four Targaryen kings; Daeron I, Baelor I, Aegon IV and Daeron II. It barely mentions the reign of Viserys II Targaryen, who ruled after Baelor and before Aegon. </p>
<p><b>Clubfoot Karl</b> is a ranger or steward of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Karlon Stark</b> was a younger son of Winterfell. He was the first Lord of Karl's Hold and the founder of House Karstark. </p>
<p><b>House Karstark of Karhold</b> is a noble house from Karhold in the north. They were founded as a cadet branch of their overlords, the Starks of Winterfell, and are among their principal bannermen. Their blazon is a white sunburst on black and their motto is "The Sun of Winter". </p>
<p><b>Karolyn</b> was a septa at the motherhouse attached to the Starry Sept in Oldtown during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Karsi</b> is a spearwife and chieftess of the ice-river clans. She appears only in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Karyl Vance</b> is a knight of House Vance of Wayfarer's Rest. He has three daughters, Liane, Rhialta, and Emphyria. </p>
<p><b>Wayfarer's Rest</b> is the seat of House Vance of Wayfarer's Rest in the riverlands, probably located in the western part of the region near the Red Fork and the border with the westerlands. </p>
<p><b>Kasporio</b>, who styles himself <b>Kasporio the Cunning</b>, is the second-in-command of the Second Sons, a sellsword company. </p>
<p><b>Katrina Umber</b>, née <b>Cerwyn</b>, was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Kayla</b> is a prostitute working in the brothel owned by Petyr "Littlefinger" Baelish in King's Landing. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is played by Pixie Le Knot. The sexual position Kayla can perform, the "Meereenese Knot" is a reference to a complex series of plot problems George R.R. Martin encountered whilst writing the fifth novel in the series, <i>A Dance with Dragons</i>, problems which delayed the novel for a considerable amount of time. </p>
<p><b>Kear Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Kedge Whiteye</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Kedry</b> is a maester of the Citadel in service to Anders Yronwood, Lord of Yronwood. He is fluent in all the tongues of the Free Cities, as well as mongrel Ghiscari. </p>
<p><b>Kegs</b> is a builder of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Kella</b> is a servant sworn to House Baelish. She is described as a fat middle-aged woman. She has many children by different fathers. She tends House Baelish's herds of sheep. </p>
<p><b>Kelvyn</b> was a maester of the Citadel during the reign of Viserys I Targaryen. He was specifically created for the television adaptation <i>House of the Dragon</i> and is not mentioned in any books. </p>
<p><b>Kem</b> is a young sellsword of the Second Sons. </p>
<p><b>Kemmett Pyke</b>, known as <b>Kemmett the Bastard</b>, is an ironborn raider and a bastard. </p>
<p><b>Kenned the Whale</b> is an ironborn raider. </p>
<p><b>Lord Kenning</b> is the head of House Kenning of Harlaw and a bannerman to Lord Rodrik Harlaw of Harlaw. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Kennos of Kayce</b> is a knight in service to House Kenning of Kayce. Lord Terrence Kenning entrusts him with the Horn of Herrock, a warhorn passed down through the family as an heirloom. </p>
<p>The <b>Horn of Herrock</b> is a black, twisted horn that is banded with gold. It is named after Herrock Kenning, the founder of House Kenning of Kayce. </p>
<p><b>Kermit Tully</b> was the Lord of Riverrun, Lord Paramount of the Trident, and head of House Tully at the end of the Dance of the Dragons and during the reign of Aegon III Targaryen. The young knight became the head of House Tully after the death of his father, Lord Elmo, during the Dance of the Dragons. Kermit was the most prominent of Tully lords, bringing them to the height of their power. </p>
<p><b>Kerwin</b> is a maester of the Citadel in service to House Chester of Greenshield. </p>
<p><b>Ketter</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Kevan Lannister</b> is a knight from House Lannister and is the younger brother of Tywin Lannister, Lord of Casterly Rock. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Ian Gelder. </p>
<p><b>Kezmya Pahl</b> is a child from the House of Pahl, one of the noble ruling families of Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Khiara the Great</b> was a God-Empress of Leng and the founder of the current dynasty that rules the island. She was of pure Lengii descent, but to please her subjects she took two husbands, one Lengii and one YiTish. This custom was followed by her daughters and their daughters in turn. By tradition the Lengii consort commands the imperial armies whereas the YiTish one commands the fleets. </p>
<p><b>Khorane Sathmantes</b> is the captain of the <i>Shayala's Dance</i>, a Lyseni galley owned by Salladhor Saan. Khorane is Lyseni. He has spent many years trading with the Seven Kingdoms. </p>
<p><b>Khrazz</b> is a celebrated pit fighter from Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Kiera of Tyrosh</b> was the wife of Prince Valarr Targaryen. An unknown amount of time after Valarr's death, she was married to Valarr's cousin, Prince Daeron Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>kindly man</b> is a servant of the Many-Faced God and the priest in charge of the House of Black and White in Braavos. One of the Faceless Men, he does not give his name. </p>
<p>The <b>Faceless Men</b> are a religious society of assassins who worship the Many-Faced God, a god of death. They are based in the House of Black and White, in the Free City of Braavos, though they claim to have originated in the Valyrian Freehold. </p>
<p><b>King Cutthroat</b> is a barber who became King of Astapor after killing Cleon the Second by slitting his throat. </p>
<p><b>Kinvara</b> is a red priestess, one of the high-ranking leaders in the religion of R'hllor, the Lord of Light. Her character was created specifically for the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, in which she is played by Ania Bukstein. She replaces Benerro, as the High Priest of Volantis, who supports Daenerys Targaryen, as well as the red priest, Moqorro, who is sent to Meereen to meet Daenerys. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Kirby Pimm</b> was a knight, during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Kirth</b> was a maester of the Citadel. He wrote the book <i>Songs the Drowned Men Sing</i>. He suggested that the Seastone Chair, which the original First Men settlers of the uninhabited Iron Islands discovered on Old Wyk, was left by visitors from across the Sunset Sea. </p>
<p><b>Kirth Vance</b> is a knight from House Vance of Atranta and the fourth son of Lord Norbert Vance. He has four brothers; Ser Ronald, Ser Ellery, Ser Hugo and Maester Jon. Kirth is a good friend of Ser Edmure Tully. </p>
<p><b>Kitty Frey</b> is the ninth wife of Lord Walder Frey in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. It is unknown what noble House she hails from. </p>
<p>This unidentified <b>Knight of Ninestars</b>, was the head of House Templeton during the latter stage of the First Blackfyre Rebellion. </p>
<p>The <b>Knight of the Red Chicken</b> supposedly fought at the Battle of the Blackwater. </p>
<p>The <b>Knight Without Armor</b> is a legendary knight of the Reach who lived during the Age of Heroes. Tales describe him as a knight even though those warriors came to Westeros thousands of years later with the coming of the Andals. </p>
<p><b>Kojja Mo</b> is the daughter of Quhuru Mo, the captain of the <i>Cinnamon Wind</i>. </p>
<p>The <i><b>Cinnamon Wind</b></i> is a swan ship captained by Quhuru Mo. Her home port is Tall Trees Town in the Summer Isles. Xhondo Dhoru is the mate, and the captain's daughter, Kojja Mo, captains the ship's red archers. The <i>Cinnamon Wind</i> is a large ship, and can outrun any galley with a good brisk wind behind her, but is helpless when becalmed. </p>
<p><b>Korra</b>, known as <b>Lady Korra</b> and <b>Korra the Cruel</b>, is a female pirate on Dagger Lake. Her ship, <i>Hag's Teeth</i>, is supposedly crewed by beautiful young maids who geld every man they capture. </p>
<p><b>Koss</b> is one of the criminals Yoren picked for the Night’s Watch when he cleaned out the dungeons of King’s Landing and is part of the group marching north to the Wall. </p>
<p><b>Kovarro</b> is a Dothraki bloodrider of Daenerys Targaryen. The character was created specifically for the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> and is played by Steven Cole. He replaces Jhogo as the third bloodrider, apparently being renamed to avoid confusion with Jhaqo, one of Drogo's kos. Though Kovarro corresponds to the book-version of Rakharo, as their descriptions from the books have basically being switched to the TV series. The name "Kovarro" was created by the writers of the series, based on the guide to making new Dothraki names that language consultant David J. Peterson developed for them. As Peterson explained in his blog, the name derives from the verb kovarat, which means 'to stand', meaning a tough guy who stands his ground. </p>
<p><b>Kraznys mo Nakloz</b> is a slaver in Astapor. He deals primarily in Unsullied. </p>
<p><b>Kromm</b> is an ironborn raider. </p>
<p><b>Kurleket</b> is a man-at-arms sworn to House Bracken. He is a great fat oaf with short-cropped hair and a pig's face. </p>
<p>The <b>Mountains of the Moon</b> are a series of mountains ruled by House Arryn of the Vale. The mountains border the riverlands to the west, the Bite to the north, and the Bay of Crabs to the south, and they surround the Vale proper. </p>
<p><b>Kurz</b> is one of the criminals Yoren picked for the Night’s Watch when he cleaned out the dungeons of King’s Landing and is part of the group marching north to the Wall. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Kyle</b>, known as the <b>Cat of Misty Moor</b> and <b>Kyle the Cat</b>, was a hedge knight from Misty Moor. </p>
<p><b>Kyle</b> is a member of the brotherhood without banners. </p>
<p>The <b>brotherhood without banners</b>, also known as the <b>knights of the hollow hill</b> and the <b>forgotten fellowship</b>, is an outlaw group who initially fights Lannister rule in the name of King Robert I Baratheon. Led by the Lightning Lord, Beric Dondarrion, the group is founded in the riverlands by soldiers and nobles who were sent by the then-Hand of the King, Eddard Stark, to bring Gregor Clegane to justice. After they are ambushed while crossing a ford and nearly defeated, the group continues the fight as a guerrilla group. Their numbers increase as they are joined by defeated soldiers from other battles, deserters, and refugees from the War of the Five Kings. Every man of the brotherhood receives a knighthood from Beric. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Kyle Condon</b> is a knight of House Condon in service to House Cerwyn. According to Roose Bolton, he is Lord Medger Cerwyn's right hand man. However, the Appendix of <i>A Storm of Swords</i> lists him as a knight in the service of Ser Wylis Manderly. </p>
<p><b>Kyle Connington</b> was the Lord of Griffin's Roost and the head of House Connington during the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Kyle Royce</b> was a member of House Royce during the reign of King Aerys II Targaryen. His relation to Yohn Royce, the Lord of Runestone, is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Kyleg of the Wooden Ear</b> is a free folk leader. </p>
<p><b>Kym</b> was the maester assigned to Riverrun when Lord Hoster Tully's children were young. He is deceased, and Riverrun's maester is now Vyman. </p>
<p><b>Kyra</b> is a tavern wench who works at the Smoking Log in the winter town outside of Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Kyra Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, the daughter of Ser Jared Frey and Alys Frey. Kyra is married to Ser Garse Goodbrook, with whom she has two children; Walder and Jeyne Goodbrook. </p>
<p><b>Kyrie</b> was a maester of the Citadel who served House Baratheon of Storm's End during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lacey</b> was an inhabitant of Pennytree. She was raped to death by the forces of House Lannister during the War of the Five Kings. </p>
<p><b>"Lady Farts-a-Lot"</b> was the nickname Princess Aerea Targaryen gave a member of Rhaena Targaryen's court in Dragonstone. </p>
<p>The <b>Lady of the Leaves</b> is an old, thin white-haired lady who lives in a village that rests in the trees. The hidden village is located in the Riverlands near the road to Hayford in the Crownlands. </p>
<p><b>Lady Stork</b> is a mummer in Braavos. She is part of the mummer's troupe at the Gate. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, the character is named <b>Lady Crane</b> and is portrayed by Essie Davis. </p>
<p><b>Laena Penrose</b> was a member of House Penrose and the first daughter of Lord Ronnel Penrose and his wife Princess Elaena Targaryen. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Laena Velaryon</b> was the eldest child and only daughter of Lord Corlys Velaryon and Princess Rhaenys Targaryen. She was the second wife of Prince Daemon Targaryen and gave birth to his twin daughters, Rhaena and Baela Targaryen. Laena was a dragonrider and rode the dragon Vhagar. She died from complications of childbirth. </p>
<p><b>Laena Velaryon</b> was a noblewoman of House Velaryon, the daughter of Lord Alyn Velaryon and his wife, Lady Baela Targaryen. She was named after her paternal great-aunt and maternal grandmother, Lady Laena Velaryon. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Laenor Velaryon</b> was the only son of Lord Corlys Velaryon and Princess Rhaenys Targaryen. He was the heir to Driftmark and the first husband of his second cousin, Princess Rhaenyra Targaryen. Rhaenyra gave birth to three sons during their marriage, Jacaerys, Lucerys, and Joffrey, although it was rumored that they had been fathered by Rhaenyra's lover instead of Laenor. He was a dragonrider whose dragon was Seasmoke. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lambert Turnberry</b> is a knight from House Turnberry. He wears a patch over his perfectly good right eye. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lambert Whitewater</b> is a knight in the service of King Stannis Baratheon. He is one of the queen's men. </p>
<p><b>Lamprey</b> is a gaoler on Dragonstone. </p>
<p><b>Lancel Lannister</b> is a member of House Lannister of Casterly Rock and is the eldest son of Ser Kevan Lannister. Lancel and his cousin, Tyrek Lannister, are squires to King Robert I Baratheon. </p>
<p><b>Robert I Baratheon</b> is the King of the Andals, the Rhoynar, and the First Men, Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and Protector of the Realm of Westeros, and the head of House Baratheon of King's Landing. Robert was crowned king after King Aerys II Targaryen, his first cousin once removed, was killed during Robert's Rebellion. Following the war, Robert married Cersei Lannister to ensure political stability. With her, Robert has three children: Joffrey, Myrcella, and Tommen. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Mark Addy. </p>
<p><b>Lancel I Lannister</b>, formally styled <b>Lancel Lannister, the First of His Name</b>, was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. He rode to war against the Gardener Kings of the Reach and conquered as far south as Old Oak. </p>
<p><b>Lancel IV Lannister</b>, formally styled <b>Lancel Lannister, the Fourth of His Name</b>, was a King of the Rock from House Lannister of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Lancel V Lannister</b> was a King of the Rock. </p>
<p><b>Lann the Clever</b> is the legendary hero who founded House Lannister in the Age of Heroes, winkling Casterly Rock from the Casterlys with only his wits. Lann is popular amongst singers and storytellers. </p>
<p><b>Lanna</b> is a pretty fourteen-year-old prostitute at the Happy Port brothel in Braavos. She is the daughter of another prostitute, the Sailor's Wife. Merry, the proprietor of the Happy Port, charges three times as much for Lanna as other whores. </p>
<p>The <b>Happy Port</b> is a brothel in Braavos, near Ragman's Harbor. It sits across an alley from the Mummer's Ship, and abuts a canal. It is run by Meralyn. The brothel is decorated with a mural of a purple galleas, crewed by women wearing nothing but thigh-high boots. </p>
<p><b>Lanna</b> is a serving wench and prostitute at the Peach in Stoney Sept. </p>
<p>The <b>Peach</b> is an inn and brothel located at the eastern side of Stoney Sept's main market square. It has white-washed walls, and its sign is a wooden shingle painted like a peach with a bite taken out of it. The inn is run by Tansy, while Alyce, Bella, Cass, Helly, Jyzene, and Lanna work there as prostitutes or "peaches". Next to the inn are stables. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Lanna Lannister</b> is the daughter of Ser Damion Lannister and Shiera Crakehall. She is the sister of Ser Lucion Lannister and the wife of Lord Antario Jast. </p>
<p><b>Larence Snow</b> is the natural son of Lord Halys Hornwood. He is under the guardianship of Galbart Glover, Master of Deepwood Motte. He has a half-brother, Daryn Hornwood. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Larissa Velaryon</b> was a noblewoman of House Velaryon. She became a close friend and favorite of her cousin Princess Rhaena Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lark</b>, known as <b>the Sisterman</b> and <b>Lark the Sisterman</b>, is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Larra Blackmont</b> is the Lady of Blackmont and the head of House Blackmont. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Larra Rogare</b> was a member of House Rogare of Lys. She married Prince Viserys Targaryen, the younger brother of King Aegon III Targaryen. With Viserys, Larra had three children: King Aegon IV, Prince Aemon, and Queen Naerys Targaryen. She eventually abandoned Viserys and returned to Lys. </p>
<p><b>Larraq</b>, known as <b>the Lash</b> for his weapons of choice, is a former slave now in training with Ser Barristan Selmy to become a knight. He serves Barristan as a squire in Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Larys Strong</b>, known as <b>Larys Clubfoot</b> or <b>the Clubfoot</b>, was the Lord of Harrenhal and head of House Strong during the latter part of the reign of Viserys I Targaryen and the reign of Aegon II Targaryen. He served on the small council as the master of whisperers and Lord Confessor for both kings. </p>
<p>The <b>last hero</b> of the First Men lived during the Long Night according to Westerosi legends. It is unknown if there is a connection with Azor Ahai, a person who saves the world from the darkness in legends from Essos. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Laswell Peake</b> is an exiled lord and sellsword in service to the Golden Company. His brothers Pykewood and Torman Peake serve in the company with him. </p>
<p><b>Laurence Karstark</b> was a member of House Karstark mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Laurent</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel. He wrote the book <i>Old Places of the Trident</i>, which states that there were thirty one weirwoods crowning High Heart at the time Erreg the Kinslayer came across the great hill and slaughtered the Children of the Forest and First Men defending it. </p>
<p><b>Layna</b> is the young daughter of an owner of an alehouse on the Goldroad. </p>
<p><b>Leaf</b> is one of the children of the forest in service to the last greenseer. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Octavia Alexandru in Season 4 and Kae Alexander in Season 6. </p>
<p><b>Leana Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, the youngest daughter of Lothar Frey and Leonella Lefford. She is an infant. </p>
<p><b>Leathers</b> is a member of the free folk of the haunted forest who joins the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Lelia Lannister</b> was a lady of House Lannister and Queen of the Iron Islands through her marriage to King Harmund II Hoare. </p>
<p><b>Lem</b>, also known as <b>Lem Lemoncloak</b>, is a one-time soldier. It is unknown if Lem is his given name; according to Tom of Sevenstreams, Lem is named after the yellow cloak he wears. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Lem is portrayed by Jóhannes Haukur Jóhannesson. </p>
<p><b>Lem</b> was a peasant sworn to House Osgrey. </p>
<p><b>Lemore</b>, also known as <b>Lady Lemore</b>, is a septa of the Faith of the Seven and the spiritual tutor for Young Griff. </p>
<p><b>Lenn</b> is a wildling raider. </p>
<p><b>Lennocks</b> was the brother of Jack-Be-Lucky and Lister. He was killed by the forces of House Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Lenwood Tawney</b>, nicknamed <b>Little Lenwood Tawney</b>, is a fiddler from House Tawney in the Iron Islands. </p>
<p><b>Lenyl</b> is a wildling raider. He is a part of the war band lead by Rattleshirt. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Leo Blackbar</b> is a knight from House Blackbar. He is married to Olene Tyrell, a cousin of Lord Mace Tyrell. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Leo Costayne</b>, known as <b>the Sea Lion</b>, was a knight of House Costayne and lord admiral of the Reach during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Leo Lefford</b> is the Lord of the Golden Tooth and the head of House Lefford. </p>
<p>The <b>Golden Tooth</b>, also called <b>the Tooth</b>, is the seat of House Lefford in the westerlands. It is located along the river road and is east of Ashemark and Sarsfield, west of Riverrun and Pinkmaiden, and north of Hornvale. </p>
<p><b>Leo Tyrell</b> was a head of House Tyrell and the second High Steward of Highgarden. He was the son of Gareth Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Leo Tyrell</b>, known as <b>Lazy Leo</b>, is a member of House Tyrell, a first cousin of Mace Tyrell, the Lord of Highgarden. He is the second son of Ser Moryn Tyrell, the commander of Oldtown's City Watch. Leo is a novice at the Citadel. </p>
<p>The <b>Citadel</b> is a complex of buildings in Oldtown that serves as the central home to the order of the maesters. The name is also employed to refer to order of maesters as an institution, or the higher placed members. At the Citadel, the residing archmaesters teach and train new students, and convene in the Conclave. The Citadel is funded by taxes from Oldtown and payments from lords for the service of maesters. Maesters rigorously copy books at the Citadel. Leyton Hightower, the Lord of Oldtown, includes Protector of the Citadel among his titles. </p>
<p><b>Leo Tyrell</b>, known as <b>Leo Longthorn</b>, was the Lord of Highgarden and head of House Tyrell during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Leo Tyrell</b> is a knight of House Tyrell, the son of Ser Victor Tyrell. He is married to Alys Beesbury, with whom he has five children. </p>
<p><b>Leobald Tallhart</b> is the younger brother of Ser Helman Tallhart and is the castellan of Torrhen's Square. </p>
<p><b>Torrhen's Square</b> is a castle in the north and the seat of House Tallhart. It is south of the wolfswood, southwest of Winterfell, and north of Barrowton, on the northern shore of a large lake. A river from the lake leads south to the Saltspear. </p>
<p><b>Leona Tyrell</b> is a member of House Tyrell. She is the daughter of Ser Leo Tyrell and Alys Beesbury, making her a distant cousin to the ruling branch. </p>
<p><b>Leona Woolfield</b> is a member of House Woolfield and is the wife of Ser Wylis Manderly. They have two daughters, Wynafryd and Wylla Manderly. </p>
<p><b>Leonella Lefford</b> is a member of House Lefford married to Lothar Frey, with whom she has four daughters: Tysane, Walda, Emberlei and Leana. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Leonette Fossoway</b> is the wife of Ser Garlan Tyrell. She is a noblewoman of House Fossoway, though it is unclear which branch of the family she is from. </p>
<p><b>Leowyn Corbray</b> was the Lord of Heart's Home and head of House Corbray during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons, later becoming Protector of the Realm in the minority of King Aegon III Targaryen. He had a younger brother, Ser Corwyn Corbray, who wielded Lady Forlorn. </p>
<p><b>Leslyn</b> works at the Peach in Stoney Sept. The character's gender and occupation are not mentioned. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Leslyn Haigh</b> is a knight of House Haigh and the husband of Perriane Frey. He is the father of Ser Harys, Ser Donnel and Alyn Haigh. </p>
<p><b>Lester</b>, known as <b>Red Lester</b>, is a guard sworn to House Lannister. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lester Dabell</b> was a knight during the reign of Daeron II Targaryen. He had two brothers: Ser Ernest and Ser Pascal Dabell. </p>
<p><b>Lester Morrigen</b> is the Lord of Crow's Nest and the head of House Morrigen in the stormlands. His heir is his younger brother, Ser Richard Morrigen. </p>
<p><b>Crow's Nest</b> is the seat of House Morrigen in the stormlands. It is located in mountainous terrain between Griffin's Roost and Stonehelm, along the western edge of Cape Wrath and the rainwood. </p>
<p><b>Lew</b> is a member of the guard at Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Left Hand Lew</b> is a steward of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Long Lew</b> is a guard at Riverrun. </p>
<p><b>Lewis Lanster</b> is a sellsword and member of the Windblown. He is said to be the company's best archer. </p>
<p>The <b>Windblown</b> are a mercenary company of two thousand mounted horse and foot soldiers. They are found in Essos near the Free Cities. They are led by a captain known as the Tattered Prince. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Lewyn Nymeros Martell</b>, better known simply as <b>Lewyn Martell</b>, was a knight from House Martell who served as a member of Aerys II Targaryen's Kingsguard. He was the uncle of the current Prince of Dorne, Doran Martell. </p>
<p>The <b>Kingsguard</b>, also known poetically as the <b>White Swords</b> or <b>white cloaks</b>, are the royal bodyguards of the Iron Throne. Regarded as the&nbsp;finest knights in the Seven Kingdoms, they are sworn to protect their king and the royal family with their own lives, to obey his commands, and to keep his secrets. The Kingsguard are sworn for life and are forbidden from owning land, taking a wife, or fathering children, although they can hold non-hereditary commands, such as being warden or Hand of the King. </p>
<p><b>Lewys</b>, known as <b>Lewys the Fishwife</b>, is a man sworn to House Baratheon of Dragonstone. </p>
<p><b>Lewys Lydden</b> is the Lord of the Deep Den and head of House Lydden. </p>
<p><b>Lewys Piper</b>, better known as <b>Lew Piper</b> or <b>Little Lew Piper</b>, is a member of House Piper, a younger son of Lord Clement Piper. </p>
<p><b>Lex Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Leygood</b> was the head of House Leygood during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Leyla Hightower</b> is a daughter of Lord Leyton Hightower. She is married to Ser Jon Cupps. </p>
<p><b>Leyton Hightower</b>, known as the <b>Old Man of Oldtown</b>, is the Lord of the Hightower and head of House Hightower. His other titles include the Voice of Oldtown, Lord of the Port, Defender of the Citadel, and Beacon of the South. Leyton's flagship is <i>Honor of Oldtown</i>. </p>
<p><b>Oldtown</b> is one of the largest and oldest cities in Westeros, built by the First Men before the Andal invasion. Oldtown was constructed around the Hightower, the seat of House Hightower in the center of the city. Oldtown is home to the Citadel and houses the Starry Sept, formerly the seat of the High Septon of the Faith of the Seven. The demonym used for its inhabitants is "Oldtowner". </p>
<p><b>Lharys</b> is a man-at-arms in service to House Bracken. He is an ungainly man, with wild tufts of rust-colored hair that stick out of a conical cap. </p>
<p><b>Lia Serry</b> is a member of House Serry. She is married to Ser Theodore Tyrell. They have two children, Elinor and Luthor Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Liane Vance</b> is a noblewoman of House Vance of Wayfarer's Rest. She is the eldest daughter of the heir of Wayfarer's Rest, Ser Karyl Vance. </p>
<p><b>Lianna Velaryon</b> was a noblewoman of House Velaryon during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. She was one of the ladies-in-waiting to her cousin, Queen Rhaena Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lily</b> was the second of the four bastard children of King Aegon IV Targaryen and his second mistress, Megette. </p>
<p><b>Liomond Lashare</b>, dubbed the <b>Lord of Battles</b>, was a sellsword captain who became one of the infamous Band of Nine, the instigators of the War of the Ninepenny Kings. </p>
<p><b>Lionel Hunter</b> is a member of House Hunter mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Lister</b> was the brother of Jack-Be-Lucky and Lennocks. He was killed by the forces of House Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Little Lord Lazyeye</b> was the nickname Prince Oberyn Martell gave to an unidentified suitor of his sister Elia Martell during the trip the siblings took in 273&nbsp;AC, during which their mother hoped to betroth either one of them, or both. </p>
<p><b>Lo Bu</b>, known as <b>the Boy Too Bold By Half</b>, was a God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti and the forty third and final ruler of his dynasty. </p>
<p><b>Lo Doq</b>, called <b>Lo Lackwit</b>, was a God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti and the thirty-fourth ruler of his dynasty. He was a simpleton cursed with an affliction that caused him to jerk and stagger when he walked, and drool when he tried to speak. Nonetheless he ruled wisely for more than thirty years. There are those, however, that suggest the true ruler was his formidable wife, Empress Bathi Ma Lo. </p>
<p><b>Lo Han</b> was a God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti and the forty second ruler of his dynasty. Three times he led armies into the Plains of the Jogos Nhai with the goal of bringing the Jogos Nhai to heel, even compeling handfuls of <i>jhats</i> to sweat fealty to him and forswear raiding forever. Yet by the time of his death the Jogos Nhai had become bolder and more rapacious than when he had first donned the imperial regalia. He was succeeded by his son Lo Bu. </p>
<p><b>Lo Tho</b>, called <b>Lo Longspoon</b> and <b>Lo the Terrible</b>, was a God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti and the twenty-second ruler of his dynasty. He was a reputed sorcerer and cannibal, said to have supped upon the living brains of his enemies with a long, pearl-handled spoon, after the tops of their skulls had been removed, earning his monikers. </p>
<p><b>Lodos</b> was a priest of the Drowned God who claimed to be his god's living son. </p>
<p><b>Lodos the Twice-Drowned</b> was a man who boasted of being the priest-king "Lodos" reborn, during the reign of King Aenys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lollys Stokeworth</b> is the youngest daughter of Lady Tanda Stokeworth of Stokeworth. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lomas Estermont</b> is a knight of House Estermont and is the father of Ser Andrew Estermont. </p>
<p><b>Lomas Longstrider</b> was a famous scribe and traveler of Westerosi origin. He is famously quoted as saying, "The gods made seven wonders and mortal man made nine". </p>
<p><b>Lommy Greenhands</b> is one of the orphan boys Yoren recruited for the Night's Watch in King’s Landing and is part of the band marching north to the Wall. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Eros Vlahos. </p>
<p>The <b>Night's Watch</b> is a military order dedicated to holding the Wall, the immense fortification on the northern border of the Seven Kingdoms, defending the realms of men from what lies beyond the Wall. The order's foundation dates back to the Age of Heroes, at the time when the Others were pushed back. The men of Night's Watch wear only black, and they are known as <b>black brothers</b>. Recruits who join the Watch are said to <b>take the black</b>. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Lomys</b> is a maester of the Citadel. He serves House Tyrell at Highgarden. </p>
<p><b>Longwater Pyke</b> is an ironborn raider in Victarion Greyjoy's crew aboard the <i>Iron Victory</i>. He is a bastard from the Iron Islands. </p>
<p><b>Longwaters</b> (given name unknown) was a knight of great renown and son of Ser Jon Waters, the bastard son of Princess Elaena Targaryen and Lord Alyn Velaryon. As a trueborn son, he added "Long" to his "Waters" name to show he was not himself baseborn. His line survives today in Rennifer Longwaters. </p>
<p><b>Lonnel Snow</b>, known as <b>Lonny</b>, was a bastard son of Lord Brandon Stark and Lady Wylla Fenn. He had three younger half-siblings by his father; Rodwell, Beron and Arsa. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Loras Tyrell</b>, also known as <b>the Knight of Flowers</b>, is a knight from House Tyrell and the third son of Lord Mace Tyrell of Highgarden and his wife, Lady Alerie Hightower. He is a highly skilled knight and jouster. His tournament successes, dazzling good looks, and ostentatious showmanship has made him a celebrated figure in the courts of the Seven Kingdoms. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> Loras is portrayed by Finn Jones. </p>
<p><b>Lorax Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Lorcas</b> is an old acolyte of the Citadel. </p>
<p><b>Lorcas the Learned</b> was a member of the Poor Fellows during the Faith Militant uprising. </p>
<p>The <b>Lord of Bones</b>, also mocked as <b>Rattleshirt</b>, is a free folk leader of renown. His given name is unknown. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Edward Dogliani and Ross O'Hennessy. </p>
<p><b>"Lord Pigface"</b> was the nickname Princess Aerea Targaryen gave a member of Rhaena Targaryen's court in Dragonstone. </p>
<p><b>"Lordling"</b> is how Arya Stark refers to a secret servant of the Many-Faced God in the House of Black and White in Braavos and a Faceless Man. </p>
<p><b>Loren I Lannister</b>, called <b>Loren the Last</b>, was the last King of the Rock and the head of House Lannister at the time of Aegon's Conquest. He submitted to the rule of House Targaryen after surviving the Field of Fire, and became the first Lord of Casterly Rock and Warden of the West. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lorence Roxton</b> was a knight from House Roxton and a member of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lorent Caswell</b> is the Lord of Bitterbridge and head of House Caswell. </p>
<p><b>Lorent Grandison</b> was the Lord of Grandview and the head of House Grandison. He was a regent for Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lorent Lorch</b> is a landed knight and the head of House Lorch. He was the heir presumptive of Ser Amory Lorch. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lorent Marbrand</b> was a knight from House Marbrand and a member of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Viserys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lorent Tyrell</b> is a member of House Tyrell, a distant cousin to the ruling branch. Lorent is the third and youngest son of Ser Leo Tyrell and Alys Beesbury. </p>
<p><b>Lorent Tyrell</b> was a member of House Tyrell and a High Steward of Highgarden during the reign of Mern VI Gardener, King of the Reach. </p>
<p><b>Loreon Lannister</b> refers to: </p>
<p>King <b>Loreon Lannister</b>, known as <b>Loreon the Lion</b>, was the first true King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock in historical record. </p>
<p><b>Loreon II Lannister</b>, formally styled <b>Loreon Lannister, the Second of His Name</b>, was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Loreon III Lannister</b>, formally styled <b>Loreon Lannister, the Third of His Name</b>, was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. He lost all of his father's conquests and earned the mocking name of <b>Loreon the Limp</b>. </p>
<p><b>Loreon IV Lannister</b>, known as <b>Loreon the Lackwit</b>, was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Loreon V Lannister</b>, formally styled <b>Loreon Lannister, the Fifth of His Name</b>, was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. He became known as <b>Queen Lorea</b> for he was fond of dressing in his wife's clothing and wandering the docks of Lannisport in the guise of a common whore. He was the grandson of Loreon the Lackwit. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Loreth Lansdale</b> was a knight from House Lansdale and a member of Rhaenyra Targaryen's Queensguard. </p>
<p><b>Loreza Sand</b> is the youngest bastard daughter of Prince Oberyn Martell and his longtime paramour, Ellaria Sand. She and her sisters are known as the Sand Snakes. </p>
<p><b>Lorimar Peake</b> was the Lord of Starpike and Dunstonbury, and the head of House Peake during the reign of Perceon III Gardener, King of the Reach. </p>
<p><b>Lorimas Mudd</b> is a sellsword in service to the Golden Company. As a serjeant, he is a high-ranking officer. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lorimer the Belly</b> is a hedge knight in service to Lord Leo Lefford. </p>
<p><b>Lormelle Long Lance</b> was once defeated by Ser Barristan Selmy. It is unknown if this was in combat or during a tourney. </p>
<p><b>Loron Greyjoy</b>, known as the <b>Old Kraken</b>, was a High King of the Iron Islands from House Greyjoy. </p>
<p><b>Loron Greyjoy</b>, known as the <b>Bard</b>, was a Lord of the Iron Islands and head of House Greyjoy. According to Archmaester Haereg's <i>History of the Ironborn</i>, Loron had a great and tragic friendship with Ser Desmond Mallister. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Lorra Royce</b> was a member of House Royce, she was married to Lord Beron Stark, second son of Lord Brandon Stark, together they had seven children; Donnor, Willam, Artos, Berena, Alysanne, Errold, and Rodrik Stark. </p>
<p><b>Black Lorren</b> is an infamous ironborn raider. </p>
<p><b> Lorren Longaxe</b> is one of the crew on Asha Greyjoy's ship, <i>Black Wind</i>. </p>
<p><b>Loso</b>, dubbed <b>Loso the Lame</b>, was a Dothraki <i>khal</i> who lived during the Century of Blood. He was one of the four <i>khals</i> that fought in the Field of Crows. </p>
<p><b>Lothar</b> was the maester at Whitewalls during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lothar Bracken</b> was a Lord of the Stone Hedge and head of House Bracken. </p>
<p><b>Lothar Frey</b>, often called <b>Lame Lothar</b>, is a member of House Frey, the twelfth son of Lord Walder Frey, and his eldest son by his fourth wife Lady Alyssa Blackwood. He is portrayed by Tom Brooke and Daniel Tuite in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Lothar Mallery</b> is the head of House Mallery. </p>
<p><b>Lotho Lornel</b> is a dealer in old books and scrolls in Braavos. </p>
<p><b>Braavos</b> is the wealthiest and likely the most powerful of the Free Cities. It is located in a lagoon on the northwestern end of Essos, where the narrow sea and the Shivering Sea meet. Braavos is also known as <b>Braavos of the Hundred Isles</b> and the <b>Secret City</b>, a name also attributed to the city Nefer, the last remaining city of N'ghai. Braavos is sometimes referred to as the "bastard daughter of Valyria". </p>
<p><b>Lotho Rogare</b> was a member of House Rogare, a Lysene noble banking family. He was the son of Lysandro Rogare, the First Magister of Lys. </p>
<p><b>Lothor Brune</b> is a freerider. He is related to the Brunes of Brownhollow in the Crackclaw Point region of the crownlands. </p>
<p><b>Lothor Burley</b> was Lord Commander of the Night's Watch during the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. He was originally from House Burley. </p>
<p><b>Loyal Spear</b> is an Unsullied sworn to Daenerys Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lucamore Strong</b>, also known as <b>Lucamore the Lusty</b>, was a knight from House Strong and a member of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. When it was discovered he had broken the vows of the Kingsguard, he was sent to the Night's Watch by King Jaehaerys I. </p>
<p><b>Lucan</b> is a blacksmith at Harrenhal. He is master at the armory. </p>
<p><b>Lucan</b> was a Grand Maester of the Citadel who served on the small council under an unknown Targaryen King. </p>
<p><b>Lucan Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lucantine Woodwright</b> is the brother of Ser Portifer Woodwright and is a household knight in King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Lucas Blackwood</b> is the second son of Lord Tytos Blackwood of Raventree Hall. </p>
<p><b>Raventree Hall</b> is the seat of House Blackwood in Blackwood Vale in the riverlands. The castle is located north of Riverrun, southwest of Oldstones, and west of Fairmarket. Ironman's Bay is to the northwest. </p>
<p><b>Lucas Codd</b>, known as <b>Left-Hand Lucas Codd</b>, is an ironborn raider and member of House Codd. </p>
<p><b>Lucas Corbray</b> is a knight of House Corbray. He is the younger brother of Lord Lyonel and Ser Lyn Corbray. </p>
<p><b>Lucas Harroway</b> was the Lord of Harrenhal and head of House Harroway during the reigns of kings Aenys I Targaryen and Maegor I Targaryen. He served as Hand of the King for Maegor I, his son-by-marriage. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lucas Inchfield</b>, known as <b>Lucas Longinch</b>, was a knight from House Inchfield and was the castellan of Coldmoat for Lady Rohanne Webber. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lucas Leygood</b> was a knight from House Leygood who served as Commander of the City Watch during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lucas Lothston</b> was a head of House Lothston, Lord of Harrenhal, and Hand of the King. </p>
<p><b>Lucas Lothston</b>, also known as <b>the Pander</b>, was a Lord of Harrenhal and head of House Lothston. He is remembered for bad deeds and fathering Manfryd Lothston. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lucas Nayland</b> was a knight from House Nayland during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lucas Roote</b> is a member of House Roote. He is squiring for Ser Andrey Charlton. </p>
<p><b>Lucas Tyrell</b> is a member of House Tyrell, a distant cousin of the ruling branch. He is the son of Ser Leo Tyrell and Alys Beesbury. </p>
<p><b>Luceon Frey</b> is a septon of the Faith of the Seven. He serves at the Great Sept of Baelor and is among the Most Devout. He is the fifth son of Lord Walder Frey and is the second son born of Walder's second wife, Cyrenna Swann. </p>
<p>The <b>Most Devout</b> are a council of the highest ranking clergy of the Faith of the Seven. </p>
<p><b>Luceon</b>, better known as <b>Luceon of Tarth</b> was a singer from the island of Tarth. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Luceon Templeton</b>, Knight of Ninestars, was an Andal knight and the head of House Templeton during the latter stage of the Andal invasion in the Vale. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Lucerys Velaryon</b>, also known as <b>Luke</b>, was the secondborn son of Princess Rhaenyra Targaryen and her first husband, Ser Laenor Velaryon. He was a dragonrider whose dragon was Arrax. </p>
<p><b>Lucerys Velaryon</b> was the Lord of the Tides and head of House Velaryon during the reign of King Aerys II Targaryen, serving on the small council as the king's master of ships. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Lucias Vypren</b> is the head of House Vypren. He is married to Lythene Frey, the second daughter of Lord Walder Frey. They have two children together: Elyana and Damon. </p>
<p><b>Lucifer Dryland</b> was a King of the Brimstone and Lord of Hellgate Hall. The last of House Dryland, he was one of the six kings sent to the Wall by Nymeria throughout Nymeria's War. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Lucifer Hardy</b> was lord and head of House Hardy. He is remembered for bringing peace to Crackclaw Point, though it did not survive him long. </p>
<p><b>Lucifer Justman</b>, known as <b>Lucifer the Liar</b>, claimed the title of river king or King of the Trident in the generations after the riverlands were conquered by the Storm King Arlan III Durrandon. Lucifer had a brief, inglorious reign before being put down by the power of Storm's End. His connection with the extinct Justman dynasty is unconfirmed. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lucifer Long</b> is a Westerosi knight and sellsword and is a member of the Windblown. The lanky Lucifer bears a grudge against Caggo, who took a slave girl from him and instead of returning her after he was done, Caggo killed her. </p>
<p><b>Lucifer Massey</b> was the Lord of Stonedance, a knight, and head of House Massey during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lucimore Botley</b> is the half-brother of Lord Sawane Botley. </p>
<p><b>Lucinda Tully</b>, née <b>Broome</b>, was a lady of House Broome who wed Prentys Tully, Lord of Riverrun. </p>
<p><b>Lucinda Penrose</b> was a member of House Penrose during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. She was a companion to Queen Daenaera Velaryon. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lucion Lannister</b> is the son of Ser Damion Lannister and Shiera Crakehall. </p>
<p><b>Luco Prestayn</b> is a member of House Prestayn of Braavos and is the captain of the trading galley <i>Lady Bright</i>. </p>
<p>Septon <b>Lucos</b> is a septon of the Faith of the Seven. He is currently assigned to Runestone. </p>
<p><b>Lucos Chyttering</b>, called <b>Little Lucos</b>, is a member of House Chyttering. </p>
<p><b>Likely Luke</b> is a member of the Brotherhood without Banners. </p>
<p>The <b>brotherhood without banners</b>, also known as the <b>knights of the hollow hill</b> and the <b>forgotten fellowship</b>, is an outlaw group who initially fights Lannister rule in the name of King Robert I Baratheon. Led by the Lightning Lord, Beric Dondarrion, the group is founded in the riverlands by soldiers and nobles who were sent by the then-Hand of the King, Eddard Stark, to bring Gregor Clegane to justice. After they are ambushed while crossing a ford and nearly defeated, the group continues the fight as a guerrilla group. Their numbers increase as they are joined by defeated soldiers from other battles, deserters, and refugees from the War of the Five Kings. Every man of the brotherhood receives a knighthood from Beric. </p>
<p><b>Luke of Longtown</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. He comes from Longtown. </p>
<p><b>Lum</b> is a guard in service to House Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Luna Royce</b> is a member of House Royce mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Luthor Largent</b> was a lowborn knight from House Largent who served as an officer and later the commander of the City Watch of King's Landing during the reign of King Viserys I Targaryen and the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Luthor Tyrell</b> was the Lord of Highgarden and the head of House Tyrell. He is the father of the current lord, Mace Tyrell. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Luthor Tyrell</b> was a knight of House Tyrell, a first cousin of Mace Tyrell, the Lord of Highgarden. He is the first son of Ser Moryn Tyrell, the commander of Oldtown's City Watch. Luthor was married to Elyn Norridge with whom he had three children, Ser Theodore, Olene, and Medwick Tyrell. He is deceased. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Moryn Tyrell</b> is a knight from House Tyrell. The uncle of Mace Tyrell, Lord of Highgarden, Moryn is the Lord Commander of the City Watch of Oldtown. </p>
<p><b>Luthor Tyrell</b> is a member of a junior branch of House Tyrell, being the grandson of Ser Luthor Tyrell, a first cousin of Mace Tyrell, the Lord of Highgarden. The only son of Ser Theodore Tyrell and his wife, Lia Serry, Luthor has an older sister, Elinor Tyrell. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Theodore Tyrell</b> is the eldest son of Ser Luthor Tyrell and Elyn Norridge. The knight is married to Lia Serry. They have two children, Elinor and Luthor. </p>
<p><b>Luton</b> is a man-at-arms sworn to House Bolton. He is one of the Bastard's Boys. </p>
<p><b>Luwin</b> is a maester in the service of House Stark at Winterfell. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Donald Sumpter. </p>
<p><b>Lyanna Mormont</b> is the youngest daughter of Lady Maege Mormont. She was named after Lyanna Stark. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Lyanna is portrayed by Bella Ramsey. </p>
<p><b>Lyanna Stark</b> was the only daughter of Lord Rickard Stark and his wife, Lady Lyarra Stark. She had two older brothers, Brandon and Eddard, and one younger brother, Benjen. Her abduction by Prince Rhaegar Targaryen was the event that ultimately triggered Robert's Rebellion and led to the downfall of the Targaryen dynasty. She is portrayed by both Cordelia Hill (as a child) in Season 6 and Aisling Franciosi (as a young adult) during Season 6 and Season 7 flashbacks in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Lyanna Stark</b> was a member of House Stark. She was only daughter of Lord Cregan Stark and his third and last wife, Lady Lynara Stark. </p>
<p><b>Lyanne Glover</b> was a noblewoman from House Glover during the early part of the third century after Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Lyarra Stark</b> was a noblewoman from House Stark during the reign of kings Aegon V, Jaehaerys II and Aerys II Targaryen. She was a daughter of Rodrik Stark and Arya Flint, and the younger sister of Branda Stark. </p>
<p><b>Lyessa Flint</b> is the Lady of Widow's Watch and the head of House Flint of Widow's Watch. She is the mother of Robin Flint. </p>
<p><b>Widow's Watch</b> is the seat of House Flint of Widow's Watch in the north. It is located at the end of a peninsula between the Shivering Sea and the Bite, east of Ramsgate and the Broken Branch. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lyle Bracken</b> was a knight of House Bracken and a member of the Warrior's Sons at the start of the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>

<p><b>Lyman Darry</b> is a nobleman of House Darry and the son and heir of Ser Raymun Darry, the lord of Castle Darry. </p>
<p><b>Lyman Lannister</b> was the Lord of Casterly Rock, Warden of the West, Shield of Lannisport, and head of House Lannister during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen and the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. He was married to Lady Jocasta Tarbeck. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lymond Fisher</b>, Knight of Oldstones, was a knight who claimed the title of river king or King of the Trident in the generations after the riverlands were conquered by the Storm King Arlan III Durrandon. Lymond had a brief, inglorious reign, presumably ruling from Oldstones, before being put down by the might of Storm's End. His connection with the extinct Fisher dynasty is unconfirmed. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Lymond Lynderly</b> is a knight of House Lynderly. </p>

<p><b>Lymond Pease</b> is a sellsword in service to the Golden Company. As a serjeant, he is a high-ranking officer. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lymond Vikary</b> is a landed knight and the head of House Vikary. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Lyn Corbray</b> is a knight from House Corbray who wields Lady Forlorn, a sword of Valyrian steel. He is the heir of his elder brother, Lord Lyonel Corbray of Heart's Home. </p>

<p><b>Lyonel Strong</b> was the Lord of Harrenhal and the head of House Strong during the reign of King Viserys I Targaryen. He served as both master of laws and Hand of the King for Viserys. He had four children from his three marriages: Ser Harwin, Larys and two daughters. According to Grand Maester Munkun and Septon Eustace, Lyonel also sired a bastard daughter, Alys Rivers. </p>

<p><b> Lyra</b> was a novice, and later septa of the Faith of the Seven, who was a beloved religious tutor of Queen Alysanne Targaryen. </p>

<p>Lady <b>Lysa Arryn</b>, née <b>Tully</b>, is a member of House Tully. She is the youngest daughter of Lord Hoster Tully of Riverrun and his wife, Lady Minisa Whent, and wife of Jon Arryn, the Lord of the Eyrie and Hand of the King to King Robert I Baratheon. Since her husband's death, she is the Lady Regent of the Vale of Arryn. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, she is played by Kate Dickie. </p>
<p><b>House Tully of Riverrun</b> is one of the Great Houses of the Seven Kingdoms. Lord Hoster Tully, the Lord Paramount of the Trident, rules over the riverlands from the Tully seat of Riverrun. Their sigil is a silver trout leaping on a striped field of blue and mud red, and their house words are "Family, Duty, Honor." </p>

<p><b>Lysa Meadows</b> is a member of House Meadows. She is married to Ser Olymer Tyrell and together they have three children, Raymund, Rickard and Megga Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Lysandro Rogare</b>, known as <b>Lysandro the Magnificent</b>, was a wealthy Lysene banker and head of House Rogare. His brother, Drazenko, was the consort of Aliandra Martell, Princess of Dorne. Lysandro's children were Larra, Lysaro, Moredo, Lotho, Roggerio, Lysara, Drako, Fredo, and Marra. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Lysara Karstark</b> was a member of House Karstark. She was married to Artos Stark, the third son of Lord Beron Stark, and had twin sons by him; Brandon and Benjen Stark. </p>
<p><b>Lysara Rogare</b> was a member of House Rogare, a Lysene noble banking family. She was the daughter of Lysandro Rogare, the First Magister of Lys. </p>
<p><b>Lysaro Rogare</b> was a member of House Rogare, a Lysene noble banking family. He was the heir to Lysandro, the nephew of Drazenko, and the elder brother of Larra (who married Prince Viserys Targaryen before his ascent to the Iron Throne) and Moredo Rogare. </p>
<p><b>Lysono Maar</b> is a sellsword from Lys in service to the Golden Company. He is the company's spymaster. He speaks the Common Tongue very well. </p>
<p>The <b>Golden Company</b> is a company of sellswords founded by Ser Aegor Rivers, a Great Bastard known as "Bittersteel". The current captain-general is Harry Strickland. </p>
<p><b>Lythene Frey</b> is the second daughter of Lord Walder Frey. She was the first daughter born between the marriage of Walder Frey and Amarei Crakehall. She is the wife of Lord Lucias Vypren. They have two children. </p>
<p><b>Mace Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Mace Tyrell</b> is the Lord of Highgarden, Lord Paramount of the Mander, Defender of the Marches, High Marshal of the Reach, Warden of the South, and head of House Tyrell. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Roger Ashton-Griffiths. </p>
<p><b>Mad Axe</b> was a member of the Night's Watch. He is famous for murdering his fellow brothers at the Nightfort. He had a red beard. </p>
<p>The <b>Mad Huntsman</b> is the owner of a pack of dogs from Stoney Sept. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p>The <b>brotherhood without banners</b>, also known as the <b>knights of the hollow hill</b> and the <b>forgotten fellowship</b>, is an outlaw group who initially fights Lannister rule in the name of King Robert I Baratheon. Led by the Lightning Lord, Beric Dondarrion, the group is founded in the riverlands by soldiers and nobles who were sent by the then-Hand of the King, Eddard Stark, to bring Gregor Clegane to justice. After they are ambushed while crossing a ford and nearly defeated, the group continues the fight as a guerrilla group. Their numbers increase as they are joined by defeated soldiers from other battles, deserters, and refugees from the War of the Five Kings. Every man of the brotherhood receives a knighthood from Beric. </p>
<p><b>Maddy</b> is a servant of House Arryn in service at the Eyrie. </p>
<p><b>Maege Mormont</b>, known as <b>the She-Bear</b>, is the head of House Mormont and the Lady of Bear Island. She inherited her title from her nephew, Ser Jorah Mormont, after he fled into exile. She is the younger sister of the Lord Commander of the Night's Watch, Jeor Mormont. </p>
<p><b>Bear Island</b> is a remote island in the north that is home to House Mormont. It lies within the Bay of Ice, north of Deepwood Motte and south of the Frozen Shore. The Mormonts live at Mormont Keep. </p>

<p><b>Maegon Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen during the Century of Blood, the first son of Lord Aegon and Lady Elaena Targaryen of Dragonstone. He had one younger brother, Aerys Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Maegor I Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Maegor the Cruel</b>, was the third Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He was the son of King Aegon I Targaryen and his elder sister-wife, Queen Visenya Targaryen. He had an older half-brother, Aenys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>King <b>Maegor III Targaryen</b> is a character mentioned in the ninth episode of the fifth season of HBO's <i>Game of Thrones</i>. The character does not appear in the books, nor has he ever existed in the universum of <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i>. It is currently unknown whether the inclusion of Maegor III in the episode was a deliberate choice, or whether it was a mistake. </p>

<p><b>Maekar I Targaryen</b> was Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and the fourteenth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He was the fourth son of King Daeron II Targaryen, and was given the Targaryen seat of Summerhall, and was thus known as the Prince of Summerhall. Maekar was a capable army commander who served in two of the Blackfyre Rebellions. After a number of unexpected deaths in the royal family, he came to the throne in 221&nbsp;AC. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Maelor Targaryen</b> was the second son and third child of King Aegon II Targaryen and his sister-wife and Queen Helaena Targaryen. Maelor had older twin siblings, brother Jaehaerys, and sister Jaehaera. He possessed a dragon egg. </p>

<p><b>Giants</b> are a race of sentient humanoids which once lived in various regions of the known world but now live only in northern Westeros beyond the Wall. The people of the Seven Kingdoms believe them to be extinct. </p>

<p><b>Malazza</b>, known as the <b>Girl General</b>, is a Yunkai'i noble. She rides a white horse with red mane, and commands a hundred young, strapping slave soldiers, bred and trained by herself. All of them are lean, young, rippling with muscle, and naked but for breechclouts, yellow cloaks, and long bronze shields with erotic inlays. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Malcolm</b> was a landed knight who lived near King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Maldon IV Durrandon</b> was a Storm King of House Durrandon. During the Andal invasion of the stormlands, as neither side defeated the other, Maldon took an Andal maiden as his wife. Durran XXIV was born of this union. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Maldon Massey</b> was a member of House Massey who built Stonedance and established his lordship over Massey's Hook. He was a vassal of the Storm King Durran the Ravenfriend. </p>
