<p><b>Malko</b> is the captain of a slaving ship operating in Slaver's Bay and the Summer Sea. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is played by Adewale Akinnuoye-Agbaje. He replaces the unidentified Yunkai’i slavers in <i>A Dance with Dragons</i>, who capture Jorah Mormont and Tyrion Lannister while aboard the <i>Selaesori Qhoran</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Mallador Locke</b> is a knight of the Night's Watch from House Locke. Sweet Donnel Hill is his squire. According to the semi-canon <i>A Song of Ice and Fire Campaign Guide</i>, he is a son of Lord Ondrew Locke. </p>
<p><b>Malleon</b> was a Grand Maester of the Citadel. He wrote a book on the lineages of the Seven Kingdoms, <i>The Lineages and Histories of the Great Houses of the Seven Kingdoms, With Descriptions of Many High Lords and Noble Ladies and Their Children</i>. </p>
<p>Wisdom <b>Malliard</b> is a member of the Alchemists' Guild in King's Landing. He is in charge of keeping track and projecting production of the wildfire at the Guild Hall. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Mallor</b> was a knight during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Mallor the Dornishman</b> is a sellsword in service to House Lannister. </p>
<p>Septon <b>Mallow</b> was a member of the Faith of the Seven that lived in the Vale during the Andal invasion. He wrote an account of the Battle of the Seven Stars. </p>
<p><b>Malo Jayn</b> is a sellsword in service to the Golden Company. His rank is serjeant. </p>
<p><b>Malora Hightower</b>, called the <b>Mad Maid</b>, is a lady of House Hightower and the eldest daughter of Lord Leyton Hightower of Oldtown. </p>
<p><b>Malthar Xaq</b> was a prince from the Summer Isles and the ruler of Koj. After the first contact with people from beyond the seas, the princes of the Summer Isles began the construction of large, strong ships that could cross long stretches of ocean and resist the fiercest storms. Prince Malthar was the greatest of these shipbuilders and is remembered as <b>Malthar the Windrider</b> and <b>Malthar the Mapmaker</b>. </p>
<p><b>Malwyn Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, the second son of Ser Raymund Frey, the eleventh son of Lord Walder Frey, and his wife Beony Beesbury. </p>
<p><b>Mancaster</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel and the author of <i>Sea Demons: A History of the Children of the Drowned God of the Isles</i>. </p>
<p><b>Mance Rayder</b> was once a man of the Night's Watch before breaking his vows and abandoning his post. He has since become extremely influential among the free folk, and is called the "King-Beyond-the-Wall". In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Ciarán Hinds. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Mandon Moore</b> is a knight from House Moore. He is a member of King Robert I Baratheon's Kingsguard. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by James Doran. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Manfred Dondarrion</b> was a knight from House Dondarrion and the son and heir of Lord Dondarrion during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Manfred Hightower</b> was Lord of the Hightower and head of House Hightower during Aegon's Conquest. He had at least four sons, including Addam and Garmon, and several daughters. </p>
<p><b>Manfred Hightower</b> was Lord of the Hightower and head of House Hightower during the reign of Kings Aegon I Targaryen and Aenys I Targaryen. He had two sons, Martyn and Morgan, and a daughter, Ceryse. </p>
<p><b>Manfred Lothston</b> was a member of House Lothston during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Manfred Swann</b> was the Lord of Stonehelm and the head of House Swann during the early reign of King Aegon V Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Manfrey Martell</b> is a knight of House Martell and a cousin to Doran Martell, Prince of Dorne. Manfrey is the castellan of Sunspear. </p>
<p><b>Manfryd Lothston</b>, better known as <b>Manfryd o' the Black Hood</b>, was the son of Lord Lucas Lothston of Harrenhal. He is not remembered fondly. </p>
<p><b>Manfryd Merlyn</b> is the captain of the ship <i>Kite</i> in the Iron Fleet and is under the command of Victarion Greyjoy. </p>
<p><b>Manfryd Mooton</b> was the Lord of Maidenpool and the head of House Mooton during the Dance of the Dragons and the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Manfryd Redwyne</b> was the Lord of the Arbor and the head of House Redwyne during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Manfryd Yew</b> is a landed knight and the head of House Yew. </p>
<p><b>Manly Stokeworth</b> was a member of House Stokeworth who served as Commander of the City Watch of King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Mara Karstark</b> was a member of House Karstark mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Mara Manderly</b> was a member of House Manderly and a daughter of Lord Theomore Manderly. </p>
<p><b>Mara Nymeros Martell</b> was the ruling Princess of Dorne and head of House Martell during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Marei</b> is a whore at Chataya's brothel in King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Margaery Tyrell</b> is the only daughter of Lord Mace Tyrell and his wife, Lady Alerie Hightower. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is played by Natalie Dormer. </p>
<p><b>Margaret Karstark</b> was a member of House Karstark. She married Bennard Stark, second son of Lord Benjen Stark and Lady Lysa Locke, with whom she had three sons; Benjen, Brandon and Elric Stark. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Margate</b> is an archmaester of the Citadel. He has suggested that the tales of freezing mists, ice ships and Cannibal Bay told by sailors who have visited the Shivering Sea are distorted reports of ice dragon activity. </p>
<p><b>Marghaz zo Loraq</b> is a Meereen noble, and is a cousin to Hizdahr zo Loraq. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Margot Lannister</b> is a member of House Lannister, a distant cousin of the main branch. She is married to Lord Titus Peake of Starpike. </p>
<p><b>Mariah Stark</b> was a member of House Stark. She was the fourth daughter of Lord Cregan Stark and Lady Alysanne Blackwood. </p>
<p><b>Marianne Vance</b> is the daughter of Ser Dafyn Vance and Maegelle Frey. </p>
<p><b>Maric Seaworth</b> is the fourth son of Ser Davos Seaworth and his wife Marya. He is the oarmaster on the war galley <i>Fury</i>. </p>
<p><b>Marilda of Hull</b>, also called <b>Mouse</b>, was a trader and captain from Hull on Driftmark. She was the mother of Ser Addam Velaryon, a dragonrider, and Alyn Velaryon, Lord of the Tides. </p>
<p><b>Marillion</b> is a singer and a musician. </p>
<p>Mother <b>Maris</b> was a septa of the Faith of the Seven during the reign of Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Maris the Maid</b>, called <b>the Most Fair</b>, is a legendary daughter of Garth Greenhand and ancestor of House Hightower. Her beauty was so renowned that fifty lords vied for her hand in the first tourney held in Westeros. The victor was Argoth Stone-Skin, but Maris wed King Uthor of the High Tower before he could claim her, and Argoth spent the rest of days raging outside the walls of Oldtown, roaring for his bride. </p>
<p><b>Maris Baratheon</b> was a noblewoman from House Baratheon during the reign of kings Viserys I, Aegon II and Aegon III Targaryen. She was one of the four daughters of Lord Borros Baratheon of Storm's End. She and her sisters were known as the Four Storms. </p>
<p><b>Black Maris</b> is a spearwife of the free folk. </p>
<p><b>Marissa Frey</b> is a member of House Frey and the third daughter of Merrett Frey and Mariya Darry. </p>
<p><b>Mariya Darry</b> is the wife of Merrett Frey, who considers her a shrew. They have four children who lived past infancy. She is the daughter of a previous Lord Darry, and according to a semi-canon source, a sister of Lord Raymun Darry. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Mark Mullendore</b> is a knight from House Mullendore in the Reach. His relation to Martyn Mullendore, the Lord of Uplands and the head of House is unknown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Mark Ryswell</b> was a knight from House Ryswell. His relation to Rodrik Ryswell, the Lord of the Rills, is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Marla Prester</b> was a member of House Prester, and the second wife of Ser Jason Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Marla Sunderland</b> was a member of House Sunderland that briefly ruled the Three Sisters as Queen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Marlon Manderly</b> is a knight of House Manderly and cousin to the head of the house, Lord Wyman Manderly. He is the commander of the garrison at the New Castle in White Harbor. His personal sigil is three silvery mermaids upon a violet field. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Marna Locke</b> was a member of House Locke. She married Lord Edwyle Stark, with whom she had one son, Rickard Stark. </p>
<p><b>Maron Botley</b>, also known as <b>Old Botley</b> or <b>Fishwhiskers</b>, is a member of House Botley. He has three sons who accompany him on raids. </p>
<p><b>Maron Greyjoy</b> was the second son of Lord Balon Greyjoy. He died during Greyjoy's Rebellion. </p>
<p><b>Greyjoy's Rebellion</b> or the <b>Greyjoy Rebellion</b> was an attempt at secession by Balon Greyjoy against the Iron Throne in 289&nbsp;AC, nine years before the beginning of <i>A Game of Thrones</i>. Balon tried to break away from the Seven Kingdoms to secure independence for the Iron Islands and restore the Old Way, lost almost three hundred years before, during Aegon's Conquest. The rebellion was crushed and Balon was forced to surrender, cementing the hold of King Robert I Baratheon on the Iron Throne. </p>
<p><b>Maron Nymeros Martell</b> was a former ruling Prince of Dorne and head of House Martell. </p>
<p><b>Maron Volmark</b> is the Lord of Volmark and the head of House Volmark. </p>
<p><b>Marq Ambrose</b> was the head of House Ambrose during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Marq Farman</b> was the Lord of Fair Isle and the head of House Farman during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen and the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Marq Grafton</b> was the Lord of Gulltown and the head of House Grafton at the time of Robert's Rebellion. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Marq Piper</b> is a knight from House Piper. He is the heir of Clement Piper, Lord of Pinkmaiden Castle. </p>
<p><b>Pinkmaiden Castle</b>, also known simply as <b>Pinkmaiden</b>, is the seat of House Piper in the southwestern riverlands. The castle is located on the Red Fork south of Riverrun, southeast of Acorn Hall, northwest of Stoney Sept, and northeast of Hornvale. </p>
<p><b>Marq Merryweather</b> was the Lord of Longtable and the head of House Merryweather during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Marq Mudd</b>, known as <b>the Mad Bard</b>, was an alleged member of House Mudd who claimed to be a river king in the generations after the riverlands were conquered by the Storm King Arlan III Durrandon. Marq had a brief, inglorious reign before being put down. His connection with the extinct Mudd dynasty is unconfirmed. </p>
<p><b>Marq Rankenfell</b>, better known as <b>Mad Marq Rankenfell</b>, is a former Lord Commander of the Night's Watch. He is considered one of the worst commanders the Night's Watch ever had. </p>
<p><b>Marqelo Tagaros</b> was one of the ruling triarchs of the Free City of Volantis during the reign of Tommen II Lannister, King of the Rock. </p>
<p><b>Marra Rogare</b> was a member of House Rogare, a Lysene noble banking family. She was the daughter of Lysandro Rogare, the First Magister of Lys. </p>
<p><b>Marrigo</b> is a pit fighter in Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Marro</b> is a mummer in Braavos. He is part of the mummer's troupe at the Gate. </p>
<p><b>Marselen</b> is the brother of Missandei. They had two other brothers. Both of them entered training as Unsullied, but one did not survive. He was purchased and then freed by Daenerys Targaryen. He is Naathi like his sister. </p>
<p><b>Marsella Waynwood</b> was a member of House Waynwood, her relation to Anya Waynwood, the Lady of Ironoaks, is unknown. She was the third wife of Ser Stevron Frey and had one son by him Walton Frey. She died in childbed. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Marston Waters</b> was a knight of Aegon II Targaryen's Kingsguard. He served briefly as Lord Commander and Hand of the King for Aegon III Targaryen. </p>

<p><b>Martyn Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>

<p><b>Martyn Hightower</b> was Lord of the Hightower and head of House Hightower at the beginning of the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. He was the brother of Queen Ceryse Hightower, one of Maegor's wives. </p>
<p><b>Martyn Hightower</b> was a squire from House Hightower during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Martyn Lannister</b> is a squire from House Lannister. He is the third son of Ser Kevan Lannister and Lady Dorna Swyft and twin to Willem. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Martyn is portrayed by Dean-Charles Chapman. </p>
<p><b>Martyn Mullendore</b> is the Lord of Uplands and the head of House Mullendore. </p>
<p><b>Martyn Rivers</b> is a bastard son of Lord Walder Frey. </p>

<p><b>Martyna Mullendore</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Marwyn</b>, also known as <b>Marwyn the Mage</b>, is an archmaester of the Citadel. </p>
<p>The <b>maesters</b> are an order of scholars, healers, messengers, and scientists. They educate new students at the Citadel, which is located in Oldtown, a city in the Reach. House Hightower was integral in the Citadel's foundation, and continues to patronize the order. As advisers to the Westerosi nobility, the maesters have largely supplanted the Alchemists' Guild. They are sometimes called "the knights of the mind." </p>

<p><b>Medwick Tyrell</b> is a member of House Tyrell and a maester of the Citadel. He is the second son of Ser Luthor Tyrell, and a first cousin once removed to Mace Tyrell, the current Lord of Highgarden. </p>

<p><b>Meg</b> can refer to: </p>
<p><b>Megette</b>, also known as <b>Merry Meg</b>, was the young and buxom wife of a blacksmith. She was the second of Aegon IV Targaryen's mistresses. </p>
<p><b>Megga Tyrell</b> is a member of a junior branch of House Tyrell, being the granddaughter of Ser Quentin Tyrell, a cousin of Mace Tyrell, the Lord of Highgarden. The only daughter of Ser Olymer Tyrell and his wife, Lysa Meadows, Megga has two older brothers: Raymund and Rickard Tyrell. </p>

<p><b>Melaquin</b> was a maester in service at Summerhall during the reigns of Daeron II and Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Melara Crane</b> is a noblewoman of House Crane and is married to Lord Alester Florent. She has one son, Alekyne, and two daughters, Melessa and Rhea. Melara is also the maternal grandmother of Samwell Tarly. </p>
<p><b>Melara Hetherspoon</b> was a member of House Hetherspoon and a childhood friend of Cersei Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Meldred Merlyn</b>, also known as <b>the Merlyn</b>, is the Lord of Pebbleton and the head of House Merlyn. </p>
<p><b>Melesa Crakehall</b> is a member of House Crakehall and the wife of Ser Lyonel Frey, the second son of Ser Emmon Frey, himself the second son of Lord Walder Frey. They have no progeny. Her relation to the main Crakehalls is currently unknown. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Melessa Florent</b> is a noblewoman of House Florent, the middle child and eldest daughter of Lord Alester Florent of Brightwater. She is married to Lord Randyll Tarly and the mother of Samwell, Talla, and Dickon Tarly, as well as two other daughters. </p>
<p><b>Meliana</b>, known as <b>Lady Meliana</b>, is a prostitute of Mole's Town. </p>
<p><b>Melicent</b> is a septa of the Faith of the Seven in King's Landing. She may be one of the Most Devout at the Great Sept of Baelor. </p>
<p><b>Melisandre</b> is a red priestess of R'hllor and a shadowbinder, hailing from the city of Asshai in the Further East of Essos. She has joined the court of Stannis Baratheon, Lord of Dragonstone, believing him to be Azor Ahai reborn, a hero destined to defeat the Great Other. She has become an influential advisor to him and his family. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Carice van Houten. She becomes a POV character in <i>A Dance with Dragons</i>. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Melissa Blackwood</b>, nicknamed <b>Missy</b>, was a noblewoman from House Blackwood during the reign of Aegon IV Targaryen. She was the sixth of Aegon's nine mistresses, and the best loved of them. </p>
<p><b>Mellara Rivers</b> is a bastard daughter of Lord Walder Frey. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Mellario</b> is a noblewoman of the Free City of Norvos, and the estranged wife of Doran Martell, the Prince of Dorne. She had three children by him: Arianne, Quentyn, and Trystane. </p>
<p><b>Mellei</b> is a servant of House Martell at Sunspear. She is the sister of Morra. </p>

<p><b>Melly</b> is a member of the brotherhood without banners. </p>
<p><b>Melony Piper</b> was a member of House Piper during the reigns of kings Aenys I Targaryen and Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Melwyn Sarsfield</b> is a knight from House Sarsfield. He is married to Shierle Swyft. </p>
<p><b>Melwys Rivers</b> is a bastard son of Lord Walder Frey. He is a maester of the Citadel, in service to House Rosby at Rosby. </p>
<p><b>Mengo</b> was a Dothraki <i>khal</i> who lived during the Century of Blood. His mother was Doshi, a reputed witch queen, and his son was Moro. </p>
<p><b>Mengo Quen</b>, known as <b>the Glittering God</b>, was a God-Emperor of the Golden Empire of Yi Ti and the third member of his dynasty. He earned his moniker because he ruled from a palace where the floors, walls, and columns were covered in gold leaf, and all furnishings were made of gold, even the chamber pots. </p>
<p><b>Meralyn</b>, more commonly called <b>Merry</b>, is the proprietor of the Happy Port, a brothel near Ragman's Harbor in Braavos. </p>
<p><b>Meredyth Crane</b>, known as <b>Merry Crane</b>, is a noblewoman of House Crane. </p>
<p><b>Meredyth Darklyn</b> was a member of House Darklyn and Lady of Duskendale through her marriage to Lord Gunthor Darklyn. </p>
<p><b>Meria Nymeros Martell</b> was the ruling Princess of Dorne from House Martell during the invasion of Westeros by Aegon the Conqueror. </p>
<p><b>Merianne Frey</b>, called <b>Merry</b> by her family, is a noblewoman of House Frey, the daughter of Ser Whalen Frey and Sylwa Paege. </p>
<p><b>Meribald</b> is a wandering septon of the riverlands. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Ian McShane portrays a similar character named Brother Ray. </p>
<p><b>Merion</b> was a maester of the Citadel. </p>
<p><b>Meris</b>, mockingly nicknamed <b>Pretty Meris</b>, is a sellsword of the Windblown. </p>
<p><b>Merle I Gardener</b>, called <b>Merle the Meek</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. Along with his father and son, he is remembered as one of the Three Sage Kings who dealt with the Andal invasion of the Reach with a policy of accord and assimilation rather then armed resistance. </p>
<p>The <b>Merling Queen</b> is a courtesan in Braavos. Her given name is unknown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Merlon Crakehall</b> is a knight of House Crakehall. He is the youngest son of Lord Roland Crakehall. </p>
<p><b>Mern II Gardener</b>, called <b>Mern the Mason</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. Before the Andals arrived in the Reach, Mern built a new curtain wall about Highgarden and commanded his lords bannermen to see to their own defenses. </p>
<p><b>Mern III Gardener</b>, called <b>the Madling</b>, was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. </p>
<p><b>Mern VI Gardener</b> was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. </p>
<p><b>Mern IX Gardener</b> was the last King of the Reach and Lord of Highgarden from House Gardener. He and King Loren I Lannister are remembered collectively as the Two Kings. </p>
<p><b>Mero</b>, better known as <b>the Titan's Bastard</b>, is the commander of the Second Sons, a sellsword company. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Mero is portrayed by Mark Killeen. </p>
<p>The <b>Second Sons</b> are a sellsword company found in the Free Cities. Their banner is a broken sword and they take commands only from their captain. </p>
<p><b>Merrel</b> is a guard of House Baratheon of Dragonstone and a queen's man. </p>

<p>King <b>Morden II Durrandon</b> was a Storm King of House Durrandon. During his reign the decline of House Durrandon turned back, thanks in part to Morden's baseborn half brother Ronard, whom he named as his castellan. A fearsome warrior, Ronard became ruler of the Stormlands in all but name and took Morden's sister to wife. Within five years, he had usurped kingship as well. Morden's own queen placed the crown on Ronard's head and, if songs are true, she shared his bed as well. In the meantime, Morden, deemed harmless, was confined to a cell in the tower. </p>
<p><b>Moredo Prestayn</b> is a member of House Prestayn and a merchant of Braavos. He is the Tradesman-Captain of the <i>Vixen</i>. </p>

<p><b>Moreo Tumitis</b> is captain of the ship <i>Storm Dancer</i>. He has a forked green beard. Hailing from Tyrosh he can speak the Common Tongue fluently. He has sailed the narrow sea for roughly thirty years, as everything from an oarsman to finally, captain. The <i>Storm Dancer</i> is his fourth ship and the fastest of them. </p>

<p><b>Morgan Liddle</b> is the second son of Lord Torren Liddle, known as the Liddle, the clan chief of House Liddle, a mountain clan in the North. Other northmen call him <b>Middle Liddle</b>, though not often in his hearing. He is the heir apparant of his father Torren, as his elder brother, Duncan, is a sworn brother of the Night's Watch. </p>

<p>The <b>free folk</b> are a race of people who live beyond the Wall in northern Westeros. They are more commonly referred to as <b>"wildlings"</b> everywhere south of the Wall. </p>
<p><b>Moro</b> is a Dothraki <i>khal</i>. He is a sometime ally of Khal Drogo. He has a son, Rhogoro. </p>
<p>The <b>Dothraki</b> people are a culture of nomadic warriors in Essos who range across the vast grasslands of the Dothraki sea in hordes known as <i>khalasars</i>. People of the Seven Kingdoms and the Free Cities also refer to the Dothraki as <b>horselords</b>. </p>
<p><i><b>Khal</b></i> is a title that the Dothraki use to designate the leader of a <i>khalasar</i>, the nomadic groupings upon which their society is based. </p>
<p><b>Moro</b> was a <i>khal</i> who lived during the Century of Blood. He was the son of Khal Mengo, who had united all Dothraki in a single <i>khalasar</i>. </p>
<p>The <b>Kingdom of Sarnor</b> is a region of northern Essos along the shores of the Shivering Sea. The Forest of Qohor and Vaes Khadokh are to the west, while the Dothraki sea extends along the south. Omber is a peninsula to the northeast of Sarnor, while the Kingdom of the Ifequevron is farther to the east. </p>

<p><b>Murch</b> is part of Yoren's band when it is marching north to the Wall to join the Night’s Watch. It is not known whether he is a recruit, a criminal or one of the orphan boys. </p>
<p>The <b>Night's Watch</b> is a military order dedicated to holding the Wall, the immense fortification on the northern border of the Seven Kingdoms, defending the realms of men from what lies beyond the Wall. The order's foundation dates back to the Age of Heroes, at the time when the Others were pushed back. The men of Night's Watch wear only black, and they are known as <b>black brothers</b>. Recruits who join the Watch are said to <b>take the black</b>. </p>
<p><b>Murch</b> is a man sworn to House Stark. He is one of the best huntsmen in service to the Starks. </p>
<p><b>House Stark of Winterfell</b> is one of the Great Houses of Westeros and the principal noble house of the north. In days of old they ruled as Kings of Winter, but since Aegon's Conquest they have been Wardens of the North and ruled as Lords of Winterfell. Their seat, Winterfell, is an ancient castle renowned for its strength. </p>
<p><b>Murenmure</b> is a maester of the Citadel. He is in service at Hammerhorn to House Goodbrother. </p>
<p><b>Murmison</b> was a septon who became a renowned member of the Faith and Hand of the King from 39&nbsp;AC - 41&nbsp;AC for King Aenys I Targaryen. He is now used as a warning about the makings of a good Hand. </p>
<p><b>Mushroom</b> was a dwarf who served as a fool at the courts of Viserys I Targaryen, Aegon II Targaryen, Rhaenyra Targaryen, and Aegon III Targaryen. He allegedly recorded the events that occurred during his time at their courts in <i>The Testimony of Mushroom</i>, written by an unknown scribe. </p>
<p><b>Viserys I Targaryen</b> was the fifth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne, ruling from 103&nbsp;AC to 129&nbsp;AC. He succeeded his grandfather, the Old King Jaehaerys I. Viserys continued the prosperous peace and legacy of his grandsire, but the seeds for the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons that would much later engulf the realm were inadvertently sown in his reign. </p>

<p><b>Mysaria</b>, also called <b>Lady Misery</b>, was a dancer from Lys who became the paramour of Prince Daemon Targaryen and the unofficial mistress of whisperers to Queen Rhaenyra Targaryen during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>King's Landing</b> is the capital of the Seven Kingdoms, located in the crownlands on the east coast of Westeros. It is situated along the kingsroad at the mouth of the Blackwater Rush and overlooks Blackwater Bay. King's Landing is the site of the Iron Throne and the Red Keep, which is the seat of the king, Robert I from House Baratheon of King's Landing. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Naerys Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen and the sister-wife to King Aegon IV, who was known as the Unworthy. Naerys was the sister of Prince Aemon the Dragonknight, and the mother of King Daeron II Targaryen and Princess Daenerys Targaryen. </p>

<p><b>Naggle</b> is the innkeep of the Old Stone Bridge, an inn that lies along the road to Duskendale. </p>
<p><b>Nail</b> is an apprentice to the Second Sons blacksmith and armorer known as Hammer. </p>
<p><b>Nan</b>, generally referred to as <b>Old Nan</b>, is a servant woman at Winterfell. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, she is portrayed by Margaret John, and in a Season 6 flashback by Annette Tierney. </p>
<p><b>Narbert</b> is a brother and proctor of the order on the Quiet Isle. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Narbert Grandison </b> is a knight from House Grandison in the service of King Stannis Baratheon. He is one of the queen's men. </p>
<p><b>Narbo</b>, better known as <b>Little Narbo</b>, is a dockside cutpurse and thief in Braavos. </p>
<p><b>Narha Otherys</b> was the second of the three bastard children of King Aegon IV Targaryen and his fourth mistress, Bellegere Otherys. </p>
<p><b>Nate</b> is a serving man and maester's assistant. He is known as <b>Feathers</b> because he has long worked with the ravens at the Water Gardens. </p>
<p><b>Naylin</b> was the maester who wrote <i>Rubies and Iron</i>. </p>
<p><b>Ned</b> was the ferryman at the old inn by the lakeshore near Whitewalls during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Ned Bean</b>, called <b>Blackbean</b>, was a notorious sellsail who became second-in-command of the royal fleet during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Ned Umber</b> is, in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, the son of Smalljon Umber and the last head of House Umber. He is presumably named after Eddard Stark, whose nickname was Ned. In the books, it is unknown if the Smalljon has any children. </p>
<p><b>Ned Woods</b>, known as <b>Noseless Ned</b>, is a member of House Woods. A man of the wolfswood sworn to House Glover of Deepwood Motte. </p>
<p><b>Nella</b> is a wildling wife of Craster. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Nestor Royce</b> is the senior member of a cadet branch of House Royce and Keeper of the Gates of the Moon. He is the cousin of Lord Yohn Royce, and is a widower. He has served as High Steward of the Vale for the fourteen years prior to Lord Jon Arryn's death. </p>
<p><b>Nettles</b>, also known as <b>Netty</b>, was a dragonseed and the first and possibly last dragonrider of the dragon Sheepstealer. </p>
<p><b>Born of dragonseed</b> or <b>seeds</b> is a term to describe some bastards of House Targaryen as well as House Velaryon. </p>
<p><b>Sheepstealer</b> was a wild male dragon during the Dance of the Dragons with a taste for mutton. It lived at the back of Dragonmont and would hunt between Driftmark and Wendwater. The smallfolk of Dragonstone named it for a self-evident reason. At the start of the Dance of the Dragons, he was one of three wild dragons living on Dragonstone. </p>

<p><b>Nettles</b> is a spearwife of the free folk. </p>
<p><b>Nevio Narratys</b> was a Prince of Pentos during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Neyela Frey</b> is a granddaughter of Lord Walder Frey in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Nicol</b> was a maester of the Citadel. He wrote the book <i>The Measure of the Days</i>. He argues that seasons of the world might once have been of regular length. </p>
<p>The <b>Night King</b> is the leader of the White Walkers in the television series <i>Game of Thrones</i>, where he is played by Richard Brake and later by Vladimir Furdik. </p>
<p><b>Night's King</b>, also called <b>the Night's King</b>, is a legendary Lord Commander of the Night's Watch who lived during the Age of Heroes. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>The Nightingale</b> is a famous courtesan in Braavos, renowned for her beauty. </p>
<p>The man known as <b>Nine Eyes</b> became one of the infamous Band of Nine, the instigators of the War of the Ninepenny Kings. </p>
<p><b>Nissa Nissa</b> was the wife of Azor Ahai. He sacrificed her to create the famous sword, Lightbringer. </p>
<p><b>Noho Dimittis</b> is a representative of the Iron Bank of Braavos. </p>
<p>Goodwife <b>Nolla</b> was an inhabitant of the Riverlands. She was slain by the forces of House Lannister during the War of the Five Kings. </p>
<p><b>Norbert Vance</b> is the Lord of Atranta and the head of House Vance of Atranta. </p>
<p><b>Norjen</b> is one of Aeron Greyjoy's drowned men. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Norman Hightower</b> was a knight from House Hightower during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. He was a grandson of Lord Donnel Hightower and an accomplished mariner. </p>
<p><b>Normund Tyrell</b> is a maester of the Citadel in service at Blackcrown to House Bulwer. He is a cousin of Lord Mace Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Norne Goodbrother</b> is Lord of Shatterstone and head of House Goodbrother of Shatterstone. </p>
<p><b>Norren</b> is an Archmaester of the Citadel. His ring, mask and rod are made of electrum. </p>
<p><b>Norren</b> was a maester in service to Lord Manfryd Mooton of Maidenpool during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. He was also the keeper of the <i>Chronicles of Maidenpool</i>. </p>
<p><b>Norwin Lannister</b> was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. He was known as <b>Norwin the Niggardly</b> for his pettiness. </p>
<p><b>Notch</b> is a longbowman of the brotherhood without banners. </p>
<p><b>"Nurse"</b> is a Ghiscari commoner and the overseer of Yezzan zo Qaggaz's slaves. </p>
<p><b>Nute the Barber</b> is an ironborn raider and the best man of Lord Victarion Greyjoy's crew aboard the <i>Iron Victory</i>. </p>
<p><b>Nyessos Vhassar</b> is one of the current ruling triarchs of the Free City of Volantis. He is of the elephant party. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Nyles Rowan</b> was a knight of House Rowan during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Nymella Toland</b> is the Lady of Ghost Hill and is the head of House Toland. She has two daughters, Valena and Teora. </p>
<p><b>Princess Nymeria of Ny Sar</b> was a princess of the Rhoynar. After the Rhoyne was conquered by the Valyrian Freehold, Nymeria led the Rhoynar to Dorne, where she took Lord Mors Martell of the Sandship as her husband. </p>
<p><b>Nymeria</b> is a direwolf bonded to Arya Stark. She is a litter-mate of Grey Wind, Lady, Summer, Shaggydog, and Ghost. She is named after Princess Nymeria of the Rhoynar. </p>
<p><b>Nymeria Sand</b>, nicknamed <b>Lady Nym</b>, is a bastard daughter of Oberyn Martell and a noblewoman from Volantis. She is the second oldest of the infamous Sand Snakes, so named for their bastard origin and the nickame of their father, the "Red Viper". In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Jessica Henwick and stated to be the daughter of a YiTish noblewoman instead of a Volantene one. </p>
<p><b>Nymor Martell</b> was the ruling Prince of Dorne and head of House Martell during the reign of King Aegon I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Nymos</b> is an archmaester at the Citadel in Oldtown. </p>
<p><b>Nysseos Qoheros</b> was a Volantene and the author of <i>Journals</i>. Among the events he reports the fate of Triarch Horonno, who tried to declare himself triarch for life and was executed for it. </p>
<p><b>Nysterica</b> is a septa assigned to House Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Obara Sand</b> is the bastard daughter of Oberyn Martell and an Oldtown whore. She is the eldest of the infamous Sand Snakes. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Keisha Castle-Hughes. </p>
<p><b>Obella Sand</b> is the second bastard daughter of Prince Oberyn Martell and his paramour Ellaria Sand. She is the sixth of the famous 'Sand Snakes'. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Oberyn Nymeros Martell</b>, also known as <b>the Red Viper</b>, is a member of House Martell and is the younger brother of Doran Martell, Prince of Dorne. Oberyn has eight bastard daughters called the Sand Snakes, the four youngest of whom are by his current paramour, Ellaria Sand. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> Oberyn is portrayed by Pedro Pascal. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Ocley</b> is an archmaester at the Citadel in Oldtown. </p>
<p><b>Ogo</b> is a Dothraki <i>khal</i>. He has a son, Fogo. </p>
<p>The <b>Old Grey Gull</b> is a priest of the Drowned God. His true name is unknown. He lives on a rock. </p>
<p><b>The Old Mother</b> was a pirate queen who became one of the infamous Band of Nine, the instigators of the War of the Ninepenny Kings. </p>
<p><b>Old Pate</b> has a cottage in the riverlands near the Inn of the Kneeling Man. </p>
<p><b>Old Tattersalt</b> is a member of the Night's Watch. He is the captain of the <i>Blackbird</i>. He is named "Old Tattersalt" for the stained and faded black clothes he wears. He has a large belly and seldom talks. </p>
<p><b>Olene Tyrell</b> is the only daughter of Ser Luthor Tyrell and Elyn Norridge. She is married to Ser Leo Blackbar. </p>
<p><b>Olenna Tyrell</b>, née <b>Redwyne</b>, is the widow of Lord Luthor Tyrell and the mother of Mace Tyrell, Lord of Highgarden. Born into House Redwyne of the Arbor, she is commonly known as the <b>Queen of Thorns</b> because of her sharp tongue. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Dame Diana Rigg. </p>
<p><b>Ollidar</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel who became the first Grand Maester. </p>
<p>Septon <b>Ollidor</b> is a follower of the Faith of the Seven. He is stationed in King's Landing and a member of the Most Devout. </p>
<p><b>Ollo</b>, dubbed <b>Ollo Lophand</b>, is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Olly</b> is a young boy who lives in the North. His character was created specifically for the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, in which he is played by Brenock O'Connor. He replaces the unknown killer of Ygritte from the novels, in the attack on Castle Black, and Satin as Jon Snow's steward. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Olymer Tyrell</b> is the only child of Ser Quentin Tyrell. The knight is married to Lysa Meadows and they have three children, Raymund, Rickard and Megga Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Olyvar</b> is a prostitute and a spy specializing in homosexual relations, in the employ of Petyr "Littlefinger" Baelish. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is played by Will Tudor. He assumes part of Dontos Hollard's storyline in <i>A Storm of Swords</i>, on obtaining information about the planned wedding of Loras Tyrell and Sansa Stark—not from Sansa, as it happens in the books, but from Loras, and later on part of Blue Bard's storyline in <i>A Feast for Crows</i> as Queen Margaery's accuser. </p>
<p><b>Olyvar Frey</b> is a member of House Frey. He is the eighteenth son of Lord Walder Frey, the fourth with his sixth wife, Bethany Rosby. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Olyvar Nymeros Martell</b> was a younger brother of Prince Doran Martell. He died as an infant. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Olyvar Oakheart</b>, known as <b>the Green Oak</b>, was a knight from House Oakheart. He was a member of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Daeron I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Olyvar Yronwood</b> was a king of House Yronwood. He repeatedly led incursions into the Stormlands during the reign of the Storm King Erich VII Durrandon. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Olyver Bracken</b> was a knight from House Bracken and a member of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Omer Blackberry</b> is a sworn sword from House Blackberry in service at Dragonstone. </p>
<p><b>Omer Florent</b> is the eldest son of Ser Colin Florent, a younger brother of Lord Alester Florent of Brightwater Keep. Omer is a maester of the Citadel in service at Old Oak to House Oakheart. </p>
<p><b>Ondrew Locke</b> is the Lord of Oldcastle and the head of House Locke. He is an old man. </p>
<p>The <b>one-eyed crone</b> is an ancient crone of the <i>dosh khaleen</i> who dwell in Vaes Dothrak. Her given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Onqo</b> was a Dothraki <i>khal</i> who lived during the Century of Blood. </p>
<p>The <b>Onyx Emperor</b> was the legendary fifth ruler of the mythic Great Empire of the Dawn. He succeeded the Tourmaline Emperor and was in turn succeeded by the Topaz Emperor. </p>
<p>The <b>Opal Emperor</b> was the legendary seventh ruler of the mythic Great Empire of the Dawn and one of its last emperors. He succeeded the Topaz Emperor and was in turn succeeded by his daughter, the Amethyst Empress, though his second son would usurp his sister and crown himself as the Bloodstone Emperor. </p>
<p><b>Oppo</b>, better known as <b>Groat</b>, is a dwarf from across the narrow sea. </p>
<p><b>Orbelo</b> is a Braavosi bravo. He has fair hair and wears a jacket made of green velvet and cloth of silver. </p>
<p><b>Orbert Caswell</b>, known as <b>the Black Centaur</b>, was a member of House Caswell who became Lord Commander of the Night's Watch. </p>

<p><b>Orland of Oldtown</b>, also known as <b>Ormond of Oldtown</b>, is a singer. He is the royal harper and bard for House Baratheon of King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Orlos the Catamite</b> is a pit fighter in Meereen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ormond</b> was a knight slain in the Riverlands by forces of House Lannister during the War of the Five Kings. He was killed in Pennytree. </p>
<p><b>Ormond Osgrey</b> was Lord of Coldmoat and head of House Osgrey during the reign of Maegor I Targaryen. </p>

<p><b>Ormond Yronwood</b> was Lord of Yronwood and head of House Yronwood. He was the father of Anders Yronwood and the son of Lord Edgar Yronwood. </p>
<p><b>Ormund Baratheon</b> was the Lord of Storm's End and head of House Baratheon during the second half of the reign of Aegon V Targaryen and during the reign of Jaehaerys II Targaryen. He served the latter as Hand of the King, until his death whilst commanding the royal army in the invasion of the Stepstones in the War of the Ninepenny Kings. He was married to Princess Rhaelle Targaryen, the youngest daughter of King Aegon V. Ormund was the father of Steffon Baratheon and grandfather to Robert Baratheon, who would eventually overthrow House Targaryen and become the ruler of the Seven Kingdoms. </p>
<p><b>Ormund III Durrandon</b> was a Storm King of House Durrandon during the coming of the Andals in the stormlands. </p>
<p><b>Ormund Hightower</b> was Lord of the Hightower and head of House Hightower during the Dance of the Dragons. He wielded the Valyrian steel blade Vigilance. Ormund was the nephew of Ser Otto Hightower, Hand of the King to Viserys I Targaryen and Aegon II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ormund Wylde</b> is a knight from House Wylde sworn to King Stannis I Baratheon. </p>
<p><b>Ornela</b> is a widowed <i>khaleesi</i> of the <i>dosh khaleen</i>. Her character was created specifically for the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, in which she is played by Hannah John-Kamen. </p>
<p><b>Oro Tendyris</b> is a merchant from Braavos. Bradamar Frey is his ward. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Orryn Baratheon</b> was a knight from House Baratheon and a younger brother of Lord Rogar Baratheon of Storm's End. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Orson Stone</b> is an exiled knight from Westeros, a sellsword and member of the Windblown. </p>

<p><b>Orwyle</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel who later became Grand Maester. He served during the reigns of kings Viserys I and Aegon II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Orys Baratheon</b>, also known as <b>Orys One-Hand</b>, was the founder of House Baratheon and was the first Lord of Storm's End after House Durrandon. During the Wars of Conquest, he slew the last Storm King, Argilac the Arrogant, married his daughter Argella, and became the first Lord Paramount of the Stormlands. Orys is also considered the first Hand of the King, serving Aegon the Conqueror. </p>
<p><b>House Baratheon of Storm's End</b> is one of the Great Houses of Westeros, and is the principal house in the stormlands, which they rule as Lords Paramount of the Stormlands. Their seat, Storm's End, is an ancient castle raised by the Storm Kings from the now-extinct House Durrandon. The Baratheon sigil is a crowned black stag on a field of gold. Members of the family tend to be tall and powerfully built, with black hair and blue eyes, as well as strong, square jawlines. They are known for their mercurial tempers, and their words are "<i>Ours is the Fury</i>". </p>
<p><b>Orys Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Orys I</b> was a Westerosi king mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Osbert Serry</b> is the Lord of Southshield and the head of House Serry, from the Shield Islands. </p>
<p><b>Southshield</b> is an island of the Shield Islands in the Reach. The southernmost of the four isles, it lies near the mouth of the river Mander. It is the seat of House Serry. </p>

<p>King <b>Osric V Arryn</b> was a King of Mountain and Vale of House Arryn. He ordered the reconstruction of the Bloody Gate from the rough-hewn, unmortarted wall that it was, to the vaunted gate on which many a army smashed themselves to pieces.. </p>

<p><b>Othgar Hoare</b>, known as <b>Othgar Demonlover</b>, was a King of the Iron Islands from House Hoare. The Hoare kings of his era were opposed by the priests of the Drowned God because of their support for the Faith of the Seven, discouraging of reaving, and promotion of trade. </p>
<p><b>Othgar Hoare</b>, known as <b>Othgar the Soulless</b>, was a King of the Iron Islands from House Hoare. The Hoare kings of his era were opposed by the priests of the Drowned God because of their support for the Faith of the Seven, discouraging of reaving, and promotion of trade. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Otho Bracken</b>, known as <b>the Brute of Bracken</b>, was a knight of House Bracken during the reign of kings Daeron II and Aerys I Targaryen. He was the second son of Lord Bracken of Stone Hedge. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Otto Hightower</b> was a knight from House Hightower who served as Hand of the King to three kings, although two of the kings removed him from office at various times. He was the younger brother of Lord Hightower, and the uncle of Lord Ormund Hightower of Oldtown. His children included Alicent Hightower, the second queen of King Viserys I Targaryen, and Ser Gwayne Hightower, second in command of the gold cloaks. Otto is remembered as a warning that knowledge is not everything. </p>
