<p><b>Padraic Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Paezhar zo Myraq</b> is a Yunkai noble known as the <b>Little Pigeon</b>. </p>
<p><b>Palla</b> is a kennel girl at Winterfell. She is the daughter of Farlen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Parmen Crane</b>, also known as <b>Parmen the Purple</b>, is a knight of House Crane. He is named to King Renly I's Rainbow Guard. </p>
<p><b>Parquello Vaelaros</b> is a candidate to become a triarch of Volantis. </p>
<p><b>Lord Parren</b> was the head of House Parren during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Pascal Dabell</b> was a knight during the reign of Daeron II Targaryen. He had two brothers: Ser Ernest and Ser Lester Dabell. </p>
<p><b>Patchface</b>, nicknamed <b>Patches</b>, is Lord Stannis Baratheon's court fool and jester at Dragonstone. His face is tattooed in motley, earning his name. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Pate</b> is a novice of the Citadel. He is the POV Character of the Prologue of <i>A Feast for Crows</i>. </p>
<p><b>Pate</b> is a boy orphaned by the War of the Five Kings who is currently living at the crossroads inn. </p>
<p><b>Pate</b> is a ranger in the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Pate</b> is a whipping boy in service to House Baratheon of King's Landing. He is the whipping boy for Tommen I and the former whipping boy for Joffrey I. </p>
<p>This <b>High Septon</b>, whose birth name was <b>Pate</b>, was appointed High Septon after King Baelor I Targaryen informed the Most Devout that the Seven had revealed the new High Septon's identity to him. </p>
<p><b>Pate the Plowman</b> is a legendary figure of the Age of Heroes who founded House Moreland. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Pate the Woodcock</b> was a knight of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Pate</b> was a peasant sworn to House Osgrey. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Pate of the Blue Fork</b>, also known as Ser <b>Pate of Sevenstreams</b>, is a hedge knight from Sevenstreams in the northern riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Pate of Fairmarket</b> was a lowborn rebel who claimed the title of river king or King of the Trident in the generations after the riverlands were conquered by the Storm King Arlan III Durrandon. Pate even had a brief, inglorious reign, presumably ruling from Fairmarket, before being put down by the might of Storm's End. </p>
<p><b>Pate of Lancewood</b> is an inhabitant of Lancewood in the riverlands. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Pate of Longleaf</b>, known as <b>Longleaf the Lionslayer</b>, was a knight from Longleaf during the Targaryen civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Pate of Mory</b> is an inhabitant of Mory in the riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Pate of Shermer's Grove</b> is an inhabitant of Shermer's Grove in the riverlands. </p>
<p>The <b>High Septon</b>, formerly known as <b>Septon Pater</b>, was the second High Septon of the Faith of the Seven during the reign of Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Patrek Mallister</b> is a member of House Mallister, the son and heir of Lord Jason Mallister of Seagard. </p>
<p><b>Seagard</b> is a town in the northern riverlands, and its castle is the seat of House Mallister. Located on the western coast along Ironman's Bay, Seagard is sheltered by the Cape of Eagles and is nestled near the headwaters of the Blue Fork. It is southwest of the Twins and northwest of Oldstones. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Patrek of King's Mountain</b> is a knight from King's Mountain in the service of King Stannis Baratheon. He is one of the queen's men. </p>
<p><b>Patrek Vance</b> is the second son of Ser Dafyn Vance and Maegelle Frey. </p>
<p><b>Paxter Redwyne</b> is the Lord of the Arbor and head of House Redwyne. He is married to his cousin, Mina Tyrell, the sister of his liege lord, Mace Tyrell; he is thus twice a nephew of the Queen of Thorns, Olenna Redwyne. Paxter and Mina have two sons, Ser Horas and Ser Hobber, and a daughter, Desmera. </p>
<p>The <b>Arbor</b> is a golden island off the southwestern-most part of Westeros, ruled by House Redwyne. It is considered part of the Reach, and is separated from the mainland by the Redwyne Straits. It is protected by the Redwyne fleet, the largest fleet of the Seven Kingdoms. </p>
<p><b>Paxter Royce</b> was a member of House Royce mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Patrice Hightower</b> was a lady of House Hightower. She was the sister of Lord Manfred Hightower of Oldtown and the aunt of Lord Martyn Hightower, Queen Ceryse Hightower, and Ser Morgan Hightower. </p>
<p><b>Patricia Redwyne</b> was a noblewoman of House Redwyne during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Paxter Redwyne</b> is the Lord of the Arbor and head of House Redwyne. He is married to his cousin, Mina Tyrell, the sister of his liege lord, Mace Tyrell; he is thus twice a nephew of the Queen of Thorns, Olenna Redwyne. Paxter and Mina have two sons, Ser Horas and Ser Hobber, and a daughter, Desmera. </p>
<p><b>Lord Peake</b> was the Lord of Starpike, Dunstonbury, Whitegrove, and the head of House Peake during the late reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>Pearl Emperor</b> was the legendary second ruler of the mythic Great Empire of the Dawn. According to the tales told by the priestly scribes of Yin, he was the eldest son and the successor of the God-on-Earth, the son of the Maiden-Made-of-Light and the Lion of Night, who ruled for ten thousand years before ascending to the heavens. The Pearl Emperor then ruled for a thousand years and was followed by the Jade Emperor. He's credited by some for the construction of the Five Forts, to keep the Lion of Night and his demons away from the realms of men. </p>
<p><b>Pearse Caron</b> was the Lord of Nightsong, Lord of the Marches, and the head of House Caron during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Penny</b> is a dwarf woman from across the narrow sea. </p>
<p><b>Perceon III Gardener</b> was a King of the Reach and head of House Gardener. </p>
<p><b>Peremore Hightower</b>, known as <b>Peremore the Twisted</b>, was the second son of King Uthor of the High Tower. </p>
<p><b>Pereno Pendaerys</b> was a Lyseni garroted in a pillow house in 135&nbsp;AC during the bloody power struggle in the city after the downfall of the Rogare family. His brother Silvario was also murdered. </p>
<p><b>Perestan</b> is one of the archmaesters at the Citadel. He wrote <i>A Consideration of History</i>. </p>
<p><b>The Perfumed Hero</b> is a name the Windblown, a sellsword company hired by Yunkai, mockingly gave to a Yunkish nobleman commanding some of the Yunkai slave solders. </p>
<p><b>Perianne Moore</b> was a member of House Moore during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and a lady companion to Jaehaerys's daughter, Princess Saera Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Perkin Follard</b> is a knight from House Follard in the service of King Stannis Baratheon. He is one of the queen's men. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Perkin the Flea</b> was a hedge knight who lived during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Perra Frey</b> is the only child of Petyr Frey and Mylenda Caron. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Perra Royce</b> was a noblewoman from House Royce, though it is not mentioned which branch of the family she came from. She married Lord Walder Frey of the Twins and was the first of his eight wives. She is long deceased. </p>
<p><b>Perriane Frey</b> is the eldest daughter of Lord Walder Frey and Perra Royce. She is married to Ser Leslyn Haigh and they have three sons Harys, Donnel and Alyn Haigh. </p>
<p><b>Perros Blackmont</b> is the son of the Lady of Blackmont and a member of House Blackmont. He is a squire. </p>
<p><b>Lord Perryn</b> was the head of House Perryn during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Perwyn Frey</b> is a knight from House Frey. He is the fifteenth son of Lord Walder Frey and the first son born in the marriage between Walder and Bethany Rosby. </p>
<p><b>Perwyn Osgrey</b>, also known as <b>Perwyn the Proud</b>, was a Lord of Coldmoat and head of House Osgrey prior to Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p><b>House Osgrey of Standfast</b> is a noble house from Standfast in the Reach. Sworn to House Rowan, its lands border those of House Webber and House Stackhouse. They have not been lords in centuries, now being landed knights, though they once had been among the greatest houses of the Reach. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Peter Plumm</b> is a knight from House Plumm and is the second son of Lord Philip Plumm. </p>
<p><b>Petra Tallhart</b> was a member of House Tallhart mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Petyr Baelish</b>, also called <b>Littlefinger</b>, is the Lord and head of House Baelish of the Fingers. He serves as master of coin on the small council of King Robert I Baratheon. Petyr wears a mockingbird as his personal crest instead of House Baelish's sigil, a titan's head. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Aidan Gillen. </p>
<p><b>Petyr Baratheon</b> was the firstborn son of Lord Stannis Baratheon and Lady Selyse Florent in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. He was stillborn. </p>
<p><b>Petyr Frey</b>, also called <b>Petyr Pimple</b>, is a member of House Frey and is the youngest of Ser Ryman Frey's three sons. His elder brothers are Edwyn and Walder Frey. Petyr is married to Mylenda Caron and they have one daughter Perra Frey.  </p>
<p><b>Petyr Karstark</b> was a member of House Karstark mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Petyr Mallister</b> was a Lord of Seagard and a head of House Mallister. </p>
<p><b>Petyr Piper</b> was the Lord of Pinkmaiden and the head of House Piper during the reign of kings Viserys I and Aegon II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Petyr Plumm</b> was a knight from House Plumm during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Phario Forel</b> is a Braavosi playwright. He is said to have the bloodiest quill of all of Braavos. His relation with Syrio Forel is unknown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Philip Foote</b> is a one-eyed knight of little note from House Foote in the westerlands. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Philip Plumm</b> is the head of House Plumm. He has three sons. </p>
<p><b>Pia</b>, also known as <b>Pretty Pia</b>, is a servant of House Whent who works in the buttery at Harrenhal. </p>
<p><b>Pilman</b> was a Westerosi ship's captain from Lannisport who provided the Citadel with an account of a water dancer duel. He claimed that the water dancers seemed to barely skim upon the surface, and insisted he never saw anything like it for grace and skill, however. </p>
<p>A <b>pimply squire</b> from House Sarsfield is part of the Mountain's men. He is a squire to Ser Gregor Clegane, along with Joss Stilwood. The given name of the boy is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Pinchbottom Pate</b> was an old man who lived in Little Dosk. When ironmen raided Little Dosk, they attempted to take Pate's daughter. Pate tried to stop them, but was killed instead. He owed Ser Bennis a silver. </p>
<p>The <b>pious dwarf</b> is a holy brother and a member of the sparrows. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Lady Piper</b> was a member of House Piper, the daughter of a Lord of Pinkmaiden Castle. She was the third and final wife of Lord Quellon Greyjoy. Her given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>"Pisswater prince"</b> is the moniker that Tyrion Lannister gives the nameless tanner's son from Pisswater Bend who, according to Illyrio Mopatis, was swapped with Prince Aegon Targaryen when he was an infant. </p>
<p><b>Plague face</b> is how Arya Stark refers to a secret servant of the Many-Faced God in the House of Black and White in Braavos and a Faceless Man. He has the face of a plague victim. </p>
<p><b>Plummer</b> was the steward of Ashford during the reign of Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Podrick Payne</b>, frequently called <b>Pod</b>, is a squire from a cadet branch of House Payne, and he is a distant cousin of Ser Ilyn Payne. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Podrick is portrayed by Daniel Portman. </p>
<p><b>House Payne</b> is a noble house from the Westerlands. It is one of the principal houses sworn to House Lannister. Their arms are purple and white chequy with gold coins in the checks. </p>
<p>The <b>Poetess</b> is a courtesan in Braavos. She always has a book in hand. She has her own barge, and servants to pole her to trysts. </p>
<p><b>Pol</b> was a maester who wrote a treatise on Qohorik metalworking. </p>
<p><b>Pol Qo</b>, called <b>Hammer of the Jogos Nhai</b>, is a YiTish general that has claimed the title of God-Emperor as the first of the orange emperors in defiance of the seventeenth azure emperor, Bu Gai. His seat is located at the city of Trader Town. </p>
<p>Wisdom <b>Pollitor</b> was a member of the Alchemists' Guild in King's Landing. He trained Widsom Hallyne and claimed that the decline in the potency of wildfire was linked to the extinction of dragons. </p>
<p><b>Polliver</b> is a man-at-arms among the Mountain's men in service to Ser Gregor Clegane. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Andy Kellegher. </p>
<p><b>Pono</b> is a <i>ko</i> in Khal Drogo's <i>khalasar</i>. </p>
<p><b>Porridge</b> is the nickname of a gaoler at Dragonstone. </p>
<p><b>Porther</b> is a member of the household guard of Lord Eddard Stark at Winterfell. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Portifer Woodwright</b> is a knight of House Woodwright. He is the brother of Ser Lucantine Woodwright and is a household knight in King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Poul Pemford</b> is a guard at Riverrun from House Pemford. </p>
<p><b>Poxy Tym</b> is a member of the household guard sworn to House Stark of Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Praed</b> is a sellsword recruited by Yoren for the Night's Watch and is part of the group marching north to the Wall. </p>
<p><b>Prendahl na Ghezn</b> is a Ghiscari captain of the mercenary company Stormcrows. </p>
<p>The <b>Stormcrows</b> are a mercenary company found in the Free Cities. Their banner displays four crows between crossed lightning bolts. They number five hundred horses. </p>
<p><b>Prendos</b> was a pirate known for his black humor. <i>Mad Prendos</i>, one of Salladhor Saan's galleys, is named after him. </p>
<p><b>Prentys Tully</b> was the Lord of Riverrun and the head of House Tully during the later reign of King Maegor I Targaryen and the early reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. He was married to the pious Lady Lucinda, of House Broome. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Preston Greenfield</b> is a knight from House Greenfield. He is a member of King Robert I Baratheon's Kingsguard. </p>
<p><b>Priscella Hogg</b> was a noblewoman from House Hogg during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. She was a companion to Aegon's second wife, Queen Daenaera Velaryon. </p>
<p><b>Priscilla Royce</b> was a member of House Royce mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Prudence Celtigar</b> was a member of House Celtigar in the reigns of kings Maegor I Targaryen and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. She later became the Lady of Gulltown. </p>
<p><b>Pruea Royce</b> is a member of House Royce mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Prunella Celtigar</b> was a member of House Celtigar in the reigns of kings Maegor I Targaryen and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. She later became the Lady of Starpike, Dunstonbury, and Whitegrove. </p>
<p><b>Puckens</b> is a guard in service to House Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Pudding</b> was a child living in King's Landing during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Puddingfoot</b> is a member of the brotherhood without banners. </p>
<p><b>Pyat Pree</b> is a warlock from the city of Qarth. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Ian Hanmore. </p>
<p><b>Pycelle</b> is a Grand Maester of the Citadel who has served in King's Landing and on the small council for over forty years. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Julian Glover. </p>
<p><b>Pycelle's serving girl</b> is Grand Maester Pycelle's servant girl in the Red Keep. She is also Pycelle's bedwarmer, although the Citadel would not approve, as maesters are supposed to be celibate. Her name is not mentioned. </p>
<p><b>Pyg</b> is a member of the Brave Companions. </p>
<p><b>Pykewood Peake</b> is a sellsword in service to the Golden Company. He is one of the brothers of the exiled Lord Laswell Peake. </p>
<p><b>Pylos</b> is a maester of the Citadel, newly sent to serve Stannis Baratheon at Dragonstone. He is to be the eventual replacement for Maester Cressen. </p>
<p><b>Pynto</b> is the innkeep of a tavern in Braavos. </p>
<p><b>Pypar</b>, commonly known as <b>Pyp</b>, is a member of the Night's Watch. He is in the same recruit class as Jon Snow. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Jozef Altin. </p>
<p><b>Pytho Malanon</b> is a sculptor of Essos. </p>
<p><b>Qalen</b> was a maester who served at Pyke for House Greyjoy. </p>
<p><b>Qano</b> was a Dothraki <i>khal</i> who lived during the Century of Blood. He was one of the four <i>khals</i> that fought in the Field of Crows. </p>
<p><b>Qarl</b>, widely known as <b>Qarl the Maid</b>, is an ironborn warrior sworn to Balon Greyjoy. He is the grandson of a thrall. </p>
<p><b>Qarl the Thrall</b> is an ironborn raider. He presumably is, or once was, a thrall. </p>
<p><b>Qarl Corbray</b> was the Lord of Heart's Home and the head of House Corbray during the reign of the kings Maegor I and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. Jaehaerys made him the Commander of the City Watch of King's Landing at the beginning of his reign. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Qarl Correy</b> was a household knight in service to House Velaryon at High Tide. Of relatively low birth, Qarl was rumored to have been a lover of Ser Laenor Velaryon. </p>
<p><b>Qarl Kenning</b>, known as <b>Queer Qarl Kenning</b>, is a member of House Kenning of Harlaw. </p>
<p><b>Qarl Quickaxe</b> is a resident of the Iron Islands. His house and allegiance are unknown. He is mentioned by Asha Greyjoy as one of many Qarls who live on the Iron Islands. </p>
<p><b>Qarl Shepherd</b> is a member of House Shepherd in the Iron Islands. </p>
<p><b>Qarlon the Great</b> was an Andal warrior who united the Lorathi isles and dreamed of making himself "King of All Andals". His seat was a large wooden keep at Lorassyon. </p>
<p><b>Qarlton Chelsted</b> was a Lord of House Chelsted who served as master of coin to King Aerys II Targaryen. He was named to the office of Hand of the King during Robert's Rebellion. </p>
<p>King <b>Qarlton II Durrandon</b>, self-styled <b>Qarlton the Conqueror</b>, was a Storm King of House Durrandon during the Andal invasion and a grandson of King Erich VII Durrandon. He was the first Storm King to face the Andals in battle. He also, after four generations of war, completed the reconquest of Massey's Hook after a year's siege and slaying the last Massey king, Josua. However, he held his conquest for less than two years, as Togarion Bar Emmon threw the stormlanders away from Massey's Hook. Qarlton II, however, soon had to face the Andals, whose longships had begun to land on the Stormlands' shores. Qarlton II was succeeded by Qarlton III Durrandon. </p>
<p>King <b>Qarlton III Durrandon</b> was a Storm King of House Durrandon during the Andal invasion and the heir and successor of King Qarlton II Durrandon. Like his father, Qarlton III reigned in times of war. He was succeeded by his son Monfryd V Durrandon. </p>
<p><b>Qarro Volentin</b> is the current First Sword of Braavos, protector of Ferrego Antaryon, the Sealord of Braavos. </p>
<p><b>Qavo Nogarys</b> is a customs officer of Selhorys near Volantis. </p>
<p><b>Qezza</b> is a girl of the House of Galare, one of the noble ruling families of Meereen. Her brother is Grazhar. She is a cousin to Galazza Galare, the Green Grace of Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Qhored I Hoare</b>, known as <b>Qhored the Cruel</b>,, was one of the greatest High Kings of the Iron Islands. While he is usually associated with House Hoare, some accounts state he was actually of House Greyiron or House Blacktyde. </p>
<p><b>Qhorin</b>, known as <b>Qhorin Halfhand</b> and <b>the Halfhand</b>, is a ranger of the Night's Watch and second-in-command at the Shadow Tower. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Simon Armstrong. </p>
<p><b>Qhorin Volmark</b> was a Lord of Volmark and head of House Volmark during Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Qhorwyn Hoare</b>, known as <b>Qhorwyn the Cunning</b>, was a King of the Iron Islands from House Hoare. </p>
<p><b>Qoren Martell</b> was the ruling Prince of Dorne, the Lord of Sunspear, and the head of House Nymeros Martell during the reign of King Viserys I Targaryen as well as during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Lord Commander Qorgyle</b> was a member of House Qorgyle and was the 996th Lord Commander of the Night's Watch. His given name has not been revealed. </p>
<p><b>Qorro</b> is a Dothraki <i>khal</i> appearing in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Qos</b> is the captain of the <i>Wind Witch</i>, a galley out of Braavos or Myr. </p>
<p><b>Qotho</b> is a bloodrider to Khal Drogo. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Dar Salim. </p>
<p><b>Quaithe</b>, also known as <b>Quaithe of the Shadow</b>, is a shadowbinder from Asshai. She is portrayed by Laura Pradelska in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Quaro</b> is a Dothraki warrior assigned to the <i>khas</i> of Daenerys Targaryen within the <i>khalasar</i> of Khal Drogo. </p>
<p>The <b>queen o' whores</b> is a prostitute with Ser Ryman Frey during the siege of Riverrun. Her true name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Queen Whore</b> was the concubine to Cleon the Second. Her given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Quellon Botley</b> is the second son of Lord Germund Botley. </p>
<p><b>Quellon Greyjoy</b> was a Lord of the Iron Islands, Lord Reaper of Pyke, and head of House Greyjoy. He was the father of the current lord, Balon Greyjoy. The longship <i>Lord Quellon</i> is presumably named in his honor. </p>
<p><b>Quellon Humble</b> is an ironborn raider and a member of House Humble. </p>
<p><b>Quence</b>, is a mummer of the Ship. He is considered to not be good enough for the Blue Lantern. </p>
<p><b>Quenn</b> is a member of the free folk. </p>
<p><b>Quent</b> is a member of the household guard sworn to House Stark of Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Quenten Banefort</b> is the Lord of Banefort and head of House Banefort. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Quentin Tyrell</b> was a knight of House Tyrell during the reign of Aerys II Targaryen. He was a cousin of Lord Mace Tyrell. He has one son, Ser Olymer Tyrell. </p>
<p><b>Quenton Corbray</b> was the Lord of Heart's Home and head of House Corbray during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Quenton Greyjoy</b> was a member of House Greyjoy, the second son of Lord Quellon Greyjoy and his first wife, Lady Stonetree. </p>
<p><b>Quenton Greyjoy</b> is a distant cousin to Asha Greyjoy. He is captain of the longship <i>Salty Wench</i>. </p>
<p><b>Quenton Hightower</b> was a head of House Hightower and Lord of the Hightower during the reign of King Maekar I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Quenton Qoherys</b> was head of House Qoherys and the first Lord of Harrenhal. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Quentyn Ball</b>, known as <b>Fireball</b>, was a knight from House Ball during the reigns of kings Aegon IV Targaryen and Daeron II Targaryen. His personal coat-of-arms was a fireball blazing red and yellow across a night black field. </p>
<p><b>Quentyn Blackwood</b> was the Lord of Raventree Hall and the head of House Blackwood during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Quentyn Nymeros Martell</b>, better known simply as <b>Quentyn Martell</b>, is a knight from House Martell. He is the second child and eldest son of Doran Martell, Prince of Dorne, and Lady Mellario of Norvos. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Quentyn Qorgyle</b> is Lord of Sandstone and head of House Qorgyle in Dorne. </p>
<p><b>Quhuru Mo</b> is the captain of the <i>Cinnamon Wind</i> out of Tall Trees Town in the Summer Islands. He has a daughter, Kojja Mo. </p>
<p><b>Quickfinger</b> was a thief caught with stolen dragon eggs during the First Blackfyre Rebellion. He had sided with Daemon Blackfyre. </p>
<p><b>Quill</b> is a Braavosi playwright who writes bawdy plays for the mummers of the Ship. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Quillion</b> is an Archmaester of the Citadel. He has put forth the theory that the mysterious black stone fortress of Battle Isle that serves as the foundation of the Hightower of Oldtown was built by the mazemakers, citing its labyrinthine nature. </p>
<p><b>Quince</b> was the first maester to serve at the Eyrie, the seat of House Arryn. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Quincy Cox</b> is the Knight of Saltpans and the head of House Cox. </p>
<p><b>Quort</b> is a wildling raider. He is still a boy around the age of fourteen. He already has a wife and a child. </p>
<p><b>Qyburn</b> is a former maester who has joined the Brave Companions. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Anton Lesser. </p>
<p><b>Qyle</b> is one of the recruits for the Night’s Watch found by Yoren and is part of the band marching north to the Wall. </p>
<p><b>Qyle Corbray</b> was the King of the Fingers and a monarch of House Corbray during the Andal invasion. </p>
<p><b>Qyle Nymeros Martell</b> was a Dornish prince and younger brother to Princess Aliandra Martell. </p>
<p><b>Racallio Ryndoon</b> was a devious Tyroshi captain-general who declared himself King of the Narrow Sea. He is remembered in the Free Cities through two scholarly studies and numerous poems, romances, and songs. </p>
<p><b>Rafe</b> was a street child from Flea Bottom in King's Landing during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Rafford</b>, known as <b>Raff the Sweetling</b>, is one of the Mountain's men, the men-at-arms in service to Ser Gregor Clegane. </p>
<p><b>Ragnor Pyke</b> is an ironborn raider and a member of Victarion Greyjoy's crew on board the <i>Iron Victory</i>. He is bastard-born. </p>
<p><b>Ragwyle</b> is a wildling spearwife. She is big. </p>
<p>A <b>spearwife</b> is a free folk woman who is also a warrior. </p>
<p>The <b>Rainbow Knight</b> is the focus of a famous love story with Lady Shella. </p>
<p><b>Rakharo</b> is a Dothraki horserider in the <i>khalasar</i> of Khal Drogo. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Elyes Gabel. </p>
<p><b>Ralf the Limper</b> is an ironborn raider and is the captain of the <i>Lord Quellon</i>. </p>
<p><b>Ralf of Lordsport</b> is an ironborn raider from Lordsport. </p>
<p><b>Ralf the Shepherd</b> is an ironborn raider. </p>
<p><b>Ragged Ralf</b> is a legendary ironborn raider who supposedly lived during the Age of Heroes. He was from Old Wyk. </p>
<p><b>Ralf Kenning</b> is an ironborn captain, raider and a member of House Kenning of Harlaw. </p>
<p><b>Ralf Stonehouse</b>, better known as <b>Red Ralf Stonehouse</b>, is an ironborn raider and a member of House Stonehouse. He is captain of the ship <i>Red Jester</i> of the Iron Fleet. </p>
<p><b>Ralph Buckler</b> is Lord of Bronzegate and the head of House Buckler. His cousin is Ser Brus Buckler. </p>
<p><b>Ramsay Snow</b> is the bastard son of Roose Bolton, Lord of the Dreadfort and head of House Bolton, and is known as <b>the Bastard of Bolton</b> and <b>the Bastard of the Dreadfort</b>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Iwan Rheon. </p>
<p><b>Randa</b> was an inhabitant of the Riverlands. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Randor the Exile</b> was a knight during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Randyll Tarly</b> is Lord of Horn Hill and head of House Tarly. He is married to Lady Melessa Florent, and is the father of the POV character Samwell Tarly. Randyll wields the Tarly ancestral blade Heartsbane, a Valyrian steel greatsword, in battle. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by James Faulkner. </p>
<p><b>Rast</b> is a recruit of the Night's Watch. Ser Alliser Thorne refers to him as <b>Rat</b>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Luke McEwan. </p>
<p>The <b>Rat Cook</b> was an infamous member of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p>The <b>Lord of Bones</b>, also mocked as <b>Rattleshirt</b>, is a free folk leader of renown. His given name is unknown. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Edward Dogliani and Ross O'Hennessy. </p>
<p><b>Ravella Smallwood</b>, née <b>Swann</b>, is the Lady of Acorn Hall. She is the wife of Lord Theomar Smallwood and the mother of Carellen Smallwood. </p>
<p><b>Ravos Hoare</b>, known as <b>Ravos the Raper</b>, was an ironborn raider and the son of Harrag Hoare, an Iron King. </p>
<p><b>Rawney</b> is a brother of the order on the Quiet Isle. </p>
<p><b>Raya Stark</b> was a noblewoman of House Stark. She was the third daughter of Lord Cregan Stark and Lady Alysanne Blackwood. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rayford Rosby</b> was a knight from House Rosby during the final days of King Aenys I Targaryen and the coronation of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Raylon Rivers</b> was a knight from House Bracken and the bastard half-brother of Ser Amos Bracken. He may have been a son of Lord Humfrey Bracken of Stone Hedge. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Raymar Royce</b> was a former head of a lesser branch of House Royce at the start of the third century after Aegon's Conquest, that may or may not be the same lesser branch that becomes House Royce of the Gates of the Moon in 300&nbsp;AC. </p>
<p><b>Raymond Nayland</b> is a knight of House Nayland. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Raymond Rychard</b> was a knight during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Raymont Baratheon</b> was a knight from House Baratheon and a younger son of Lord Orys Baratheon and Lady Argella Durrandon. He was a member of King Aenys I Targaryen's Kingsguard during the Faith Militant uprising. </p>
<p><b>Raymun Redbeard</b> was a King-Beyond-the-Wall. He is renowned for having led an invasion of the north in the time of Jon Snow's grandfather's grandfather. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Raymun Darry</b> is a knight of House Darry and the lord of Castle Darry. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Raymun Fossoway</b> was a knight and the founder of House Fossoway of New Barrel in 209&nbsp;AC. </p>
<p><b>Raymund Connington</b> is the younger brother and heir of Ser Ronnet Connington, the Knight of Griffin's Roost. He resides in Griffin's Roost. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Raymund Frey</b> is a knight from House Frey and is the eleventh son of Lord Walder Frey, the sixth born of his marriage to Amarei Crakehall. Raymund is married to Beony Beesbury. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Raymund Mallery</b> was a knight from House Mallery and a member of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Raymund Tyrell</b> is the son of Ser Olymer Tyrell and Lysa Meadows. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Raynald Westerling</b> is a knight from House Westerling, the eldest son and heir of Lord Gawen Westerling and Lady Sybell Spicer. </p>
<p><b>Raynard</b> is a septon of the Faith of the Seven. He is stationed in King's Landing and is of the Most Devout. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Raynard Ruttiger</b> is a landed knight and the head of House Ruttiger. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Raynard Ruskyn</b> was a knight who became Lord Commander of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Red Flea</b> is one of the daily-assigned names of an Unsullied purchased by Daenerys Targaryen. He has previously been known as <b>Black Rat</b>, <b>Brown Flea</b>, and possibly <b>Blue Toad</b> or <b>Blue Worm</b>. </p>
<p>The <b>Red Lamb</b> is a former slave in Meereen training to become a knight with Ser Barristan Selmy. His real name is not known. </p>
<p>The <b>Red Oarsman</b> is an ironborn captain. </p>
<p>The <b>Red Raven</b> was a member of the free folk and was the younger brother of Raymun Redbeard, a legendary King-Beyond-the-Wall. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Red Rolfe</b> is an ironborn warrior. </p>
<p><b>Redtusk</b> was a supporter of Daemon I Blackfyre during the First Blackfyre Rebellion. </p>
<p><b>Redwyn</b> was a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Lord Redwyne</b> was the Lord of the Arbor and head of House Redwyne during the reign of kings Viserys I, Aegon II and Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Reek</b> is a man-at-arms in service to House Bolton. His real name may be <b>Heke</b>. Reek is the personal servant of Ramsay Snow. He is reportedly never far from his master, and is almost as renowned for his cruelty as Ramsay is, and appears to practice necrophilia. Due to his stench, he is rumored to never bathe. </p>
<p><b>Regan Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Regenard Estren</b> is the Lord of Wyndhall and head of House Estren. </p>
<p><b>Reginald Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Reginald Lannister</b> is a member of House Lannister of Lannisport and one of Tywin Lannister's bannermen at Harrenhal. The character was created specifically for the TV series and he is played by Patrick Fitzsymons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Regis Groves</b> was a knight of the Kingsguard during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Regnar Drumm</b>, known as <b>Raven-feeder</b>, was a High King of the Iron Islands from House Drumm. </p>
<p><b>Rego Draz</b> was a merchant-trader and money-changer from Pentos. He became the master of coin in King's Landing during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen after the king reached majority. </p>
<p><b>Renfred Rykker</b> is Lord of Duskendale and head of House Rykker, a noble house of the crownlands. </p>
<p><b>Renly Baratheon</b> is the Lord of Storm's End and Lord Paramount of the Stormlands. The younger brother of King Robert I and Lord Stannis, Renly serves as master of laws on Robert's small council. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> Renly is played by Gethin Anthony. </p>
<p><b>Highgarden</b> is a castle which serves as the seat of House Tyrell, the regional capital of the Reach, and the heart of chivalry in the Seven Kingdoms. It lies on the Mander where the ocean road meets the roseroad, making it an important crossroads. </p>
<p><b>Renly Norcross</b> is the second son of Ser Hosman Norcross and lady Delena Florent. He is the younger brother of Alester Norcross, and a half-brother of Edric Storm. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rennifer Crabb</b> was a knight from House Crabb during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Rennifer Longwaters</b> is the chief undergaoler of the dungeons beneath the Red Keep. He is a bowed old man. He is descended from Ser Jon Waters, the bastard son of Princess Elaena Targaryen and Alyn Velaryon. He keeps the counts of the prisoners in the cells. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Reynard Reyne</b> was a knight from House Reyne and the younger son of Lord Robert Reyne. Reynard had two older sibings, Roger and Ellyn. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Reynard Webber</b> was Lord of Coldmoat and head of House Webber. </p>
<p><b>Lord Reyne</b> was the Lord of Castamere and head of House Reyne during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Reysen</b> is one of the recruits for the Night’s Watch found by Yoren and is part of the band marching north to the Wall. </p>
<p><b>Reznak mo Reznak</b> is the Ghiscari seneschal of the city of Meereen. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Rhae Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen, the second daughter and youngest child of King Maekar I Targaryen and Lady Dyanna Dayne. </p>
<p><b>Maekar I Targaryen</b> was Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and the fourteenth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He was the fourth son of King Daeron II Targaryen, and was given the Targaryen seat of Summerhall, and was thus known as the Prince of Summerhall. Maekar was a capable army commander who served in two of the Blackfyre Rebellions. After a number of unexpected deaths in the royal family, he came to the throne in 221&nbsp;AC. </p>
<p><b>Rhaegar Frey</b> is a member of House Frey and the second son of Ser Aenys Frey and Tyana Wylde, who died in childbirth. Rhaegar is married to Jeyne Beesbury and has three children with her, Robert, Walda, and Jonos. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Rhaegar Targaryen</b> was the firstborn son of King Aerys II Targaryen and his sister-wife, Queen Rhaella. As heir-apparent, he was the Prince of Dragonstone and crown prince for the Iron Throne. Rhaegar was popular with the smallfolk during his lifetime, but he died in Robert's Rebellion which was triggered in part by his abduction of Lyanna Stark. He was slain in single combat by Robert Baratheon at the ruby ford during the Battle of the Trident. Rhaegar was the elder brother of the exiled last members of House Targaryen, Prince Viserys and Princess Daenerys. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Rhaegel Targaryen</b> was the third son of King Daeron II Targaryen and Queen Myriah Martell. </p>
<p><b>Rhaego</b> is son of Daenerys Targaryen and <i>Khal</i> Drogo. He was named after his late uncle, Prince Rhaegar Targaryen. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Rhaella Targaryen</b> was the sister, wife, and queen of King Aerys II Targaryen and the only daughter of King Jaehaerys II Targaryen and his sister-wife, Queen Shaera Targaryen. Her grandfather was King Aegon V Targaryen. Rhaella was the mother of Prince Rhaegar, Prince Viserys, and Princess Daenerys. She died shortly after Daenerys's birth. </p>
<p>Septa <b>Rhaella</b>, born <b>Rhaella Targaryen</b>, was a daughter of Prince Aegon and Princess Rhaena Targaryen. She had an older twin sister, Aerea. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Rhaelle Targaryen</b> was the youngest child of King Aegon V Targaryen and Queen Betha Blackwood. She was married to Lord Ormund Baratheon of Storm's End. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Rhaena Targaryen</b> was the eldest of the six children of King Aenys I Targaryen and Queen Alyssa Velaryon. She was a dragonrider and rode the dragon Dreamfyre. </p>
<p>Lady <b>Rhaena Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Rhaena of Pentos</b> and <b>Rhaena Corbray</b>, was one of the twin daughters of Prince Daemon Targaryen and Lady Laena Velaryon; Baela Targaryen was her older twin. Rhaena was the niece of King Viserys I Targaryen and the cousin of King Aegon II Targaryen. She was also the half-sister of Kings Aegon III and Viserys II Targaryen, as well as the stillborn Visenya Targaryen. Rhaena was a dragonrider who rode Morning. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Rhaena Targaryen</b> was the second daughter of King Aegon III Targaryen and his second wife, Queen Daenaera Velaryon. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Rhaenyra Targaryen</b>, cheered as <b>the Realm's Delight</b> when she was young and later called <b>the Half-Year Queen</b>, was the first-born child of King Viserys I Targaryen. Rhaenyra was King Viserys I's only living child by his first wife, Queen Aemma of House Arryn. At the age of eight, she was made her father's heir and grew up expecting to become the first ruling Queen of Westeros. Rhaenyra was a dragonrider whose mount was Syrax. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Rhaenys Targaryen</b> was the youngest sister of King Aegon I Targaryen, the first Lord of the Seven Kingdoms. Both she and her older sister Visenya were married to Aegon, and it was said that she was Aegon's favorite. Through her son with Aegon, Aenys I, the line of the dragonkings continued, with fifteen of the sixteen Targaryen kings being direct descendants of Rhaenys and Aegon. She was a dragonrider who rode the dragon Meraxes. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Rhaenys Targaryen</b>, known as <b>the Queen Who Never Was</b>, was the daughter of Prince Aemon Targaryen and Lady Jocelyn Baratheon. She was married to Lord Corlys Velaryon of Driftmark. She was a dragonrider whose dragon was Meleys, the Red Queen. </p>
<p><b>Rhaenys Targaryen</b> was the daughter of Prince Rhaegar Targaryen and Princess Elia Martell. </p>
<p><b>Rhalko</b> is a Dothraki <i>khal</i> appearing in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Rhea Florent</b> is the second daughter of Lord Alester Florent. She is the fourth wife of Leyton Hightower, Lord of the Hightower. It is unknown if Rhea is the mother of any of Leyton's ten children. </p>
<p><b>Rhea Royce</b> was the Lady of Runestone and the head of House Royce during the reigns of kings Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Viserys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Daemon Targaryen</b> was a member of House Targaryen, being a younger son of Prince Baelon Targaryen and a brother of King Viserys I Targaryen. Daemon was the second husband of Rhaenyra Targaryen, Princess of Dragonstone, following Ser Laenor Velaryon. </p>
<p><b>Runestone</b> is the seat of House Royce in the Vale of Arryn. It lies on a peninsula north of the Bay of Crabs, east of Redfort and south of Old Anchor. While Runestone is on the northern shore of the peninsula, the nearby city of Gulltown is on the southern shore. </p>
<p><b>Rhialta Vance</b> is a noblewoman of House Vance of Wayfarer's Rest. She is the second daughter of the heir of Wayfarer's Rest, Ser Karyl Vance. </p>
<p><b>Rhodry</b> is a maester of the Citadel in service to House Cerwyn. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rhogar Velaryon</b> was a knight from House Velaryon. He was a nephew of Lord Corlys Velaryon by his youngest brother. He had four brothers, including Ser Malentine, and several cousins. </p>
<p><b>Rhogoro</b> is the son and <i>khalakka</i> of the Dothraki horselord, Khal Moro. </p>
<p><b>Rhonda Rowan</b> is a member of House Rowan. She is married to Ser Baelor Hightower, the heir of House Hightower. Her relation to Lord Mathis Rowan of Goldengrove is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Ricasso</b> is Prince Doran Martell's seneschal at Sunspear. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Richard Farrow</b> is a knight of House Farrow. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Richard Horpe</b> is a knight of House Horpe in service to Stannis Baratheon. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Richard Lonmouth</b> was a knight from House Lonmouth. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Richard Morrigen</b> is a knight from House Morrigen. He is the brother and heir to Lester Morrigen, Lord of Crow's Nest. </p>
<p><b>Richard Rodden</b> was the head of House Rodden during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Richard Roote</b> was a knight from House Roote. </p>
<p><b>Rickard Karstark</b> is the Lord of Karhold and head of House Karstark. He has three sons, Harrion, Eddard, and Torrhen, and one daughter, Alys. </p>
<p><b>Rickard Liddle</b> known as <b>Little Liddle</b>, is the youngest son of Lord Torren Liddle, known as the Liddle, the clan chief of House Liddle, a mountain clan in the north. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rickard Redwyne</b> was a knight from House Redwyne during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. He was the second son of Lord Manfryd Redwyne of the Arbor. </p>
<p><b>Rickard Rowan</b> was the Lord of Goldengrove and the head of House Rowan during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen and the beginning of the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Rickard Ryswell</b> is a son of Lord Rodrik Ryswell and a member of House Ryswell. </p>
<p><b>Rickard Stark</b>, known as <b>the Laughing Wolf</b> for his good nature, was a King in the North and a member of House Stark. He was the son of King Jon Stark. </p>
<p><b>Rickard Stark</b> was Lord of Winterfell, Warden of the North, and head of House Stark during the reign of King Aerys II Targaryen. He was the only child of Lord Edwyle Stark and Lady Marna Locke. Rickard was the father of the current Lord of Winterfell, Eddard Stark. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Wayne Foskett in a Season 6 flashback. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rickard Thorne</b> was a knight from House Thorne and a member of the Kingsguard during the reigns of kings Viserys I and Aegon II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Rickard Tyrell</b> is a member of House Tyrell, a distant cousin of the ruling line. He is the son of Ser Olymer Tyrell and Lysa Meadows. </p>
<p><b>Rickard Wylde</b> is the son of Ser Jon Wylde and Elyana Vypren. </p>
<p><b>Rickon Stark</b> is Eddard and Catelyn's youngest child, only three years old when the series begins. Rickon is a naturally aggressive and strong-willed child, but his youth makes it difficult for him to cope with the terrible changes that come to his family and life. He is usually accompanied by his direwolf, Shaggydog. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> Rickon is played by Art Parkinson. </p>
<p><b>Rickon Stark</b> was the Lord of Winterfell and the head of House Stark during the reign of King Viserys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Rickon Stark</b> was a member of House Stark, the eldest son and heir of Lord Cregan Stark and Lady Arra Norrey. He married Jeyne Manderly, with whom he had two daughters, Sansa and Serena Stark. </p>
<p><b>Rigney</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel. </p>
<p><b>Rob</b>, better known as <b>Big Rob</b>, was a simpleton in service to House Osgrey during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. Squinty Jeyne was his mother. </p>
<p><b>Rob</b>, better known as <b>Rob the Starvling</b>, was a member of the Poor Fellows during the Faith Militant uprising. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robar Royce</b>, also known as <b>Robar the Red</b>, is a knight from House Royce. He is the second son of Yohn Royce, Lord of Runestone. </p>
<p><b>Robar Royce</b> was a Lord of Runestone and head of House Royce mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Robar II Royce</b> was a Bronze King from House Royce. Robar became High King of the Vale, the Fingers, and the Mountains of the Moon and nearly held back the coming of the Andals, but he was ultimately slain in the Battle of the Seven Stars. </p>
<p><b>Robard Cerwyn</b> was the Lord of Cerwyn and the head of House Cerwyn during the latter half of the second century after Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robb Reyne</b> was a knight from House Reyne during the reign of Daeron II Targaryen. He was considered one of the finest knights of his time. </p>
<p><b>Robb Rivers</b>, known as <b>Red Robb Rivers</b> and <b>the Bowman of Raventree</b>, was a bastard of House Blackwood of Raventree Hall. </p>
<p><b>Robb Stark</b> is the eldest son of Eddard Stark and Catelyn Tully and is the heir of House Stark to Winterfell and the north. He is called <b>the Young Wolf</b> by friend and foe alike. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Richard Madden. </p>
<p><b>Robert Arryn</b>, also known as <b>Sweetrobin</b>, is the only son of Lord Jon Arryn and Lady Lysa Tully. He is the new head of House Arryn, Lord of the Eyrie, Defender of the Vale, and Warden of the East. </p>
<p>The <b>Eyrie</b> is an ancient castle and seat of House Arryn, one of the oldest lines of Andal nobility, within the Vale of Arryn. It is situated in the Mountains of the Moon on a shoulder of the peak known as the Giant's Lance, several thousand feet above the valley below. Although small compared to the seats of other Great Houses in Westeros, the Eyrie is considered impregnable to attack. During wintertime, the Arryns seek refuge against the cold in the Gates of the Moon at the base of the mountain. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robert Ashford</b> was a knight from House Ashford, and the younger son of the ruling Lord Ashford during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Robert I Baratheon</b> is the King of the Andals, the Rhoynar, and the First Men, Lord of the Seven Kingdoms and Protector of the Realm of Westeros, and the head of House Baratheon of King's Landing. Robert was crowned king after King Aerys II Targaryen, his first cousin once removed, was killed during Robert's Rebellion. Following the war, Robert married Cersei Lannister to ensure political stability. With her, Robert has three children: Joffrey, Myrcella, and Tommen. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Mark Addy. </p>
<p><b>Robert Blackwood</b> is the sixth and youngest son of Lord Tytos Blackwood of Raventree Hall. </p>
<p><b>Robert Blackwood</b> was a nobleman of House Blackwood during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robert Brax</b> is a knight from House Brax. He is the second son of Lord Andros Brax. </p>
<p><b>Robert Brax</b> is a member of House Brax, the eldest son of Ser Flement Brax and Morya Frey. He is a page at Casterly Rock. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Flement Brax</b> is a knight from House Brax and the third son of Lord Andros Brax. He is married to Morya Frey and they have three sons together: Robert, Walder and Jon. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robert Darklyn</b> was a knight from House Darklyn and was briefly a member of the Kingsguard during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robert Flowers</b>, known as <b>Red Robert Flowers</b>, was a knight of the Kingsguard and a bastard from the Reach. Despite his bastard origin, he rose to become Lord Commander of the Kingsguard. </p>
<p><b>Robert Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, the eldest son of Rhaegar Frey and Jeyne Beesbury. He is one of the numerous great-grandchildren of Lord Walder Frey. </p>
<p><b>Rhaegar Frey</b> is a member of House Frey and the second son of Ser Aenys Frey and Tyana Wylde, who died in childbirth. Rhaegar is married to Jeyne Beesbury and has three children with her, Robert, Walda, and Jonos. </p>
<p><b>Robert Frey</b> is the eldest son of Ser Raymund Frey, the eleventh son of Lord Walder Frey, and his wife, Beony Beesbury. He has six younger siblings: Malwyn, Sarra, Serra, Cersei, Tywin and Jaime Frey. </p>
<p><b>Robert Paege</b> is a knight from House Paege. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robert Quince</b> was a knight and the castellan of Dragonstone during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robert Redwyne</b> was a knight from House Redwyne during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Robert Reyne</b> was the Lord of Castamere and head of House Reyne during the time Gerold the Golden was Lord of Casterly Rock. He was the father of Roger, Reynard, and Ellyn. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robert Rowan</b> was a knight from House Rowan and the heir to Goldengrove during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robert Stone</b> is the name of the knight that Ser Osmund Kettleblack claimed knighted him on the battlefield. Ser Osmund claims he is dead. According to the naming conventions for bastards, Robert must have been a bastard from the Vale. He is not known to Ser Jaime Lannister, who believes Stone was made up by Osmund. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robert Tyrell</b> was a knight of House Tyrell and the High Steward of Highgarden during the reign of Mern VI Gardener, King of the Reach. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Robert Vance</b> was the head of one of the branches of House Vance four centuries before the Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Robeson</b> was a septon during the rule of Lord Damon Hightower over Oldtown. </p>
<p><b>Robett Glover</b> is a member of House Glover. He is the brother of Galbart Glover, the husband of Sybelle Glover, and the father of two children, Gawen and Erena. The appendices of <i>A Clash of Kings</i> and <i>A Storm of Swords</i> state that Gawen is the heir to Deepwood Motte, while the appendices of <i>A Feast for Crows</i> and <i>A Dance with Dragons</i> state that Robett is the heir of Galbart. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Tim McInnerny. </p>
<p><b>Robin</b> was a brother of Septon Meribald. He died in the War of the Ninepenny Kings. </p>
<p><b>Black Robin</b> was an outlaw. The singers made a sad song about him "The Day They Hanged Black Robin". It is unknown if Black Robin really existed. </p>
<p><b>Robin</b> was a candlemaker's daughter who lived in Flea Bottom during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Robin Arryn</b> was a King of Mountain and Vale from House Arryn. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robin Darklyn</b>, known as <b>Darkrobin</b>, was a knight from House Darklyn. </p>
<p><b>Robin Flint</b> is a member of House Flint of Widow's Watch and the son of Lyessa Flint, Lady of Widow's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Robin Greyjoy</b> was the ninth son of Lord Quellon Greyjoy, and his only son by his third wife, Lady Piper. </p>
<p><b>Robin Hill</b> was a bastard from the westerlands who rose to become Lord Commander of the Night's Watch. He is considered one of the worst Lord Commanders after almost destroying the Watch. </p>
<p><b>Robin Hollard</b> was a member of House Hollard and a squire during the Defiance of Duskendale. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robin Massey</b> was a knight from House Massey and was briefly made Lord Commander of the Kingsguard during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Robin Moreland</b> is the head of House Moreland in the westerlands. </p>
<p><b>Robin Peasebury</b> is the Lord of Poddingfield and the head of House Peasebury. </p>
<p><b>Robin Penrose</b> was the only son and eldest child of Lord Ronnel Penrose and his wife Princess Elaena Targaryen. He was presumably the heir of Parchments. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robin Potter</b> is a knight of House Potter. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robin Ryger</b> is a knight of House Ryger who serves as the captain of the guard at Riverrun. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robyn Rhysling</b> was a knight from House Rhysling during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robin Shaw</b> was a knight of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Robyn Rhysling</b> was a knight from House Rhysling during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Robyn Ryswell</b> was a noblewoman from House Ryswell during the latter half of the second century after Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Roderick Blackwood</b> was a Lord of Raventree Hall and head of House Blackwood four centuries before Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Roderick Dustin</b>, known as <b>Roddy the Ruin</b>, was the Lord of Barrowton and the head of House Dustin during the Targaryen civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Roderick Stark</b> was the Lord of Winterfell and the head of House Stark during the first half of the first century after Aegon's Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Rodrik Arryn</b> was the Lord of the Eyrie and the head of House Arryn during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rodrik Cassel</b> is a knight from House Cassel and a member of the Stark household. He is the uncle of Jory Cassel and is the master-at-arms of Winterfell. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Ron Donachie and in a Season 6 flashback by Fergus Leathem. </p>
<p><b>Rodrik Flint</b> was a member of House Flint who became Lord Commander of the Night's Watch. It is unknown from which branch of House Flint he came from. </p>
<p><b>Rodrik Freeborn</b> is an ironborn raider. He descends from either thralls or salt wives. </p>
<p><b>Rodrik Greyjoy</b> was a claimant Lord of the Iron Islands from House Greyjoy during the regency of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Rodrik Greyjoy</b> was the oldest son of Balon Greyjoy, Lord of the Iron Islands. He was killed during Greyjoy's Rebellion. He may have been named after his maternal uncle, Lord Rodrik Harlaw of Harlaw. </p>
<p><b>Greyjoy's Rebellion</b> or the <b>Greyjoy Rebellion</b> was an attempt at secession by Balon Greyjoy against the Iron Throne in 289&nbsp;AC, nine years before the beginning of <i>A Game of Thrones</i>. Balon tried to break away from the Seven Kingdoms to secure independence for the Iron Islands and restore the Old Way, lost almost three hundred years before, during Aegon's Conquest. The rebellion was crushed and Balon was forced to surrender, cementing the hold of King Robert I Baratheon on the Iron Throne. </p>
<p><b>Rodrik Harlaw</b> is the Lord of Harlaw, Lord of the Ten Towers, and head of House Harlaw. He is nicknamed <b>Rodrik the Reader</b> because he is always reading, which is uncommon amongst the ironborn. He is the captain of <i>Sea Song</i>. </p>
<p><b>Rodrik Ryswell</b> is Lord of the Rills and the head of House Ryswell in the north. He has at least two daughters, Bethany who is deceased and Barbrey, the Lady of Barrowton, and three sons, Roger, Rickard, and Roose. Rodrik's personal coat of arms is an alteration of the Ryswell horse head, golden instead of black. </p>
<p>The <b>Rills</b> is an area in the north ruled by House Ryswell. It is located southeast of the Stony Shore, north of Blazewater Bay, and west of the barrowlands. The area's name suggests it has numerous streams and brooks. </p>
<p><b>Rodrik Sparr</b> is a member of House Sparr from the Iron Islands. He is the captain of the ship <i>Grief</i> in the Iron Fleet and is under the command of Victarion Greyjoy. His crew call him the <b>Vole</b>. </p>
<p><b>Rodrik Stark</b> was a King in the North and head of House Stark. His statue is in the crypts of Winterfell, near that of Torrhen Stark. </p>
<p><b>Rodrik Stark</b>, known as <b>the Wandering Wolf</b>, was a member of House Stark, the fifth son and youngest child of Lord Beron Stark and Lady Lorra Royce. He married Arya Flint of the mountain clans and had two daughters; Branda and Lyarra Stark. </p>
<p><b>Rodwell Stark</b> was the Lord of Winterfell and the head of House Stark during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Roelle</b> was a septa of the Faith for Brienne of Tarth when she was growing up at Evenfall Hall. </p>
<p><b>Rogar Baratheon</b> was the Lord of Storm's End and head of House Baratheon during the reigns of kings Maegor I Targaryen and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. During the minority of Jaehaerys I, Rogar served as Hand of the King and Protector of the Realm. Throughout the long reign of King Jaehaerys I, Lord Rogar proved to be both a loyal friend and brief adversary to the king. </p>
<p><b>Rogar Bolton</b>, known as <b>Rogar the Huntsman</b>, was the last Red King of the Dreadfort from the dynasty of House Bolton. </p>
<p><b>Roger of Pennytree</b> was the squire and nephew of Ser Arlan of Pennytree. </p>
<p><b>Roger Blackwood</b> was a member of House Blackwood during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Roger Corne</b> was a landed knight from the Blackwater Rush during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Roger Hogg</b> is the Knight of Sow's Horn and head of House Hogg. He is a bannerman of House Hayford. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Roger Reyne</b>, known as <b>the Red Lion</b>, was a Lord of Castamere and head of House Reyne. He was a famous knight and considered one of the deadliest men of the westerlands. </p>
<p><b>Roger Ryswell</b> is a son of Lord Rodrik Ryswell and a member of House Ryswell. </p>
<p><b>Roggerio Rogare</b> was a member of House Rogare, a Lysene noble banking family. He was the son of Lysandro Rogare, the First Magister of Lys. </p>
<p><b>Red Roggo</b> is a cutpurse in Braavos. He is a frequent patron of the Happy Port. </p>
<p><b>Roggon Rustbeard</b> is a member of the crew on Asha Greyjoy's ship, <i>Black Wind</i>. </p>
<p><b>Rogin Salt­-Beard</b> is an ironborn raider. He is one of Euron Greyjoy's captains or sworn swords. </p>
<p><b>Rognar II Greyiron</b> was the last King of the Iron Islands from House Greyiron. </p>
<p><b>Rogo</b> was a Dothraki <i>khal</i> who lived during the Century of Blood. He sacked the city of Ibbish a generation after Khal Scoro, putting the city to the torch and marching ten thousand women into slavery. </p>
<p><b>Rohanne of Tyrosh</b> was the wife of Daemon I Blackfyre, with whom she had seven sons and several daughters. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, she is replaced with Serena Blackfyre. </p>
<p><b>Rohanne Tarbeck</b> was a member of House Tarbeck and the elder daughter of Lord Walderan and Ellyn Tarbeck. </p>
<p><b>Rohanne Webber</b>, known as the <b>Red Widow</b>, was the Lady of Coldmoat and head of House Webber during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. She was the daughter of Lord Wyman Webber. Later, she married Lord Gerold Lannister and became Lady of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Roland of the Horn</b> is a legendary knight of the Reach who lived during the Age of Heroes. Tales describe him as a knight even though knights came to Westeros thousands of years later with the Andal invasion. </p>
<p><b>Roland I Arryn</b> was the fourth King of Mountain and Vale from House Arryn. He is noted for ordering construction of the Eyrie. </p>
<p><b>Roland II Arryn</b> was a King of Mountain and Vale from House Arryn. </p>
<p><b>Roland Blackwood</b> was a member of House Blackwood during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Roland Crakehall</b> is the Lord of Crakehall and the head of House Crakehall. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Roland Crakehall</b> was a knight from House Crakehall and a member of the Kingsguard during the reigns of the kings Daeron II and Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Roland Darry</b> was a Lord of Darry and head of House Darry during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Roland Waynwood</b> is a knight of House Waynwood. He is a grandson of Lady Anya Waynwood, Lady of Ironoaks. He appears to be the son of Lady Anya's heir, Ser Morton Waynwood. </p>
<p><b>Roland Westerling</b> was the Lord of the Crag and the head of House Westerling during the Dance of the Dragons. With the coronation of the young Aegon III Targaryen, Lord Roland was one of the seven regents that would rule until Aegon came of age. </p>
<p><b>Rolder</b> is a guard sworn to House Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Rolfe</b> is an ironborn warrior. It is unknown if he is the same character as Red Rolfe or Rolfe the Dwarf. </p>
<p><b>Rolfe the Dwarf</b> is one of the crew on Asha Greyjoy's ship, <i>Black Wind</i>. </p>
<p><b>Red Rolfe</b> is an ironborn warrior. </p>
<p><b>Rollam Westerling</b> is the second son of Gawen Westerling, Lord of the Crag, and Sybell Spicer. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rolland Darklyn</b> was a knight of House Darklyn. He was a member of the Kingsguard at an unknown time, one of seven members from House Darklyn. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Rolland Longthorpe</b> is Lord of Longsister and head of House Longthorpe. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rolland Storm</b>, known as <b>the Bastard of Nightsong</b>, is a knight of House Caron. He is the bastard son of the late Lord Bryen Caron of Nightsong and the half-brother of Lord Bryce Caron. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rolland Uffering</b> was a knight from House Uffering during the reign of Daeron II Targaryen. He was Lady Rohanne Webber's fourth husband. His sister was Lady Helicent Uffering. Rolland died in the Great Spring Sickness. </p>
<p><b>Rohanne Webber</b>, known as the <b>Red Widow</b>, was the Lady of Coldmoat and head of House Webber during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. She was the daughter of Lord Wyman Webber. Later, she married Lord Gerold Lannister and became Lady of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p>The <b>Great Spring Sickness</b> was a plague epidemic which took place in 209&nbsp;AC and 210&nbsp;AC, killing tens of thousands in the Seven Kingdoms. Victims are said to have "died in the spring". </p>
<p><b>Rolley of Sisterton</b> is a steward of the Night's Watch. His cousin is Lark the Sisterman. </p>
<p><b>Rollo</b> was a septon of the Faith of the Seven during the reign of Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rolly Duckfield</b>, also known as <b>Duck</b>, is a knight in service to Young Griff. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rolph Spicer</b> is a knight from House Spicer and is the castellan of the Crag for House Westerling. He is the brother of Sybell Spicer and grandson of Maggy the Frog. </p>
<p><b>Rommo</b> is an old <i>jaqqa rhan</i> of the Dothraki that follows Daenerys Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Romny Weaver</b> is an ironborn raider from House Weaver. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ronald Connington</b> was the Knight of Griffin's Roost and head of House Connington. He had three children: Ronnet, Raymund and Alynne. </p>
<p><b>Ronald Storm</b> is the bastard son of Ser Ronnet Connington, the Knight of Griffin's Roost. He is most likely named for his grandfather, Ronald Connington. He resides in Griffin's Roost. </p>
<p><b>Ronald Vance</b>, known as <b>Ronald the Bad</b>, is a knight from House Vance of Atranta and the eldest son and heir of Lord Norbert Vance. He has four brothers; Ser Hugo, Ser Ellery, Ser Kirth, and Maester Jon. </p>
<p><b>Ronard Storm</b>, known as <b>Ronard the Bastard</b>, was a bastard of House Durrandon who became a Storm King. </p>
<p><b>Ronel Rivers</b> is a member of House Frey and a bastard son of Lord Walder Frey. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ronnal Baratheon</b> was a knight from House Baratheon and a younger brother of Lord Rogar Baratheon of Storm's End. </p>
<p><b>Ronnel Arryn</b> was the last King of Mountain and Vale, reigning until the invasion of Westeros by Aegon the Conqueror. Only a boy, rule of the Vale of Arryn fell to his mother, Queen Regent Sharra Arryn, who was regarded as one of the most beautiful women of Westeros. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ronnel Arryn</b> was a knight of House Arryn and was the younger brother of Lord Jon Arryn. He was wed to a noblewoman from House Belmore. They had one son, Elbert Arryn. </p>
<p><b>Ronnel Harclay</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch from House Harclay. </p>
<p><b>Ronnel Penrose</b> was the Lord of Parchments and the head of House Penrose during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. He later married Princess Elaena Targaryen and had four children together. </p>
<p><b>Ronnel Stout</b> is a member of House Stout. </p>
<p><b>Ronnel Vance</b> was the head of House Vance during the reign of Maegor I Targaryen. It is unknown if he was the Lord of Atranta or Wayfarer's Rest. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ronnet Connington</b>, also known as <b>Red Ronnet</b>, is the Knight of Griffin's Roost. He is a landed knight and the head of House Connington. Ronnet has a bastard son, Ronald Storm. </p>
<p><b>Griffin's Roost</b>, or simply the <b>Roost</b>, is the seat of House Connington in the stormlands. The castle is located between Storm's End and Crow's Nest in northwestern Cape Wrath. It is ruled by Ser Ronnet Connington, the Knight of Griffin's Roost. </p>
<p><b>Rook</b> is one of the crew on Asha Greyjoy's ship, <i>Black Wind</i>. </p>
<p><b>Roone</b> is a young novice at the Citadel. </p>
<p><b>Roone</b> is the maester at Castle Lychester. </p>
<p><b>House Lychester</b> is a noble house from Castle Lychester in the riverlands. According to semi-canon sources they blazon their arms with orange and white gyronny, a black talon. </p>
<p><b>Roose Bolton</b> is the Lord of the Dreadfort and head of House Bolton. He is convinced that regular leechings improve a person's health, and as such frequently has himself leeched, which has led to some calling him <b>the Leech Lord</b>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Michael McElhatton. </p>
<p>The <b>Dreadfort</b> is a fortress in the north and the seat of House Bolton in northeastern Westeros. Located on the banks of the upper Weeping Water, it is southeast of the Lonely Hills and north of the Sheepshead Hills. The Dreadfort is north of Hornwood, south of Last Hearth, and southwest of Karhold. </p>
<p><b>Roose Ryswell</b> is a son of Lord Rodrik Ryswell and a member of House Ryswell. </p>
<p><b>Rorge</b> is one of the criminals Yoren picked for the Night's Watch when he cleaned out the dungeons of King’s Landing and is part of the group marching north to the Wall. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Andy Beckwith. </p>
<p>The <b>black cells</b> are in the third level of the dungeons of the Red Keep in King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Roro Uhoris</b> was a Tyroshi smuggler and pirate, captain of the <i>Cobblecat</i>. He was known as the <b>Blind Bastard</b> up and down the narrow sea though he was neither blind nor a bastard. </p>
<p><b>Rory</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Roryn Drumm</b>, known as <b>Roryn the Reaver</b>, was a member of House Drumm. </p>
<p><b>Rosamund Ball</b> was a lady of House Ball during the reign of Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Rosamund Darry</b> was a member of House Darry during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Rosamund Lannister</b> is a member of House Lannister of Lannisport. </p>
<p><b>Lord Rosby</b> was the Lord of Rosby and the head of House Rosby during the reigns of kings Viserys I and Aegon II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Rose of Red Lake</b> is a legendary daughter of Garth Greenhand and ancestor of House Crane of Red Lake. According to legend, she was a skinchanger who could transform into a crane at will. Some say this ability manifests in women of House Crane from time to time. </p>
<p><b>Rosey</b> is the daughter of Emma, a serving wench at the Quill and Tankard in Oldtown. Early in 300&nbsp;AC, she is fifteen years old and freshly flowered. Her mother is demanding a gold dragon for her maidenhead. </p>
<p><b>Rosey</b> was the youngest of the four bastard children of King Aegon IV Targaryen and his second mistress, Megette. </p>
<p><b>Roslin Frey</b> is a noblewoman of House Frey, the only daughter of Lord Walder Frey by his sixth wife, Lady Bethany Rosby, but his fifth overall. Roslin has four older brothers –Ser Perwyn, Ser Benfrey, Maester Willamen, and Olyvar– and many half-siblings. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is played by Alexandra Dowling. </p>
<p>Lord <b>Rossart</b> was a member of the Alchemists' Guild in King's Landing. He served as the Hand of the King to Aerys II Targaryen for a fortnight. </p>
<p><b>Rowan</b> is a spearwife of the free folk. </p>
<p><b>Rowan Gold-Tree</b> is a legendary daughter of Garth Greenhand. </p>
<p><b>Rowena Arryn</b> was a member of House Arryn, the cousin and second wife of Lord Jon Arryn. She died of a winter chill. They were childless. </p>
<p><b>Rowley</b> was a maester who became Lord Confessor for King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Roy Connington</b>, known as <b>Red Roy Connington</b>, was the Lord of Griffin's Roost and the head of House Connington during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
