<p><b>Royce Blackwood</b> was a member of House Blackwood during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Royce Caron</b> was the Lord of Nightsong, Lord of the Marches, and head of House Caron during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons and the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Royce Coldwater</b> is Lord of Coldwater Burn and head of House Coldwater. </p>
<p><b>Rudge</b> is a steward of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Rue</b> was the author of <i>Bastard Born</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rufus Leek</b> is a knight of House Leek and the castellan of the Dun Fort in Duskendale. </p>
<p><b>Rugen</b> is an undergaoler in charge of the third level of the dungeons of the Red Keep, known as the black cells. </p>
<p><b>Rugen Saltbeard</b> is an ironborn captain under Euron Greyjoy. </p>
<p><b>Runceford Redwyne</b> was a Lord of the Arbor and head of House Redwyne. He was the father of Lady Olenna Tyrell and grandfather of Lord Paxter Redwyne. </p>
<p><b>Runcel Hightower</b> was a member of House Hightower and a former Lord Commander of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Runciter</b> was a Grand Maester during the late reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and the early reign of King Viserys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rupert Brax</b> is a knight from House Brax. He is the brother of Lord Andros Brax of Hornvale. In <i>A Clash of Kings</i>, he is mistakenly called <b>Rubert Brax</b> in chapter 32. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rupert Crabb</b> was a knight from House Crabb who became a member of the Kingsguard at an unknown time. </p>
<p><b>Rupert Falwell</b>, known as <b>the Fighting Fool</b>, was a Lord of House Falwell during the Faith Militant uprising. </p>
<p><b>Rus</b> is one of Aeron Greyjoy's drowned men. </p>
<p><b>Rusalia Egen</b> was a lady of House Egen mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Russ Barleycorn</b> is a member of the Night's Watch. He is captain of the <i>Storm Crow</i> at Eastwatch-by-the-Sea. He shares a surname with Tom Barleycorn, a ranger. </p>
<p><b>Russell Merryweather</b> is the son of Lord Orton Merryweather and Lady Taena of Myr and the heir to Longtable. </p>
<p><b>Russell Stillman</b> was the former squire of Lord Alyn Velaryon and the author of <i>Hard as Oak</i>. </p>
<p><b>Rusty Flowers</b> is a member of the Night's Watch. His surname suggests he is a bastard from the Reach. </p>
<p><b>Lord Ruthermont</b> was an Andal lord during the Andal invasion of the Vale. </p>
<p><b>Ryam</b> is an archmaester of the Citadel. He has a poor opinion of Archmaester Marwyn. His ring, rod and mask are of yellow gold. His maester's chain has no link of Valyrian steel. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ryam Florent</b> was a knight of House Florent, the father of Selyse, Imry and Erren. He was a younger brother of Lord Alester Florent. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ryam Redwyne</b> was a famed knight from House Redwyne who served as Lord Commander of the Kingsguard under Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Viserys I Targaryen. He also briefly served as Hand of the King for Jaehaerys I. </p>
<p><b>Ryben</b> was a maester of the Citadel. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rycherd Crane</b> is a knight from House Crane and is the husband of Rylene Florent, the sister of Lord Alester Florent. </p>
<p><b>Ryella Frey</b> is the eldest child of Ser Arwood Frey and Ryella Royce. </p>
<p><b>Ryella Royce</b> is a member of House Royce and the wife of Ser Arwood Frey, a grandson of Lord Walder Frey of the Twins. They have four young children together; Ryella, Androw, Alyn and Hostella Frey. </p>
<p><b>Ryger Rivers</b> is a bastard son of Lord Walder Frey of the Crossing. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Ryger is portrayed by Bryan McCaugherty. </p>
<p><b>Ryk</b>, known as <b>Longspear Ryk</b>, is a free folk raider and a member of Rattleshirt's war band. </p>
<p><b>Rylene Florent</b> is the only sister of Lord Alester Florent of Brightwater Keep. She is married to Ser Rycherd Crane. </p>
<p><b>Ryles</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Rylona Rhee</b> is a former slave freed by Daenerys Targaryen. She was enslaved and trained in Yunkai and while there was taught to play music. She plays the harp beautifully and played for many of the noble families of Yunkai. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ryman Frey</b> is a knight from House Frey of the Twins. He is the eldest son of Ser Stevron Frey and second in line to inherit the title of Lord of the Crossing if his grandfather, Lord Walder Frey, dies. </p>
<p><b>Rymolf Stormdrunk</b> is an ironborn steersman in the crew of Victarion Greyjoy. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Rymond Arryn</b> was a knight from House Arryn during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Rymund the Rhymer</b> is a singer and harper. </p>
<p><b>Anvil Ryn</b> was an inhabitant of the riverlands. He was slain by the forces of House Lannister during the War of the Five Kings. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Ryon Allyrion</b> is a knight from House Allyrion. He is the son and heir of Delonne Allyrion, Lady of Godsgrace. Ryon is married to Ynys Yronwood, with whom he has children, at least two sons. He also has a bastard son, Ser Daemon Sand. </p>
<p><b>Lord Ryswell</b> is thus far unnamed. He was lord of House Ryswell at some point, and his youngest son had joined the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Lord Ryswell's youngest son</b> is thus far unnamed. He was a son to Lord Ryswell, and eventually joined the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>S'vrone</b> is a dockside whore in Braavos of a murderous bent. She is said to have killed and robbed a dozen men, rolling their bodies into the canals to feed the eels. </p>
<p><b>Braavos</b> is the wealthiest and likely the most powerful of the Free Cities. It is located in a lagoon on the northwestern end of Essos, where the narrow sea and the Shivering Sea meet. Braavos is also known as <b>Braavos of the Hundred Isles</b> and the <b>Secret City</b>, a name also attributed to the city Nefer, the last remaining city of N'ghai. Braavos is sometimes referred to as the "bastard daughter of Valyria". </p>
<p><b>Saathos the Wise</b> was a visitor to Qarth. According to legend, he thought the city so beautiful that he blinded himself because he knew that all he would see after would be ugly in comparison. </p>
<p><b>Saathos Saan</b> was a Lysene pirate-lord who named himself King of the Basilisk Isles. He was a member of the Saan family and ancestor of Salladhor Saan. </p>
<p><b>Sabitha Frey</b>, née <b>Vypren</b>, was a noblewoman of House Vypren and the wife of Lord Forrest Frey, the head of House Frey and the Lord of the Crossing during the reigns of kings Viserys I and Aegon II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Princess <b>Saera Targaryen</b> was the ninthborn child of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen and Queen Alysanne Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Jaehaerys I Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>the Conciliator</b>, <b>the Wise</b>, or later in life as <b>the Old King</b>, was the fourth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne. He ascended the throne in 48&nbsp;AC following the death of his uncle, Maegor I Targaryen. Jaehaerys was the longest reigning Targaryen monarch, sitting on the throne for fifty-five years. He was a dragonrider, riding Vermithor, the largest dragon after Balerion and Vhagar. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Alysanne Targaryen</b>, also known as <b>Good Queen Alysanne</b>, was the queen consort of her brother, King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. Alysanne was a dragonrider, whose mount was Silverwing. </p>
<p><b>Saffron</b> is the daughter of a spice merchant from Gulltown, one of the richest men in the city. Recently, Ser Harrold Hardyng has impregnated her with his second bastard. </p>
<p>The <b>Sailor's Wife</b> is a prostitute who works at the Happy Port brothel in Braavos. Her real name is unknown, but she is called the Sailor's Wife because she only beds those who marry her. She sometimes marries three or four times a night. She has a fourteen-year-old daughter, named Lanna, who also works at the brothel. </p>
<p><b>Salladhor Saan</b>, known as <b>Salla</b> to his friends, is a notorious Lysene pirate, sellsail, smuggler, trader, and banker. He styles himself the Prince of the Narrow Sea and is a descendant of the Saan family. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Salladhor is portrayed as a Lysene citizen of Summer Islander descent and is played by Lucian Msamati. </p>
<p><b>Sallei Paege</b> is a member of House Paege and is married to Ser Jammos Frey with whom she has three children, Walder, Dickon and Mathis Frey </p>
<p><b>Sallor the Bald</b> is a Qartheen captain of the mercenary company, Stormcrows. </p>
<p>The <b>Stormcrows</b> are a mercenary company found in the Free Cities. Their banner displays four crows between crossed lightning bolts. They number five hundred horses. </p>
<p><b>Salloreon</b> is a master armorer in King's Landing. </p>
<p><b>Sally</b> is the daughter of a farmer in the riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Sam Stoops</b> was the steward of Standfast for House Osgrey during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Standfast</b> is the stronghold of House Osgrey in the Reach. It is called a castle by courtesy, but more closely resembles a towerhouse. Three villages fall within its dominion. Its exact location has not yet been published, but it is located a few leagues west of Coldmoat in the north of the Reach; the Osgreys were once Marshalls of the Northmarch. Standfast is sworn to House Rowan of Goldengrove. </p>
<p><b>Sam Stoops' wife</b> served at Standfast during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. The name of Sam Stoops' spouse is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Sam Salt</b> was a pretender Lord of the Iron Islands who claimed descent from the black line, House Hoare. </p>
<p><b>Samantha Stokeworth</b> was a member of House Stokeworth in the reigns of kings Aenys I, Maegor I, and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Samantha Tarly</b>, known as <b>Lady Sam</b>, was a member of House Tarly who wed first Lord Ormund Hightower and later his son, Lord Lyonel Hightower. She was the founder of the Bank of Oldtown. </p>
<p><b>Samarro Saan</b>, known as <b>the Last Valyrian</b>, was a Lysene pirate who became one of the infamous Band of Nine, the instigators of the War of the Ninepenny Kings. He is an ancestor of Salladhor Saan. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Samgood of Sour Hill</b>, known as <b>Sour Sam</b>, was a knight of the Kingsguard during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. Prior to this, he was a hedge knight and boasted to be a veteran of hundreds of battles. </p>
<p><b>Samwell Blackwood</b> was the Lord of Raventree Hall and head of House Blackwood at the start of the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>

<p><b>Samwell Tarly</b> is the eldest son of Lord Randyll Tarly and his wife Lady Melessa Florent. A recruit of the Night's Watch originally from House Tarly, he is popularly called <b>Sam</b>. He becomes a POV character in <i>A Storm of Swords</i>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by John Bradley. </p>

She has three brothers: Robb, Bran and Rickon; a younger sister: Arya; and a half-brother: Jon Snow. Sansa Stark is one of the major POV characters in the books. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, she is played by Sophie Turner. </p>

<p><b>Savo</b> was a Dothraki <i>khal</i> and the husband of a woman who later became high priestess of the <i>dosh khaleen</i>. He has only been mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>

<p><b>Scales</b> is one of the children of the forest in service to the last greenseer. He/she does not speak the Common Tongue. His/her true name is too long for the human tongue according to Leaf, so Meera Reed and Bran make up the name Scales. </p>

<p>Lady <b>Serenei of Lys</b>, also called <b>Sweet Serenei</b>, was the ninth and last mistress of Aegon IV Targaryen. There was one child of their union, Shiera Seastar, the last of the king's Great Bastards. </p>

<p><b>Shadd</b> is a member of the household guard sworn to House Stark of Winterfell. </p>

<p>The <b>Shady Glen</b> is a place in Westeros, although its location is unknown. </p>
<p>A <b>hedge knight</b> is a wandering knight without a master. Hedge knights travel the length and breadth of the Seven Kingdoms looking for gainful employment. </p>

<p>The <b>Stone Crows</b> are one of the mountain clans that inhabit the Mountains of the Moon, in the Vale of Arryn. </p>

<p><b>Sharra Arryn</b>, known as <b>the Flower of the Mountain</b>, was Queen Regent of the Kingdom of Mountain and Vale, ruling in the name of her son, the boy-king Ronnel Arryn, during the invasion of Westeros by Aegon I Targaryen. Sharra was regarded as one of the most beautiful women of Westeros. </p>

<p><b>Harrenhal</b>, the largest castle in the Seven Kingdoms, is the seat of House Whent in the riverlands, on the north shore of the Gods Eye. Since the burning of Harrenhal by dragonfire in Aegon's Conquest, however, the castle has become a dark and ruinous place. </p>

<p><b>Simon Toyne</b> was the leader of the Kingswood Brotherhood, an outlaw group active during the reign of Aerys II Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>Kingswood Brotherhood</b> was an infamous outlaw organization during the reign of King Aerys II. Operating out of the Kingswood, the Brotherhood gained recognition by kidnapping several nobles and evading early attempts to capture them. Ultimately, they became such a nuisance that King Aerys sent a detachment of soldiers led by notable members of the Kingsguard to destroy them. Lord Sumner Crakehall and his two squires, Jaime Lannister and Merrett Frey, were also part of the retinue. </p>
<p><b>Skahaz mo Kandaq</b>, also known as the <b>Shavepate</b>, is a Ghiscari noble of the city of Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Skinner</b> is a man-at-arms sworn to House Bolton. He is one of the Bastard's Boys. </p>
<p><b>Ramsay Snow</b> is the bastard son of Roose Bolton, Lord of the Dreadfort and head of House Bolton, and is known as <b>the Bastard of Bolton</b> and <b>the Bastard of the Dreadfort</b>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Iwan Rheon. </p>
<p>The <b>Bastard's Boys</b> are men-at-arms of House Bolton, in service to Ramsay Bolton. </p>
<p><b>Skittrick</b> is a member of the household guard sworn to House Stark of Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Skyte</b> is an ironborn sailor sworn to Balon Greyjoy. </p>
<p><b>Lord Slate</b> is the head of House Slate of Blackpool. </p>
<p><b>Sloey</b> is a mummer of the Ship. </p>
<p><b>Sly</b> was a stableboy at Hogs Head, a disreputable inn in Bitterbridge, during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>The <b>Hogs Head</b> was a disreputable inn in the town of Bitterbridge owned by Ben Buttercakes. It was destroyed during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Small Paul</b> is a steward of the Night's Watch. His nickname is ironic, as he is a very big man. </p>
<p><b>Smike</b> was a maester of the Citadel who served House Farman of Fair Isle during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>The <b>Smiling Knight</b> was an infamous outlaw and robber knight of the Kingswood Brotherhood. He was thought to be insane, but was also a deadly swordsman. The Smiling Knight's given name has not been published. </p>
<p><b>Snatch</b> is a sellsword of the Second Sons. His rank is serjeant. He is one handed and chews sourleaf. </p>
<p><b>Snowylocks</b> is one of the children of the forest in service to the last greenseer. She does not speak the Common Tongue. Her true name is too long for the human tongue according to Leaf. </p>
<p><b>Softfoot</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p>An exile <b>sorcerer lord</b>, who claims to be the sixty-ninth yellow God-Emperor of Yi Ti, lives in the city of Carcosa in the Further East of Essos. </p>
<p><b>Soren Shieldbreaker</b> is a free folk leader. </p>
<p><b>Spare Boot</b> is a builder of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>The Sparr</b> is the head and lord of House Sparr of Great Wyk. His son, Steffarion Sparr, is his heir. His given name has not been published. </p>
<p>The <b>Spice King</b> is an extremely rich merchant in Qarth and a member of the Thirteen. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is played by Nicholas Blane. However in the books, there is an Ancient Guild of Spicers in the city of Qarth, that does not appear in the TV Series. Thus the Spice King is a composite character. </p>
<p>The <b>Spotted Cat</b> is a pit fighter famed in Meereen. His origin is unknown, but he supports the pit fighting culture of the city. </p>
<p><b>Spotted Pate</b> is a character from a thousand stories. </p>
<p><b>Spotted Pate of Maidenpool</b> is a builder of the Night's Watch. He comes from Maidenpool in the riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Squint</b> is an ironborn raider. </p>
<p>The <b>squinter</b> is a secret servant of the Many-Faced God in the House of Black and White in Braavos and a Faceless Man. </p>
<p><b>Squire Squishlips</b> was the nickname Prince Oberyn Martell gave to an unidentified suitor of his sister Elia Martell during the trip the siblings took in 273&nbsp;AC, during which their mother hoped to betroth either one of them, or both. </p>
<p><b>Squirrel</b> is a spearwife of the free folk. </p>
<p>A <b>spearwife</b> is a free folk woman who is also a warrior. </p>
<p><b>Lord Stackhouse</b> was the head of House Stackhouse during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Stafford Lannister</b> is a knight of House Lannister. He is the good-brother to the Warden of the West as his sister, Lady Joanna, married their cousin, Lord Tywin Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Stalwart Shield</b> is an Unsullied sworn to Daenerys Targaryen. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is named <b>White Rat</b>. </p>
<p>The <b>Unsullied</b> are eunuch slave soldiers, trained from a young age in Astapor to unquestioning obedience and martial prowess. Sold by the century or the thousand, they are used as guards all over the Free Cities. They make excellent guards, do not loot, and will never rape. </p>
<p><b>First Ranger Stane</b> was a member of House Stane who briefly served as First Ranger of the Night's Watch over a thousand years ago. His given name has not been revealed. </p>
<p><b>Stannis Baratheon</b> is the head of House Baratheon of Dragonstone and the Lord of Dragonstone. He is the secondborn son of Steffon Baratheon, Lord of Storm's End, and Lady Cassana Estermont. He has an older brother, King Robert I Baratheon, and a younger brother, Lord Renly Baratheon. Stannis serves on Robert's small council as the master of ships. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> Stannis is played by Stephen Dillane. </p>
<p><b>Stannis Seaworth</b> is the sixth son of Ser Davos Seaworth and his wife Marya. He is presumably named after Stannis Baratheon. He lives at the family keep on Cape Wrath with his mother and his younger brother Steffon. </p>
<p><b>Stanton Piper</b> was a Lord of Pinkmaiden and head of House Piper during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>The <b>starved man</b> is a secret servant of the Many-Faced God in the House of Black and White in Braavos and a Faceless Man. </p>
<p><b>Lady Staunton</b> was the wife of Lord Staunton, the ruling Lord of Rook's Rest and head of House Staunton during the Dance of the Dragons. Her given name and birth house are unknown. </p>

<p><b>Lord Staunton</b> was the Lord of Rook's Rest and the head of House Staunton during the reign of kings Maegor I Targaryen and Jaehaerys I Targaryen. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Steelskin </b> is a younger pit fighter in Meereen, not regarded as the first rank. </p>

<p><b>Steffar Stammerer</b> is an ironborn raider in Victarion Greyjoy's crew. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Steffon Stackspear</b> is a knight from House Stackspear. He is the eldest son and heir of Lord Selmond Stackspear. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Stevron Frey</b> is a knight from House Frey, Lord Walder Frey's firstborn son, and heir to the Twins. His mother was Lady Perra Royce. Stevron has had several children through his marriages to Corenna Swann, Jeyne Lydden, and Marsella Waynwood. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Colin Carnegie. </p>
<p>The <b>Twins</b>, sometimes known as the <b>Crossing</b>, is the seat of House Frey in the northern riverlands. It is a fortified crossing of the Green Fork of the Trident and consists of two identical castles and a tower in the middle of their bridge. It is one of the most formidable strongholds of the Seven Kingdoms. </p>

<p><b>Taena of Myr</b>, also known as <b>Taena Merryweather</b>, is the Myrish wife of Lord Orton Merryweather and is the Lady of Longtable. They have one child, Russell. </p>

<p><b>Terro</b> is a Braavosi Bravo. </p>

<p><b>The Rat, the Hawk, and the Pig</b> are three individuals who are mentioned in the history of Westeros. Their real names are not known. </p>
<p><b>Theo</b> is a man-at-arms in service to House Lannister. He was specifically created for a scene in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>

<p><b>Theo Charlton</b> was Lord and head of House Charlton, who joined Harwyn Hoare in the battle at Fairmarket against King Arrec Durrandon. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Theo Frey</b> is a knight from House Frey. His relationship with Lord Walder Frey is undetermined. </p>
<p><b>Theo Teague</b> was the fourth monarch of House Teague to rule the riverlands. He was known as <b>Theo the Saddle-sore</b> because he spent his entire reign on horse, crushing rebellions and hanging hostages. </p>
<p><b>Theo Tyrell</b> was the Lord of Highgarden and head of House Tyrell. He was the son of Lord Harlen Tyrell, the first Lord Paramount of the Mander. </p>
<p><b>Theo Wull</b>, also known as <b>Buckets</b> because of his clan's sigil, was a member of the Wulls. His relation to Hugo Wull, the clan chief of the Wulls, is unknown. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Theobald</b> is an archmaester of the Citadel. His ring, mask and rod are made of lead. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Theodan Wells</b>, called <b>Theodan the True</b>, is a pious knight. Theodan is either from House Wells of the north or from House Wells of Dorne. </p>
<p><b>Theodor Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Theodore Tyrell</b> is the eldest son of Ser Luthor Tyrell and Elyn Norridge. The knight is married to Lia Serry. They have two children, Elinor and Luthor. </p>
<p><b>Theomar Smallwood</b> is the Lord of Acorn Hall and head of House Smallwood. He is married to Lady Ravella Swann and is the father of Carellen Smallwood. </p>
<p><b>Acorn Hall</b> is the seat of House Smallwood in the riverlands. It is located southeast of Riverrun, northeast of Pinkmaiden, and north of Stoney Sept. High Heart and Blackbottom Bend are nearby. </p>
<p><b>Theomore</b> is a maester of the Citadel, in service to House Manderly of White Harbor. He is a member of House Lannister of Lannisport. </p>
<p><b>White Harbor</b> is a harbor city in the north which contains the New Castle, the seat of House Manderly. Located south of Winterfell, it is the largest settlement north of the Neck, but the smallest among the five major cities of Westeros. White Harbor is the north's primary trade port. Its location on the mouth of the White Knife provides opportunities for trade further north. </p>
<p><b>Theomore Harlaw</b> was the head of House Harlaw who raised the Ten Towers to replace Harlaw Hall. He had six wives and was the great-great grandfather of Lord Rodrik Harlaw. </p>
<p><b>Theomore Manderly</b> was the Lord of White Harbor and the head of House Manderly during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Theon Greyjoy</b> is a member of House Greyjoy and is the sole surviving son and heir apparent of Balon Greyjoy, Lord of the Iron Islands. At the end of Greyjoy's Rebellion, Theon was taken to Winterfell as a hostage and ward to Lord Eddard Stark. He becomes a POV character in <i>A Clash of Kings</i>. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Alfie Allen. </p>
<p>The <b>Iron Islands</b> is one of the constituent regions of the Seven Kingdoms. Until Aegon's Conquest it was ruled by the Kings of the Iron Islands and then briefly the Kings of the Isles and the Rivers. </p>
<p><b>Theon III Greyjoy</b> was a High King of the Iron Islands from House Greyjoy. </p>
<p><b>Theon Stark</b>, known as <b>the Hungry Wolf</b>, was a King in the North and head of House Stark. Theon Greyjoy refers to Theon Stark as his namesake. </p>
<p><b>Theresa Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Theron</b> was a maester of the Citadel who lived a century ago. </p>
<p><b>Therry</b> is a young turnkey in the Wolf's Den. He is the son of one of the two washerwomen at the Wolf's Den. His mother is bedding two of the guardsmen. He wants to go off to war and become a knight. </p>
<p><b>Thistle</b> is a wildling spearwife. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Thomas the Threadbare</b> was a knight during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Thomax</b> was a maester the author of the book <i>Dragonkin, Being a History of House Targaryen from Exile to Apotheosis, with a Consideration of the Life and Death of Dragons</i>. </p>
<p><b>Thoren Smallwood</b> is a member of House Smallwood and a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Thormor Ironmaker</b> is an ironborn raider from House Ironmaker. He is a grandson of Erik Ironmaker. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Thoron True</b> was a knight and a sworn sword to Corlys Velaryon, Lord of the Tides and Hand of the Queen to Rhaenyra Targaryen, during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Thoros of Myr</b> is a red priest of R'hllor from the Free City of Myr, and a member of King Robert I Baratheon's court at King's Landing. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Paul Kaye. </p>
<p><b>Three-Tooth</b> is the steward of Ten Towers for Lord Rodrik Harlaw. She has been the steward since she was known as Twelve-Tooth. She is very old. She only has one tooth at present. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Thurgood</b> was an archmaester of the Citadel. He wrote the book <i>Inventories</i>, which listed the existence of 227 Valyrian steel blades in all of Westeros. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Thurgood Fell</b> was a knight from House Fell during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Three Toes</b> is a member of the Brave Companions. </p>
<p><b>Three-Tooth</b> is the steward of Ten Towers for Lord Rodrik Harlaw. She has been the steward since she was known as Twelve-Tooth. She is very old. She only has one tooth at present. </p>
<p>The <b>Tickler</b> is a man-at-arms and torturer in service to Ser Gregor Clegane. One of the Mountain's men, his given name is unknown. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Anthony Morris. </p>
<p><b>Tigaro Moraqos</b> was a Lysene magister. </p>
<p><b>Tim Stone</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. He is a bastard from the Vale of Arryn. </p>
<p><b>Tim Tangletongue</b> is a steward of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Castle Black</b> is the main stronghold of the Night's Watch and the seat of their Lord Commander. The castle is situated along the Wall between Queensgate to the west and Oakenshield to the east, near the center of the Wall, at the northern end of the kingsroad. The village of Mole's Town is located half a league to the south along the kingsroad. </p>
<p><b>Timeon</b>, also known as <b>Timeon of Dorne</b>, is a Dornish sellsword of the Brave Companions. </p>
<p><b>Timett</b> is a red hand, a type of war chief, of the Burned Men, one of the most-feared Vale clans of the Mountains of the Moon. He is commonly known as <b>Timett son of Timett</b>, after his father, and is also called <b>Timett One-Eye</b>. </p>
<p>The <b>Burned Men</b> are one of the mountain clans of the Vale of Arryn. They are feared by the rest of the clans. </p>
<p><b>Timett</b> is the father of Timett of the Burned Men in the Vale of Arryn. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Timon</b>, better known as <b>Timon the Scrapesword</b>, is a famed knight. </p>
<p><b>Timoth</b> is a servant of House Martell at Sunspear. He is very dignified. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Timotty</b> is an Archmaester of the Citadel and the author of <i>Conjectures</i>, where he suggests that Aegon I Targaryen spared Sunspear during the "Dragon's Wroth" in the First Dornish War hoping that the Dornishmen would turn on House Martell for not falling prey to dragonfire.. </p>
<p><b>Timotty Snow</b>, known as <b>the Bastard of Flint's Finger</b>, was a member of House Flint of Flint's Finger. </p>
<p><b>Tion Frey</b> is the third son of Ser Emmon Frey and Genna Lannister. He is a squire. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tion Lannister</b> was a knight of House Lannister. He was the second son of Lord Gerold Lannister and Lady Rohanne Webber, and the twin brother of Tywald. </p>
<p><b>Tion Tarbeck</b>, nicknamed <b>the Red</b>, was a member of House Tarbeck. He was the son of Lord Walderan Tarbeck by his third wife, Lady Ellyn Reyne. According to semi-canon sources, the red-haired Tion was named after the late Tion Lannister, Ellyn's first husband, as an attack against Gerold Lannister, Lord of Casterly Rock. He had two sisters and several half-siblings. </p>
<p><b>Titus Peake</b> is the Lord of Starpike and the head of House Peake. He is married to Lady Margot Lannister. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Titus Peake</b> was a knight from House Peake and the heir to Starpike, Dunstonbury, and Whitegrove during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Tobbot</b> is an armsman in service to Ser Gregor Clegane. </p>
<p><b>Tobho Mott</b> is a Qohorik master armorer whose shop is at the top of the Street of Steel in King's Landing. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is played by Andrew Wilde. </p>
<p><b>Todder</b>, nicknamed <b>Toad</b> by his peers, is a recruit of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Todric</b> is a fat ironborn raider. </p>
<p><b>Toefinger</b> is a wildling raider. </p>
<p><b>Togarion Bar Emmon</b>, known as <b>Togarion the Terrible</b>, was an Andal warlord who established his own kingdom north of Blackwater Bay during the Andal invasion. He was being hard-pressed by the Darklyn king of Duskendale. Sensing weakness to the south, Togarion took the daughter of Josua Massey and crossed Blackwater bay with all his power to establish a new kingdom on Massey's Hook. He built the castle of Sharp Point at the Hook's end, whilst driving the stormlanders from Stonedance and installing his wife's brother as a puppet king. </p>
<p><b>Togg Joth</b> is a member of the Brave Companions. He is Ibbenese. </p>
<p><b>Ibben</b> is an island nation in the Shivering Sea, which is the polar sea north of the eastern continent, Essos. </p>
<p><b>Togosh</b> is a pit fighter in Meereen. </p>
<p><b>Tom</b>, dubbed <b>Spotted Tom the Butcher</b>, was the captain of a sellsword company in the Disputed Lands who became one of the infamous Band of Nine, the instigators of the War of the Ninepenny Kings. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tom the Strummer</b>, known as <b>the Bard of Flea Bottom</b>, was a knight and singer during the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Tom Barleycorn</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch at Castle Black. He shares a surname with Russ Barleycorn, a fellow member of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Tom Codd</b>, known as <b>Bloodless Tom</b>, is the captain of the ship <i>Lamentation</i> in the Iron Fleet. He is under the command of Victarion Greyjoy. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tom Costayne</b>, better known as <b>Long Tom Costayne</b>, was a knight from House Costayne who became a member of the Kingsguard at an unknown time. </p>
<p><b>Tom Flowers</b>, known as the <b>Bastard of Bitterbridge</b>, was a bastard from House Caswell of Bitterbridge. </p>
<p><b>Tom Tanglebeard</b> was a man from Dragonstone. His son was Tom Tangletongue, and his nephew was Ser Marston Waters. Tom and his son were referred to collectively as the "Two Toms". </p>
<p><b>Tom Tangletongue</b> was a inhabitant of Dragonstone during the Dance of the Dragons. His father was Tom Tanglebeard, and his cousin was Ser Marston Waters. Tom and his father were referred to collectively as the "Two Toms". </p>
<p><b>Tom Tidewood</b> is an ironborn raider in Victarion Greyjoy's crew. </p>
<p><b>Tom Turnip</b> was a royal jester and fool at court in the Red Keep during the late reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Tom</b>, known as <b>TomToo</b>, is the son of Tomard, one of the House Stark guards at Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Toman</b> is a maester of the Citadel. He serves House Toland at Ghost Hill. </p>
<p><b>Tomard</b>, better known as <b>Fat Tom</b>, is a guard sworn to House Stark. He has a son, TomToo. </p>
<p><b>Tomarro</b> is from Braavos. He is one of the regulars at the Gate. </p>
<p><b>Tommard Baratheon</b> was the secondborn son of Lord Stannis Baratheon and Lady Selyse Florent in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. He was stillborn. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tommard Heddle</b>, known as <b>Black Tom</b>, was a knight from House Heddle. He was the son-in-law of Lord Ambrose Butterwell of Whitewalls. </p>
<p><b>Tommard Karstark</b> was a member of House Karstark mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Tommax Baratheon</b> was an early member of House Baratheon mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Tommen Baratheon</b> is known to the Seven Kingdoms as the youngest child of King Robert I Baratheon and Queen Cersei Lannister. A member of House Baratheon of King's Landing, his siblings are Prince Joffrey and Princess Myrcella. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by Callum Wharry in seasons 1 and 2 and by Dean-Charles Chapman in seasons 4, 5 and 6. </p>
<p><b>Tommen Costayne</b> is Lord of the Three Towers and head of House Costayne in the Reach. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tommen Costayne</b> was a knight of House Costayne  during the reign of King Daeron II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Tommen I Lannister</b> was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Tommen II Lannister</b>, known as the <b>Lion King</b>, was a King of the Rock from before the War of Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Tommen Tully</b> was Lord of Riverrun and head of House Tully during the reign of the Storm King Arrec Durrandon's rule over the riverlands. </p>
<p><b>Tommy</b> is the barber at Winterfell. The character was created specifically for the TV series and is portrayed by Tommy Dunne. </p>
<p>The <b>Topaz Emperor</b> was the legendary sixth ruler of the mythic Great Empire of the Dawn. He succeeded the Onyx Emperor and was in turn succeeded by the Opal Emperor. </p>
<p><b>Torbert</b> is a septon of the Faith of the Seven in King's Landing. He is of the Most Devout. </p>
<p><b>Toregg</b>, called <b>Toregg the Tall</b> and <b>Tall Toregg</b>, is the eldest son of Tormund Giantsbane. </p>
<p><b>Torgen Oakheart</b> was the Lord of Old Oak and the head of House Oakheart during the reign of King Maegor I Targaryen and the beginning of the reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Torghen Flint</b>, known as <b>Old Flint</b> and <b>the Flint</b>, is clan chief of the First Flints, one of the northern mountain clans. He is the father of Donnel and Artos Flint, each by a different woman. </p>
<p><b>Torgold Tollett</b>, called <b>Torgold the Grim</b>, was an Andal warrior from House Tollett that lived during the Andal invasion. </p>
<p><b>Torgon Greyiron</b>, also known as <b>Torgon the Latecomer</b>, was a High King of the Iron Islands from House Greyiron during the Age of Heroes. </p>
<p><b>Torgon the Terrible</b> is a legendary ironborn raider from the Age of Heroes. </p>
<p><b>Torman Peake</b> is a sellsword in service to the Golden Company. He is one of the brothers of the exiled Lord Laswell Peake. </p>
<p><b>Tormo Fregar</b> is a Braavosi noble of House Fregar. </p>
<p><b>Tormund</b>, often called <b>Tormund Giantsbane</b> or <b>Tormund Thunderfist</b>, is a famous free folk raider from Ruddy Hall. He has four sons, Toregg, Torwynd, Dryn, and Dormund, and one daughter, Munda. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Kristofer Hivju. </p>
<p><b>Toron Greyjoy</b> was the Lord of the Iron Islands, Lord Reaper of Pyke, and the head of House Greyjoy during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Torrek</b> is a member of the Stone Crows, one of the Vale mountain clans found in the Mountains of the Moon. </p>
<p><b>Torren Liddle</b>, called <b>the Liddle</b>, is the clan chief of House Liddle, a mountain clan in the North. He is the father of Duncan, Morgan and Rickard Liddle. </p>
<p><b>Torrence Teague</b> was an adventurer of uncertain birth who was the eventual victor in the century-long conflict that arose in the riverlands after the death of King Bernarr II Justman. He was the founder of House Teague of the riverlands. Having seized a fortune in gold in an attack upon the westerlands, he used this wealth to bring large numbers of sellswords from across the Narrow Sea. After six years of war, Torrence was crowned King of the Trident at Maidenpool. However, he was so little loved he was forced to keep sons and daughters of the riverlords as hostages to ensure their loyalty. </p>
<p><b>Torreo Haen</b> was a Lysene magister who briefly became First Magister of Lys. </p>
<p><b>Torrhen Karstark</b>, affectionately called <b>Torr</b> by his sister Alys, is the youngest son of Lord Rickard Karstark of Karhold. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Tyrone McElhennon. </p>
<p><b>Torrhen Manderly</b> was a knight from House Manderly during the Dance of the Dragons and the second son of Lord Desmond Manderly. He later became the Lord of White Harbor, as well as Lord Regent and Hand of the King during the minority of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Torrhen Stark</b>, known as <b>the King Who Knelt</b>, was a head of House Stark who reigned as King in the North until Aegon I Targaryen invaded Westeros with his dragons. He was named Lord of Winterfell and Warden of the North after submitting to Aegon during the War of Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Torrhen Stark</b> was a member of House Stark. He was the younger brother of his twin Cregard, and the youngest son of Edric Stark and Serena Stark. </p>
<p><b>Torwold Browntooth</b> is an ironborn raider. He has one wife. </p>
<p><b>Torwyn Greyjoy</b> was a Lord of the Iron Islands and head of House Greyjoy. </p>
<p><b>Torwynd</b>, known as <b>Torwynd the Tame</b>, is a son of Tormund. </p>
<p><b>Tothmure</b> is a maester of the Citadel at Harrenhal. </p>
<p>The <b>Tourmaline Emperor</b> was the legendary fourth ruler of the mythic Great Empire of the Dawn. He succeeded the Jade Emperor and was in turn succeeded by the Onyx Emperor. </p>
<p><b>Trebor Jordayne</b> is Lord of the Tor and head of House Jordayne in Dorne. </p>
<p>The <b>Tor</b> is the seat of House Jordayne in Dorne. It is located on the southern shore of the Sea of Dorne, north of the Scourge. </p>
<p><b>Tregar</b> is a guard sworn to House Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Tregar Ormollen</b> is a merchant prince of Lys. He shares his manse with the exiled Lynesse Hightower, who became his chief concubine after leaving her husband, Ser Jorah Mormont. </p>
<p><b>Tremond Gargalen</b> is the Lord of Salt Shore and the head of House Gargalen. </p>
<p><b>Salt Shore</b> is the seat of House Gargalen in Dorne. It lies on the southern coast along the Summer Sea. </p>
<p><b>Trianna</b> was a triarch of the Free City of Volantis who lived at the end of the Century of Blood. </p>
<p><b>Tristan Mudd</b> was a member of House Mudd who became Lord Commander of the Night's Watch. He is considered one of the worst commanders the Night's Watch has ever had. </p>
<p>The <b>Night's Watch</b> is a military order dedicated to holding the Wall, the immense fortification on the northern border of the Seven Kingdoms, defending the realms of men from what lies beyond the Wall. The order's foundation dates back to the Age of Heroes, at the time when the Others were pushed back. The men of Night's Watch wear only black, and they are known as <b>black brothers</b>. Recruits who join the Watch are said to <b>take the black</b>. </p>
<p><b>Tristan Ryger</b> is a member of House Ryger. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tristan Rivers</b> is a Westerosi sellsword in service to the Golden Company. He is a bastard. </p>
<p><b>Tristan Vance</b> was the Lord of Wayfarer's Rest and the head of House Vance of Wayfarer's Rest during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Tristifer Botley</b>, known as <b>Tris</b>, is the second son of Lord Sawane Botley. </p>
<p><b>Tristifer IV Mudd</b>, also known as <b>the Hammer of Justice</b>, was the fourth King of the Rivers and the Hills to bear that name. A monarch of the First Men from House Mudd, his crypt lies among the ruins of Oldstones. </p>
<p><b>Tristifer V Mudd</b>, also known as <b>Tristifer the Last</b>, was the fifth King of the Rivers and the Hills to bear that name. A monarch of the First Men from House Mudd, and with him his royal line became extinct. </p>
<p><b>Tristifer Wayn</b> was a Lord of House Wayn during the Faith Militant uprising. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tristimun</b> was an old knight during the reign of Aerys II Targaryen. He commanded with the sea watch out of Dragonstone. For smugglers it meant death. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Triston of Tally Hill</b> is a knight in service to House Sunglass. He is from Tally Hill. </p>
<p><b>Triston Farwynd</b> is the Lord of Sealskin Point and the head of House Farwynd. </p>
<p><b>Sealskin Point</b> is the seat of House Farwynd on Great Wyk. </p>
<p><b>Triston Hightower</b> was a head of House Hightower and Lord of the Hightower. </p>
<p><b>Triston Massey</b> was the Lord of Stonedance and the head of House Massey during the War of Conquest. </p>
<p><b>Triston Sunderland</b> is the Lord of the Three Sisters and head of House Sunderland. He has seven sons, all of whom desire to be knights. </p>
<p>The <b>Three Sisters</b> are a group of three islands—Sweetsister, Longsister, and Littlesister—found in the Bite, located south of White Harbor and north of the Mountains of the Moon. The islands owe loose allegiance to House Arryn of the Vale. </p>
<p><b>Black Trombo</b> was a Myrish sellsword in the service of House Vance of Wayfarer's Rest during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p>Prince <b>Trystane Nymeros Martell</b>, better known simply as <b>Trystane Martell</b>, is the youngest child of the ruling Prince of Dorne, Doran Martell, and his wife, Lady Mellario of Norvos. He is affectionately called <b>Trys</b> by his sister Arianne. </p>
<p><b>Trystane</b>, later called <b>Trystane Truefyre</b>, was a squire to Ser Perkin the Flea, a hedge knight, during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Tuffleberry</b> is a servant at Harrenhal who takes care of the brewhouse. </p>
<p><b>Tulip Umber</b> was a member of House Umber mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Lord Tully</b> was the Lord of Riverrun and the head of House Tully during the early reign of King Aerys II Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Lord Tully</b> was the Lord of Riverrun and the head of House Tully during the reign of King Aerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Tumberjon</b> is a ranger of the Night's Watch. </p>
<p><b>Tumco Lho</b>, nicknamed <b>Tum</b>, is a former slave in Meereen training to become a knight. </p>
<p><b>Turnip</b> is a scullion and the child of Gage, the cook at Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Turquin</b> is a maester at the Citadel. </p>
<p>The <b>two female puppeteers</b> are women of King's Landing that end up in the Red Keep's black cells, used by Qyburn for his experiments. </p>
<p>A <b>two-headed girl</b> from Mantarys is a slave owned by Yezzan zo Qaggaz. She is a part of Yezzan's grotesquerie, one of Yezzan's <i>special treasures</i>. </p>
<p><b>Two Swords</b> is a sellsword in service to the Golden Company. His given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Ty</b> is a steward to the Night's Watch at Castle Black. </p>
<p><b>Tya Lannister</b> was a member of House Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Tyana Wylde</b> was a member of House Wylde. She was the wife of Ser Aenys Frey, with whom she had two sons, Aegon and Rhaegar. </p>
<p>Queen <b>Tyanna of the Tower</b>, also known as <b>Tyanna of Pentos</b>, was a courtesan from Pentos who married King Maegor I Targaryen, becoming the third of his six wives. </p>
<p><b>Tybald</b> is a maester of the Citadel in service to the Dreadfort. </p>
<p><b>Tybero Istarion</b>, better known as <b>Inkpots</b>, is the paymaster of the Second Sons, a mercenary company. </p>
<p>The <b>Second Sons</b> are a sellsword company found in the Free Cities. Their banner is a broken sword and they take commands only from their captain. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tybolt Crakehall</b> is a knight of House Crakehall. He is the eldest son and heir of Lord Roland Crakehall. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tybolt Hetherspoon</b> is a landed knight and head of House Hetherspoon. He had a daughter, Melara, who drowned in a well when she was young. </p>
<p><b>Tybolt Lannister</b> was Lord of Casterly Rock and head of House Lannister. He was the eldest son and heir of Lord Damon Lannister. He had a younger brother, Gerold, who was his advisor. </p>
<p>King <b>Tybolt Lannister</b>, dubbed <b>the Thunderbolt</b>, was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Tycho Nestoris</b> is a representative of the Iron Bank of Braavos. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Mark Gatiss. </p>
<p><b>Tyene Sand</b> is the bastard daughter of Prince Oberyn Martell and a septa. She is one of the infamous Sand Snakes. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Rosabell Laurenti Sellers. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tygett Lannister</b>, called <b>Tyg</b> by his family, was a knight from House Lannister. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tyland Lannister</b> was a knight from House Lannister. He served on the small council at King's Landing, as master of ships for Viserys I Targaryen, as master of coin for Aegon II Targaryen, and as Hand of the King for Aegon III Targaryen. He was the younger twin brother of Jason Lannister, the Lord of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tyler Hill</b> was a knight in the service of House Lannister and a bastard son of Lord Lyman Lannister of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tyler Norcross</b> was a knight and the head of House Norcross during the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons. </p>
<p><b>Tyler Teague</b> was one of the last monarchs of House Teague. He was the youngest son of Humfrey I Teague, who caused a massive uprising of Riverlords by attempting to suppress worship of the old gods. In the campaign's final battle, Humfrey I perished, and the crown passed to Tyler's eldest brother, who became Humfrey II. However, Humfrey II was also killed, whereupon Hollis, Tyler's second eldest brother, picked up the crown, only to be killed in turn. Thus Tyler became the King of the Rivers and the Hills, but also died, inheriting the crown to his uncle Damon, who was also killed. By the end of the day, House Teague was extinct. </p>
<p><b>Poxy Tym</b> is a member of the household guard sworn to House Stark of Winterfell. </p>
<p><b>Tymond Lannister</b> was the Lord of Casterly Rock and the head of House Lannister during the late reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Tymor</b> is an ironborn raider sworn to House Greyjoy. He has brothers who are also raiders. </p>
<p><b>Tyrek Lannister</b> is a member of House Lannister. He is the son of Ser Tygett Lannister and Lady Darlessa Marbrand. </p>
<p><b>Tyrek Tallhart</b> was a member of House Tallhart mentioned in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Tyrion Lannister</b> is a member of House Lannister and is the third and youngest child of Lord Tywin Lannister and the late Lady Joanna Lannister. His older siblings are Cersei Lannister, the queen of King Robert I Baratheon, and Ser Jaime Lannister, a knight of Robert's Kingsguard. </p>
<p><b>Tyrion II Lannister</b>, called <b>the Tormentor</b>, was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Tyrion III Lannister</b> was a King of the Rock from House Lannister of Casterly Rock. </p>
<p><b>Tyrion Tanner</b> is the bastard son of Lollys Stokeworth and an unknown father. </p>
<p>A <b>Tyroshi sellsword</b> commands the freeriders of Ser Forley Prester within the Lannister host led by Ser Jaime Lannister during the early stages of the War of the Five Kings. The mercenary comes from Tyrosh, and his given name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Tysane Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, the eldest daughter of Lothar Frey and Leonella Lefford.  </p>

<p><b>Tyta Frey</b>, better known as <b>Tyta the Maid</b> is the fourth daughter of Lord Walder Frey, the second daughter born of his marriage to Alyssa Blackwood. She is supposedly still a maid. </p>
<p><b>Tytos Blackwood</b> is the Lord of Raventree Hall and the head of House Blackwood in the riverlands. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tytos Brax</b> is a knight of House Brax. He is the eldest son of Lord Andros Brax and the heir to Hornvale. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tytos Frey</b> is a knight from House Frey and is the eldest son of Ser Jared Frey and Alys Frey. He is married to Zhoe Blanetree and has two children; Zia and Zachery Frey. </p>
<p><b>Tytos Lannister</b> was the Lord of Casterly Rock and the head of House Lannister during the reigns of kings Aegon V, Jaehaerys II, and Aerys II Targaryen. He is the grandfather of Cersei, Jaime and Tyrion by his eldest son, Tywin Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Tytos Lannister's first mistress</b> was a lowborn woman who served as a wet nurse for House Lannister. Her name is unknown. </p>
<p><b>Tytos Lannister's second mistress</b> was a lowborn woman, the daughter of a candlemaker. Her name is unknown. </p>
<p>Ser <b>Tywald Lannister</b> was a knight from House Lannister, the eldest son and heir of Lord Gerold Lannister and Lady Rohanne Webber, the twin of Tion and elder brother of Tytos and Jason Lannister. </p>
<p><b>Tywell II Lannister</b>, formally styled <b>Tywell Lannister, the Second of His Name</b>, was a King of the Rock of House Lannister of Casterly Rock. He was identified by some as the Andal king in the tale of the Rat Cook. </p>
<p><b>Tywin Frey</b>, affectionately called <b>Ty</b> by his grandmother, is a member of House Frey and is the eldest son of Ser Cleos Frey and Jeyne Darry. </p>
<p><b>Tywin Frey</b> is the fourth son of Ser Raymund Frey and Beony Beesbury, the twin of Jaime. </p>
<p><b>Tywin Lannister</b> is Lord of Casterly Rock, Shield of Lannisport, and Warden of the West. The head of House Lannister, Tywin is one of the most powerful lords in Westeros, and he is the father of Queen Cersei, Ser Jaime of the Kingsguard, and Tyrion. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, Tywin is portrayed by Charles Dance. </p>
<p><b>Casterly Rock</b>, nicknamed <b>the Rock</b>, is a castle and the seat of House Lannister. The capital of the westerlands, it is on the ocean road and overlooks the harbor of Lannisport and the Sunset Sea. Nearby strongholds include Kayce and Feastfires to the west, Sarsfield to the north, and Cornfield and Clegane's Keep to the south. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Ulf White</b>, also known as <b>Ulf the White</b> and <b>Ulf the Sot</b>, was a dragonseed who became a dragonrider during the Dance of the Dragons. </p>

<p>Ser <b>Ulwyck Uller</b> is a knight from House Uller and the younger brother of Lord Harmen Uller. He is the uncle of Ellaria Sand, the paramour of Prince Oberyn Martell. This makes him the granduncle of the four youngest Sand Snakes: Elia, Obella, Dorea and Loreza. </p>
<p><b>Umar</b> is the father of Ulf, a member of the Moon Brothers in the Vale of Arryn. </p>

<p><b>Urron Greyiron</b>, known as <b>Urron Redhand</b> and <b>Urron of Orkmont</b>, was a member of House Greyiron. He was the first King of the Iron Islands to make the throne hereditary, five thousand years before the War of the Five Kings. </p>

<p><b>House Tully of Riverrun</b> is one of the Great Houses of the Seven Kingdoms. Lord Hoster Tully, the Lord Paramount of the Trident, rules over the riverlands from the Tully seat of Riverrun. Their sigil is a silver trout leaping on a striped field of blue and mud red, and their house words are "Family, Duty, Honor." </p>

<p>The <b>master of whisperers</b> or <b>mistress of whisperers</b> is the spymaster for the Lord of the Seven Kingdoms, the monarch on the Iron Throne. He or she is charged with gathering intelligence from informants in the Red Keep, in King's Landing, around the Seven Kingdoms, across the narrow sea, and other places. Unlike the other positions of the small council, this title was not created by Aegon I Targaryen. </p>

<p>Prince <b>Viserys Targaryen</b> is the heir of his father, King Aerys II Targaryen, following the death of his older brother, Prince Rhaegar, during Robert's Rebellion. The war turned Viserys and his younger sister, Daenerys, Princess of Dragonstone, into exiles from the Seven Kingdoms who can only plot to regain control of the Iron Throne. </p>
<p><b>Viserys I Targaryen</b> was the fifth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne, ruling from 103&nbsp;AC to 129&nbsp;AC. He succeeded his grandfather, the Old King Jaehaerys I. Viserys continued the prosperous peace and legacy of his grandsire, but the seeds for the civil war known as the Dance of the Dragons that would much later engulf the realm were inadvertently sown in his reign. </p>
<p><b>Viserys II Targaryen</b> was the tenth Targaryen king to sit the Iron Throne as Lord of the Seven Kingdoms. He was the son of Rhaenyra Targaryen and Daemon Targaryen, the brother and Hand of King Aegon III Targaryen, and the father of King Aegon IV Targaryen, Queen Naerys Targaryen, and Prince Aemon "the Dragonknight". </p>

<p><b>Walder Frey</b>, nicknamed <b>Big Walder</b>, is the son of Ser Jammos Frey and Sallei Paege. His personal coat of arms quarters the twin towers of House Frey with the tree and ravens of House Blackwood and the twinning snakes of House Paege. </p>
<p><b>Walder Frey</b>, called <b>Black Walder</b> to differentiate him from others with the same name, is a member of House Frey. Tim Plester portrays "Black Walder Rivers", a combination of Black Walder Frey and Walder Rivers, in the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>. </p>
<p><b>Walder Frey</b>, nicknamed <b>Little Walder</b>, is the son of Merrett Frey and Mariya Darry. His personal coat of arms is the twin towers of House Frey quartered with the brindled boar of House Crakehall and the plowman of House Darry. </p>
<p><b>Walder Frey</b>, known as <b>Red Walder</b>, is the youngest son of Ser Emmon Frey, the second son of Lord Walder Frey, and Genna Lannister, the sister of Lord Tywin Lannister. He has three brothers: Ser Cleos, Ser Lyonel, and Tion Frey. </p>
<p><b>Walder Frey</b> is the Lord of the Crossing and head of House Frey. Though almost ninety years old and infirm, he still maintains an active hand in the running of his house at the Twins. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is played by David Bradley. </p>

Walder's personal coat of arms is a silver-grey castle on blue (the colors of House Frey reversed) beneath a red bend sinister. <p><b>Waltyr Frey</b>, called <b>Tyr</b>, is the twenty-first born son of Lord Walder Frey, the third son of his marriage to his seventh wife, Lady Annara Farring. However, rumor in the Twins is that Annara was sleeping with Black Walder Frey making Waltyr's parentage dubious. </p>

<p><b>Wyman Manderly</b> is the Lord of White Harbor and the head of House Manderly. He also holds several honorary titles: Warden of the White Knife, Shield of the Faith, Defender of the Dispossessed, Lord Marshal of the Mander, and Knight of the Order of the Green Hand. A widower for the past eight years, Wyman has two adult sons, Ser Wylis and Ser Wendel Manderly. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is portrayed by Sean Blowers. </p>
<p><b>Wyman Webber</b> was the Lord of Coldmoat and head of House Webber during the reign of Daeron II Targaryen. He had one daughter, Rohanne Webber. </p>

<p><b>Xanda Qo</b>, Princess of Sweet Lotus Vale, was a warrior woman from the Summer Isles. She was the mother of Chatana Qo, the Arrow of Jhahar. </p>

<p><b>Xaro Xhoan Daxos</b> is a merchant prince of Qarth. He is a member of the Thirteen, a prominent group of traders within the city. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Nonso Anozie as an immigrant from the Summer Isles. </p>
<p><b>Qarth</b> is an ancient port city located on the southern coast of Essos. It has been referred to as the <b>Queen of Cities</b>, a title also claimed by Yunkai in Slaver's Bay. </p>
<p><b>Xhobar Qhoqua</b>, known as <b>the Ebon Prince</b>, was a member of the Band of Nine. He was an exile prince from the Summer Isles who found fortune in the Disputed Lands leading a sellsword company. </p>

<p><b>Yandry</b> is the master and captain of the poleboat, <i>Shy Maid</i>. He is married to Ysilla. </p>
<p><b>Yezzan zo Qaggaz</b> is an extremely wealthy slave trader, and is one of the Wise Masters from Yunkai. He is said to be the richest man in the Yellow City, and has great influence because of this. </p>
<p><b>Ygon Farwynd</b> is the son of Lord Gylbert Farwynd. He resembles his father. </p>
<p><b>Ygon Oldfather</b> is a wildling clan chief. He commands a following composed mostly of his own sons and grandsons. He has eighteen wives, half of whom were stolen on raids. </p>
<p><b>Ygritte</b> is a spearwife of the free folk. She is a member of Rattleshirt's war band. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> she is portrayed by Rose Leslie. </p>
<p><b>Yna</b> is a prostitute at the Happy Port brothel in Braavos. </p>
<p>The <b>Happy Port</b> is a brothel in Braavos, near Ragman's Harbor. It sits across an alley from the Mummer's Ship, and abuts a canal. It is run by Meralyn. The brothel is decorated with a mural of a purple galleas, crewed by women wearing nothing but thigh-high boots. </p>
<p><b>Ynys Yronwood</b> is the eldest daughter of Lord Anders Yronwood. She is married to Ser Ryon Allyrion, with whom she has children, at least two sons. </p>
<p><b>Yohn Farwynd</b> is the son of Lord Gylbert Farwynd. He resembles his father, tall, with color changing eyes. </p>
<p><b>Yohn Royce</b>, known as <b>Bronze Yohn</b>, is the Lord of Runestone and the head of the senior branch of House Royce. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i>, he is portrayed by Rupert Vansittart. </p>
<p><b>Runestone</b> is the seat of House Royce in the Vale of Arryn. It lies on a peninsula north of the Bay of Crabs, east of Redfort and south of Old Anchor. While Runestone is on the northern shore of the peninsula, the nearby city of Gulltown is on the southern shore. </p>
<p><b>Yorbert Royce</b> was the Lord of Runestone and the head of House Royce during the late reign of King Jaehaerys I Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Yoren</b> is a sworn brother of the Night's Watch. A recruiter, or wandering crow, he travels the Seven Kingdoms, and is responsible for collecting recruits and prisoners who would take the black. He then escorts them to Castle Black for training. In the television adaptation <i>Game of Thrones</i> he is portrayed by Francis Magee. </p>
<p><b>Yoren Yronwood</b> was a member of House Yronwood who fought alongside Wylla of Wyl against King Durran the Young at the Battle by the Bloody Pool and turned back. </p>

<p><b>Yormwell</b> was the personal maester of Prince Baelor Targaryen. </p>
<p>Maester <b>Yorrick</b> was a maester of the Citadel who served at White Harbor. He wrote the book <i>Wed to the Sea, Being an Account of the History of White Harbor from Its Earliest Days</i>. </p>
<p>King <b>Yorwyck VI Royce</b> was a Bronze King of House Royce of Runestone who lived during the Andal invasion. He claimed the Runic Crown when his sire died in battle against House Shett. </p>
<p><b>Yrma Peake</b>, known as <b>Yrma of the Golden Bowl</b>, was a Lady of Starpike. She was an illustrious and legendary ancestor of House Peake. </p>
<p><b>Ysabel</b> was a septa of the Faith of the Seven during the reign of Jaehaerys I Targaryen and one of the "Wise Women". </p>
<p><b>Ysabel Staunton</b> was a member of House Staunton during the reign of King Aegon III Targaryen. </p>
<p><b>Ysilla</b> is Yandry's wife. She is one of the crew of the <i>Shy Maid</i>. She is an orphan of the Greenblood come home to Mother Rhoyne. </p>
<p><b>Ysilla Royce</b> is a noblewoman of House Royce and is the daughter of Lord Yohn Royce of Runestone. </p>
<p><b>Yurkhaz zo Yunzak</b> is a Yunkish noble and the Supreme Commander of the Armies and Allies of Yunkai. </p>
<p><b>Zachery Frey</b> is a member of House Frey, the eldest son of Ser Tytos Frey and Zhoe Blanetree. He is studying at the Sept of Oldtown. </p>
<p><b>Zahrina</b> is a slave trader from Slaver's Bay. She purchases cheap slaves for the fighting pits, expecting them to be slain by heroes. She is also either the owner or proprietor of the Purple Lotus, a winesink in Meereen. </p>
<p>Archmaester <b>Zarabelo</b> is an archmaester at the Citadel in Oldtown. </p>
<p><b>Zeggo</b> was a Dothraki <i>khal</i> who lived during the Century of Blood. He sacked the city of Sarys, the last city of the Kingdom of Sarnor to fall to the Dothraki. </p>
<p><b>Zei</b> is a whore in Mole's Town. She is good with a crossbow. </p>
<p><b>Zekko</b> is a Dothraki <i>khal</i>. It is said every three to four years he visits Qohor to get a sack of gold so his <i>khalasar</i> will turn away. </p>
<p><b>Zhako</b> was a Dothraki <i>khal</i> who lived during the Century of Blood. He was one of the four <i>khals</i> that fought in the Field of Crows. </p>
<p><b>Zharaq zo Loraq</b> was a famous Ghiscari citizen of the city of Meereen. He is an ancestor of Hizdahr zo Loraq. </p>
<p><b>Zhea</b>, also known as <b>Zhea the Barren</b>, <b>Zhea the Cruel</b>, and <b>Zhea Zorseface</b>, was the first <i>jhattar</i> of the Jogos Nhai. </p>
<p><b>Zhoe Blanetree</b> is a member of House Blanetree and the wife of Ser Tytos Frey, a grandson of Lord Walder Frey. They have two children together: Zia and Zachery Frey. </p>
<p><b>Zia Frey</b> is the daughter of Ser Tytos Frey and Zhoe Blanetree. </p>
<p><b>Zollo</b>, better known as <b>Zollo the Fat</b>, is a Dothraki member of the Brave Companions. </p>
